# Igros Kodesh

## Volume 4

## 766

B"H, Erev Rosh Hashanah, 5711

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, and distinguished R' Moshe, may he live:

Greetings and blessings!

I hereby acknowledge with thanks the receipt of your telegram of blessing. May the one who blesses be blessed with all that he requires, both materially and spiritually.

Although the responsibilities placed upon ministers, soldiers, and the people as a whole differ in their details, at the time of the coronation of a king, the common denominator among them all is that they all accept upon themselves the yoke of kingship. Through this, the people and the king are bound together in the relationship of kingship, even though, in essence, there is no comparison between them. This is especially true in the present context regarding Rosh Hashanah, when the Holy One, Blessed be He, says to His people: "Make Me king over you."

Just as a body is healthy only if its connection with the head is complete, so too is the year "healthy" only when its connection with its "head" (Rosh Hashanah) is healthy.

That is to say, the resolutions that one accepts upon oneself on Rosh Hashanah—out of *kabbalas ol* (acceptance of the yoke), even when the intellect does not necessarily agree—must be carried out in practice throughout the year.

The advantage of a Chossid in this regard—a Chossid of any type, whether Polish, Chabad, Galician, etc.—is that he performs even the matter of *kabbalas ol* with joy, and consequently, the *avodah* is performed in its completeness.

With blessings for a *Kesivah Vachasimah Tovah* for a good and sweet year.

Rabbi Menachem Schneerson

What, in the final analysis, is the state of the education of the immigrant youth? And what are the peaceful ways to improve it?

## 7057

B"H, Erev Rosh Hashanah, 5711

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of 23 Elul:

...Regarding the question of where to send your daughter to study: Certainly, you must reach an understanding regarding your grievances with the yeshiva administration in a peaceful manner. However, your child is surely not to blame, and she must, in any event, receive a genuine Yiddishe education. Your child must not suffer because of a dispute that has not yet been resolved, and a child’s chinuch cannot be changed on a whim.

Erev Rosh Hashanah does not allow the time to elaborate as is required, but I believe that the few lines written above are sufficient. May Hashem help you and your wife, may she live and be well, to have much Yiddishe nachas from your daughter.

Rabbi Menachem Schneerson

**Admur Shlita**

## 758

B"H,

The significance of these days—the ten days between Rosh Hashanah and Yom Kippur in general (regarding which the prophet commanded, "Seek Hashem when He is found, call upon Him when He is near," for then there is a closeness of the Luminary to the spark), Shabbos Shuvah (for every Shabbos is an acronym for *tashuv enosh* [return, O man], and on this Shabbos in particular, the custom is to give a *drasha* to arouse the people to *teshuvah*), and Yom Kippur (which is a time of *teshuvah* for every individual and for the collective... therefore everyone is obligated to perform *teshuvah* and confess on Yom Kippur) in particular—

Their essence is *teshuvah*, and in the two levels contained within *teshuvah*: a) *Teshuvah Tata'ah* (lower *teshuvah*), *teshuvah* for the sin, iniquity, and transgression that one has committed. b) *Teshuvah Ila'ah* (higher *teshuvah*), to return one's spirit in a state of *bitul* and *mesiras nefesh* to the Elokus that gave it, to its root and essential source, just as it was before its descent, **and even beyond that**.

It is understood from this that *Teshuvah Tata'ah* can be applied even to specific matters and parts of the soul's faculties—those specific faculties and matters in which one has sinned and caused a blemish.

However, *Teshuvah Ila'ah* is "Shema Yisrael"—the gathering and collecting of all the soul's faculties that had become scattered, their elevation, and **the longing of the soul** (*kallos hanefesh*), from below to above, and subsequently, the drawing down from above to below **into all parts of the soul**.

And just as it is in the individual, so too is it in the general, complete stature of all Bnei Yisrael, "your heads, your tribes... down to the drawer of your water," that they must all be gathered and standing as one, so that the totality of the souls of Yisrael may return to their source and root.

Among the factors that assist in the unification of all the particulars is the *hiskashrus* with the collective, in which they were all included as one, and where they remain compatible even now.

Regarding us, the Chassidim of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, *ztz"l*, *anash* who are connected to him or even just associated with him, this is the *hiskashrus* to him through studying his Torah, walking in the straight path that he taught us, etc.—as has been explained many times.

This is indeed a preparation and assistance for the fulfillment of the blessing with which my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, *ztz"l*, would bless those who came to him to request a blessing on Erev Yom Kippur after midday. And this is his language:

"May the Almighty grant a *chasimah* and *gmar chasimah tovah*, a year that is good and sweet in both material and spiritual matters, to be active in Torah and *avodah*. Those who have children, may the Almighty help them to have *nachas* from them, and *parnassah* with abundance. Those who need to build a home, may the Almighty help them in both material and spiritual matters."

Menachem Mendel ben Chana Schneerson

Erev Shabbos Shuvah, 5711, Brooklyn, N.Y.

## 459

B"H, Erev Shabbos Kodesh, Shabbos Shuvah, 5711
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed and distinguished Rabbi, etc., R' Y.
Shalom u’vrachah!

Enclosed is the Kuntres for Shabbos Shuvah — the upcoming Yom Kippur. You will surely merit to share it with all those around you; and how good it would be if they were to gather and assemble, etc.

See the marked sections in the introduction to the Kuntres, where the concept of Teshuvah Ilaah (in which lies the primary merit of those who do teshuvah, as written in Iggeres HaTeshuvah, end of Chapter 4) is explained. It is the gathering and collecting of all the powers of the soul, *tashuv enosh* [returning man to dust/source]. And in these days, it is also the gathering and collecting of all the details of the complete stature of Bnei Yisrael—"your heads, your tribes," etc., until "drawing from your water"—for "He became King in Yeshurun—when the heads of the people were gathered, the tribes of Israel together." 

The merit of Teshuvah Ilaah is great, especially at this time. For in the time of the Sanhedrin, those liable for the death penalty by the court who performed teshuvah were not pardoned by the **lower** court; but now, when only the **judgment** of the four death penalties remains, and it is handed over to the Heavenly Court—if one performs teshuvah, the Heavenly Court pardons him, and there is no trace left of his previous deeds (Makkos 13b; see also Shu"t Noda B'Yehudah, Mahadura Kamma, Orach Chaim 35).

And if, regarding the atonement of Yom Kippur, Chazal limited it by saying that it does not atone for half a measure, and some say that one who is liable for a punishment but did not sin is not exempted from the punishment by Yom Kippur (Kerisos 18b; Tosafos, s.v. *d'chankatei*, 7a), nevertheless, nothing stands in the way of those who do teshuvah.

May it be the will that there be fulfilled in each and every one of us the blessing of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, who was accustomed to bless those who entered to him on Erev Yom Kippur after midday to request his blessing:

"May the Almighty awaken a true awakening of teshuvah from the depths and the point of the heart."

And may we merit the fulfillment of the prophecy: "Israel, as soon as they perform teshuvah, they are **immediately** redeemed."

Blessing and being blessed with a *chasimah v'gmar chasimah tovah*,

Menachem Mendel ben Channah Schneerson

His *pidyon nefesh*, as well as that of the students, I read on Erev Rosh Hashanah at the Ohel, and on Rosh Hashanah in the hall of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory.

I received your letter, and in the meantime, you have surely received my letter containing the Kuntres for Rosh Hashanah.

Regarding what you wrote concerning...—you should occupy yourself with Chassidus, and set aside time specifically for the teachings of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, and for the dissemination of this Torah—for then we are all walking on the Rebbe’s shoulders, and he will do what needs to be done, **if** it needs to be done.

B"H, 6 Tishrei, 5711

To the esteemed and distinguished, Torah-scholar and G-d-fearing, R' Yaakov, may he live.

Greetings and blessings!

I was pleased to receive good regards from you through our friend, the esteemed Rabbi and Chassid, etc., etc., R' Sh. A. Kazarnovsky, may he live. He also conveyed to me your contribution of $0, which you placed at my disposal, and which I have distributed among the holy institutions and the work established by my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, for charity and discreet assistance. And as with all matters that live and grow, all the activities of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, are being directed and are expanding, B"H. It is to be hoped that with the Rebbe’s blessing and with the assistance of all the friends of the Rebbe and his activities—especially those friends who were privileged to be with him personally and to benefit from his influence—all matters of charity, proper education, and the dissemination of Torah, mitzvos, and good deeds will develop to an ever-higher degree.

I was also pleased to hear from Rabbi Kazarnovsky good regards from...

May he live, especially in matters of Yiddishkeit. I hope that beyond the other matters of Torah and mitzvos, he also occupies himself with setting fixed times to study, from time to time, the Torah of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, and Chassidus in general, as this provides a vitality in all the matters that each one of us must carry out.

With the blessing of *chasimah* and *gmar chasimah tovah* to you and your family, may they live,

**Menachem Schneerson**

## 711

B"H, 6 Tishrei, 5711

To the esteemed and G-d-fearing, etc., R' Shimon, may he live:

Peace and blessing!

I was pleased to receive your regards through our friend, the esteemed and G-d-fearing, etc., R' Avraham Chaim, may he live, Block. I was especially pleased to hear that you succeeded in ensuring that *netilas yadayim* is performed as it should be. We see here once again how correct the words of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, are: "There is a *chazakah* for *taamulah* that it does not return empty"—that when a Yid truly desires something, Hashem helps him so that his *ratzon* is fulfilled.

I trust that this will give you strength and encouragement to continue to utilize every opportunity to act for *Yiddishkeit*. When one accomplishes something with another person, it serves as a *keli* for *bracha* and *hatzlacha* in one’s own needs, for Hashem does not remain a debtor and repays many times over with everything that is necessary.

It will give me pleasure to hear from you from time to time with good news, both in *gashmius* and in *ruchnius*.

With the blessing of *chasimah* and *gmar chasimah tovah* for you and all your household, may they live,

Menachem Schneerson

## 712

B"H, 6 Tishrei, 5711

To the esteemed and distinguished R' Moshe Zev, may he live and be well,

Shalom u'Bracha!

You surely remember your visit with me, when you told me about the business you intend to begin after Yom Kippur. I would like to take this opportunity to wish you a *Chasimah v'Gmar Chasimah Tovah*, which also includes the wish that the new business you are about to undertake should proceed with *hatzlachah* in *gashmius*. And what *hatzlachah* in *gashmius* is, my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, explained with a saying from the Alter Rebbe: Hashem gives Jews *gashmius*, and Jews make *ruchnius* out of *gashmius*.

Since you are surely reciting Tehillim, I would like to suggest that for the next three months you recite chapter 71 of Tehillim every day, in addition to the *shiur* of Tehillim that you recite in any case, and I hope that this will be a *keli* for *bracha*.

I would also suggest that you ask our friend, the esteemed R' D. Edelman, may he live and be well, to establish a regular time to study the Rebbe’s Torah together.

Please convey my regards to your brothers and partners, may they live and be well. I hope you will report good news in general and in particular.

With the blessing of *Chasimah v'Gmar Chasimah Tovah*,

**Menachem Schneerson**

## 763

B"H, 7 Tishrei, 5711
Brooklyn

To the illustrious Rabbi, the G-d-fearing, the distinguished, scion of holy lineage, etc., Moreinu HaRav R' Y. shlita,

Greetings and blessings!

I hereby wish you a *chasima v’gmar chasima tova* for a good and sweet year, both materially and spiritually.

May it be the will of Hashem that our efforts succeed, that we be among those who assist in spreading the teachings of the Baal Shem Tov even to the "outside," for this is the preparation and the vessel for the coming of Mashiach Tzidkeinu.

With the blessing of *chasima v’gmar chasima tova*,

**M. Schneerson**

Enclosed is the *kuntres* for Rosh Hashanah—from the teachings of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory—which has just been published. I am certain you will find it of interest.

A brief note regarding the concept of a person’s *avodah* to their Creator during these days of *teshuvah*: At the beginning of the creation of the world, it is written, "And it was evening and it was morning, one day" (*Bereishis 1:5*). There are two opinions regarding time: whether it is one continuous flow or whether the days are distinct from one another. It could be said that this is the subject of the dispute in the Gemara and Rava in *Nazir (7a)*. Yet, according to all opinions, night and day are one, and they are not distinct, for "day" and "night" are merely incidents added to time, not its essence.

However, one day from another **is** distinct, for "each and every day performs its specific task" (*Zohar III 94b*). Therefore, there **are** seven days, distinct from one another—and **only** seven—because afterward, the cycle repeats: the first day, etc.

Regarding a person’s *avodah* to their Creator: Night and day—ultimately, "no one shall be cast away from Him" (*Shmuel II 14:14*), and deliberate sins become like merits, for he will remove the spirit of impurity, and "the night shall shine like the day" (*Tehillim 139:12*). But the days are distinct, for even in the time to come, "each *tzaddik* is scorched by the canopy of his fellow." And this is not the place to elaborate.

## Nine

9

B"H, 7 Tishrei, 5711

Mrs. Sarah, may she live, and Mrs. Leah, may she live,

Blessings and peace!

I have received your letter of September 5th, and for the New Year, I wish you and all your family a *chasima v’gmar chasima tova* in everything that each of you requires.

You are surely aware of the Jewish expression that a woman is called the *akeres habayis* (the mainstay of the home), because she is the *ikar* (essence/foundation) of the home. This is because the will and conduct of her husband and children depend upon her own will and conduct. From this, we learn two things: firstly, how great is the responsibility that the Ribono shel Olam has placed upon the woman; and secondly, since the Ribono shel Olam has placed such a responsibility upon the Jewish woman, He has surely given her the *kochos* (strength/powers) to be able to fulfill her *shlichus* in the best possible manner.

The significance of Rosh Hashanah is that it is the "head of the year." Just as whatever the head wills can be carried out by the body, so too, the good resolutions of the *bnei* and *bnos Yisrael* during these days—to draw closer to the Ribono shel Olam through Torah and *mitzvos*—are carried out in practice throughout the days of the entire year. This is the *segulah* for health, *parnassah*, and *hatzlacha* in all matters.

With blessings for a *chasima v’gmar chasima tova* for you and all your family, may they live,

Menachem Schneerson

## 796

796

B"H, 7 Tishrei, 5711

Mrs. ..., may she live.

Blessings and peace!

I have received your letter in which you write about yourself, your husband, may he live, and your daughter, may she live. You write that for some time now your husband’s business has not been going well, and you ask for a blessing.

We are now entering a new year; therefore, Jews must be certain that, being the children of Hashem and having a merciful Father (Av Harachamim) who certainly wishes to help all His children in whatever they lack—especially since His children have turned to Him on Rosh Hashanah and during these current days with a heartfelt request to help them—we must be certain that Hashem has accepted these requests and will grant you a *shanah tovah umetukah*—a good and sweet year. May your husband be stronger in health, may your *parnassah* improve, and may you have much *nachas* from your daughter, may she live—true Jewish *nachas*.

You write that you still remember what your grandfather told you. I am certain that you are passing this on to your daughter, so that from childhood she will be accustomed to the Jewish way and grow up to be a Jewish daughter in every detail. It is never too early to begin a child’s Jewish education; the more one gives and the earlier one begins, the more certain one can be that, regardless of the surrounding environment, the child will remain a *Yiddishe kind* and the parents will have much *nachas*—true Jewish *nachas*.

I would be interested to know in what kind of institution your daughter is receiving her education. Surely she attends a school where she is taught *Yiddishkeit*. I would also be interested to know what kind of business your husband manages, and whether he participates actively in synagogue life and in *shiurim* of *limud Torah* at the shul.

It would be appropriate for you, on Erev Shabbos and Erev Yom Tov, before lighting the candles, to set aside money for *tzedakah* in the *pushke* of Rebbe Meir Baal HaNes, as this is a *segulah* for health and *parnassah*.

I have passed your donation to the *Lishkat Chashaim*, the *tzedakah* fund from which help is given to individuals and institutions in a discreet manner, which is one of the highest forms of *tzedakah*. The receipt is enclosed.

With the blessing of *Chatimah v’Gmar Chatimah Tovah*,

**Menachem Schneerson**

## 757

I hope that you maintain a connection with them and utilize your influence over them, not only in matters of *tzedakah*, but also in bringing them closer to *Torah* and *mitzvos*—each in the way best suited for them, and with words that will be most effective. And if a father’s love for his son expresses itself in matters related to the body, then *kal v'chomer* (all the more so) it must express itself in matters related to the *neshamah*, which is relevant both in *Olam Hazeh* and in *Olam Haba*.

With blessings for a *kesivah v'chasimah tovah*,

**Menachem Schneerson**

## 759

[Between Rosh Hashanah and Yom Kippur, 5711]

...The recitation of "Chazak Chazak V’nischazeik" by the one called to the Torah is not considered an interruption, as it pertains to the conclusion of the reading (see Shulchan Aruch HaRav, 167:9). Furthermore, he himself says it, for our version is "V’nischazeik"...

#### 759

Printed in Likkutei Sichos, Vol. 21, p. 411.

## 480

B"H,

There is a unique dimension to the fulfillment of the mitzvah of Sukkah, and that is **the knowledge**. Since it is written, "In order that they may know," etc., one has not fulfilled the mitzvah properly if one does not know the intent of the mitzvah of Sukkah—that we were commanded to sit in the Sukkah as a remembrance of the exodus from Egypt.

It has already been explained in several places that the essence of *da'as* is not merely knowledge acquired from teachers or books; rather, the essence is to establish one's mind and fix one's thought with strength and courage of heart and mind, until one's thought is bound to this with a firm and powerful bond.

This knowledge is that "I made the Children of Israel dwell in Sukkos when I brought them out of the land of Egypt". Now, every single day, morning and evening, a person is obligated to see himself as if he is at the time of the exodus from Egypt. This is the exodus of the *nefesh elokis* from the imprisonment of the body, etc., through involvement in Torah and *mitzvos* in general, and specifically through the acceptance of the yoke of Heaven.

In the words of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe :

"The first thing is the exodus from Egypt and [its] boundaries. In terms of *avodah* in general, these are the general paths of life—the plans a person makes for his lifestyle, with the limitations and boundaries that are created for him according to his status and situation; that is, according to how he wants to position himself in life, etc.

"The first thing must be the exodus from Egypt—to go out from all these limitations. This means that no matter what plans he may have, he must have *kevius itim l'Torah* every day, and his *davening* must be 'prayed'—not just 'gotten through.' After the exodus from Egypt comes the splitting of the Red Sea. For as soon as a person begins the paths of *avodah*, various obstacles immediately arise for him, each of which is strong and tremendously great—just as it was for the Jews at their exodus from Egypt: behind them the enemy, in front of them the sea, and they themselves are in the desert.

"The splitting of the Red Sea was from above. The Almighty, blessed be He, split the sea and made it a path for the Jews, like dry land. But first, there had to be a 'leaper' into the sea. And when there was that 'leaper'—the person of *mesiras nefesh*—then Hashem made 'the sea into dry land.'"

And then the Holy One, blessed be He, caused them to dwell in the Sukkah. "As in the parable of an infant: as soon as he is born, they wash him of his filth and wrap him in clean cloth. Through this, not only is he protected from the external filth, but his limbs are also straightened and strengthened. And even though this is only for a time, it acts to strengthen his limbs for the entire duration of his growth and his becoming a man.

"So it is in *avodah*: when a person effects within himself the exodus from his own Egypt and boundaries—that he should emerge from the plans he makes for his lifestyle, at which time the evil of the *nefesh hativ'i* with its physical and bodily life-needs is more refined—then there must immediately be the 'journeying to Sukkos.'

"The Sukkah is a *makif*, but it is a *makif* that acts upon the *penimi* (the internal), just like the wrapping of the infant mentioned above, which affects the strengthening of his limbs even when he becomes a man.

"And this is [the meaning of], 'For I made the Children of Israel dwell in Sukkos when I brought them out of the land of Egypt.'"

Assistance and strength for this throughout all the days of the year are drawn from the festival of Sukkos in general, and the fulfillment of the mitzvah of sitting in the Sukkah in particular.

Mentioning our *Nesi'im*, their activities, and their teachings assists in this, as is known from the saying of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe: "There are the Chassidic *ushpizin*: the Baal Shem Tov, the Maggid, the Alter Rebbe, the Mitteler Rebbe, the Tzemach Tzedek, the Maharash, and the Rashab."

And we also add: my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe.

**Menachem Schneerson**

The day after Yom Kippur, 5711, Brooklyn, N.Y.

## 581

B"H, 13 Tishrei, the Hillula of the Rebbe Maharash, 5711

To the esteemed Chossid, the man of action, etc., Rabbi Y. [may he live],

Greetings and blessings!

Enclosed is the Kuntres for the upcoming holiday of Sukkos, which includes a Maamar, a Sicha, and a collection of customs. Its purpose is to enable you to share this merit with the many, each in his own environment, in an appropriate manner.

For more than at any other time of the year, we are all called upon to demonstrate love for our fellow and to achieve a state of total unity—this being the essence of the month of Tishrei:

On Rosh Hashanah, the day of the coronation of the King, the King of the world, for "make Me King over you" is fulfilled specifically when the leaders of the people gather together, the tribes of Israel.

On Yom Kippur, when one must first appease his fellow, and we are likened to the angels, among whom there is neither jealousy nor competition.

On the holiday of Sukkos, regarding which our Sages hinted in their sweet language: "All of Israel are fit to sit in one Sukkah."

And on Shemini Atzeres, when the Holy One, blessed be He, says: "Bring one bull, one ram," for "your separation is difficult for Me."

This is emphasized even more on Sukkos through the mitzvah of "And you shall take for yourselves the four species," the meaning of which is explained in many places—including in the teachings of the Baal HaHillula (e.g., Torah Or, 5637, Chapter 87 and onwards)—as to why specifically these four species are chosen, for each of them hints at unity. Furthermore, one must bind them all together as one (see Beis Yosef and Taz, Orach Chaim 651, in the name of the Recanati), even though the Esrog is like those in Israel who possess Torah and mitzvos, the Lulav and Hadassim are like those who possess either Torah or mitzvos, and the Aravah represents those who possess neither Torah nor mitzvos. And it is precisely then, says the Holy One, blessed be He, that I will raise a sign: Esrog, Aravah, Lulav, Hadass (Zohar III, 259a; Tikkunei Zohar, Tikkun 13, and elsewhere)—"like a palm tree" (Shir HaShirim 7:8), this is the Community of Israel, "this stature of yours is like a palm tree."

By way of a clever insight, one might say regarding the aforementioned teaching of our Sages that all of Israel are fit to sit in one Sukkah, that this is the source for the halacha that a borrowed Sukkah is valid—because one does not possess the value of a *perutah* on his own, except through borrowing (Rashi, Sukkah 27b).

For the "one Sukkah"—the *makif* of the essence of the *Atzmus* of the Ein Sof, as explained at the end of the Maamar of the Rebbe Rayatz in the Kuntres—also requires the condition of the Torah, "you shall make for yourself"—from your own, specifically through your *avodah* in keeping the Torah and mitzvos and the *avodah* of *birurim*. One must possess at least a *perutah* in it, for "with a *perutah* one acquires his soul" (Kiddushin 3b) and lives before Him with internal vitality (see the end of the Maamar). And our Sages explained and made known that one does not possess the value of a *perutah* on his own—whoever he may be—except by borrowing from other Bnei Yisrael, for every person is "repaired by his fellow," and all are in need of one another.

With blessings for a happy holiday and success in sharing this merit with the many, that they may all form one group to do the will of our Father in Heaven with a whole heart,

M. Schneerson

## 582

B”H,

It is explained at the end of the maamar in this kuntres that Shemini Atzeres is the gathering of all the lights and general revelations drawn down during the seventh month—the absorption and retention through good sowing, so that there may be growth from it in great abundance.

It is explained even further in the aforementioned place, that “the month of Tishrei is the general head for all the months, and within it are days that serve as roots and sources for the entire year: Rosh Hashanah—the root and source for yirah, as Yisrael receives yirah on that day for the entirety of the year. Yom Kippur—for teshuvah, pardon, and forgiveness. The seven days of Sukkos—for ahavah and simcha for the entirety of the year. But the day of Simchas Torah is a greater principle, encompassing the entire month of Tishrei, for then the level of the supreme general makif is drawn down—the level of the King’s own delights, the Keter of Torah, and this revelation is drawn down on Simchas Torah through the dancing, which is not a matter of the intellects at all.”

And as is written in the maamar in the kuntres, that the simcha relates to the letters of the Torah; in the letters of the Torah, their vowel points, and their cantillation marks—in this study, all of Yisrael are equal. Therefore, the simcha is expressed in dancing, which means that the simcha reaches the very lowest power of the soul and the lowest vessels—the feet.

The saying of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe (Rashab), is well known: that after Simchas Torah begins the order of “And Yaakov went on his way”—the way of Havayah, the way of Torah and mitzvos. My revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, explained the matter of Shemini Atzeres and Simchas Torah: At a fair, one purchases merchandise, and upon coming home—throughout the days of the year—one unpacks it and begins to do with it what needs to be done.

So it is with every single one of Yisrael: in the seventh month, which is satiated with all good, they give them and us “merchandise” with which to sustain ourselves for the entire year. But one must open the sacks, unpack, and do with that merchandise what is necessary.

My revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, cautioned in the name of his father, my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe (Rashab): The forty-eight hours of Shemini Atzeres and Simchas Torah—these days will bring the simcha of mitzvah to all the days of the year, and consequently, all limitations, hindrances, and obstacles to the study of Torah and the fulfillment of mitzvos will be removed. For Simchas Torah must be held very dear; every moment one can draw treasures by the bucketful and by the barrelful, both in gashmius and in ruchnius, and this is through the dancing.

Menachem Schneerson

Erev Sukkos, 5711. Brooklyn, N.Y.

## 583

B.H., Chol Hamoed Sukkos, 5711
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed and distinguished Rabbi Y.Y., may he live and be well,

Greetings and blessings!

Enclosed is the Kuntres for the upcoming Shemini Atzeres and Simchas Torah. I trust you will merit to use it to awaken, strengthen, and illuminate—now and throughout the year—the *simchas Torah* of all those around you. Through this, their *simchas mitzvah* will be awakened, strengthened, and illuminated, and consequently, their Torah study and performance of *mitzvos* will be on a higher level.

For just as Torah is equivalent to and leads to all the *mitzvos*, so too, *simchas Torah* is equivalent to and leads to *simchas mitzvah*. And *avodah* performed with joy and a good heart breaks through all barriers and limitations, both below and above; it distances one from base desires and nullifies *dinim*—and then, "in the light of the King’s countenance is life."

As we approach the conclusion of the *yomim tovim*—Rosh Hashanah, Yom Kippur, the days of Sukkos, Shemini Atzeres, and Simchas Torah—a Jewish person must prepare to enter the *yemei hachol*. Furthermore, these are the *yemei hachol* of the winter months—a period of about half a year without *regalim*. One must therefore take along "provisions for the journey"—powers and *hemshechim* that will grant him the ability so that when he fulfills the command, "And Yaakov went on his way," he will be able to walk his path securely, even though all paths are presumed to be fraught with danger.

This is the purpose of Shemini Atzeres: the gathering and absorption of all the general *hemshechim* of the month of Tishrei. And Simchas Torah is the beginning of the revelation and *hemshech*, which makes it easier to bring into actual practice, throughout all the days of the year, all the good resolutions made during the month of Tishrei.

Especially since Simchas Torah is the highest *makif*, which also includes the general *makifim* of the month of Tishrei.

With this, we can understand why we find two seemingly contradictory aspects regarding Shemini Atzeres and Simchas Torah: 
a) The custom of Israel, which is Torah, is to rejoice in this joy more than in the *Simchas Beis Hasho'evah*, and more than in the joy of a regular *yom tov*. 
b) The joy of *yom tov* is a *mitzvah asei* from the Torah. The additional joy of the days of Sukkos, and the *Simchas Beis Hasho'evah* included in this, is explicitly stated in the verse. The same applies to *simchas mitzvah*. In contrast, the joy of the final day of the *chag* is learned only from a *drashah* (and it is understood that the "additional joy" is not learned from this), and some say it is not from the Torah at all.

The reason for this can be explained as follows: Precisely because this joy is the most sublime and all-encompassing, it is not counted among the specific *mitzvos*—similar to what the Rambam writes regarding general commandments—and some say it is merely a custom, similar to what is explained regarding the *hakafos*.

May the Ribono shel Olam grant us that this joy reaches the very last power of the soul, and that we make a pact and resolution to accept the yoke of Heaven, to set fixed times for Torah, to perform *mitzvos*, and to engage in *avodah shebalev*, and to bring this resolution from potential into action. And then—as my father-in-law, the Rebbe, concludes in his *maamar* in the Kuntres—the light of "that it is good" will be drawn down with an abundance of material and spiritual good.

(Due to the sanctity of the *mo'ed*, I have not signed my name.)

Menachem Schneerson

## 795

B.H., 5 Cheshvan, 5711
Brooklyn

To the esteemed and distinguished Rabbi M.M., may he live:

Peace and blessing!

In response to your letters from Friday, Erev Shabbos Parshas Vayeshev, the 5th of Aseres Yemei Teshuvah, and the 5th of Isru Chag—which, due to the pressures of the month of Tishrei, I did not have the time to answer until now, and even now time is short, so I will write briefly:

I read the *pidyonos* you sent, along with the list of students, at the *tziyun* of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, on Erev Rosh Hashanah, and in his chamber, where one enters for *yechidus* and to submit *pidyonos*, during the days of Rosh Hashanah. Surely the *tzaddik* of the generation, the *Nasi*, my father-in-law the Rebbe, of blessed memory, has bestowed his blessings, and may Hashem fulfill them completely, both materially and spiritually.

I also mentioned at the *tziyun* the three householders from the city of Midelt whom you specifically mentioned, and I am enclosing the letters to them as you suggested. You will surely inform me of what transpires regarding this.

Regarding what you write about the financial strain: there were several secondary reasons for this, but in any case, my hope is that the situation will steadily improve and become more organized.

You have surely received all the *kuntresim*, including the *kuntres* for Shemini Atzeres, along with the letters attached to them.

I am interested to know if there was an opportune time to publicize the content of the *sichos*—at least those in the aforementioned *kuntresim*—in wider circles and in various towns.

Many thanks for sending the book that the Rabbi of Midelt gave you. Please be kind enough to remind me from time to time about other books. Furthermore, if there are other authors there, or those descended from authors of holy books, it would be appropriate to encourage them to send their books as a gift to our library. It is understood that if they wish... we will send them books that we have published. You will surely inform me which types of books it is appropriate to send to whom, specifically.

It is very, very good that you are utilizing every opportunity to explain the concept of Chassidus wherever possible, and I look forward to further news regarding this. Without a doubt, the blessing of my father-in-law the Rebbe, of blessed memory, will accompany you in this work as well, so that it will be met with great success.

I will also write to the Rabbi of Midelt, G-d willing, in these coming days.

Regarding the student Mr. [...], it is worthwhile to draw him close in an appropriate manner. When you have the opportunity, please be kind enough to ask him on my behalf if he received my letter and what has been done with him regarding the organization in general. As requested, I will write in these coming days to his wife, may she live.

You will surely inform me that his visa matter is being arranged, and certainly, through the connections he already has there, you will see to it that everything is handled in the most appropriate manner.

Regarding what you write—that you feel lonely and isolated, etc., and that a great weakness in all your work is falling upon you—the end of your words proves the beginning: this is a tactic of the *yetzer hara*, which strives to weaken everyone in the fulfillment of their *shlichus* using arguments suited to the nature of the *shaliach*. The saying of my father-in-law the Rebbe, of blessed memory, is well known: "Chassidus has accomplished that one is never lonely. Wherever one finds himself, there are Rebbes." This is especially true regarding my father-in-law the Rebbe, of blessed memory, who himself wrote upon the passing of his father, the Rebbe Rashab, that the shepherds of Israel do not abandon their flock, as explained in *Iggeres HaKodesh* (Section 27) and its *biur*. Since the physical limitations have now been removed, they are present with each and every one of those who belong to them and are connected to them, wherever they may be—especially in places to which they were sent to fulfill a *shlichus*, and in the most specific detail, as the *shlichus* is to spread the wellsprings of the Baal Shem Tov outward, which is the preparation and introduction to the coming of Moshiach and the resurrection of the dead, "Awake and sing, you who dwell in the dust," and he is among them. See the *sicha* of 13 Tammuz 5709, printed in the *kuntres* of 12 Tammuz 5710, from which you can draw vitality, inspiration, and strength for your work in your location now. From there, you will see that even through human intellect, it is understood that there is no room for the thought that you are lonely and isolated, G-d forbid, and it goes without saying that there is no basis for weakness in your work. If only *Anash*, and especially the *Temimim*, would be meticulous in the words of my father-in-law the Rebbe, of blessed memory, even in his *sichos*, and especially those from the year 5710 and the year preceding it.

Regarding what you write about the *esrogim*—that they are now taking *esrogim* in your area that grow there, and the Rabbi says they are presumed to be kosher and not grafted, and when he checked them he did not find seeds: if it is certain that there is a *chazakah* (presumption) of kashrus regarding them, then they are kosher for the mitzvah of the Four Species, as the signs mentioned are not *d'oraisa*, and the power of a *chazakah* is great, provided it is **clear** that there is a *chazakah* of kashrus. See the *kuntres* for *Chag HaSukkos*, where it is noted that we have a tradition to seek out specifically the *esrogim* of Calabria, and the Alter Rebbe said regarding this that it is for a reason known to him. Nevertheless, since in many countries they take other *esrogim*, and their usage is based on a *chazakah* from many generations, it is difficult for me to cast doubt upon them—to "throw them into a doubt." It is understood that this does not apply to us, the Chassidim of Chabad, and all those who belong to us, for we have only the custom of the Alter Rebbe, which is to make the blessing over the *esrogim* of Calabria. Regarding the signs, see also the books cited in *Shaar HaKolel*, Chapter 37, where it cites from the *Responsa Chasam Sofer* that *esrogim* coming from Yanova do not require any signs at all.

Seemingly, this implies that even for the sake of stringency, the signs are not that relevant. I am interested to know from where they are obtaining *lulavim* and *aravos* in your country now.

Awaiting good news, and regards to all those who seek your welfare.

Menachem Schneerson

Regarding what you ask about *Birkas Hamazon*: it is brought in *Sefer Likutei Meir* and *Sefer Birchas Yaakov* (from the fundamentals of *Darchei Teshuvah*, Section 9, Paragraph 426) and from *Responsa Teshuras Shai*, Section 571, that if one recited *Al HaMichyah* instead of *Birkas Hamazon*, he has not fulfilled his obligation and must recite *Birkas Hamazon*. I do not have these books at hand, but apparently, the reason is that it does not contain the covenant and the Torah. See *Shulchan Aruch Orach Chaim*, Section 187.

I have now received your letter from Monday, Parshas Noach, and the copy of the letter from Thursday, Parshas Noach. I have already written that the financial matter will be arranged, and we are writing today to Paris regarding a fixed order for this... If only we had enough *shluchim* and enough funds to cover all the work needed in Morocco and its surroundings.

Regarding the *Gemaras* and *kuntresim* you requested, I have passed this on to the office.

Regarding the evening classes for those who visit the Alliance schools during the day, it is not worthwhile to expand on this, as it is a form of validation for those who wish to educate their children in Alliance schools.

In general, our network of schools will be called by the general name **"Ohalei Yosef Yitzchak,"** and this is divided into categories: *Talmud Torah*, *Tiferes Bachurim*, etc.

## 585

B”H, 5 MarCheshvan, 5711
Brooklyn

Greetings and blessings to the illustrious Rabbi, the G-d-fearing man, who sits in judgment, a man of vitality and many accomplishments, who leads his congregation with integrity, who illuminates and shines, whose words are pleasant and whose insights are clear, of holy lineage, etc., our teacher Rabbi Meir Abichatzira, shlita, leader of the holy congregation of Midelt, may it be rebuilt and established.

Peace and blessings!

Due to the many preoccupations of the month of Tishrei, I did not have the time to write to you, and I trust you received my letter from the 25th of Elul. Even now, I will write only briefly, due to the pressure of time.

I will begin by expressing my gratitude for what the illustrious Rabbi, the G-d-fearing man, who engages in communal needs with faith, a man of many accomplishments, etc., our teacher Rabbi Michael Lipsker, shlita, wrote to me—that he has already handed over to you some seforim to send to me. Many thanks for this.

At the beginning of the new season, the 5711 academic year, I will transcribe here a saying of the Alter Rebbe, author of the Tanya and the Shulchan Aruch, who said: Why is a Rabbi called a *mara d’atra* (master of the place)? Because from Above, he has been granted the powers, the privilege, and the duty to be the *mara*—the master of the house—of his entire locale. This applies to spiritual matters as well. Even though every Jewish person possesses free will, and everything is in the hands of Heaven except for the fear of Heaven, nevertheless, since in the innermost part of every Jewish person there is a desire to fulfill the will of Hashem through the study of Torah and the performance of mitzvos, but sometimes their yetzer hara overcomes them, it is within the power of the *mara d’atra*, through appropriate effort and by gently admonishing the members of his congregation, to show them the great goodness and boundless happiness that is intertwined with the study of Torah and the performance of mitzvos. And our Sages have already said that words that come from the heart enter the heart.

In our own situation, too, this is the case. My hope is strong that your honor, shlita, as the *mara d’atra*, will use your great influence to strengthen and expand the Talmud Torah in our camp. It is clear that the members of your congregation will assist you in magnifying Torah and making it glorious. According to the aforementioned saying of the Alter Rebbe, he is the *mara d’atra*, and for your honor, shlita, and those like you, further elaboration on this is unnecessary.

I thank you in advance for the good news I hope to receive regarding everything that is done in this regard. And just as our Sages said that Jerusalem was destroyed only because the children of the schoolhouse were neglected, so too, through the expansion of the study halls for the children of the schoolhouse, we will merit speedily and in our days the coming of Mashiach Tzidkeinu and the true and complete Redemption, amen.

May your peace and your Torah increase with tranquility and peace of mind.

Awaiting good news,

Menachem Schneerson

## 487

B"H, 5 Cheshvan, 5711
Brooklyn

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, and distinguished individual, who engages in communal needs with faithfulness, etc., Moreinu HaRav Binyamin, may he live and be well, of the Abu family.

Peace and blessing!

It was with pleasure that I learned from our representative, the esteemed Rabbi, the G-d-fearing and distinguished individual, who engages in communal needs with faithfulness, a man of many accomplishments, etc., Moreinu HaRav Michael, may he live, Lipsker, of your dedicated work for the education of the children of Yisrael in general, and for the support of the Talmud Torah in the holy community of Midelt in particular.

At his request, I mentioned you at the holy resting place of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, for blessing and success in all that you and your household, may they live, require. Surely, the righteous one on high will intercede for you in the heavens, that you and your household, may they live, be blessed with all that is good, both physically and spiritually, and that you may know no sorrow, harm, or anguish, Heaven forbid, and that only goodness and kindness may follow you all the days of your life.

My father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, explained in several places in his maamarim the teaching of our Sages, "The reward of a mitzvah is the mitzvah itself," meaning that the greatest reward for fulfilling a mitzvah is the very fact that a Yid is granted the ability to fulfill the commandments of the King of Kings, the Holy One, blessed be He. Yet, it is simple and clear that, as a secondary result of this reward, there is also a great reward for mitzvos in both physical and spiritual terms. If this is true for all mitzvos in general, how much more so for mitzvos that are "good for Heaven and good for people," and especially for the mitzvah of Talmud Torah, which is equivalent to them all. And how much more so for Talmud Torah that is connected with the mitzvah of educating the children of Yisrael, which contains all the virtues: Talmud Torah, bringing the children of Yisrael to the World to Come (through the study of Hashem’s Torah) and to this world (through learning good and upright conduct: good character traits, acts of loving-kindness, charity, etc.), the fruits of which a person consumes in this world, while the principal remains for the World to Come.

The magnitude of these fruits is understood from the story of our Sages regarding the reward for the three steps that the wicked Nevuchadnetzar took for the sake of the Place (Hashem), which resulted in the merit of royalty being granted to him and his descendants for three generations. How much more so, then, for the children of Yisrael who exert their souls, bodies, and wealth for the sake of the Place in the education of the children of Yisrael; surely the Holy One, blessed be He, will grant them an abundance of good, both physical and spiritual, to them and their households, may they live.

I am confident that you will continue to gather strength in your holy work of supporting and expanding the Talmud Torah in your city, and that you will be able to share good news regarding your positive activities in this regard, the fruits of these efforts, and also good news regarding your personal affairs.

Blessing you and your entire household, may they live, with all that is good, physically and spiritually,

Menachem Schneerson

## 359

B"H, 5 Mar Cheshvan, 5711
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, and distinguished, etc., R' Mendel Glatt, may he live.

Greetings and blessings!

I was pleased to receive your regards through our friend, the esteemed Rabbi and Chossid, a man of action and many accomplishments, etc., R' Yosef Halevi Weinberg, may he live.

The interpretation of the statement, "All of Israel are *areivim* (sureties) for one another," is well known: the word *areivim* implies: 1) sweetness, 2) mixture, 3) responsibility. This means that because of *ahavas Yisrael*, all of Israel are intermingled with one another and each is responsible for the other. All of this is found even in the physical realm in the insurance business, and all the more so in the spiritual realm.

My revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, emphasized the great responsibility placed upon every person in Israel to give *tzedakah*—spiritual *tzedakah*—with a generous spirit to those who are "poor in knowledge" within their surroundings and communities. This means to provide merit for the many by establishing public study sessions and influencing them to draw closer to Torah and *mitzvos*. All of these are broad vessels for receiving blessings of all good, both physically and spiritually. One should also learn from this regarding the magnitude of the *tzedakah* that every person in Israel is obligated to bestow upon their own *neshamah elokis* by setting fixed times for Torah study—both the revealed Torah and the inner dimension of Torah, which is the study of *Chassidus*.

I hope to hear good news from you regarding your work in this area, and thank you for informing me of it.

With blessings for much success, both physically and spiritually,

**Menachem Schneerson**

## 793

793

B”H, 8 Marcheshvan, 5711
Brooklyn

To the Tamim, the G-d-fearing, the distinguished and esteemed, who engages in communal needs, etc., Moreinu Harav Moshe Dolzin, may he live.

Shalom u’Bracha!

I was pleased to receive regards from you through our friend, the distinguished Rabbi and Chassid, the G-d-fearing, the man of action and many accomplishments, etc., Moreinu Harav Yosef Halevi Weinberg, may he live. I am interested to hear about your communal work, and I am certain that you also have fixed times for Torah in general, and for the teachings of Chabad in particular, to learn, to teach, and to bring merit to your surroundings.

The saying of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe (the Rashab), of blessed memory, is well known: that the Temimim are candles meant to illuminate. And my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, always emphasized to all those of Anash who were destined to wander to distant lands—and especially to the Temimim, may they live—that "the steps of man are established by Hashem." This means that a Jew does not set out on a journey for the sake of material livelihood, but rather because of a spiritual mission that he must carry out in a specific place and a specific country.

The Chassidic interpretation of the verse "Lech Lecha" is well known: that every person of Israel, the children of Avraham Avinu, peace be upon him, must grasp the path of our father Avraham, who would wander from place to place. And in every place he arrived, "he would call out in the name of Hashem"—do not read it as "he would call out" (*vayikra*), but as "he would cause others to call out" (*vayakri*), meaning he would publicize His Divinity, may He be blessed. And although this work is difficult for a traveler, everyone has been given the strength to carry out their task and the mission of their soul.

The beginning of this work is, as mentioned, to be a "candle to illuminate"—that is, to bring the "candle of mitzvah and the light of Torah" into the entire environment. Since, thank G-d, Hashem has graced you with strength, with manifest abilities and talents, and you are also respected in your community, you can surely accomplish much. And my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, said: "It is a certainty that propaganda [outreach] does not return empty."

I hope to hear good news from you regarding your communal work and the fixed times for Torah that you have, and thank you for informing me of this.

With wishes for all the best to you and all those associated with you.

**Menachem Schneerson**

Enclosed is a receipt for your contribution to the Maamad.

I am interested to hear about the welfare of your son, who visited here a few years ago.

[Enclosed] Kuntres of Shabbos Bereishis.

## 494

B"H, 5 MarCheshvan, 5711
Brooklyn

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, and distinguished [man], etc., R' Moshe, may he live,
Brachfeld

Greetings and blessings!

I was pleased to receive regards from you through our friend, the esteemed Rabbi and Chassid, the G-d-fearing and distinguished man of action, etc., R' Yosef, may he live, HaLevi Weinberg, and I am interested to know the details of your avodah in bringing merit to your surroundings.

The explanation in Chassidus regarding the verse "Lech Lecha" is well known: that every person of Yisrael, the children of Avraham Avinu, a"h, must grasp the path of our father Avraham, who would wander from place to place, and in every place he arrived—"he called out in the name of Hashem." Do not read it as "he called out" (vayikra), but rather "he caused others to call out" (vayakri), as the Gemara (Sotah 10a) states—meaning he would publicize His divinity, may He be blessed. And although this avodah is difficult for a traveler, nevertheless, every person has been given the strengths to bring their task and the mission of their soul to fruition.

My revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, the Rebbe, may his merit shield us, emphasized the great responsibility placed upon the students and alumni of the yeshivos, specifically to give spiritual tzedakah with a generous spirit to the "poor in knowledge" who are in their surroundings and communities—to bring merit to the public through public study shiurim and to influence them to bring them closer to Torah and mitzvos. All of these are broad vessels for receiving blessings of all good, both physically and spiritually.

I hope to hear good news from you regarding your avodah in this, and surely you will increase your courage and go from strength to strength, both in your own fixed times for Torah study and in your shiurim for the public. Thank you for informing me of this.

I hereby bless you with much success in your livelihood with abundance, and in your spiritual avodah, and I await good news.

**Menachem Schneerson**

Enclosed is the Kuntres for Shabbos Bereishis.

Your contribution for the Maamad is hereby acknowledged, and the receipt is enclosed.

## 495

B"H, 9 Cheshvan, 5711

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your recent letter: I have asked you several times, and also warned you, not to be in a state of sadness or *marah shechorah*.

I emphasized to you that my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, blessed you many times, and "a *tzaddik* decrees and the *Ribono shel Olam* fulfills," as per the ruling of the *Gemara*.

Heaven forbid to cast even the slightest doubt on this, or to weaken the strength of your *bitachon*. Aside from all the statements of our Sages that explain the reprehensibility of this, it also, Heaven forbid, damages the channels [of blessing]. This is the language of the *Zohar*, *Parshas Tetzaveh* 184b:

"Come and see: the lower world stands ready to receive constantly, and it is called a 'good stone.' The upper world only gives to it in the manner in which it stands. If it stands with a shining countenance from below, then it is made to shine from above. But if it stands in sadness, they give it judgment in return. This is the meaning of (Tehillim 100), 'Serve Hashem with joy,' for the joy of a person draws toward him another, higher joy."

And it is high time that you begin to follow this.

With blessings for all the best and for a speedy recovery in particular,

**Menachem Schneerson**

## 399

15 MarCheshvan, 5711
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the President, the Gabbaim, and the congregants of the Nusach HaAri Synagogue, Montreal, may they live:

Greetings and blessings!

It was with great pleasure that I learned through the esteemed Rabbi Moshe Chaim Sapatshinsky that the Mishnayos shiur which he leads in your distinguished shul is proceeding with success, and that this coming Sunday, G-d willing, you will be making a *siyum* on Seder Moed.

I wish to send my blessing that you should continue with even greater success than until now. Like every living thing, it should constantly grow—both in quantity and in quality. This means that the number of participants should increase, and even more so, the vitality in the learning should increase, as well as the depth of understanding and comprehension.

Our holy Torah, which was given by the Ribono shel Olam, who is *Ein Sof*, is itself *Ein Sof*. It applies with the same strength in all places and at all times, just as it was strong when the Ribono shel Olam gave it to the Jewish people through Moshe Rabbeinu on Har Sinai. It is just as strong in our times of dark *galus* and in all corners of the globe.

The Torah is also *Ein Sof* in that every subject within the Torah has *Ein Sof* interpretations, which are divided into four categories: *Pshat, Remez, Drush, Sod*.

***

Mishnayos Seder Moed (Maseches Chagigah) concludes with the ruling that the Golden Altar and the Copper Altar do not become *tamei* because they are like the earth—this is the view of Rabbi Eliezer. The Chachamim say they do not become *tamei* because they are merely plated.

The simple meaning of this is: the Golden Altar that was in the Beis Hamikdash, as well as the Copper Altar that was in the Beis Hamikdash, did not become *tamei*. Rabbi Eliezer explains that the reason for this is that the Torah equates them to the earth, and the earth does not become *tamei*. The Chachamim say they do not become *tamei* because they were nothing more than covered with gold or copper; therefore, the plating is *batel* to the interior, and the interior does not become *tamei*.

The *remez* and the moral lesson that we can learn from this Mishnah at the end of Seder Moed and apply to our daily lives:

Every person, in their own city and according to their situation, is a *mikdash* where the *Shechinah* rests—"And I will dwell **within them**." In the Beis Hamikdash there were various vessels; likewise, within every Jew there are various faculties: intellect, emotions, etc. In these matters, it can happen that an extraneous thought—a mundane, non-holy thought—interferes. It can even happen that not just a mundane thing interferes, but even an impure thing—something connected to an *aveirah*, Heaven forbid, which is the opposite of the will of the Ribono shel Olam, the opposite of Torah and *mitzvos*.

In other words: the person’s vessel—the intellect, or thought, or another faculty—has become *tamei*, and one must find ways for it to become pure again and once more become a vessel of the *mikdash*. For the Ribono shel Olam’s *mikdash*—every Jew, man and woman—must be *tahor*.

People are divided (physically or spiritually) into rich and poor. Of the rich, it is said that for them everything is "gold," and of the poor—that their coins are "copper."

However, for every Jew without exception, wherever they may be in their internal or external affairs and feelings, the *nekudas hayahadus*—the "point of a Jew"—remains intact. This is the desire to do the will of the Ribono shel Olam, as the Rebbe, my father-in-law, of blessed memory, said: A Jew neither wants to be, nor can be, severed from G-dliness. And this is called an *mizbeach*. *Mizbeach* means slaughtering (*zevicha*) and bringing a *korban* to the Ribono shel Olam.

The Mishnah says that whether it is the Jews who are the "Golden Altar"—the wealthy Jews—or those who are the "Copper Altar"—the poor Jews—when one remembers that one is an *mizbeach*, that the inner, true desire is to slaughter the *yetzer hara* and do the will of the Ribono shel Olam, then they do not become *tamei*. The reason given for this is that they are "like the earth." Just as the earth is trodden upon by all, so too (as we pray, "may my soul be as dust to all"), one has no personal will, only the will that Hashem has revealed to us in the holy Torah.

The words of Rabbi Eliezer (ben Hyrcanus), who is called Rabbi Eliezer the Great, who was equal to all the sages of Israel—despite his greatness, he did not occupy any space for himself, to the point that, as the Gemara says, he never said a thing he had not heard from his teachers. Consequently, he saw in every Jew their inner essence, the *nekudas hayahadus*—"Israel, the Torah, and the Holy One, blessed be He, are all one"—that the entire life of a Jew is to fulfill Torah and *mitzvos*. He taught his students the path that this tremendous intellect is accompanied by **complete** *bitul*, as expressed in the principle: "He never said a thing he had not heard from his teachers."

*Chachamim* say—the other sages held that this path is too strict for everyone; not many can carry out this approach. They therefore took into account the *chitzoniyus*, the external aspect of Jews: it happens sometimes that one becomes *nichshal*, Heaven forbid, and especially the "Golden Altar," who is often preoccupied with "gold" matters until it leads him for a time not to do the will of the Ribono shel Olam. And also among the poor ("Copper Altar"), because their money comes to them with greater difficulty, they too sometimes transgress the will of Hashem. Nevertheless, say the *Chachamim*, the *nekudas hayahadus* (the *mizbeach*) does not become *tamei*, because they are "plated."

For both the gold of the wealthy person and the copper of the poor person are only a covering on the outside, but the inside is pure and cannot become *tamei*. The *pnimiyus* is so strong that, in the end, the plating is *batel* to the *pnimiyus*. And they will eventually surely do *teshuvah* and arrive at the truth: that the life and existence of a Jew is nothing but G-dliness, which is attained only through *limud haTorah* and the fulfillment of *mitzvos*.

And these are also the vessels for the material blessings that the Ribono shel Olam promised in the Torah: "If you walk in My statutes and keep My commandments... the land will yield its produce and the tree of the field will yield its fruit."

With blessings for success and all the best to all the students of the shiur.

**Menachem Schneerson**

P.S.

The above matter, in greater depth and very briefly: See *Sefer HaMitzvos* of the Tzemach Tzedek, *Mitzvas Binyan Mikdash*, Chapter 5. There were four main vessels in the *mikdash*: the Menorah, the Shulchan, the Inner Altar, and the Outer Altar, corresponding to *Chessed, Gevurah, Tiferes, Malchus*. With this, the beginning of the aforementioned Mishnah is understood: the Menorah and Shulchan are subject to *tumah*, whereas the Inner Altar and the Outer Altar, which are on the middle line (see also *Likutei Torah* Bamidbar 60a, 51a), ascend to the *pnimiyus* of *Keter*. The Ark (which was hidden, for no control, Heaven forbid, applies to it) is in the Holy of Holies, where the Tablets are placed. Regarding all this, a reason is needed, since these are *middos* on the middle line. The reason is that they are "like the earth," like the *ayin* and *efes* of *Keter* (*Hosafos to Torah Or*, beginning of *Megillas Esther*).

In all this, it is explicitly written in Scripture that it is like the earth—only regarding the Outer Altar, as it is written: "An altar of earth you shall make for Me," for their end is rooted in their beginning and their beginning in their end. And to the extent that even in *Shemoneh Esrei*—the earth is (only) *misbatel*. And regarding the two altars themselves—the Inner Altar, the *Tiferes* of *Ze'er Anpin*, is "rich" compared to the Outer Altar, the *Malchus* that has nothing of its own.

The reason they do not require *tevilah* (immersion)—the letters of *bitul*—is because they themselves are *bitul*, similar to the earth, or because their plating is *batel* to the *pnimiyus*.

And Rabbi Eliezer, who hints at the *Atzmus* and *Mahus* of the *Ein Sof*, who is called by the name "G-d of my father is my help" (Bamidbar 19:7), and is called "the Great"—in the place of His greatness, etc.—saw even in the *chitzoniyus* the *pnimiyus*, and there is no need for the plating to be *batel* to the *pnimiyus*, because the plating itself, from its own perspective, is *batel*; there is nothing else.

This is not the case for the *Chachamim*, and the *halachah* follows them, for "it is not in heaven," but rather the conduct of the *Seder Hishtalshelus*. The plating, from its own perspective, can receive *tumah*, but through the fact that it becomes a plating for the *pnimiyus*, it is *batel*. This is enough for the wise, and a word to the wise is sufficient.

However, one must have a *keli* through which the *ratzon elyon* can be channeled, and the *keli* for this is to recite several chapters of Tehillim each day, to give *tzedakah* according to your ability, and to participate in a *shiur* that is taught in a shul.
