## 802

B"H, 15 Marcheshvan, 5711

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of 11 Marcheshvan regarding whether to participate in the Melaveh Malkah of the Bureau of Jewish Education, which will feature a lecture on the teachings of the Baal Shem Tov: It seems from your letter that: a) you are not obligated to attend, as there will be no harm to the Talmud Torah even if you do not participate; and b) you are concerned about the undesirable impression your participation in their Melaveh Malkah might create. Since you do not foresee any great benefit from a single lecture, why involve yourself in a questionable matter? In such cases, "sit and do nothing" is preferable.

Regarding what you wrote about the young men and women in your shul who want to organize and improve the shul, including establishing a club affiliated with the shul and the like: In my opinion, this is correct and good. As for your concern that this might lead to mixed dancing or similar things, you will surely find appropriate ways to prevent this and the like, without any controversy, by engaging them in proper and good activities: lectures (with their participation, meaning that they themselves will also be speakers), debates on questions pertaining to Torah and mitzvos or Jewish history, establishing a library and reading room, founding a gemach or charity fund, an exhibition of items related to Chanukah prior to Chanukah, and so on.

I was very pleased to hear your report about the Shemini Atzeres gathering at your Talmud Torah. This is further proof of the saying of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, that propaganda [outreach] never returns empty. The same applies to your shul, and especially to the young men and women; with appropriate avodah, you will rise and succeed in these matters, and this itself will draw down success in your personal affairs as well.

With blessings for success in your personal and communal matters,

**Menachem Schneerson**

## 803

B"H, 21 MarCheshvan, 5711
Brooklyn

To the esteemed Rav, G-d-fearing, and distinguished scholar, etc., Moreinu HaRav Yechezkel Yehuda, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

I received your letter dated Monday of Parshas Zos Os HaBris. Due to the pressures of the month of Tishrei—which is the general month [for all the year]—my response has been delayed.

It was a pleasure to hear that you are beginning to involve yourself in the matter of Taharas HaMishpacha, which, unfortunately, is so neglected and abandoned. The sorrow is even greater because, due to a misplaced sense of shame, there are even G-d-fearing and complete individuals who are embarrassed to speak about it.

How true are the words of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, in his sichos: that the Yetzer Hara is called "der kluginker" (the clever one) because he dresses himself in garments appropriate for each individual to lead them astray. As he said in the name of his father, the Rebbe (Rashab), of blessed memory: the Yetzer Hara is called the nefesh habehamis not because it is necessarily a beast—for sometimes it is the cleverest of animals, a fox, and one requires great wisdom to understand its stratagems—but rather because it sometimes dresses itself in the guise of a righteous, pious, and humble person with good character traits.

In every individual, their nefesh habehamis is according to their own specific essence, etc.

We see this clearly in the case at hand. For the trait of bashfulness is one of the three traits of the Jewish people—they are merciful, bashful, and perform acts of kindness—yet the Yetzer Hara uses this very trait to prevent necessary speech that concerns the happiness of a husband and wife and their children after them until the end of all generations.

Regarding your request for booklets on the subject of Taharas HaMishpacha in English, I have instructed the office to send them to you via regular mail in a separate package.

With blessing and in anticipation of hearing good news regarding the above,

**Menachem Schneerson**

## 404

22 Marcheshvan, 5711

To the esteemed Rabbi and Chassid, the distinguished scholar, etc.,
Rabbi [Name]... may he live,

Peace and blessing!

In response to your letter of 14 Marcheshvan—I am somewhat surprised, for when your daughter, Mrs. [Name]..., was here, she spoke with me at length about the entire matter. She promised me that she would write to you and to her mother regarding the subject of our conversation, as the content of your letter does not quite align with what we discussed.

The matter is as follows:

(1) It is generally not my way to issue commands, except in exceptional cases. Only when people ask for my advice do I express my opinion as it appears to me. This was the case here as well, for back in the middle of the summer, the distinguished *tamin* and *avreich*, the esteemed [Name]..., spoke with me. At that time, I clarified my **perspective** to him regarding how his life should be arranged so that it would be suitable both materially and spiritually. That is the proposal—not a command—that I have now offered to him and to your daughter.

(2) The content of my proposal is not about settling in Brooklyn, New York, or the United States, but rather in a place where he can utilize his own talents, and where your daughter can also utilize her talents to their fullest. There are currently two or three such places that I hope are suitable for achieving this goal.

(3) When I spoke with the aforementioned *avreich* and with your daughter, I immediately emphasized to them that even if there were to be difficulties, or even a sense of self-sacrifice—as you write in your letter—from whom should we expect such things if not from a *tamin* son of *taminim* and a *temimah* daughter of *taminim*?

(4) However, success has smiled upon the aforementioned *avreich* and your daughter, in that this proposal, in my opinion, is as good for them materially as it is spiritually. My reason for this is that regarding the future they might hope for if they were to settle in the United States or in [Place]—experience has already shown what the most successful situation is that *avreichim* of their caliber can expect after settling in those places. I do not wish to elaborate on this, for as you are on the scene, you surely know the "outcome" of what has become of the young men in our camp, and during the weeks they were in Brooklyn, you surely observed what has become of those young men—who are of the same caliber as the aforementioned *avreich* and your daughter—who settled in Brooklyn and New York. On the other hand, if my proposal is brought from potential into action, and they travel to one of the aforementioned places, it is to be hoped that the blessing of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, will accompany them on their path in life, and within a short time they will be able to settle properly—he as a leader of a community in Israel. I specify "leader," not "rabbi," because, in my view, they could arrange it so that under his leadership there would be a rabbi, a teacher, a *shochet*, and various institutions, etc. Furthermore, with the proper energy, your daughter could also occupy a similar position in life.

(5) In addition to all the above, and this is the main point: it was the intense desire of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, to establish centers of settlement for *Anash* in all corners of the globe. This was his intention in sending several of *Anash* to Australia, and several to Canada, and in his speaking several times about South America and South Africa. We have seen, and you surely have seen, that whoever accepted the Rebbe’s *shlichus* was saved from every trouble and distress and placed in a position of light, both materially and spiritually, even when it required success that was specifically above the natural order. In the present case, even according to the natural order, there is room here for a good settlement; if so, the blessings of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, will add to this many times over.

(6) The aforementioned *avreich* agreed to all of this back in the middle of the past summer, but at that time it was not yet a practical matter, as I did not want to suggest that he travel before the *shidduch* with your daughter was finalized. Thus, the current situation is that you, your wife, and your daughter do not see it this way and do not want the proposal that the *avreich* has already accepted—to be one of the representatives of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, who even now is a leader of Israel in general, and of his community of Chassidim in particular.

(7) Proof of the above is the story you bring at the end of your letter (which is a contradiction in terms). You write that when my father-in-law, the Rebbe, told him that there was no need to be particular about the *shidduch* for his daughter being specifically with a *tamin*, he said to the Rebbe that "when we (surely referring to himself and his wife) remember that we will have to marry our daughter to someone who is not a *tamin*, our lives are truly not lives." Consider this: the blessing of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, succeeded in that his daughter was indeed engaged to a *tamin* *avreich*. And now, they are trying to ensure that this *tamin* breaks away from the work of my father-in-law, the Rebbe—from being his *shaliach* to carry out his holy desires—and they are content with the merits he had until now.

(8) After asking your forgiveness—and surely you will not take offense at what follows—you are surely familiar with the saying of my father-in-law, the Rebbe (the Rashab), that the *taminim* are candles to illuminate. It is also known how grave the words of our Sages are regarding "according to the camel is the load," and if one does a little, but not according to one's strength, that too is considered a deficiency, etc. Both the parents of the groom and the parents of the bride are all *taminim*, and consequently, the aforementioned saying of the Rebbe applies to them as well: that they must continue to illuminate even now. I do not know if they have fulfilled this role of theirs completely, but in any case, the definition of the title "to illuminate" also includes their offspring—meaning that the *taminim* must also illuminate through their children. Now, consider the method of illumination that will be achieved when your daughter and the *avreich* settle in [Place], versus when they settle in one of the aforementioned places.

(9) Once again, I repeat that this is not a command, but a response to your request for my advice on how to arrange their lives. I cannot answer otherwise than as it appears to me. I would like to add that this does not seem to me to be a matter of doubt; rather, as one can hope from the outset, the greatness of the happiness they would attain if they accepted the aforementioned proposal is clear to me—material happiness included.

(10) Regarding your concluding remark about the current situation with you and your daughter, that it is a "disturbed joy" (*farshtarte simcha*), I was alarmed to read such words. For what is this about? That one should travel to a city of tens of thousands of Jews, may they live, and be able to observe Torah and *mitzvos* in the most elevated manner, traveling with a *shlichus* from my father-in-law, the Rebbe, to carry out his desires—and since "a person's agent is like himself," he goes with the Rebbe's strength—to arrive there with a position and with expansion, and to disseminate there the light of Torah and Judaism, the wellsprings of the Baal Shem Tov, and the teachings of the living G-d among our brethren, the Children of Israel, who currently know nothing of this, or know only a little? And for a reason unknown to me, to you, and to people of our caliber—and see *Iggeres HaKodesh*, end of section 27—they chose for this purpose so-and-so and such-and-such, who did not labor or toil for this. Not only that, but they take it upon themselves—and even so, they are pampered, indulged, and given "candies." And this you call a "disturbed joy"! I am astonished!

You conclude your letter by asking for my forgiveness. I do not know for what I need to ask for forgiveness, as this is no more a private matter of mine than it is of yours. Surely, in the inner sense, each and every one of us wants to fulfill the desire of my father-in-law, the Rebbe. Surely you and your wife also know—if not for the fact that the issue regarding your daughter is confusing you—that through work of this nature in [Place], one fulfills the desires of my father-in-law, the Rebbe. Who am I that you should need to ask for my forgiveness in this?

In any case, since it is impossible to delay the work of disseminating the wellsprings in [Place] for long, I strongly request that you inform me of the decision as soon as possible, preferably by telegram. As stated, I am not giving any command, G-d forbid, and this is only a proposal; but since this matter has come to my attention, I am looking for suitable people for it, and then I will turn to the right, etc.

With blessing and regards to your wife,

## 415

B"H, 26 MarCheshvan, 5711
Brooklyn

Greetings and blessings!

In addition to the telegram, I hereby repeat my blessing of Mazal Tov on the birth of your daughter, may she live and be well. May you merit to raise her to Torah, to the chuppah, and to good deeds, in comfortable circumstances.

I was pleased to hear that you named your daughter on Thursday. Regarding this, my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, once told me that when one of the daughters of the Mitteler Rebbe was born, the Alter Rebbe called him and said that although there is a reason to suggest waiting to name the child until the Torah reading on Shabbos, nevertheless, for known reasons, one should not do so, and one should name the daughter on the day of the Torah reading closest to the day of birth.

The fact that my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, shared this matter with me regarding an individual here is proof that this is a general instruction for everyone.*

As you requested, your daughter’s name has been recorded in the Sefer HaChaim VeHaOhr.

Awaiting good news, especially regarding the proper health of your wife, may she live and be well, your newborn daughter, may she have good fortune, and your son, may he live and be well.

Blessings to you and your household,

**Menachem Schneerson**

Enclosed is the receipt, as well as the *Reshimos* from Shabbos Bereishis. I am certain you will read sections 21 and 22 therein with attention and publicize them in an appropriate manner.

In any case, we have only the instructions of our Nasi.

## 440

B"H, 26 Marcheshvan, 5711

Greetings and blessings!

I have received your letter from Sunday, Parshas Vayeira, in which you write that your granddaughter, the girl... may she live, does not feel comfortable in her Yiddish class and cries often, and you believe that this is due to the influence of her Yiddish studies.

I have inquired as to what kind of studies and textbooks are used there, and according to the information I have received, I do not believe the root cause is as you think. Rather, it is likely that the reason is that she does not have a suitable friend or the like.

Therefore, you should make an effort to ensure that the teacher of the class finds suitable friends for her. Your granddaughter will likely feel better, and you will see that there are absolutely no reasons to be concerned about this.

You should know that the fact that your granddaughter is learning in an institution that was founded by my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, and stood under his leadership—and still stands under that same leadership today—is not a matter that can cause distress, Heaven forbid. On the contrary, it brings health in both material and spiritual matters, and through the children who learn in these institutions, Yiddish and Chassidic warmth and light are brought into the homes of their parents.

I hope to hear good news from you that your granddaughter, may she live, is feeling better and is making good progress in her Yiddish studies.

With blessings and the hope to hear good news,

**Menachem Schneerson**

Enclosed is the Reshimos from Shabbos Parshas Bereishis, and surely you will read it with the proper attention, especially sections 21 and 22.

## 808

B"H, 27 MarCheshvan, 5711, Brooklyn

Greetings and blessings!

I was pleased to receive regards from you through our dear friends, the esteemed Rabbis, who engage in communal needs with faith, etc., Rabbi Sh. Levitin and Rabbi A. Simpson. They related how in your home, the chinuch you received from your father, a"h—who was one of the old Lubavitcher Chassidim—is clearly evident.

This good news confirms what one sees constantly in life: how correct is the statement of Chazal, "Throw a stick into the air, and it falls back upon its root"—when one throws a stick into the air, it falls back to its root.

The deeper meaning of this is: A tree spreads out, and both the trunk (the tree itself) and the branches grow further and further away from the root. Especially when, due to various reasons, it **seems** as though a branch has been cut off, ch"v, and has become a dry stick on its own, one might think that it no longer has any connection to its root. But in truth, a Yid never truly departs from his root; the proof is that even the dry stick falls back to the root. One only needs the appropriate person to remind one of the root using appropriate words.

It gladdened me that in your family, there is no need for such a reminder from the outside, for within you burns the light and warmth of Chassidim that you inherited from your parents. I hope that this light and warmth will continue to strengthen and find their true expression in matters of Torah and mitzvos.

There is a saying from my father-in-law, the Rebbe, that the Ribono shel Olam does not remain a debtor. Therefore, I bless you that in the merit of your participation in various tzedakah, and especially those connected with the mosdos of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, may Hashem gladden your hearts, particularly [with children who are alive and enduring], and may He fulfill your heart's desires for the good, both materially and spiritually.

I would suggest that your wife, Mrs. ... tichyeh, should place tzedakah into the pushke of R' Meir Baal HaNes every Erev Shabbos and Yom Tov before lighting candles, and that you yourself, at the time of putting on tefillin, should remind yourself that you are connected to my father-in-law, the Rebbe. This will serve as the channel through which the blessing [for children who are alive and enduring] will be fulfilled.

With blessings,

**Menachem Schneerson**

## 809

By the Grace of Hashem
28 Cheshvan, 5711
Brooklyn

Greetings and Blessings!

Enclosed is a copy of my letter to Mr. David, may he live, Bobis. It would be appropriate for you to find an opportunity to speak with him regarding his visit here, to strengthen him in actually fulfilling everything that was discussed here, and in general, to encourage him to exert influence upon his surroundings.

I hope to hear good news regarding his success in this.

Following up on the two letters I wrote to him even before the Yom Tov, and because of the preoccupations of the month of Tishrei—which is the general month—I was unable to continue the matter. And although I have not yet received a response to the two aforementioned letters, I am hereby continuing our conversation (regarding the college), and in continuation of the above:

Seemingly, it is within his power to say: Since it appears to me (contrary to what the Rambam wrote in Hilchos Geirushin, end of Chapter 2) that I desire to visit and study at college, but there is someone who says that this is not appropriate for my standing and situation in general, for it does not befit the image of a *tamim* and the image of a student of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory—who then accompanies him in all his ways, and if so, by my going to college, he is, so to speak, compelled to go with me there, according to the ruling of our Sages, "A student who is exiled, his teacher is exiled with him" (Makkos 10a)—who says that I am compelled in all of this? And for a time, I will, Heaven forbid, suspend the image of a *tamim*, and likewise, I will, Heaven forbid, suspend for a time the image of a Chossid of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, and consequently, the arguments will fall away.

But this is no longer in his power. And according to what is known even in the revealed Torah, that a convert who has converted can no longer return, Heaven forbid, and even if he sins afterward, he is still a Jew since he has converted once. In this same way, it is within *kedushah* itself: for one who has become a Chossid once, and one who has connected himself to the Rebbe—which was, in any case, "as face reflects face in water," and the Rebbe connected himself with him—he no longer has the ability to cease, Heaven forbid, the *hiskashrus*. Since this depends also upon the Rebbe, and he, in his abundant goodness and kindness, is bound with him in shackles—similar to what is written in *Iggeres HaTeshuvah*, Chapter 2, "The King is bound in the tresses (rehatim)—in the tresses of the mind, etc.," and therefore Hashem is called a "humble King," see there. And in this manner, it is with the *tzaddikim*, and especially with the *Nesi'ei HaDor*, and in the most minute particulars, the *Nesi'im* of the *Toras HaNistar*, as is known in the *Zohar* (Vol. II, 34a) that "the face of the Master, Hashem—this is Rabbi Shimon bar Yochai."

[Regarding] what is explained there in the commentary *Nitzutzei Oros* in the name of the Ya'avetz, that this is learned from the word "es" to include a *talmid chacham*, in *Divrei Elokus Chassidim* (*Sha'u Marom* 5688, *Lo Avo* 5699, and elsewhere) it is explained to the contrary, that this refers to Hashem. And it has already been brought in the commentaries of the *Zohar* as an example for the aforementioned statement from *Bava Basra* (75b), the *Yerushalmi Bikkurim* (Chapter 3, Halacha 3), *Midrash Shmuel* Chapter 7, *Zohar* Vol. II 124b, 163b, *Zohar* Vol. III 79b, and *Rabbeinu Bachya* on *Parshas Tisa* on the verse "And it shall be that everyone who seeks Hashem." See also *Ohr HaTorah* by the Tzemach Tzedek, *Parshas Shemos*, page 39 and onwards.

I do not wish to elaborate on this, for I am certain that in the end, "throw a stick into the air, it falls on its root," and the essence and the root will be revealed within him—which is the *hiskashrus* to my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, by our walking "in the straight path which he taught us, and we shall walk in his ways." And may he bring me good news regarding this. It is understood that promptness in this is praiseworthy, as is known that "days are formed," that a number of days is allotted to a person to clarify his portion in the world. And if so, it is a pity for every day, hour, and moment that one does not fill them appropriately for the fulfillment of his soul's mission in this world.

In the hope of hearing good news, and regards to his wife, may she live,

**Menachem Schneerson**

## 410

B"H, 28 Cheshvan, 5711, Brooklyn

Mrs. Chana, may she live,

Blessings and peace!

I was pleased to receive your letter from Motzaei Shabbos Parshas Lech Lecha, along with the enclosed photos of your two children, may they live. May you and your husband be privileged to raise them to Torah, to the chuppah, and to good deeds.

I derived particular pleasure from your writing that you have been chosen as president of the organization for Taharas HaMishpacha, and that the work is continuing to grow.

The Rebbe, my father-in-law, of blessed memory, once said that a good melamed is one who teaches a student in such a way that, in the end, he is able to learn on his own and does not need to rely on the melamed. The same is true in communal work: a good communal worker is one whose work instills such vitality that the members of the organization themselves have the desire to work, and do not need to rely every time on an awakening from the president of the organization or other officers...

**Menachem Schneerson**

## 1411

1411

B”H, 28 Marcheshvan, 5711, Brooklyn

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, learned, and distinguished, the Temim, Rabbi Yitzchak Aharon, Shochet u’Bodek, may he live and be well.

Greetings and blessings!

It was with pleasure that I read your letter (which lacked a date of writing) informing me that the campaign regarding the Talmud Torah has begun, as well as the matter of the teachers going to the students to study with them in their homes.

Your previous letter, received before Rosh Hashanah, was also received, in which you briefly outlined the course of your life. In connection with this, I am writing with a double and redoubled request: since you mention that you were among those who served my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, in Rostov in the year 5681, please record **everything** you remember from that time. I would be very grateful if you would fulfill this request of mine; the more detailed your notes are, the better. I hope these matters are preserved in your memory and that you will fulfill my request completely.

I would like to address a few points from the matters in your letter:

(a) At the end of your life summary—may you live long and good years—you conclude, “All the days of my years have been evil.” This comes after you mention that you studied for six years in the Tomchei Temimim Yeshiva, merited to serve my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, in his private matters (though the private matters of a *neshamah kelalit* are themselves general in nature), and merited to fulfill the wishes of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, through work in communal affairs. Following this, for six years you were imprisoned, and even there, my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, influenced others through you in the dissemination of Torah and Yiddishkeit and in the actual performance of mitzvos, and so on. If, after all this, you write that all the days of your years were evil, I do not understand what constitutes "good" in this world.

(b) I was very pleased to read in your letter before the holiday about your work in Paris, in the city of Metz, and their surroundings, regarding kosher education, the strengthening of Yiddishkeit, and the dissemination of the study of Chassidus—both in quality and in quantity, in the number of students and the homes you visit from time to time.

Therefore, it was with a heavy heart that I read in the letter received today that you have opened one cheder and are teaching eight students there, etc. However, my hope is strong that this is only for a **very brief** moment, and that you will immediately gather strength so that the number of students and homes will reach what it was at the end of last summer. Naturally, you should not be satisfied with that, but should increase the number even further. It would bring me joy if you would inform me of good news in this regard; the more one increases and the sooner one acts, the more praiseworthy it is.

...Enclosed is a short letter for those engaged in this holy work under your leadership. If the content of the letter is appropriate for the situation, please deliver it to them and inform me of this.

With blessings for proper health and success in your holy work, that it may be *tofeach al menat lehatfiach* (overflowing and causing others to overflow),

**Menachem Schneerson**

## 412

B"H, 28 Marcheshvan, 5711, Brooklyn

To the esteemed Chassidim, men of accomplishment, who engage in the dissemination of Torah and Yiddishkeit, and—last but certainly not least—who are connected to our Nasi, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, the Nasi of our generation, by fulfilling his mission in the field of proper chinuch, may they live.

Greetings and blessings!

I read with pleasure the letter from our friend, the esteemed Chassid, man of many accomplishments, R' Yitzchak Aharon, may he live, regarding the order of their avodah in the chinuch of the children of Israel, and their influence even within their parents' homes, by illuminating them with the light of Torah and mitzvos as explained in the teachings of our Nasi—the teachings of Chassidus.

It is understandable that it may seem to them that they do not succeed in every single action in awakening the recipient to a tangible result. But this is not the case. As is known from a sicha of the Rebbe, of blessed memory, while he was still in Russia, he explained how significant a single movement of a Yid is. He brought proof from our Sages regarding the greatness of baalei teshuvah, that even complete tzaddikim cannot stand in their place. He raised the difficulty: since the tzaddik has served Hashem his entire life through Torah and mitzvos, while the baal teshuvah—including one who did teshuvah a moment before his death, as in the story of R' Eliezer ben Durdia—did not, how is it possible that the baal teshuvah is greater than the complete tzaddik? The answer is that from this we see how precious a single movement of a Yid is, to the point that it is possible that in one moment—with one "turn"—he acquires his world.

And in avodah, it is the same. Even if sometimes a tangible effect is not apparent in their students or in their parents' homes, despite their proper efforts, nevertheless, we do not know what has been accomplished in the heart of the other. It is possible that they have brought about a "turn," and with that one turn, the other person can acquire his world.

It is understood that this does not diminish the intensity of the interest in fulfilling their work properly. For this, it is necessary that it be in accordance with the words of our Sages, "Words that come from the heart," which means, in the literal sense as well, heartfelt words. What is relevant is the observance of time—both regarding the students, which teaches them and habituates them in maintaining order, and regarding visits to homes, where punctuality and order help ensure that the words are heard and accepted more readily.

I do not intend this as a reprimand, and it is possible that these matters are in order even without my letter, but I find it my duty to express what I see in this, and my hope is that my words will be of benefit.

It is surely known to you, and it is unnecessary to elaborate, how much the Rebbe, of blessed memory, sacrificed himself for proper chinuch and the strengthening of Yiddishkeit, even in the most "simple" matters, even though it was within his power to use those times for the study of the secrets of Torah and the secrets of secrets. This is a lesson for each one of us. For it is possible that due to the counsel of the yetzer hara—which can disguise itself, putting on the cloak of a pious tzaddik—it can argue with a person: "Why occupy yourself with teaching the aleph-beis to others and saying 'Modeh Ani,' especially when the result of your action is in doubt? Instead, you could be occupying yourself with the study of Chassidus, the teachings of the living G-d, and in this, you are certain that there will be benefit, since you are a Chassid and connected to the Rebbe, and thus the study will surely affect you."

But the Rebbe, of blessed memory, taught through his own conduct that he did not spare his time or his strength to consider what he could accomplish personally, even in the most lofty matters, and he dedicated his best efforts to the dissemination of proper chinuch, starting from the aleph-beis and the like, even among simple people in Israel—which was a matter of mesiras nefesh. To note from the sicha of 20 Kislev 5693, end of section 17, which states: The Rebbe the Tzemach Tzedek said that all the mesiras nefesh of the Zayde—our great Rebbe—are as nothing compared to the mesiras nefesh of tearing oneself away from the state of "I do not desire your people," and dedicating oneself to doing a favor, wanting a Yid to do teshuvah through his own strength and to be a true servant of G-d. It appears that this is also what is demanded of us, and for this, too, we have been given the ability and the strength; nothing is lacking but the will alone.

I sign with a blessing for success in being truly connected to the Rebbe, of blessed memory, through which, naturally, each one will fulfill the mission he has placed upon him with pleasure and willingness, and the wellsprings will spread outward, and "they shall awaken and sing," and the Rebbe, of blessed memory, will lead us upright to our land, speedily in our days, amen.

## 815

The words of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, in his letter regarding the obligation of **all Bnei Yisrael** to study the teachings of Chassidus, require no further explanation. The connection between the inspiration to study Chassidus and the day of 19 Kislev is also understood, for this day is the Rosh Hashanah of Chassidus, and it is "propitious for strengthening and encouraging oneself in the study of the revealed Torah and Chassidus, for dedicating oneself to the avodah of tefillah, and for awakening the refinement and purification of character traits according to Chassidus, and for the love of fellow Jews without limit".

The connection between the dissemination of the study of Chassidus among all circles of our brethren, the Bnei Yisrael, may they live, and the day of 19 Kislev is understood even more clearly based on the words of the Rebbe (Rashab), of blessed memory, that "the essential matter of **'your springs will spread outward'** began after Petersburg. Before that, the approach of Chassidus was that not every Yid could grasp Elokus. For that, one needed a higher neshamah, or, for one who did not have a high neshamah, it was through having rectified all matters that required rectification and having purified oneself.

Chassidus accomplished that **every Yid** should be able to understand an Elokus concept and internalize it. This began in earnest specifically after Petersburg, because after Petersburg he (the Alter Rebbe) was elevated to a higher madregah".

***

Regarding the question of the Baal Shem Tov, "When will you come?", Mashiach was precise in his reply by quoting the verse (Mishlei 5:16): "When **'your springs'** spread outward." It is known that there is nothing higher than spring waters; wherever they flow, even to a distant place, they retain the status of a "spring," provided that their connection—their hiskashrus—to their source is not severed. For spring waters that have been cut off no longer have the status of a "spring".

All these matters demand of each and every one of us: a) **to spread**, b) **the springs**, c) **outward**. And this is impossible except through an unceasing connection with the source—a connection that grows ever stronger with the Nasi, who is my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, the source of the dissemination of these springs to all corners of the globe.

May our eyes behold the fulfillment of the promise of our righteous Mashiach, that then "all the kelipos will cease to exist, and it will be a time of favor and salvation," and may he redeem us with the true and complete Geulah.

**Menachem Schneerson**

Rosh Chodesh Kislev, 5711
Brooklyn, N.Y.

**Menachem Schneerson**

## 417

B"H, 7 Kislev, 5711, Brooklyn

To the esteemed *avreich*, G-d-fearing, etc., [Name]... may he live.
To the esteemed young lady... may she live.

Peace and blessing!

The esteemed *Chossid*, G-d-fearing, etc., who engages in communal needs with faithfulness, etc., has conveyed to me your letter to him regarding your request for my *haskamah* and blessing for your *shidduch*, and also regarding what you wrote to him concerning how to establish your future life, *im yirtzeh Hashem*.

Among people in general, and among *Yidden* in particular, when a *shidduch* is made, it is a matter for which one prays to the *Ribono shel Olam* that it should be successful. And if one prays from the depths of the heart, *Hashem* will grant success so that it should be a *binyan adei ad*—a firm and eternal structure.

Every word in an expression used by our Sages *z"l* is precise. The expression "*binyan*" (structure) is likewise accurate in all its details.

When one builds a structure, one of the primary conditions for it to be strong is to ensure that the foundation upon which the building stands is strong.

The main difference between the foundation and the entire building is that regarding the building as a whole, one pays attention not only to the internal properties but also to the external appearance. However, regarding the foundation, external appearance is irrelevant.

The main thing is that the foundation should be strong and firm and built from the best materials.

So too, in a *shidduch* between Jewish children, it is relevant that the materials of the foundation should be suited to the requirements of a Jewish home, and that it should be strong enough to withstand various *nisyonos*.

The materials of the building among *Yidden* in general are *Torah* and *mitzvos*. Furthermore, in *Chassidishe* homes, it is the internal warmth and light that *Toras HaChassidus* has brought into *Torah* and *mitzvos*, and which has been disseminated through the *Nesi'ei Chabad* in every generation, and in our generation in particular, through our *Nasi*, *k"k mo"ch Admur* *haKadosh*.

In *po'el mamash*, this means taking upon yourselves the study of *Torah* and the performance of *mitzvos ma'asiyos* in daily life, and especially in the matter of *midos tovos* and *midos chassidiyos*, the primary trait of which is *ahavas Yisrael*, as is explained in many places in the *sichos* of *k"k mo"ch Admur* *haKadosh*. This means: *kashrus*, *shemiras Shabbos*, *taharas hamishpachah*, *kevi'us itim laTorah*, *tzedakah*, *ahavas achim*, etc.

—And to fulfill all these matters as *Chassidus* demands of us all.

If you will take these things upon yourselves, I send you my blessing that the *shidduch* [should take place] at a *shaah tovah u'mutzlachas*, and that you should build a *bayis b'Yisrael* upon the foundations of *Torah* and *mitzvos* as explained in *Toras HaChassidus*.

With blessing.

## 418

B"H, 8 Kislev, 5711, Brooklyn

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, etc., R' Shlomo, may he live:

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of Rosh Chodesh Kislev, I hasten to reply and inform you that, in my opinion, you should stand firm in your resolve. You are one of those who have merited to participate in one of the branches of the avodah of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory—especially a branch that serves to disseminate the wellsprings outward (*hafatzas hamaayanos chutza*) in the fullest sense of the term. The meaning is literal: to bring the wellsprings to the land of Africa and disseminate them there, even among circles that **for the time being** must still be called "outward." It will be one of your tasks to bring them in and establish them in the radiant light of the light of Torah, together with the "light" within it, which is the inwardness of Torah—namely, the teachings of Chassidus.

As for the fact that there may still be some obstacles and delays, this is merely further proof of the greatness and preciousness of the matter. As is known in the teachings of Chassidus regarding the explanation of the concept of "preciousness" (*yoker*), which has two meanings: *shver* (difficult) and *teyer* (dear/precious).

A telegram was sent today to Casablanca regarding the papers for you and your wife, may she live. In any event, my hope is that in this month—the month of Redemption—this matter, too, will be victorious, and the wellsprings will be disseminated outward.

I have already written briefly in the introduction to the *Kuntres* of 19 Kislev regarding the expression of Moshiach, "the wellsprings shall be disseminated outward." It is a known law that wellspring waters have the power to purify even drawn water, provided they do not cease from their source. As the Mishnah in *Mikvaos* (Chapter 5) states: "A spring that one diverted over a pool." Conversely, a spring that has been cut off no longer has the status of a spring. This is the conclusion of the Tzemach Tzedek in his *Responsa* (Yoreh Deah, 164:2) and in *Shaar HaMiluim* (Part 3, p. 37a-b), following the opinion of the Ra'avad, the Rashba, the Rambam in his Commentary on the Mishnah, and others, who hold that the Mishnah is speaking of an empty pool—unlike the opinion of the Maharik (cited in *Beis Yosef*).

Even according to the opinion of the Maharik, a pool full of water is considered a spring only through spring water that is connected to its source.

An additional condition for this, according to the Rambam (Chapter 9, Law 10), is that the spring water must flow out of the pool.

Regarding our matter—the dissemination of the **wellsprings** outward—the water that we influence must be connected to its source through our *hiskashrus* to the *Nasi* of our generation, my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, who is the Baal Shem Tov of this generation of ours. And according to the Rambam, there is a further condition: the spring water must spread even further. That is, we must not be satisfied with merely being "moist enough to moisten" (*tofeach al menas lehatfiach*), but rather, the moistening must be such that it, too, is "moist enough to moisten." Like the waters of a spring that do not remain in the pool, but act so that the water flows even outside the pool, performing its work even in the "outward of the outward."

It can be said that this matter is alluded to in *Iggeres HaKodesh* (27) regarding the *histalkus* and its explanation, in the expression "the growth of the growth of the growth," etc., and in the revealed Torah in the teaching of our Sages on the verse, "They shall not depart from your mouth, nor from the mouth of your seed, nor from the mouth of your seed's seed," etc.

With blessings for success and a good settlement, together with your wife, may she live, in body and soul,

**M. Schneerson**

Just now, your letter of 4 Kislev was received. We have already written to the esteemed Chossid, R' M. Lipsker, may he live, that he should provide the details on this as soon as possible, and then he will submit, together with your wife, may she live, a request for a visa to enter Meknes.

## 419

B"H, 8 Kislev, 5711

...Once again, I am writing to you what I have already told you several times: it is for nothing that you increase your melancholy and waste your money, your peace of mind, and, quite simply, your nerves, on baseless worries. ## 420

B"H, 10 Kislev, 5711, Brooklyn

To the honorable, the righteous Rabbi, son of holy lineage, the G-d-fearing, learned, and distinguished, etc.,
Rabbi Y. Shlita, Admur of...

Greetings and blessings!

The day of the nineteenth of Kislev is approaching—a Tuesday (corresponding to the portion *es achai anochi mevakesh* [I am seeking my brothers], Zohar Vol. I, 184a), a day upon which "it was good" was doubled. It is the day of the great *hillula* of Admur the Maggid of Mezritch—the great disciple and successor of Admur the Baal Shem Tov—whose waters we drink and by whose light we walk.

It is the day of the redemption of Admur HaZaken and the victory of the Torah of Chassidus—the Torah of the Baal Shem Tov—through which the children of **Yisrael** emerged with a high hand.

The question posed by the Baal Shem Tov to Mashiach is well known: "When will the Master come?" and the response of our righteous Mashiach: "When your teaching becomes publicized and **revealed in the world, and your springs spread outward."** For this is the preface and preparation for the coming of Mashiach.

In light of the holy obligation incumbent upon all of Yisrael, and especially upon the leaders of Yisrael in general and the leaders of the Chassidic communities in particular—and in light of their great privilege—to spread the springs of Chassidus, as they were bequeathed to us by our teacher the Baal Shem Tov, and after him our teacher the Maggid and their disciples, the Nesi’im of the Chassidic communities—

I hereby propose to your honor that on this bright day, the upcoming 19th of Kislev, or also on the Shabbosos preceding and following it, you arrange gatherings and *farbrengens* for all those under your influence. In these *farbrengens*, they should be specifically inspired toward the *avodah* of spreading the springs—the springs of the Torah of the Baal Shem Tov, his disciples, and his disciples' disciples—outward. And in general, toward setting fixed times for Torah study, observing the *mitzvos* with *hiddur*, and [cultivating] love for one's fellow and the refinement of character traits according to the Torah of Chassidus.

May the merit of our Nesi’im, the Nesi’im of Yisrael, protect us all, that we may succeed in fulfilling our mission in this world, and may our eyes behold the coming of our righteous Mashiach speedily in our days, in our immediate time, Amen.

With blessings for all that is good,

**M. Schneerson**

**Son-in-law of the Nasi,**
**His Holiness,**
**Admur (of Lubavitch)**
**May the merit of the righteous protect us, Amen.**

770 Eastern Parkway, Brooklyn, N.Y., U.S.A.

821

B”H, 11 Kislev, 5711, Brooklyn

The esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, refined, and distinguished, engaged in communal needs, etc.,
Rabbi Michael, may he live, Shaliach

Peace and blessing!

Your letter from Wednesday of Parshas Toldos has been received, and in response:

(a) I was happy to learn that all obstacles and delays have been removed. You will surely make every effort to ensure that both the esteemed Rabbi Toledano, may he live, and the activist Mr. Yosef Bardugo, may he live, **both** participate in our work there, and I rely on your understanding as to how to manage these matters.

(b) Regarding the name of the institutions, I have already conveyed that there must be a general name, "Ohalei Yosef Yitzchak," and beneath it (perhaps in a semi-circle?), "In his name and under the presidency of the Rebbe of Lubavitch." In addition to this general name, the specific name pertaining to the individual institution to which the letterhead refers should appear, such as the Teachers' Seminary, Yeshiva, Tiferes Bachurim, etc. I hope there will be no difficulties in agreeing upon the above format; in any case, the name "Lubavitch" must be mentioned in the format of the letterhead.

(c) Regarding what you write about forming a committee of five people and that from now on they will direct their requests through this committee, it is self-understood that this should be done in a way that preserves the spirit of the institutions in its purity, and that no foreign spirit should intermingle within them.

...Regarding what you ask about participation in girls' education, it is difficult from here to express an opinion on the specific details. The general point in this matter is that among the Sephardim, there are many customs of modesty regarding women, as well as young women and girls, which they have accepted upon themselves for several generations. Therefore, regarding the education of their daughters, one must be extremely careful that it should not be said that from the day Lubavitch arrived in their camp, they transitioned from a stricter level of holiness to a lighter one. Consequently, it is understood that one must first inquire among their G-d-fearing elders as to the custom their ancestors followed in this regard, and even if some changes are needed, the change should be made in such a way that it does not lead to criticism that they have moved from a higher level of holiness, etc.

I am rushing to send this letter, and I will answer the other matters, G-d willing, in my next letter.

With blessings for much success,

**M. Schneerson**

Just now, the lists of students from Meknes and Midelt have been received (in the latter, the mother’s name was not recorded). However, the names of the teachers' mothers are still missing. G-d willing, I will read them at the Tziyun on the upcoming Rosh Chodesh.

## 525

*[Copy of the text written at the end of the letters to the students of the Yeshiva in Meknes, 17 Kislev, 5711, by Rabbi M. Lipsker]*

Regarding your question as to whether you acted correctly by speaking with your employer about continuing your work with him: since the agreement has already been made, it is surely by *Hashgacha Pratis*. Nevertheless, do not stop looking for work elsewhere, and *Hashem* will guide you on the straight path in this as well. It is possible that when your employer learns that you are being offered higher pay elsewhere, he will increase your salary.

***

In response to your question regarding your work and your desire to leave the employer for whom you currently work: you do not state the reason why you wish to change your place of employment. If you have the ability to work for yourself, perhaps it is worth considering; consult with the esteemed Rabbi Michael, and let me know his opinion. Then, *bli neder*, I will write to you again.

I am sure you are exerting the proper effort in searching for a suitable *zivug*, and *Hashem* will guide you to success.

***

Regarding what you write about not yet being married: you are surely exerting the proper effort in this. Perhaps it would be worthwhile to learn a new trade that does not require much time to master and from which you can hope to earn a livelihood. But first, try once more in your current job, and speak with people in a pleasant manner. May it be the will of *Hashem* that He provide your livelihood very soon, and that you find a suitable *zivug* in every detail; please share good news regarding this.

***

Regarding what you mention in your letter about your older brother, Mr. ... who is already thirty years old and has not yet succeeded in marriage: tell him that he should set aside time for daily *shiurim* in Torah, and all the more so on *Shabbos Kodesh*. He should exert effort in searching for a suitable *shidduch*. He should remember the statement of our Sages that a man’s conduct with his wife must be with gentleness. The merit of setting fixed times for Torah study will help him find the woman suitable for him. If he conducts himself in the manner described above, *Hashem* will grant that their *zivug* will be a beautiful, lasting union, and he will be blessed with a generation of upright descendants.

## 426

B"H, 17 Kislev, 5711, Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and Blessings!

...It is a well-known verse: "If you walk in My statutes and keep My mitzvos and perform them, then I will give your rains in their season, etc." Rashi explains, "And keep My mitzvos" — [this means] you should be toilers in Torah. My revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, explained that the essential point is the toil in Torah; that is, that one dedicates his time and exerts his intellect to toil in the Torah of Hashem. Even if, due to his circumstances—due to the pressure of earning a livelihood, etc.—according to the law of the Torah he is unable to study for the majority of the day, nevertheless, when Hashem, blessed and exalted be He, sees that he is toiling in Torah, He grants him His blessing, "I will give your rains in their season, etc." Consequently, his livelihood gradually improves, and as a result, he is able to increase his Torah study and the performance of mitzvos over time, and he goes from strength to strength, both materially and spiritually.

I am certain that you also look favorably upon others and strive to include them in holy studies. I would be pleased to hear from you regarding the improvement of your situation in general, your progress in your studies, and the increase in the number of students participating in your shiurim.

With blessings for success in your Torah study, the performance of mitzvos, and a good understanding of the teachings of Chassidus.

Blessing you,

#### ***426***

Published in Likutei Sichos, Vol. 2, p. 682.

## 827

17 Kislev, 5711
Brooklyn

Greetings and blessings!

Due to the multitude of pressures, time does not permit me to respond to letters immediately upon their receipt, nor at the length they deserve. To a certain extent, I endeavor to address the **common** denominator in the questions of several letters received during the times of the farbrengens on Shabbos Mevarchim and the like. You, too, will surely find answers to some of your questions in my introductions to the kuntreisim being published, as well as in the *Reshimos* from Shabbos Parshas Bereishis and Parshas Lech Lecha, which are enclosed.

Specifically, regarding your letter and your request that I respond to your correspondence: it is **obvious** that I will do so to the extent possible, **provided** that you do not mind if my response is delayed due to the many pressures.

(a) Regarding what you write in your letter that the Conservatives and Reformers are gaining strength and succeeding: we have heard several times from my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory—and it is based on what is written in several of our Sages' books—that the existence of the *kelipah* is nothing more than a lack, and there are two ways this manifests: either as a matter of *birur* (refinement) or as a matter of *nisayon* (a test). In the first instance, there is a spark of good within the opposing side, and it must be refined and elevated. In the second instance, its destruction and rejection constitute its rectification; when one stands firmly against it, it is nullified of its own accord. Then one sees even with **physical** eyes that from the outset, there was no substance to it at all, only a matter of *nisayon*.

I have also seen this in several matters regarding your own affairs, where you viewed them as something opposing and fighting against you; all of this was nothing but a matter of *nisayon*. That is to say, there was no foundation for concern from the start, and furthermore, with the proper firmness, the opposition would have been nullified without leaving any trace of anguish, Heaven forbid.

(b) Regarding what you write that your desire is to fulfill the will of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory: there has **never** been any doubt in my mind about this. However, the *yetzer hara* sometimes acts craftily, explaining through various ruses that it is impossible to fulfill the will because there is no ability to do so due to various and sundry reasons (which have no substance). In my opinion, what requires a fundamental change is the approach—the *tzugang*—to the matter. Since this is the will of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, it is **certainly** possible to fulfill it. One must simply seek counsel and ways to fulfill it in a manner that involves a minimum of friction and in the most peaceful way possible.

(c) A general instruction regarding your conduct: you must know clearly that my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, wanted you to influence the spirituality of the city... and to be their spiritual leader, primarily for the Bnei Yisrael living in... and only secondarily regarding matters pertaining to... And yet, to my regret, according to reports, you are preoccupied with the second matter, while in the first matter, relative to your strengths, the activities are few. The fact that it is possible that for another person, their activities among the living might be even fewer than yours is not a sufficient excuse, for "according to the camel is the load." See the *Reshimos* of Shabbos Parshas Lech Lecha, end of section 25.

You will surely forgive me for these words, but is it not painful to see a city of several hundred thousand of our brethren, may they live, where there is a vast field for *avodah*, and where there are also people suitable for the *avodah*, and yet there is still so much lacking in what could have been done there in matters of Yiddishkeit, Torah, and *mitzvos*, and certainly regarding Chassidus.

...(f) Regarding the incident on the night of Simchas Torah past in your shul: I have already told you by telephone that in my opinion, you should endeavor that they recite three (or five) chapters of Tehillim every day after *davening*, **in addition** to the *shiur* of Tehillim that they recite regardless. Furthermore, on one of the upcoming fast days—which is now Asarah B'Teves (since BeHa"B has already passed)—you should endeavor that a full *minyan* of those who attend the shul should fast.

(g) A general letter and *kuntreisim* pertaining to 19 Kislev have already been sent; you surely have the *Megillas 19 Kislev*. You will surely share good news regarding the celebration of 19 Kislev, the *Chag HaGeulah*, in every place your influence reaches. In places where it is difficult to gather a large crowd in the middle of the week, perhaps it is worthwhile, in addition to the celebration on 19 Kislev, to arrange something on the following Shabbos and emphasize then that it is connected to 19 Kislev, etc.

I hope to hear good news from you in general and in particular, and especially regarding the health of your wife, may she live.

I will conclude with a blessing in the formula established by my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory: "May you be written and sealed for a good year in the study of Chassidus and the ways of Chassidus."

Waiting for good news.

**Menachem Schneerson**

The list for your *minyan* has just been received, and G-d willing, I will read them tomorrow at the *tziyun*.

## 428

B"H, 17 Kislev, 5711, Brooklyn

Greetings and blessings!

I received your letter of 26 Cheshvan in due time. Due to the heavy workload I have, I have not had the opportunity to respond to your letter until now.

You ask in your letter that since you have two children, may they be healthy, and the doctor is advising you to use birth control, you would like to know my opinion on the matter.

Surely you know that, in general, birth control is not in accordance with the perspective of the Torah, which views children as a blessing from the Ribono shel Olam, with which the Ribono shel Olam blesses the parents. Furthermore, the Torah maintains that among Jews there are no purely private matters, for every Jew is a part of the entire Jewish people, and all "private" matters of every Jew have an effect on the entire Jewish people. This is especially true regarding the present times, following the decrees and destruction, may Hashem spare us, through which so many millions of Jews perished al kiddush Hashem.

Nevertheless, in a case where it concerns the health of a Jew—husband, wife, or child—and the health of a Jew, according to the expression of the Rambam, is one of the ways of serving Hashem Yisbarach, the Torah does recognize **specific** forms of birth control in **specific** cases.

However, it is difficult to issue a general directive on this, because it depends on the nature of the harm that childbirth might bring to the mother, as well as the method by which the control is implemented.

Therefore, I would advise you that after you speak once more with your doctor and he indicates to you what form of birth control he has in mind, you should turn to a Chassidic, Orthodox Rav and hear his opinion.

May the Ribono shel Olam guide you in the proper path, that you should be completely healthy and have much nachas from your children, may they live, together with your husband, the Rav, may he live.

With blessings,

Menachem Schneerson

## 829

B"H, Monday, the second day of the week of Parshas Es Achai Ani Mevakesh, 18 Chai Elul, 5711, Brooklyn, N.Y.

To all the participants in the meeting for the support of the institutions: Merkos L'Inyonei Chinuch, Machne Israel, and Kehot — the institutions founded by my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, may his merit shield us and all of Israel — and under his presidency and leadership — may Hashem grant them life.

Greetings and abundant blessings!

Among the most important institutions founded by my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, were Merkos L'Inyonei Chinuch, Machne Israel, and Kehot. They were extremely dear to him, and he held them in special affection, concerning himself with every single detail of their activities, with every matter and affair conducted according to his instruction and approval.

Even in these recent months, in accordance with the instructions of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, given in the weeks prior to his passing, the scope of these institutions' work has expanded. New work has also begun: the work of education in North Africa, which is steadily growing. In it, we see tangibly how success accompanies the handiwork of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe.

Now, although the scope of the aforementioned institutions' activities in the field of education, strengthening Yiddishkeit, rescue, and so on, encompasses all strata of our brethren, the Children of Israel, in every country of the world—which, as is understood, involves great expenses—these institutions have not, until now, organized public fundraising campaigns. Their entire basis of support was received through my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe.

It is understood that from the time of the passing of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, the primary income of these institutions ceased. For more than ten months now, a great danger has hovered over them due to a lack of financial means.

The hour demands **urgently** from each and every one of us that we remember the holy duty and privilege incumbent upon us. The main thing is to **act in practice** to fulfill this obligation, which is to be among those who do and act to the full extent of our ability to support these institutions, which my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, nurtured, raised, and into which he invested his best strengths. And thank G-d, **the strength of the craftsman is evident in the vessel**. Especially since the hands of the craftsman are not removed, G-d forbid, from this vessel. **For just as he stood and led until now, so too does he stand and lead hereafter.**

My revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, said in one of his sichos that sometimes, when speaking of a matter that was most internal and heartfelt, he would specifically use Yiddish. He brought as an example what the Alter Rebbe writes in Iggeres HaKodesh regarding the mitzvah of "You shall surely rebuke your fellow": *Gwald, gwald!*

A person is obligated to speak in the language of his Rebbe: *Gwald, gwald!* How long shall we remain silent? How shall we justify ourselves, and what shall we answer to the question of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe: "Is this your participation in my handiwork and in my work, for which I sacrificed my life?"

You are gathering on the eve of Rosh Hashanah LaChassidus. May it be the will that your good resolutions and your vigorous actions in fulfilling these resolutions—actions immediately and actions in the very near future—will give Merkos L'Inyonei Chinuch, Machne Israel, and Kehot the possibility to fulfill the mission that my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, charted for them. And we shall not be ashamed or disgraced, for we will be able to say with justice: "We have done what you asked of us."

— It is self-understood that this letter, written on the occasion of the meeting, is directed also to those who are not present at this meeting but are connected to my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe. For surely they appreciate his work and activities as is fitting, for "the activity of a tzaddik is for life, for all who live; it is the soul of every living thing that is bound to his soul with cords of great love and eternal love that shall never falter." —

Blessing and being blessed with success in our aforementioned joint work, and signing in the language of the Rebbe, my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe: May you be inscribed and sealed for a good year in the study of Chassidus and in the ways of Chassidus,

**Menachem Schneerson**

## 430

B"H, 18 Kislev, 5711

To the esteemed Rabbi and Chassid, G-d-fearing and pious, etc., [Name]...

## 331

18 Kislev, 5711
Brooklyn

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, and distinguished activist in the cause of *Maamad*, etc., R' Levi Yitzchak, may he live.

Greetings and blessings!

I have received your letter and the enclosed checks with thanks. You have surely by now received the receipts directly from the office.

As a veteran activist in matters of *Maamad*, it is surely unnecessary for me to elaborate on the importance of this cause. However, as we are on the eve of *Yud-Tes Kislev*, I wish to underscore the special connection between the matter of *Maamad* and the month of Kislev in general, and *Yud-Tes Kislev* in particular.

You are certainly familiar with the details of the arrest and liberation of the Alter Rebbe—*Yud-Tes Kislev*—and the arrest and liberation of his son, the Mitteler Rebbe—*Yud Kislev*.

The Rebbes of all generations, from the Baal Shem Tov (founder of the general *Toras HaChassidus*) and the Alter Rebbe (founder of *Toras HaChassidus HaChabad*) until our own time—notwithstanding the fact that they possessed the greatest of souls and understood in the deepest manner the greatness and preciousness of studying Torah, both *nigleh* and *nistar*, and were immersed in matters of *Elokus*—nevertheless, they did not look to themselves. They occupied themselves with all the needs of the *klal*. Not only that, but they went to the point of *mesiras nefesh* to do a favor even for a private individual. My father-in-law, the Rebbe, *k.k. mo.ch. Admur h.k.m.*, related that the Tzemach Tzedek said that all the *mesiras nefesh* of his grandfather (the Alter Rebbe) was as naught (*k'la*) compared to the *mesiras nefesh* of tearing oneself away from the state of *v'amcha lo chafatzti* (the deepest contemplation and longing—*klos hanefesh*—for *Elokus*) to occupy oneself with doing a favor for a Yid.

All the *Nesi'ei Chabad* from the Alter Rebbe until my father-in-law, the Rebbe, *k.k. mo.ch. Admur h.k.m.*, followed this same path. According to this path, their activity was not only in *ahavas Hashem* and *ahavas haTorah*, but also in *ahavas Yisrael*—without distinction as to whether one was a Chossid or a layman, a *lamdan* or a simple person, an adult or a child.

A portion of these activities, as circumstances permitted, was done openly. Another portion—such as *tzedakah* to individuals or institutions in certain cases where publicity was not required, and similar activities—was done in secret (*b'chashai*), and to a great extent from the personal funds of the *Nesi'ei Chabad*.

All these activities continue today, and we hope to *Hashem* that with the help of the *mekusharim*, Chassidim, and students of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, *k.k. mo.ch. Admur h.k.m.*, it will be possible for them to continue further, commensurate with the necessity, which is unfortunately growing—especially in the matter of *tzedakah b'chashai*, which is in part drawn from the *Maamad* fund.

In these days before *Yud-Tes Kislev*, and on *Yud-Tes Kislev* itself—which is, as my father-in-law, the Rebbe, *k.k. mo.ch. Admur h.k.m.*, said, the *Rosh Hashanah* of *Chassidus* and the ways of *Chassidus*—all the Rebbes, and especially the *baal hasimcha*, the Alter Rebbe, arouse mercy for all those who help to carry on the work of all these matters that he, the *baal hasimcha*, founded and which his successors after him carry out in practice, generation after generation.

I conclude with a blessing that your activity in the matter of *Maamad* should draw down upon you blessing and success in all that you require. I also ask that you convey my regards to all those who participate in this and assist you in your work.

With the blessing of *Chag HaGeulah*, our redemption and the liberation of our souls,

**Menachem Schneerson**

Enclosed is the booklet for *Yud-Tes Kislev* in Yiddish and English, as well as my general letter regarding *Yud-Tes Kislev*.

## 432

B"H, 19 Kislev, the festival of our redemption and the salvation of our soul, 5711, Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, and distinguished, who engages in communal needs with faithfulness, etc., Rabbi Yitzchak Aharon, may he live.

As you requested, I read the list of the students and their teachers while I was at the Tziyun of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, today, on the Rosh Hashanah of Chassidus and the ways of Chassidus. And a tzaddik who has departed, who is found in this world more than during his lifetime, will surely grant his blessing for a *kesivah v'chasimah tovah* in this.

It may be said that for Chassidim and those who are *mekushar*, this [the Tziyun] is the gate through which all Torah and mitzvos ascend on high, and through which all influences are drawn down in both physicality and spirituality. This is similar to what is written in Iggeres HaKodesh, Epistle 7, regarding the matter that in a specific way, every *nefesh, ruach, neshamah* has a specific light, etc.—see there. And based on this, one can also understand the connection of the matters at the conclusion of the letter from my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, dated 10 Kislev 5710, which is printed in the *Kuntres* for 19 Kislev of this year. It begins with "a good year in the study and dissemination of Chassidus," etc., and immediately thereafter he writes, "And you, all who are joined with you, shall all be blessed with everything you require, in both physicality and spirituality."

I sign with the blessing of the festival and for all the *chavurah*, may they live,

**Menachem Schneerson**

## 833

B”H, 19 Kislev, the Festival of our Redemption and the Liberation of our souls, 5711, Brooklyn

To the esteemed and distinguished individual, who engages in communal needs with faithfulness, etc., R’ Moshe Zalman, may he live:

Greetings and blessings!

I received your letter from Erev Rosh Chodesh Kislev, in which you inform me that the wedding of your granddaughter, Maras Esther, may she live, is to take place on 19 Kislev.

In addition to the telegram I sent you, I wish to express my blessing here once again in writing: Mazal Tov, Mazal Tov. May it be in a propitious and successful hour, a building that will endure forever, and may you be blessed among a generation of upright people. May you, the parents of the bride, and the entire family derive much nachas—Yiddishe nachas and Chassidishe nachas.

My revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, once said at a farbrengen that a person’s completeness is achieved in the third generation—with the grandchildren. This is based on the verse, “A threefold cord is not quickly broken,” and the statement of our Sages that when the Torah is maintained for three generations, one can then say, “It shall not depart from your mouth.”

While I do not know your granddaughter personally, I can judge from your letters and the reports I receive from Australia regarding your work and the lifestyle of you and your family, may they live, that one can hopefully apply the aforementioned verse and statement of our Sages to your case. This brings a sense of completion to you yourself, in that you have, B”H, raised your children in the Jewish path, and not only your children, but their upbringing was such that they have also raised their own children, may they live, in the Jewish path.

This is especially valuable in the time of Galus, particularly in these current years when the darkness is so dense, and even more so in a country that for so many years was far from the centers of Torah. To carry out what a Jew must carry out under such circumstances is connected with mesiras nefesh, which one has inherited from parents and grandparents.

I am certain that you, your children, and the entire family, may they live, will continue to proceed with your work to help make Australia a place of Torah and Chassidus, through yeshivos and kosher educational institutions in general, both for boys and for girls, and that this entire endeavor will be saturated with Chassidishe light and warmth.

I conclude with the blessing that the Rosh Hashanah of the teachings of Chassidus and the ways of Chassidus should bring you and the entire family a *kesivah v’chasimah tovah* in the study of Chassidus and the ways of Chassidus. By way of consequence, this will also bring you blessing and success, as my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, concludes in his letters: “in everything you require, both materially and spiritually.”

With blessings of Mazal Tov,

**Menachem Schneerson**

***

**833**

**R’ Moshe Zalman:** Feiglin.

## 834

B”H, 19 Kislev, the Festival of our Redemption and the deliverance of our souls, 5711, Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter regarding the dispute you had concerning... Ever since you first wrote to me about this matter, I have been in correspondence with the representatives of Anash in Eretz Yisrael, may it be rebuilt and established, regarding this. In the latest letter I received from there, they inform me that they have come to... Also, the representative of Anash from... and at a gathering in which **you, too, participated**, they reached a compromise in an agreement among all of them.

I was very happy to receive this news, and I am confident that it is indeed true, for peace is upon Yisrael in general, and upon Anash in particular, and in Eretz Yisrael, may it be rebuilt and established, in the most specific detail. It is well known how much [our predecessors] feared and dreaded the matter of dispute in Eretz Yisrael, may it be rebuilt and established. I am sure that you, too, will gladden me with a letter confirming that the land is quiet and there is peace upon Yisrael.

I will conclude with what was discussed at this 19 Kislev farbrengen: "The Holy One, Blessed be He, found no vessel that could hold blessing for Yisrael other than peace." On the face of it, this is self-contradictory, for the blessing of the Holy One, Blessed be He, is as the prophet says, "And I will pour out for you a blessing until there is no room [literally: until there is no sufficiency]," and a vessel that holds [a blessing] stands in contradiction to this, for if it is the one, it is not the other, and if it is the other, it is not the one.

The brief resolution to this is that it is precisely from the greatness of the Holy One, Blessed be He, and the power of the Holy One, Blessed be He, that He connects two opposites together: a blessing "until there is no room" with a fitting vessel. Yet, such a vessel cannot exist except through peace, the essence of which is to connect two opposites: fire, which contracts and constricts, and water, which spreads and expands, and they do not extinguish one another. This is as our Sages said in the Midrash on the verse, "Dominion and fear are with Him; He makes peace in His high places."

And it is the same here, following the path of the statement of our Sages in Chagigah regarding His legions having no number, and each legion being limited—"a thousand thousands shall serve Him," etc.—even though, as is known in the books of the philosophers, and cited in *Sefer HaChakirah* by the Tzemach Tzedek, according to logic, it is impossible for the infinite to be composed of finite elements.

This is the meaning of "The Holy One, Blessed be He, found no vessel that could hold His blessing"—for His blessing is "until there is no room"—"other than peace," which connects the two opposites: a vessel and a blessing "until there is no room." Based on this, the precision of the Mishnah is also resolved, for it uses the language of negation. On the face of it, it should have used the language of affirmation, stating that the vessel that holds blessing is only peace, rather than negating from the outset by saying "He found no... other than," etc. But this is not the place to elaborate.

Enclosed is my general letter for 19 Kislev. I will conclude with the blessing of *kesivah vachasimah tovah* in the study of Chassidus and the ways of Chassidus, through which there will naturally be blessing and success in everything required, from the material to the spiritual.

Awaiting good tidings,

**Menachem Schneerson**

## 355

B"H, 19 Kislev, the Festival of our Redemption and the Liberation of our souls, 5711, Brooklyn

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, and honorable Mr. Yitzchak Shpalter,

Peace and blessing!

I received your letter in good time and was pleased to read that everything went well, B"H, and that you are completely free.

Furthermore, and even more so, I was pleased to read in your letter that you are fulfilling and doing what I suggested to you. I write "even more so" regarding the second point, because as for the liberation, the Ribono shel Olam certainly wants a Yid not to have any trouble, so the joy is that you received the blessing and were worthy of it.

The second matter, however, is something that depends on your own will, and regarding this, the Ribono shel Olam has given every Yid free choice (*bechirah chafshis*). Consequently, there is a possibility that the *yetzer hara* might intervene and want to prevent you from carrying out the good deed in practice. Therefore, the fact that you write that you are doing what I suggested, and that it is to be hoped that this will persist with you, has caused me special joy.

Surely you know about the Yom Tov of 19 Kislev. In any case, I am enclosing here the description we have printed in English regarding it. From it, you will gain an insight into some of the fundamentals of Chassidus, and I hope that you will set aside time to study it. Our mutual friend, Mr. Aaron Katz, will surely help you with this.

I conclude with a blessing and a wish that you should always be able to report good news about yourself and your family, may they be well,

**Menachem Schneerson**

Enclosed is a receipt for the check that I handed over to the secret office at "Machne Israel" — the special fund that was established by my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, for charity without publicity for individuals and institutions. This work, like all other activities of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, continues to be conducted and expanded, B"H.

## 837
