**Menachem Schneerson**

## 838

B"H, 3rd day of Chanukah, 5711, Brooklyn

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter describing your situation, where you feel you do not have enough time to manage the work of principal at the yeshiva and teach classes there, while simultaneously managing your book and holy items business, and you therefore wish to leave the position of principal at the yeshiva and are asking for my opinion on this.

In my opinion, if there is not enough time for all the aforementioned matters, you should give up the teaching of classes and the like, but not the position of principal. Some of my reasons for this are that even a minor position is appointed from Heaven, and especially since this greatness was bestowed upon you by my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory.

This is from your perspective. From the perspective of the yeshiva, it is not clear whether the person who would replace you would be better than you or the opposite.

And there are other reasons as well.

It is my hope that you will be able to manage the work of principal alone, together with the participation in the book business that is indispensable, in a way that will not cause damage to either endeavor.

With the blessing of Chanukah, which increases and goes on, and illuminates even the outside,

**Menachem Schneerson**

I am interested to know what **actions** were taken regarding what I spoke to him about before he left, concerning the formation of a minyan and the like.

## 441

B.H., 7th of Chanukah, 5711, Brooklyn

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, and distinguished individual, occupied with communal needs, etc.,
R. M. Wechsler

Peace and Blessing!

I was pleased to hear about the upcoming conference at your home this coming Wednesday, with the participation of Mr. Ben Plet and other esteemed baalei-batim, in order to establish a foundation for tangible support for the "Merkaz L'Inyonei Chinuch."

For ten years now, the Merkaz L'Inyonei Chinuch has been conducting its wide-ranging educational work here in this country and in almost every corner of the world. This vital work is carried out without stormy campaigns, because it has the assistance of responsible individuals who know how to appreciate this work. My sainted father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, personally provided for a large portion of the budget of the Merkaz L'Inyonei Chinuch.

However, after the passing of my sainted father-in-law, the Rebbe, a critical situation has arisen that threatens the very existence of the Merkaz L'Inyonei Chinuch. On the other hand, knowing the will of my sainted father-in-law, the Rebbe, the work is being continued in its full scope. The circumstances have also demanded that we expand the work in North Africa, where we have established a series of educational institutions for children and youth, in the name of the great founder — "Ohalei Yosef Yitzchak."

It is impossible to describe the great zechus of participating in this holy work of illuminating Jewish hearts and Jewish homes with the light and warmth of our holy Torah and mitzvos, and the Yom Tov of Chanukah that we are currently celebrating should certainly inspire us to maasim b'poel. The situation is very critical; the time is very short. We hope that the conference will bring good and significant results in actual practice. And I hope to hear good news from you.

Since my sainted father-in-law, the Rebbe, continues to lead this institution, he will surely send his blessing to you, your family, and all those who participate with you in this important undertaking for the benefit of the Merkaz L'Inyonei Chinuch. May Hashem bless you in your endeavors, both personal and for the benefit of the public, and especially for the benefit of the Merkaz L'Inyonei Chinuch, and bless you with health and parnassah in abundance.

With Chanukah blessings,

**Menachem Schneerson**

## 842

B"H, 7th of Chanukah, 5711, Brooklyn

To the esteemed and distinguished Chossid, etc., R' Shneur Zalman [Kaselman], may he live,
Shaliach

Shalom u’Bracha!

Enclosed is the Kuntres for Chanukah, the publication of which was delayed due to the many pressures of the time.

Regarding your request for my opinion on the proposal to move the Yeshiva from Tel Aviv to Lod—with your reasoning being that the noise of the city of Tel Aviv should not disturb the diligence in studies, etc., and also out of concern for the loss of time spent walking from one building to another, etc.—in my opinion, this is **very** correct. I have heard many times from my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, about the difficulties of a Yeshiva in a large city, and he would praise the advantage that the Yeshiva in Lubavitch had, where the Yeshiva was the primary focus, and the other affairs of the city did not occupy any place at all to distract the students—neither the younger ones in their thinking, nor even the older ones—unlike in New York, etc.

And this is all the more so in your current situation, where one can hope for great benefit if the Yeshiva is in a place where it will be the primary focus, and the other affairs of the location will be secondary or occupy no place at all.

However, in any case, in my opinion, you should leave some class or department in Tel Aviv as well, so that it may serve as a bridge and a conduit through which it will be easier to attract the children of Tel Aviv and its surroundings to the Yeshiva in Lod.

It is understood that this is only a response to your question based on how you describe the local situation, and perhaps, depending on the conditions of the place, the people, and the time, there are matters that I am unaware of that require caution.

Regarding your question about the study of Chassidus—I cannot elaborate without knowing more details about the state of the students' talents, the qualities of the Mashpi'im, etc. However, there are two general points regarding the study of Chassidus that, in my opinion, should be present in all Lubavitch Yeshivos: (a) The students must be prepared in such a way that within a short time, each one will be able to repeat Maamarim of Chassidus in a manner that will influence the listeners, even those who are not learned in the teachings of Chassidus. (b) A broader knowledge of the teachings of Chassidus. Regrettably, a very great deficiency is felt in this second point, even among students who have studied Chassidus for several years; they know several topics in depth, but the number of topics they know is very, very small. If it were in my power, I would institute in every place a study of Chassidus not only for deep analysis, but a special shiur for **memorization** (even though Chabad generally demands inwardness), simply to know the topics.

Please convey my regards to the entire group, may they live, and may you have success in your influence upon your students, may they live. May you be able to go from strength to strength in illuminating the light of Chassidus and to illuminate also "outside," which is the concept of Chanukah: lighting a light, increasing in light and holiness, and decreasing in the side of the opposition. The lighting is to "extinguish the feet of the Tarmodai from the marketplace," as explained in Chassidus, and in our days this is accomplished through the efforts in spreading the wellsprings outward.

With blessings and regards,

**M. Schneerson**

I am sure you will share good news regarding the welfare of your grandchildren, may they live.

The Pidyon Nefesh—I read it at the Tziyun—on the eve of the 10th of Teves and on the eve of Rosh Chodesh.

**Menachem Schneerson**

#### ***843***

Sent to several of the leaders of Anash in Eretz Yisrael. Regarding its content, see Letter 873 below.

## 444

B"H, Zos Chanukah, 5711, Brooklyn

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, etc., R' Menachem Shmuel Dovid HaLevi, may he live, Shaliach.

Peace and Blessing!

Your letter from the 27th of Kislev has just been received, describing your farbrengen on the past 19th of Kislev, and concluding with the decision to hold a parlor meeting this coming Wednesday at the home of Mr. Wechsler, may he live, with Mr. Plet, may he live, serving as chairman.

May their strength be fortified in this. Although it is a pity that such matters were not put into action in the time that has already passed, one does not cry over the past; provided that from here on out, you will act and exert yourselves in this with the energy appropriate to the great value of these matters. Enclosed is a copy of my letter to Mr. Wechsler and Mr. Plet, may they live. It is appropriate that you publicize the content of my letter among the participants of the meeting, etc.

You ask in your letter about wanting to travel from Los Angeles immediately after the meeting so that you will be in New York for the Yahrtzeit.

In general, it is correct that you wish to be here for the Yahrtzeit. Regarding the time to travel from Los Angeles, this depends on the results of the meeting. For it is obvious that after the aforementioned meeting, it will still be necessary to bring the decisions and the collection of funds into action, and I fear that if you are not there to oversee them, who knows what the actual results will be. Only after the meeting, and once you see the progress of matters thereafter, will you be able to decide when to travel from Los Angeles.

...And another point. I believe I have already told you that it would be appropriate for there to be a group of avreichim hatmimim in Los Angeles, full of energy, so that little by little they can gather around them anash and those connected to anash, in such a way that anash in Los Angeles and its surroundings will occupy their proper place. Therefore, I requested that you inform me if there is a possibility for anash to settle there as shochtim of poultry, shochtim of cattle, and the like, the size of the rent, etc., etc.

Please convey the content of this letter also to R' Y.L. Poizner, may he live, or show him the letter itself, for due to the multitude of preoccupations, I do not know when I will be able to answer his letter separately.

I await good news as soon as possible.

You mention in your letter R' Shraga Feivush Weiler; surely you know that the son of the aforementioned is a public activist and a very wealthy man, and he gives specific sums to his father to distribute to tzedakah and institutions as his father, Shraga Feivush, may he live, sees fit.

While at the Tziyun of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, I mentioned you for good, and consequently, this also includes success in this week's meeting in particular, and in all your communal activities in general, which are also the channels for blessing and success in your personal affairs.

With the blessing of Chanukah, that it should be "increasing and continuing" in the lighting of the candles, and also outside — until the foot of the Tarmodai ceases.

**Menachem Schneerson**

## 449

B"H, Chanukah, 5711, Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, and distinguished, etc., Moreinu Harav Y. [may he live],

Greetings and blessings!

Enclosed is the Kuntres for Chanukah. May it be the will of Hashem that you illuminate your entire surroundings with the light of Torah and the "light within the Torah," in a manner of *mosif v'holech* (increasing and continuing). As is known, the word "Chanukah" is an acronym for *Ches-Nun* (eight candles), and the *halacha* follows Beis Hillel, who brought many converts into the fold of Israel through his conduct.

Our Rebbe, my father-in-law, of blessed memory, instructed us in this path as well—each and every one of us. For throughout the days of his life in this world, he would go and light the candles of the sons and daughters of Israel—"The candle of Hashem is the soul of man." He would increase and continue this lighting from time to time and from year to year. His lighting was at the entrance of his house, yet facing outward, so that the candles would illuminate the marketplace—a place of darkness and gloom, for the sun had set.

Our Sages have long promised us that a blessing rests upon this lighting of candles, provided that a person performs it with a desired *kavanah*—an internal *kavanah*. As they expressed it: "The candles shall always shine toward the face of the Menorah, and all the blessings that I have given you to bless My children shall never be nullified."

With Chanukah blessings that the light may increase and continue to shine until the day is established—the day of the Geulah.

**M. Schneerson**

#### ***449***

General-specific. Printed in Likkutei Sichos, Vol. 15, p. 527, and completed based on a photocopy of the letter. **The Kuntres for Chanukah:** The *maamar* "Baruch She'asah Nissim" by the Admur the Tzemach Tzedek. Printed in Ohr HaTorah, Bereishis, Vol. 5, p. 957b.

## 446

446

B"H, 3 Teves, 5711, Brooklyn

Greetings and blessings!

I was informed that you are suffering from headaches, may Hashem protect you, etc. In accordance with your request, I mentioned you for good and for blessing while at the Tziyun of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory. Surely, the Rebbe, my father-in-law, of blessed memory, has blessed you with a *refuah*, and may you have *arichas yamim* and good years.

Our Sages, of blessed memory, in interpreting the words of the Torah, "and he shall surely heal" (*v'rapo yerapei*), state that the Torah has granted permission for doctors to heal the sick, because the Ribono shel Olam desires that the world be conducted in a natural manner. However, one must know that it is the Ribono shel Olam who conducts the world, and He desires that Yidden should have goodness, so He grants them goodness. To you, in particular, He will grant *arichas yamim* and good years, and you should have *nachas* from all your children and grandchildren, *yichyu*—both Yiddishe *nachas* and Chassidishe *nachas*.

With blessings,

Menachem Schneerson

## 847

847

B”H, 4 Teves, 5711, Brooklyn

To my dear friend, the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, and distinguished man, who occupies himself with communal needs, etc., Moreinu Harav Azriel Zelig, may he live.

Greetings and blessings!

On this day, the day your son Moshe Shlomo, may he live, enters the age of Bar Mitzvah, I hereby send my blessings—in addition to the telegram I sent—that he may grow to be a G-d-fearing Chossid and a scholar, and that you may raise him for Torah, for the chuppah, and for good deeds in a state of expansion, as all these matters are explained in the teachings of Chassidus.

Thank you for sending here the announcement regarding the elections, as well as the clipping from the publication regarding the nigun of the Rebbe of Liadi. I am certain you will continue to do so in the future, and I thank you in advance for the effort involved.

I await good news regarding the girl... may she live, and may it be Hashem’s will that you be able to report only good, both generally and specifically.

Thank you for informing me about the celebrations of 9-10 and 19-20 Kislev, as well as on Shabbos Mevarchim. I am certain you will continue to make an effort to farbreng at frequent intervals and to increase your strength in spreading the wellsprings outward, for this is our task at this time.

I read the *pidyon nefesh* for your son, may he live, while I was at the Tziyun on Erev Rosh Chodesh. A *tzaddik* who has departed is found in this world even more than during his lifetime; he surely gave his blessing, and may Hashem fulfill it completely.

I have been informed that in the Beis Yisrael neighborhood there is a shiur in Chassidus, and the mashpia is the esteemed Chossid, etc., R’... who is also among those receiving support from Kolel Chabad. However, for several months now, his support has been discontinued, and consequently, it is possible that this will lead to a weakening, or even a complete cancellation, Heaven forbid, of the aforementioned shiur.

I do not know the reason why the support for the aforementioned was discontinued, and surely they had their reasons and justifications. But considering that this casts doubt on a public shiur in the teachings of our Nasi, I hope you will endeavor to find a way so that there will not be, Heaven forbid, an interruption in the shiur. If it is impossible otherwise, we will also participate from here in the aforementioned support.

Regarding what you write about establishing shiurim in Chassidus in several places, and that you write that this requires a mashpia and seforim: please be kind enough to provide me with more details on this—namely, in which neighborhoods, who the mashpiim are, etc., and which seforim you are referring to—and I will endeavor, G-d willing, to see what is within my power to do regarding this.

With blessings,

**Menachem Schneerson**

## 848

B"H, 4 Teves, 5711, Brooklyn

Greetings and blessings!

I received your letter some time ago, but due to the pressure of many preoccupations, I have not been able to reply until now.

You ask in your letter that, since travel to the United States has become somewhat easier, whether you should endeavor to travel here, though your desire is to settle only as a *yoshev ohel*, as a *rosh yeshiva*.

In general, finding a position here as a *rosh yeshiva* or the like is extremely difficult, especially to be certain of such a position in advance, as a matter of this nature requires searching and significant effort on the spot. It is understood that if you wish and are able to clarify the possibilities for this through letters from Paris, you may try, but I doubt you will succeed.

On the other hand, finding a position here as a *shochet* for poultry and large livestock is relatively easy and pays quite well, though for this, it may be necessary to live in the provincial cities. If you are capable of this and desire it, then it is appropriate that you endeavor to obtain the necessary papers for the United States. May Hashem guide you on the straight path so that you reach your desired destination—the desire of a Jewish person, which is the desire of his *neshamah elokis*, as brought in *Chassidus* from the Rambam, *Hilchos Geirushin*, end of chapter 2, that the inner will of a Jewish person, which is what is called *chefetz*, is solely Torah and *mitzvos*.

With blessings for a successful settlement and proper health,

**Menachem Schneerson**

## 550

550

B.H., 5 Teves, 5711, Brooklyn

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, learned, etc., Rabbi Nissan Nemanov, may he live.

Greetings and blessings!

I received your letter of 13 Kislev. In general, please know that if a response is delayed, it is only due to the multitude of burdens that surround me, which increase from day to day. This is especially true regarding the preparation for print of the maamarim and sichos, which require peace of mind and depth of thought—things that can only be achieved through great exertion, even to the point of having to tear oneself away from the daily matters that demand attention.

At times, it is difficult to decide what takes precedence: answering an individual regarding their personal question—which touches them in their inner life—or utilizing the time to publish a maamar or sicha. Although the latter affects many, there are already several maamarim and sichos that have been published but have not yet been studied to their full potential. It is difficult to reach a decision on this matter.

On the Chag HaGeulah, this past 19 Kislev, while I was at the Tziyun, I read the lists of the administration, the teachers, and the students, based on the lists that you sent me before Rosh Chodesh Kislev. Surely our Nasi, the Rebbe, may his merit protect us, granted his blessing to each and every one according to their needs, and may Hashem fulfill the blessings of the Tzaddik in both material and spiritual matters.

Thank you for your efforts in sending the letter to the esteemed Rabbi, and it is my hope that this was beneficial in the matter of spreading the wellsprings outward...

Regarding what you wrote concerning the proposal to establish a daily study session in the Torah of the Rebbe, may his merit protect us: in general, this is a correct thing. However, it is difficult for me to establish new study sessions, especially since there is no time limit on this. Although I have proposed several matters, there was a time limit attached to them—namely, the eleven months following the histalkus, or the entire year of the histalkus. But to establish a study session for the masses from now on, I have not yet reached a decision. It is understood that anyone who feels this matter within themselves should be commended if they establish a regular study session, a few times a week or every single day, to study the aforementioned maamarim. Surely, through this, they will gain courage and strength in their hiskashrus.

It is also understood that the above does not refer to study within the Yeshiva; it goes without saying that in the study of Chassidus, the Torah of the Rebbe, may his merit protect us, must occupy an important place, especially in the higher classes.

What I have proposed here is based on the maamar "Ve'hadarta Pnei Zakein" in Likutei Torah, and what was discussed regarding this in the sicha printed in the Kuntres of 19 Kislev: that every person should have some maamarim of the Rebbe, may his merit protect us, engraved in their memory—especially a maamar, or a part of one, from the day of the histalkus, 10 Shevat 5710, as explained at length in the farbrengen of 19 Kislev of this year.

I will conclude with a Mazal Tov, Mazal Tov on the birth of your granddaughter, may she live. May it be His will that your daughter and son-in-law, may they live, raise her to Torah, to the chuppah, and to good deeds, in comfort and abundance, and may you and your wife, may you live, see much nachas from them in all good things.

With blessings for Mazal Tov,

**Menachem Schneerson**

There are no more Pidyon Nefesh notes from his students (from this past Rosh Hashanah) here. However, several Pidyon Nefesh notes were received without the family name of the sender (even on the envelope) and without their address. Perhaps the aforementioned are included among these.

Please, I ask you to send me a copy, word for word, of what I wrote to you regarding 5709.

## 451

451

B"H,

This *kuntres* is being issued in connection with the conclusion of the recitation of *Kaddish* upon the passing of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory...

* * *

There are several opinions regarding the duration of the recitation of *Kaddish* : throughout one's entire life; twelve months; eleven months and one day (which is a complete cycle, including the leap month); twelve months; twelve months less a week; eleven months; and eleven months less one day.

We, however, follow only the custom of our *Nesi'im*, based on what is recorded in a passage from the *tzava'ah* (will) of the Rebbe (Rashab), of blessed memory: regarding the eleven months—to stop one month and one day prior. For example, if the *yahrzeit* is on the 10th of Shevat, one recites *Kaddish* until the 9th of Teves, and including that day. This is also the opinion of the overwhelming majority of the later *poskim*.

* * *

It is stated in the writings of the Arizal —and cited by the *poskim*—that the recitation of *Kaddish* also pertains to the ascent of the *neshamah* from level to level within *Gan Eden* itself.

It is understood from this that with the conclusion of the eleven months of reciting *Kaddish*, this order of ascents is completed, and a new order of the *neshamah’s* ascents begins; for our Sages have said that *talmidei chachamim* have no rest in the World to Come, for they go from strength to strength.

It is therefore necessary for everyone who is *mekushar* to my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, to now add strength to the reinforcement of their *hiskashrus*, and to make an accounting of their soul—*alibi d’nafshi*—regarding what they have accomplished in this regard during these eleven months, to fill in what is lacking. This should be done through the methods that our *Nasi*, my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, has instructed—to connect with him with greater intensity and greater strength, meaning to him, so that he, too, may be elevated in his ascent.

And one who sanctifies himself a little below—is sanctified much from above.

**Menachem Schneerson**

Erev Shabbos, *Vayigash Elav Vayomer Bi Adoni*, 5711. Brooklyn, N.Y.

## 852

B"H, 9 Teves, 5711, Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, etc., R. Y. shlit"a,

Shalom u’vracha!

Enclosed is the Kuntres for the ninth of Teves—the conclusion of the eleven months from the day of the histalkus of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, ztzk"l, nbg"m, zy"a, hk"m. Like the previous kuntresim, the purpose is to bring merit to the public and to those in your surroundings in particular. "Merit" (*zechus*) comes from the word *zichuch* (refinement) and *birur* (clarification); through additional refinement below, we draw down additional lights from above and receive them in a positive way.

As explained in the introduction to the Kuntres, it should be noted that after eleven months, a new order begins in the soul’s ascents within Gan Eden itself (similar to how those who belong to this level then ascend from Gehenom to Gan Eden).

If so, it is the obligation and the privilege of all those who are connected to also ascend from their current state and standing, so that there will be no weakening, chas v’shalom, in the hiskashrus—but rather the opposite.

The ways of hiskashrus have already been explained by my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, hk"m, in many places.

I would also like to suggest that from now until the day of the Yahrtzeit (the tenth of Shevat)—the ascent that follows the aforementioned ascent, for that is when the matters of the day of histalkus are aroused—each person should endeavor to increase, **without a vow**, in the three pillars of Torah, avodah, and gemilas chasadim:

1) Complete five chapters of Mishnayos (the letters of *mishnah* are the same as *neshamah*, and it is called by five names) by the Yahrtzeit, either by heart or from the text. It would be excellent to divide the entire Shas Mishnayos in this manner. You may coordinate this together with a shul or groups of anash.

2) Recite Tehillim every day specifically for this purpose, in such a way that the entire Tehillim is completed once by the Yahrtzeit.

3) Give tzedakah every day until the Yahrtzeit (excluding Shabbos, of course) "before davening or after it, in *prutot*—that is, in small coins which the Alter Rebbe called *kashkashim*. One should vary the amount from time to time so that it does not become a binding vow, and distribute them afterward to various charities."

In addition to all this, one should study by heart and engrave in one’s memory the maamarim of the Torah of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, hk"m, until the Yahrtzeit—especially the **maamar of the day of histalkus** (the maamar beginning *Basi L’Gani*, Kuntres 5710), whether the entire maamar or a part of it. Through this, his Torah will dwell within him even when he is occupied with worldly matters.

It is understood that whoever increases in all of the above—is increased for from Above.

I look forward to hearing good news regarding all of the above.

**M. Schneerson**

## 553

B"H, 9 Teves, 5711

Greetings and blessings!

I have received your letters from the 1st and 2nd of Chanukah, in which you ask for a remedy and teshuvah for your transgressions and sins.

The first condition for a remedy and teshuvah is complete regret for the past and a firm resolution for the future not to return to such folly again. From here on, as a remedy and teshuvah, you should establish for yourself set times for reciting the letters of the Torah, Tehillim, and Zohar. Naturally, this is in addition to the regular study sessions that every single Jew must take upon themselves, without a vow.

Furthermore, you should be diligent in reciting *Amen, yehei shmei rabba*, *Kedushah*, and *Barechu*. Most importantly, strive to influence the children of Israel, bringing them close to the love of Hashem Yisbarach, to the love of His holy Torah, and to the love of a fellow Jew—for each and every one of them is a child of Hashem our G-d.

I am certain you will inform me of your progress in all of this.

Please also inform me if you are studying in the yeshivah.

With blessings for a proper teshuvah and for success in your studies,

**Menachem Schneerson**

## 454

[9 Teves]

...Your letter from 16 Kislev was received in due time. I read the *pidyon nefesh* that was enclosed with it at the *tziyun hakadosh*.

I was very pleased to hear of your learning *Chassidus* in the *beis knesses*. Heaven forbid that you should stop this. Surely there are, and will be, further activities. You must make an effort to broaden the circle of listeners, and ensure that young people attend as well.

Seemingly, the dissemination of *Chassidus* should be your primary *avodah*, rather than the collection of funds.

The essence and the beginning of the *tikkun*—for *chassidim*—is to bring the youth closer to *yiras shamayim* and the observance of *Torah u’mitzvos*, and to increase the recitation of the letters of Torah and *tefillah*, with the former being the primary focus...

## 455

B"H, 9 Teves, 5711, Brooklyn

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, and distinguished, etc., Rabbi Meir, may he live, Hakohen

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of 10 Kislev, I was delighted to hear of your good work in the field of proper chinuch. Surely you will continue to increase your efforts in this, and you are aware of the statement of our Sages: "Open for Me an opening the size of a needle's eye, and I will open for you an opening the size of a hall." Through the initial action of *is'arusa d'lesata* (arousal from below), one is assisted greatly so that the efforts will be successful and he will see good fruit from his labor.

I read the *pidyon nefesh* and the list that were enclosed in your letter, as you requested, at the *tziyun* of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, on Erev Rosh Chodesh Teves. A *tzaddik* who has departed, who is found in this world even more than during his lifetime, surely gave his blessing, and may Hashem fulfill it in both material and spiritual matters...

I will conclude with my blessing for the entry of your son, Shlomo, may he live, into *cheder*—may you merit to raise him to Torah, to the *chuppah*, and to good deeds, with abundance, as explained in the teachings of Chassidus. May there be fulfilled in him that which is written in *Midrash Tanchuma, Parshas Kedoshim*, on the verse "And you shall plant all manner of trees for food"—it speaks of a young child, etc. "And in the fourth year all its fruit shall be holy"—this refers to the father sanctifying him to Torah, "praises to Hashem"—what are these praises? From the time he begins to praise the Holy One, blessed be He. "And in the fifth year you shall eat of its fruit"—from the time he begins to read Torah, "that it may yield unto you the increase thereof"—from here our Sages taught: "At five years old [one begins] the study of Scripture," etc. See also the *Hilchos Talmud Torah* of the Alter Rebbe at the beginning, and in *Likutei Torah* on the aforementioned verse.

Enclosed is the *kuntres* for Chanukah along with the general letter pertaining to it. Although it is a bit late, in truth its content is relevant for the entire year.

With blessings for proper organization and that you bring good tidings soon,

**Menachem Schneerson**

**Rabbi Meir:** Zarchi.

## 459

B”H, the Tenth of Teves—may Hashem turn it into joy and gladness speedily—5711, Brooklyn

Greetings and blessings!

I am sure you received my letter from yesterday, and enclosed is the *kuntres* for the 9th of Teves, which was only just brought from the bindery.

Regarding your telegram concerning your health: in my opinion, there is no reason to be concerned at all. You should follow the doctors’ instructions, as the Torah has granted the physician permission to heal, and I am sure you will follow their guidance. However, in my opinion, you should be extra careful to observe the three *shiurim* that are equal for every soul, which my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, established: the *parsha* of the *Chumash* with Rashi every day, *Tehillim* as divided for the days of the month, and *Tanya* as divided for the days of the year, as brought in the *Moreh Shiur* and in *Hayom Yom*. And before sleeping, you should study—for the sake of reading through, not for deep analysis—one of the *maamarim* or *sichos* of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory; the quantity does not matter, as long as you complete a topic. I am confident that after all this, you will inform me very soon that you have returned to your strength and are occupied with your affairs with peace of mind and physical well-being.

While I was at the *tziyun* of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, yesterday, I mentioned you for a blessing.

My wife, the Rabbanit, and my family send their regards, and I await good news soon.

**Menachem Schneerson**

A telegram was sent to him today, which reads: "I have written, with blessings for a speedy recovery, M. S."

I trust you are keeping the Chitas study schedule, and that your wife, tichyeh, gives to tzedakah before lighting the Shabbos candles.

With blessings, and awaiting good news,

**Menachem Schneerson**

## 458

458

B"H, 11 Teves, 5711, Brooklyn

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter dated 26 Kislev:

(1) You inform me that you are a teacher for students in a Talmud Torah in an advanced grade, and that you wished to leave this work to enter as a student in the holy Yeshiva "Ohalei Yosef Yitzchok Lubavitch," but the director, the esteemed and G-d-fearing man, who engages in communal needs with faith, etc., R' M. [Lipsker] shlita, prevented you from doing so.

You did well to continue in the work of chinuch, teaching the Torah of Hashem, may He be exalted and elevated. Since, as per your letter, you visit our holy Yeshiva several times a week and hear words of Chassidus, then according to the statement of our Sages (Temurah 15a), your teaching as an instructor will lead to better understanding and a quicker grasp in your own studies. Furthermore, as a teacher, you have merited the "ray of light" to bring the hearts of the children of Yisrael closer to their Father in Heaven. And what can compare or equal the great nachas ruach that you cause Above, on high, through this?

(2) You also write that for three years you have felt pain at times, and according to your account, the doctors you have visited have not found a cure for it.

In my opinion, you should visit a specialist in internal medicine and a specialist in nerves (nerven), and endeavor that they consult with one another and provide you with instructions for your conduct. And the observance of the three daily study portions established by my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory—namely: reciting Tehillim every day as divided for the days of the month; Chumash with Rashi (on Sunday, the portion of the week until Sheni; on Monday, from Sheni until Shlishi, etc.); and studying Tanya as divided for the days of the year—these are broad vessels to draw down a blessing for a speedy recovery.

(3) You also ask whether you should consider a shidduch with your brother's daughter. In general, it is worthwhile to also look into other suggestions, and afterwards compare them to the suggestion with your brother's daughter, tichyeh. May Hashem guide you on the straight path so that you may choose your zivug in a good and successful hour. Recite Psalm 71 of Tehillim every day, and continue doing so until the upcoming 12 Tammuz.

I would be interested to know what the curriculum is that you teach in the Talmud Torah, how many students are in your class, and whether you teach them dinim and matters of yiras shamayim.

With blessings for a speedy recovery and proper arrangement,

**Menachem Schneerson**

#### ***458***

**R' M.:** Lipsker.

## 449

B"H, 11 Teves, 5711, Brooklyn

To the esteemed avreich, G-d-fearing and so on, R' [Name] shlita,

Peace and blessing!

I received your letter of 10 Kislev in due time, in which you inform me that, in your opinion, the condition of your daughter [Name] tichyeh is serious, and you ask that I pray on her behalf. You conclude by committing yourself, the moment she recovers completely, to becoming a Jew who observes the religion.

I did not answer you immediately due to the multitude of pressures, though when I was at the tziyun of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, I mentioned your daughter tichyeh with a request for a speedy recovery. He surely granted his blessing. Furthermore, your brother-in-law shlita has informed me that your daughter’s condition has improved, and I hope that you will soon be able to inform me that she has returned to full health.

Although you write in your letter that you are a freethinker, I nevertheless address you with the title "G-d-fearing man," for as we have heard more than once from my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, he would call a Jewish person a "G-d-fearing man" because that is his nature. In his words: "A Jew—neither can he nor does he want to be detached from Elokus." It is only that sometimes, due to external factors, he may imagine that he is not G-d-fearing, chas v'shalom, or as you write in your letter, that you are a freethinker.

We see in nature that in order to perceive the inner essence of a person's soul, it is generally brought about through a shock, which can occur in two ways: 1) through an unfortunate event, chas v'shalom, or 2) through an extraordinary matter of joy. Through both of these, the soul is shaken, the external garments fall away, and its purity and inner essence are revealed.

In your case, this inner essence was revealed through the matter of your daughter’s illness, tichyeh. May it be His will that from here on, this inner essence remains revealed, and if it be His will that the "inner essence of the inner essence" also be revealed, may this come about through matters and events of joy.

I hope to hear good news from you soon regarding your daughter’s health, tichyeh, and regarding your affairs in general.

With blessing, that you may share good news in a revealed and revealed way soon,

**Menachem Schneerson**

I am currently preparing it for publication.

- At that time, I mentioned to my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, that there are some Chassidim who are complaining to me about my proposal to print this *Pelach HaRimon*, saying that we have nothing but the Torah of our *Nesi'im*, the *Nesi'ei Chabad*. My father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, dismissed these complaints and **commanded** that this book be printed. -

## 461

B"H, 11 Teves, 5711, Brooklyn

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter from the 8th of Chanukah, I was pleased to hear of the *kvius itim* (fixed times) you have for Torah study. However, you must also add *kvius itim* for the study of Chassidus. A suitable time for this is at least on Mondays, Thursdays, and Shabbos Kodesh, so that three days do not pass without the *pnimiyus haTorah* (inner dimension of Torah). And whoever adds, they add to him. Surely you are aware of what is written in several places, that a *shochet* must be exceptionally *yirei shamayim* (G-d-fearing). (See also *Shu"t Tzemach Tzedek, Yoreh Deah, Siman 12*).

It is very good that you guard against fatigue when you must go to perform your work, the work of *shechitah*. May it be His will that everything should be in order, and that you will be able to share good news regarding your affairs in general, and that you be blessed with *zera chaya vekayama* (living and enduring offspring) in particular.

With blessings to you and your household, may they live and be well,

**Menachem Schneerson**

## 862

B"H, 12 Teves, 5711, Brooklyn

The esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, learned, and distinguished, etc., R' Chanoch Hendel, may he live.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of 2 Teves, conveying the news that your daughter, Malka Yehudis, may she live, has given birth to a daughter, in a good and auspicious hour, I hereby send my blessing of Mazal Tov, Mazal Tov. May her parents raise her to Torah, to the chuppah, and to good deeds, in a state of abundance.

Surely you have already named her; it is surprising that you did not mention this, as the instruction of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, is well-known. It is based on an incident involving the instruction of the Alter Rebbe to the Mitteler Rebbe: one should not wait to name a newborn daughter until Shabbos Kodesh, but rather, one should name her at the first opportunity for a Torah reading, contrary to what is brought in books of customs to wait several days.

I sign with a blessing that you derive nachas from this granddaughter, may she live, and from all your descendants, in both material and spiritual matters, and that you always hear only good news, all the days.

**Menachem Schneerson**

## 453

15 Teves, 5711
Brooklyn

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of 27 Kislev:

I read and re-read your letter, and I could not believe my eyes. Hashem has placed you in a most fortunate position, without any effort on your part, and has merited you to know of the teachings of Chassidus and even to study them. Yet, you stand in doubt as to whether you should study this "Torah of life"—the inner dimension of Torah and the light within Torah, the hidden aspect of Torah that connects the hidden aspect of Yisrael with the hidden aspect of Hashem—and you even provide several justifications for this.

Hashem has orchestrated various circumstances until it fell to your lot to educate the children of Yisrael in the ways of Chassidus—that is, to instill in them vitality, warmth, and light—yet you again hesitate as to whether you should continue this avodah, and for this, too, you already have "reasons of holiness" at the ready.

You received a clear instruction from my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, to learn the craft of shechitah (and it is evident from your own letter that you are well-suited for this), yet you are in doubt as to whether you should do so, and naturally, there is no shortage of reasons for this either.

And in place of all the above, you are thinking about amulets, people who claim to read faces, palmistry, fortune tellers, those who administer lashes, and so on and so forth.

"Days are fashioned"—and it is explained in the teachings of Chassidus that every person is given a set number of days to fulfill the mission of the Ribono shel Olam in this world. Every hour and day spent on matters that are not one's own is a deficiency in the fulfillment of that mission. On the other hand, Hashem does not come with unreasonable demands upon His creatures; since He has entrusted you with a mission, He has certainly granted you the strength to carry it out.

If you will listen to my voice, you will abandon all these fortune tellers, diviners, sorcerers, and the like.

More than this: for the next few weeks, you should divert your mind from thinking about your spiritual state—that you have doubts in faith (which is certainly not the case, for you are a believer, the son of a believer), that you lack the power of concentration in thought (which is nothing but the laziness of the nefesh habehamis, which does not wish to exert itself), that you are empty of Torah (the remedy for which is Torah study, not sadness and dwelling on idle thoughts), that you require "rectifications" (which, according to Chassidus, are accomplished through teshuvah, tefillah, Torah, and tzedakah, not through amulets and lashes), and so on.

During the coming weeks, be joyful that you have merited to be among those called "children to Hashem your G-d," that you have merited to grow up in the "tent of Torah" (and not among those who sit on street corners), and that you have merited to see the lights of the inner dimension of Torah and to cleave to the "Tree of Life." Remember what the Rambam rules in Hilchos Deos (Chapter 4, Halacha 1): that maintaining a healthy and sound body is among the ways of Hashem. Maintain your position in the yeshivah if, in the opinion of the administration, you are capable of it. Your study should be aloud, either from a book or in writing. After studying for a reasonable amount of time, take a break of five or ten minutes (to rest or to contemplate the content of what you have studied), and only then continue. If it does not contradict the above, study the craft of shechitah (and also nikur, if they are relevant to one another in Eretz Yisrael, may it be rebuilt and established). Take an interest in a shidduch if one is suggested to you. Keep the Chitas lessons as explained in the introduction to Hayom Yom and the Moreh Shiur. Recite the daily chapter of Tehillim until 12 Tammuz, may it come upon us for good. Give a small coin to tzedakah daily until that day. Do not eat or drink for about an hour before sleeping. Before going to sleep, study at least a few minutes of the teachings of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory. All of this, of course, is without a vow.

When you encounter one of the yeshivah students or someone from the religious youth, explain to him how the teachings of Chassidus are like a fountain of living waters, the light within Torah that can return every person to the proper path. In our days, studying it is an obligation and a holy merit **for all the children of Yisrael**.

Seek ways to bring closer to the avodah of Hashem those youth who are currently distant from Torah and mitzvos.

If that scoundrel bothers you again by troubling you with thoughts about yourself, remember immediately that you are a servant of the Ribono shel Olam, and that your avodah is to return His children to the proper path—and your time is not your own.

With blessings, awaiting confirmation of the receipt of this letter.

**Menachem Schneerson**

## 764

B"H, 15 Teves, 5711, Brooklyn

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letters from the days of Thursday, 14 Kislev and 26 Kislev...

3) It is in vain to worry (one must make an effort, but worry is destructive)... In general, it would be worthwhile to publicize among Anash the passage from the Zohar regarding the damage caused by worry. It is in Parshas Tetzaveh, 184b: "Come and see, the lower world, etc." See there. For in addition to the confusion it causes in one’s avodah, in Torah study, in physical health, etc., it also causes damage, Heaven forbid, to the very matter about which one is worrying. And this is understood.

4) I received a letter from [Name] that he has already begun making efforts regarding... and "his donkey is his master's, and he is indebted to him" (since he is a person with free choice! As explained in Sefer HaMitzvos of the Tzemach Tzedek, Mitzvas Milah).

5) Regarding what you wrote about your conversation with several of the residents of... concerning the laying of Tefillin (surely you also showed them the printed material from the Meluchah in English on this subject), and they acted brazenly toward you, etc. — see on this subject in Toras Shalom — know that since they acted brazenly (and did not pass by with indifference or silence, etc.), this is the beginning of the activity (see Kuntres HaTefillah, Chapter 8, and Toras Shalom there regarding the virtue of an ox over a goat). You must find the right words and the appropriate time to continue the conversation with them in this vein, and only in this vein—namely, that the mitzvah of Tefillin is fulfilled by the act of laying them, while the matter of prayer is a separate thing. I am confident that in time they will lay Tefillin, and afterwards they will draw closer to other matters of Torah and mitzvos.

6) Thank you, thank you for the news regarding the farbrengen of Yud-Tes Kislev, and surely you also gathered on the fifth night of Chanukah. Please write about this as well. Please, I beg you, make every effort—you and your entire group—to conquer the "outside." And if, for the moment, there is a lack of motivation, let them contemplate that this is what delays the Geulah, Techiyas HaMeisim, and the opportunity to see the Rebbe, my father-in-law, and the Rebbe, his father, etc., etc. Truly, do you not yearn for this? Is there any effort that would be too difficult for them, provided they could attain this? And these are matters to be taken literally, not as a mere figure of speech.

7) Regarding the fact that due to the danger and the decree of the government, your parents were buried without taharah: given the situation as you describe it, their honor was maintained in that manner. Nevertheless, since you have asked—in my opinion: a) You should go to the gravesite with two upright individuals and tell them that you are giving charity on their behalf, and ask them to convey to your father, [Name], and your mother, [Name], that you are asking for their forgiveness regarding the aforementioned, as you were under duress. b) You should resolve, G-d willing, to study on the yahrtzeit of your father and mother, in addition to your regular studies, Maseches Mikvaos and Chassidus. c) Be careful to honor those from whom you have heard a Torah thought—and the main thing is to cast off melancholy, as mentioned above.

Best regards to the entire group,

**Menachem Schneerson**

## 465

B"H, 17 Teves, 5711, Brooklyn

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, and distinguished individual, who engages in communal needs, etc.,
Mr. Aryeh Leib Gelman

Greetings and blessings,

I recall the words of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, regarding you: that although you stand at the head of a political party, you possess the ability to rise above party lines when it comes to a question that concerns our people as a whole—a question of the utmost importance. It is upon these words that I rely in writing this letter.

It is surely unnecessary to draw your attention to the state of education for the children and youth immigrating to our Holy Land, may it be rebuilt and established, and the magnitude of the pain and danger inherent in this issue—a danger that you, without a doubt, also feel in your heart. Surely it has not escaped your notice that, as bad as the situation was in the past, it has deteriorated even further since the children were moved to the ma'abarot (transit camps).

There are problems, and then there are problems.

There are problems that concern passing and transient matters; there are problems of a broader scope; and there are those that touch not only upon our generation, but upon future generations as well.

There are problems that concern external matters, and there are those that concern internal matters, or even vital matters upon which our very existence depends.

And although various problems—some of them urgent—are on the agenda, the aforementioned issue of education takes precedence, as it concerns the very existence of our people, which depends on its religious and moral state (for even the study of ethics is rooted in religion), and it concerns not only our generation, but the generations to come.

It is self-evident that while peace is great in all matters, and the Torah commands us to initiate peace, one must not make this issue of the children’s education a total sacrifice upon the altar of peace.

After this introduction, with which I am certain you agree, I wish to express my great astonishment at the prolonged silence on the part of those under your influence in general, and on your part in particular, regarding the issue of the education of the children immigrating to our Holy Land. Even if, from time to time, a protest has been heard from your side in public, until now that protest has not resulted in any practical action to improve the situation.

My bewilderment grew even greater when I read in the press about the Mizrachi convention in Atlantic City. Although a few speakers touched upon this issue, when it came time for resolutions, the entire matter was passed over in complete silence—as if the question had been resolved properly, or as if the situation were beyond hope, Heaven forbid.

I hope, based on the words of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, mentioned above, that you will rise above party limitations in this matter and exert all your efforts to do everything possible to rectify the terrible situation prevailing in the education of the immigrant children, and to fulfill your duty and your share in saving tens of thousands of sons and daughters of Israel from the terrible danger hovering over them—the danger of heresy, may the Merciful One save us.

And if this letter of mine assists in bringing this ability of yours from potential into action—that will be my reward.

With blessings,

**Menachem Schneerson**

Through this, one also creates the keilim to receive the brachos that he surely wishes to bestow upon those who are mekushar to him and his helpers, that they and their households may be blessed with all good things, both materially and spiritually.

**Menachem Schneerson**

## 477

By the Grace of Hashem, 17 Teves, 5711, Brooklyn

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, and upright R' Aharon Hakohen, may he live:

Greetings and blessings!

Your brother, our dear friend, the esteemed, G-d-fearing, and upright R' Yaakov Hakohen, may he live, forwarded to us your check for $100, which you sent according to my discretion. I have distributed this into four parts: *Maamad*, work in Africa, *Lishkas Chashaim*, and *Merkaz L’Inyonei Chinuch*. You will receive the receipts with this letter.

Regarding *Maamad*, *Merkaz L’Inyonei Chinuch*, and *Lishkas Chashaim*, I will refrain from writing to you, as you are surely familiar with the work. I would like to pause here to focus on the new area of our work in Africa, which I am certain you will be pleased to become acquainted with.

A few weeks before the *histalkus* of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, when the conversation turned to the work of *Merkaz L’Inyonei Chinuch* through the *Lishkas Haplitim* in Europe, my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, said to me: Since there is a large community of Jews in North Africa, with many boys and girls—may they increase—and since the poverty there is, G-d forbid, very great, it results that the majority of them cannot receive any education, even though they are all *yirei-shamayim* to the highest degree. Therefore, we must begin to work there, especially since the cost of living there is relatively low, and with small amounts of money, one can accomplish great things. Needless to say, "whoever sustains one soul of Israel, it is as if he sustained an entire world."

Based on these instructions from my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, we immediately began to investigate the situation in North Africa. At the beginning of the summer, we sent our representative there to become acquainted with the situation on the ground. In the middle of the summer, our representative traveled there, and our work began to prepare the ground, organize educational institutions suitable for that country, and so on. Our representative is still there, managing the work on a permanent basis.

Needless to say, the work is greatly hindered by the lack of funds, and the heart aches even more when one considers that with a few dollars more, one could have accomplished so much more. For example, the education of one child for a month costs about eight to nine dollars in the *yeshiva*, and one to one-and-a-half dollars in the *Talmud Torah*. This includes the expenses for a *melamed*, rent, and providing food once or twice a day.

However, despite the lack of funds, and remembering the instructions of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, we have taken out various loans. As is known, we already have there a *Beis Medrash L’Morim* (to train *melamdim* from the local population, so that the children will not have difficulties with the language); a *Yeshiva Gedola*; a *Yeshiva Ketana*; a *Talmud Torah* for boys; a *Talmud Torah* for girls; and evening *shiurim* for tradesmen and employees who are occupied during the day. We are also conducting negotiations regarding opening an entire network of *Talmud Torahs* in 20 to 30 cities.

All the institutions that we have founded there, and which we will, with the help of Hashem, yet found, bear the general name **"Ohalei Yosef Yitzchak Lubavitch."** One sees at every step how the work is, thank G-d, proceeding with success, and how the Rebbe, my father-in-law, of blessed memory, is leading it even now. We will surely all enjoy the great merit of participating in this work and will do our duty, with the help of Hashem.

I hope that everything is going well with you. I ask you to convey my regards to Mr. Yitzchak Shpalter (I replied to his letter some time ago), as well as to your butcher, Mr. Rivkin.

I hope to hear good news from you.

With blessings,

**Menachem Schneerson**

Enclosed is the *kuntres* that was published not long ago for 9 Teves, the day the eleven months of the *histalkus* concluded, as well as a letter that pertains to the *kuntres*.

## 768

[15 Teves 5711]

...All twelve months of this year of passing* are most auspicious for strengthening our hiskashrus with our Nasi, the Rebbe, of blessed memory.

And participating in this completion of the Shas—a **takanah that the Rebbe, of blessed memory, exerted himself to strengthen and disseminate**—will, in addition to the other matters involved, also add strength to our aforementioned hiskashrus, to walk in the paths he taught us and to follow in his ways forever and ever.

#### 768

Printed in Igros Kodesh Vol. 4, p. 1166; Vol. 11, p. 215. **Regarding the completion of Torah:** See Rema in Shulchan Aruch, Orach Chaim 669—and this is discussed at length in the commentaries (Magen Avraham, 3)—regarding the Written Torah. It is the custom of Yisrael to celebrate with extra joy at the completion of the Shas compared to the completion of a single masechta, even though the latter is also a seudas mitzvah (ibid., Rema 551:10).

**Regarding the study of the masechta, etc.:** There are several examples of this, one of which is: According to Reish Lakish, a "half-measure" (chatzi shiur) is permitted, but if one **intends** to complete it, it is forbidden (Yerushalmi, Terumos 6:1)—and see Shaar HaYichud VeHaEmunah, beginning of Chapter 12.

## 669

B.H., Erev Shabbos Kodesh, 21 Teves, 5711, Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed Chossid, the distinguished scholar, etc., R’ Y.Y., shliach:

Shalom u’vracha!

Enclosed is the booklet for the upcoming 24th of Teves, the day of the Hillula of Rabbeinu HaZaken. I request that you facilitate the spreading of this merit among the public, and exert effort to organize a *Chayukas HaShas* in your location and camp, whether independently or by joining with those in other places, as explained in the booklet.

It can be said that in such an arrangement, there are several aspects: a) The *Talmud Torah* of the specific tractate one has taken upon himself. b) Just as the study of the entire Shas is greater than the mere sum of the study of the individual tractates contained within it—which is why a new element is added, the *seudah* and joy that are performed specifically upon the completion of Torah—so too, the study of a tractate as part of the study of the entire Shas is greater than the study of that tractate in isolation. c) By participating with others who are taking part in the *Chayukas HaShas*, one has a connection to their study as well, and it is as if he has studied the entire Shas. d) Through the aforementioned participation, perhaps it can be said that it is considered like study in a group of ten or more, the merit of which is greater than study in isolation. e) Before studying, one can acquire merit and give a portion of his *Talmud Torah* to others (*Shulchan Aruch, Yoreh Deah* 246), and in this case, the desire of each participant is for the merit of the study of the entire Shas, and consequently, he transfers and grants merit to every other participant through his study.

May it be the will of Hashem that through the fulfillment of this *takanah* of the *Baal HaHillula*, the "Root of our souls will illuminate with light and abundant influence in his merit, to shield and protect our souls, for us and for all of Israel, from the Source of Life and the Life of Life, to elevate them higher and higher, level after level, and to bind them with a firm and strong bond to the One Hashem, through the Torah, by which Israel is bound to the *Kudsha Brich Hu*."

Especially in this year of the passing of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, when, in the words written by the sons of Rabbeinu HaZaken, "Glory has been taken from our house of life, our crown of splendor, the pride of Israel, the ornament of glory," until the time that in our days, Hashem "will send us the righteous Redeemer and lead us from darkness to light, and those who dwell in the dust will awaken and sing, and He will cause us to hear wonders from our Torah, the perfect Torah of Hashem that restores the soul. Amen, may it be His will."

**M. Schneerson**

***

To the esteemed Chossid, the activist, the distinguished scholar, etc., R’ S. Jacobson, shliach:

I was pleased to read in your letter from some time ago regarding the countries you visited, that you are interested in the state of Yiddishkeit there and are striving to improve it—even though, for several reasons, I did not reply at the time. Certainly, you should continue to do so in the future, and also write your suggestions regarding the above, within the realm of what is possible. Without a vow, I will see what I can do in this matter.

I trust you remain in contact with those you spoke with, even now, and continue to arouse them from time to time as necessary.

How have the brother and sister who were redeemed from among the nations settled in?

***

I received your letters in due time, and when I am at the holy *tziyun*, I will mention you, etc., as discussed.

Regarding your situation and the concerns that you have: in my opinion, a shadow of mountains appears to you as mountains. Especially since "even the mountains shall move," etc. And from Heaven, he was appointed—so what can a human being do to him? See *Zohar Chadash*, Vol. 3, 184b: "Come and see," etc.

I look forward to hearing good news soon.

## 770

B"H, 22 Teves, 5711, Brooklyn

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, and distinguished, etc., R' A.A., may he live:

Greetings and blessings!

Your letter dated Sunday, Parshas Shemos, 15 Teves, was received. I was distressed to hear from your letter that your father, the esteemed Chossid, etc., has passed away. May Hashem grant that from now on you know no further sorrow or distress, and may you always hear only of goodness and kindness all the days.

Enclosed is the receipt for the sum sent by your mother’s sister’s sons for the *ilui neshamah* of your father, of blessed memory. As per your letter, it has been delivered to Merkos L'Inyonei Chinuch...

I hope that soon you will share good news regarding the improvement of your wife’s health, may she live, that it is steadily getting better.

With blessings that you hear only good news,

**Menachem Schneerson**

Enclosed is a booklet for 24 Teves, along with my general letter pertaining to it; I am sure you will publicize them in an appropriate manner.

Regarding your question as to whether it is customary to set up two chairs at a *bris milah*: The *Sefer Minhagim* "Kesser Shem Tov," page 574, section 31, states: "The custom in Eretz Yisrael, Sefard, Amsterdam, and all the cities of the West is to prepare two chairs, one for Eliyahu and the second for the *sandak*, and they are placed side by side. In London, they prepare one chair for both." And in the book *Darchei Chaim V'Shalom* (a collection of Munkatch customs), section 619, it writes: "That which is explained in *Derech Pikudecha* (on the mitzvah of *milah*, letter 13) that the chair should be divided and appear as two—one for Eliyahu HaNavi and one for the *sandak* (and see also *Rokeach*, section 113)—our Rebbe was not particular about this, only that it be wide." However, in the *Zohar* (Vol. I, 93a), it is somewhat implied that two chairs are necessary, as it writes "a different chair." Now, as to what our custom is, I have not heard clearly, but it seems **highly probable** that when I was present at a *bris milah* where my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, was the *sandak* (in Warsaw), there was only **one** chair.

## 771

B"H, 23 Teves, 5711, Brooklyn

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your question regarding a shidduch and your future spouse: before you become engaged, you must be certain that your home will be built upon the foundations of Torah and mitzvos. This means that not only you, but your chassan as well, must take upon yourselves with full commitment the promise to observe the mitzvos and for the chassan to establish fixed times for Torah study. It is understood that this promise must be made with sincerity and truth, for the happiness of a Jewish man and woman depends upon this. If, in addition to this, you feel an inclination of the heart toward this shidduch, then you may proceed with the proposal, and may it be in a good and auspicious hour.

I am interested to know who your family members are—that is, the occupation of your parents, long may they live, and the situation of your household, etc.

With blessings,

**Menachem Schneerson**

## 772

772

B"H, 23 Teves, 5711, Brooklyn

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter from Thursday, Parshas Vayechi, in which you inform me that you have undergone surgery several times, etc.

Generally, it is a pity that you are concerning yourself and contemplating medical books regarding what you imagine to be your illness. In my opinion, you should do only what the Torah has commanded—namely, to act in practice according to the instructions of the doctors—and occupy your mind and heart, that is, your power of thought, regarding your situation with a strong trust in Hashem, who is the Healer of all flesh and performs wonders. You should not involve yourself in the matters of medical science, for that does not pertain to you, especially if it disturbs your peace of mind and arouses feelings of melancholy. It is a well-known saying that several of the Chabad Nesi'im have stated, and they have said it many times: "Think good and it will be good."

Regarding your recovery: (a) Surely you are following the doctors' instructions; (b) you should divert your attention, as much as possible, from delving into the matter of your health; (c) your trust should be strong in Hashem, for there is no obstacle before Him, and who can say to Him, "What are You doing?"; (d) you should connect yourself with additional connection to the "Tree of Life," which is the study of Chassidus, the words of the Living G-d. This means: regarding yourself, you should set fixed times for the study of Chassidus and increase this as much as possible, in addition to your regular fixed study times. Regarding your shul: you should strive to make the shul a *Chassidishe shul* through classes in the study of Chassidus and frequent *Chassidishe farbrengens*, and you should be among the primary participants. And regarding your wider environment—that is, the Bnei Yisrael—since all Jews are responsible for one another, if something is lacking for one, it can be filled by receiving from another. This is also evident in the human body: if, for some reason, one limb is weakened, it draws vitality and strength to overcome its weakness from the vitality of the other limbs. Therefore, you should print, at your own expense, a *sefer*—not a *kuntres*—of the *maamarim* of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory. Through this, you will influence spiritual vitality into the hearts of many Bnei Yisrael, and they will influence additional physical vitality to you. Do not be alarmed by the expenses involved in printing such a *sefer*, for Hashem will grant you long life and give you the ability to cover the aforementioned printing costs.

May Hashem lengthen your days and years in goodness, and may He add strength and power in the study of Torah and the performance of *mitzvos* with beauty, and may you bring good tidings regarding all of the above.

With blessings,

**Menachem Schneerson**

Enclosed is a receipt from the "Secret Bureau" founded by my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, to help the needy in a secret manner, which is one of the highest levels of *tzedakah*.

All the aforementioned seforim have also been sent to Jerusalem, the Holy City, may it be built and established. Anyone who seeks Chassidus will be able to come there to quench their thirst. Surely, you too will be able to drink thirstily from the seforim of the holy ones of Yisrael and its Nesi'im: the Alter Rebbe, the Mitteler Rebbe, the Tzemach Tzedek, the Rebbe Maharash, the Rebbe Rashab, and my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory.

I am interested to know if you also serve in a rabbinical position in Jerusalem, and what fixed times for Torah study exist in your community, etc.

With blessings,

**Menachem Schneerson**

## 775

B"H, 23 Teves, 5711, Brooklyn

Greetings and blessings!

...In my opinion, it was not the right course of action to stop seeing the doctor. It would be best to be examined by a specialist once more and to follow their instructions.

Regarding what you mentioned about separation, etc., G-d forbid that you should think in such terms—especially since you received a blessing from my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, that you should be blessed with children who are alive and enduring. He is someone who keeps his word. Furthermore, the righteous are even greater after their passing than during their lifetime; the righteous one who has departed is found in this world even more than during his life. You will see that his blessing will be fulfilled, and I look forward to hearing good news regarding this.

You conclude your letter by mentioning that you were forced to stop your public shiurim. It would be good if you could continue them, but you should endeavor to teach them in a way that will not, G-d forbid, weaken your health.

Awaiting good news,

**M. Schneerson**

## 776

B"H, 23 Teves, 5711, Brooklyn

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, and distinguished, etc., R' A. Tz. [Brahall], Shochet u'Bodek,

Greetings and blessings!

...You have surely heard the saying of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, which he stated several times in his holy sichos: that a shochet is not merely a man with a slaughtering knife in his hand — a *skatabayetz* — but rather his role is to influence the city in which he resides, to draw it away from the matters of the body and the animal soul, and to bring it closer to Hashem through ahavas Hashem, ahavas haTorah, and ahavas Yisrael. As our Sages of blessed memory said, "The term *v'shachat* (and he shall slaughter) implies nothing other than *v'mashach* (and he shall draw/attract)."

And this is also true in the simple sense: through the act of shechitah, for when there is *v'zavachta* (and you shall slaughter), then there can be *v'achalta* (and you shall eat), whereby the meat of the animal or bird is transformed into the blood and flesh of a human being—from the expression *adamah l'elyon* (I will be like the Most High). For beloved are Yisrael, who are called children to Hashem, and a special affection is known to them, for they are called children to Hashem. Fortunate is the man who brings about closeness between the son and the Father, and especially such precious children and such a precious Father. Great is this merit to draw down upon him every good, in all that he requires, both materially and spiritually.

With blessings,

**Menachem Schneerson**

Enclosed is the booklet for 24 Teves, along with the letter pertaining to it.

776

Therefore, as it appears from his words, if you wish to arrange the matter, you need to obtain a letter in which it is stated that the rabbis support the matter, etc.

May Hashem grant that the desire of Hashem shall succeed in his hand.

With blessings,

**Menachem Schneerson**

## 778

B"H, 23 Teves, 5711, Brooklyn

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, and distinguished, etc., R' Chaim, may he live:

Greetings and blessings!

I was pleased to receive regards from you in due time through the esteemed Rabbi and Chossid, G-d-fearing and distinguished, etc., R' Avraham, may he live, Simpson. I am certain that in the future you will gladden me with direct letters containing good news regarding [yourself] and your entire family, may they live, and regarding your well-being in both material and spiritual matters. I thank you in advance.

According to what R' Avraham Simpson related, there is a broad field for the dissemination of Chassidus in your camp in Toronto. It is appropriate and necessary that you consult with those suitable for this in your camp, and that you all strive together in the most fitting manner to fulfill the supernal intent that the Ribono shel Olam desired: to have a dwelling place in the lower worlds. The explanation for this in Chassidus is well known: the concept of a "dwelling place" is a location where the person is revealed, without concealment or hiddenness. Regarding the Ribono shel Olam, "no thought can grasp Him at all" except through Torah and mitzvos, for the Torah and the Ribono shel Olam are entirely one. Yet, in the revealed Torah, this is still in a state of concealment. It is specifically through the teachings of Chassidus—which engage in the love and fear of Hashem and in contemplation of His greatness, etc.—that a dwelling place is truly created in the lower worlds.

I await good news, and convey my regards to the entire group, may they live.

**Menachem Schneerson**

Enclosed is a booklet for 24 Teves, along with a general letter pertaining to it.

And surely, all who participate in this holy work will be blessed by my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, with success, both materially and spiritually.

## 880

B"H, 25 Teves, 5711, Brooklyn

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, and distinguished individual, who occupies himself with communal needs, etc.,
R' Moshe HaKohen, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

I was happy to receive regards from you, and I hope that you will always be able to share good news regarding your own well-being and that of your wife, may she live, in both material and spiritual matters.

Enclosed is a booklet published for 24 Teves, as well as a general letter pertaining to it. If you have any comments regarding this, I would be pleased to hear them.

As I have said before, the acronym for *Gabbai* (גבא"י) is: **A**na **B**'choach **G**edulas **Y**eminecha ("We beg, by the power of the greatness of Your right hand"). This means that one who, through the providence of the Creator, may He be blessed, has been chosen to be a *gabbai* in a *beis medrash*, must possess strength through *chesed* (the right hand), and in a manner of supplication (*ana*). That is to say, his influence should be powerful, but at the same time, he must utilize it through the attribute of *chesed*—to make the *beis medrash* a *chassidishe shul* and to illuminate and warm the entire environment.

Awaiting good news,

With blessing,

**Menachem Schneerson**

Enclosed is a receipt from Merkos L'Inyonei Chinuch for your contribution. Surely you will continue to strive, with added vigor, to participate in this holy work in a manner that will satisfy my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory. Through this, you will also create vessels for receiving his benevolent influence in both material and spiritual matters.

Enclosed is the letter you sent me—after I have made copies of it. Many thanks for this.

B"H, 25 Teves, 5711, Brooklyn

I am certain that you will continue to stand on guard to expedite the process with the Immigration authorities and others involved in this matter. May it be the will of Hashem that the desire of Hashem shall succeed in his hand to help the aforementioned reach their place of rest and inheritance.

I was very pleased to read that you keep in your memory the words of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, that a person is given the strengths to rectify and elevate his surroundings. This memory itself will assist you in bringing from potential into action the strengths you possess to act and influence your environment, to bring them closer to Yiddishkeit, to illuminate them with the light of Torah, and to warm them with the warmth of the teachings of Chassidus, which is the "light" within the Torah.

The main thing is to remain strong in your trust in Hashem. Since you made your journey to this country with the agreement and blessing of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, He assumes the responsibility, and with the appropriate hishtadlus, you will surely succeed in all of the above. Do not be anxious about what you describe—in your own words—as being surrounded by material debts in addition to spiritual obligations, which are the duty of the place upon you. For "he who lends to Hashem favors the poor," and since you have incurred debts in order to favor the poor—whether in spiritual or material matters—then Hashem is the borrower, and consequently, you can be certain that the debt will be repaid in full.

As you requested, I will mention you and your wife, may they live, and the esteemed Rabbi and Chossid, etc., Moreinu Harav... at the holy resting place. Surely the *tzaddik* who has departed, who is found in this world more than during his lifetime, will bestow his blessing, and may Hashem fulfill it in both material and spiritual matters.

Enclosed is the Kuntres for 9 Teves, the booklet for 24 Teves, and the general letters pertaining to them.

Although these dates have already passed, the matters themselves are timely at all times.

With blessings for success and regards to your family, may they live, and to your entire group, may they live,

**M. Schneerson**
