## 843

B"H, 26 Teves, 5711, Brooklyn

To the esteemed Rabbi and Chossid, G-d-fearing and learned, possessing noble character traits, etc., Moreinu HaRav R. N. shlita,

Peace and blessing!

I have received your two letters. Thank you for the discussion and analysis in the first one regarding a spring that has ceased to flow.

Regarding what you wrote in the second letter—that the Gadol of Minsk instructed that Kaddish be recited after him specifically by a son [who is a] *ben chacham*—it is worth noting what is written in the sefer *Mishmeres Shalom*, that in such a case one should heed the words of the deceased. If so, it would imply that there is no disgrace to the mourner in this, [even if it implies] that his father was wicked (Sanhedrin 46b). Yet, it is a matter that requires further study, as we see clearly that this is not the case. See also *Shulchan Aruch* 20:30.

Enclosed is the booklet for 24 Teves, as well as a copy of my letter pertaining to this, which I hope will be of interest to you, shlita.

Also enclosed is the receipt for your donation to the Merkos L'Inyonei Chinuch. May it be the will of Hashem that you be blessed with the blessing of the Alter Rebbe (in the beginning of *Torah Or*), that through the mitzvah of tzedakah, one’s mind and heart become purified a thousand times over—and see the *hagah* (gloss) to this *drush* in *Likutei Torah* regarding the three parshiyos that pertain to "this, so, and thus."

As you requested, I mentioned you for what you need when I was at the Tziyun of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, *ztzukulleh"h, nbg"m, zye"a, h"k"m*. And a *tzaddik* who has departed, who is found in this world even more than during his lifetime, will surely bestow his blessing, and may the Ribono shel Olam fulfill it in both material and spiritual matters.

With blessings to you and your Torah,

**Menachem Schneerson**

## 884

B”H, Rosh Chodesh Shevat, 5711, Brooklyn, N.Y.

To Anash, the Talmidei HaTemimim, and all those close to Chassidus and Chassidim in every place, may Hashem grant them life.

Peace and blessing!

As we approach the great and holy day, the tenth of Shevat, the yom hilula of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory—I wish to call your attention to the maamar he instructed to be printed for the day of his passing, the maamar entitled *Basi L’Gani*—10 Shevat 5750.

I am certain that you will study it on the night and day of the hilula.

In the words of our Nasi in his letters (Kuntres 3, Kuntres 36):

This day is *mesugal* (propitious) to connect to the Tree of Life, so that each and every one of Anash may merit that the merit of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory—who sacrificed and gave his holy soul for us, to guide us in the paths of the *tzaddikei yesod olam*, the glory of our holy forefathers and Rebbes, of blessed memory—should shine upon him and his entire household, may they live, to be blessed with children, life, and abundant sustenance.

Anash and Talmidei HaTemimim, may you live: Awaken and come to the courtyards of Hashem, to the shuls and beis medrashos, for tefillah and for the study of shiurim in public. Gather together with brotherly love to strengthen the study of Torah and to support those who study Torah and engage in the avodah of Hashem.

Anash, Talmidei HaTemimim, and all who take part in the ways of the Chassidim and Chassidus: Stand ready, all of you—you, your wives, your sons, and your daughters—to receive the blessing of Hashem with an abundance of life, good livelihood, and nachas from your descendants. May Hashem bestow this upon you and upon us through the awakening of great mercy from the Source of true mercy and kindness, in the manner of *machnisei rachamim*, which will be awakened by my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, the master of the hilula. May you be blessed with children, life, and abundant sustenance.

**Menachem Mendel Schneerson**

#### 884

This letter and those that follow were printed in *Sefer HaMaamarim 5710*, pp. 5–7, and in *Likkutei Sichos*, Vol. 11, p. 216. "I am hereby": See also the letter of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, regarding the first yahrtzeit of his father, the Rebbe (Rashab), of blessed memory (*Chachmei Yisrael B’Shem Tov*, p. 33).

## 485

B.H., Rosh Chodesh Shevat, 5711, Brooklyn, N.Y.

To Anash, the Talmidei HaTemimim, and all those who are connected or belong to my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, may his merit protect us, may he live [in the World to Come]:

Greetings and blessings!

In response to the questions of many regarding a detailed order for the tenth of Shevat, the upcoming Yahrtzeit of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, I hereby propose the following:

On the Shabbos Kodesh preceding the Yahrtzeit, one should endeavor to receive an aliyah to the Torah.

If there are not enough aliyos, one should read from the Torah in different rooms, but **do not add** to the number of those called up.

One should endeavor that the Maftir be the most distinguished person in the group—with the consent of the majority—or by lottery.

One should choose and appoint those who will lead the davening on the day of the Yahrtzeit. It is proper to divide the honors so that one person leads Maariv, a second leads Shacharis, and a third leads Mincha, in order to allow a greater number of Anash to merit this.

Light a candle that will burn for the entire twenty-four hours. If possible, it should be a beeswax candle.

During the davening, five candles should be lit.

After davening (in the morning, after reciting Tehillim), the person who led the davening should study (complete) the 24th chapter of Keilim and the 7th chapter of Mikvaos. Afterward, he should recite the Mishnah, "Rabbi Chananya ben Akashya..." and Kaddish DeRabbanan.

In a whisper—a few lines of Tanya, and Kaddish DeRabbanan.

After Maariv, one should review a portion of the Maamar of the day of his passing (the Maamar beginning *Basi LeGani*, printed in the Kuntres of the same name) by heart. If there is no one who can recite it by heart, it should be studied from the text. The same should be done after Shacharis.

And complete it after Mincha.

In the morning, before davening—a chapter of Tanya. The same should be done after Mincha.

In the morning, before davening, each person should give a donation to the causes associated with our Nasi, my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, **on his own behalf and on behalf of each member of his household**, and likewise before Mincha.

After Shacharis and the review of the Chassidus, each person should read a Pidyon Nefesh (naturally, while wearing a gartel). Those who merited entering for Yechidus, or at least seeing the face of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, should visualize themselves, while reading the P.N., as if standing before him. Afterward, place the P.N. between the pages of a Maamar, Kuntres, etc., of the teachings of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe. And send it (if possible, **on that very day**) so that it may be read at his gravesite.

During the twenty-four hours—study the chapters of Mishnayos corresponding to the letters of his name.

During the twenty-four hours—hold a farbrengen.

Set aside an hour during the twenty-four hours to explain to one's household about my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, and the avodah he performed throughout his life.

During the twenty-four hours—visit (those who are suited for this) shuls and batei medrash in the city to review a saying or a teaching from my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe; to speak about his love for **every Jew**; to announce and explain his takanah regarding the recitation of Tehillim and the study of Chumash with Rashi—and in appropriate places—also regarding the study of Tanya as divided for the days of the year. If possible, all of the above should be done within the framework of a farbrengen.

During the twenty-four hours—visit (those who are qualified for this) the gatherings of the Chareidi youth—and endeavor, as much as possible through peaceful means, even in places of youth gatherings that are not yet Chareidi—to explain to them the great love that my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, always had for them; to explain to them what he demanded of them, and the hope and confidence he placed in them, that they would ultimately fulfill their role in strengthening Yiddishkeit and spreading Torah with all the energy, warmth, and vitality that are the unique characteristics of youth.

***

It is understood that if it is appropriate for the local conditions, one should continue all of the above in the days following the Yahrtzeit, and especially on the Shabbos following it.

***

May Hashem hasten the coming of our Redeemer, and may those who dwell in the dust awake and sing for joy, and our Nasi, my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, the master of the Hillula, among them, will reveal wonders to us and lead us on the path that ascends to the House of Hashem.

**Menachem Mendel Schneerson**

## 888

888

B"H, Erev Shabbos Kodesh, 5 Shevat, 5711, Brooklyn

To the 7th Annual Conference of the Vaad Megini U’Marhivei HaChinuch HaKasher, under the leadership of Merkos L’Inyonei Chinuch

Greetings and Blessings!

Divine Providence has granted you the merit to participate in the great and important work of the **Vaad** in the field of chinuch, and specifically in the "Hour for Torah Study." Through this—in the words of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory—you have removed, and continue to remove, from thousands of Jewish children the stain of complete ignorance regarding Yiddishkeit. Hundreds of children, boys and girls—may they increase—have begun to receive a kosher chinuch through your positive influence.

The work you are doing in this field is the greatest spiritual charity for those who are "poor in knowledge," and it is a matter of *hatzalas nefashos* in the literal sense. For such a mitzvah, especially one that cannot be performed by others, no self-sacrifice is too great.

I hope that you will strive with all your capabilities to increase and expand your work, to grow the number of children and locations for the "Hours for Torah Study" under your program, in order to bring back those Jewish children who are still alienated to their source in Torah and Yiddishkeit.

I also wish to hope that the widest circles of conscious Jews, men and women, will recognize their **duty** and **privilege** to support your work with all their capabilities.

In the merit of saving the souls of Jewish children, may you and your fellow workers and supporters be blessed by Hashem in your work and in your personal affairs, in everything you need, according to the blessing of the Rebbe, my revered father-in-law, in both material and spiritual matters.

With blessings for great success,

**M. Schneerson**

## 889

B"H, 5 Shevat, 5711, Brooklyn

The distinguished avreich, G-d-fearing and esteemed, etc., Moreinu Harav Yechiel, may he live.

Greetings and blessings!

I was pleased to read in your letter that you are influencing the bochur... may he live, regarding the study of Chassidus. You should certainly not be satisfied with one or two, but **increase** the number of companions for the aforementioned study. In general, you should emphasize that it is impossible to learn Torah without this, specifically in a manner of yiras shamayim. If not, our Sages of blessed memory have already warned (Shabbos 31a): "It would have been better had he not been brought up."

Regarding what you noted concerning the ruling of the Alter Rebbe in his Siddur to pause for *Anenu* and *Barchu*, etc., between *Tefillin Shel Yad* and *Tefillin Shel Rosh*, which differs from what he wrote in his Shulchan Aruch, section 25:

This is one of those matters where the Alter Rebbe’s opinion in his Siddur differs from that in his Shulchan Aruch, and the halacha follows the later authority, which is the **Piskei HaSiddur**. All these variations have been collected in the book *Piskei HaSiddur* by Rabbi Naeh (Jerusalem, 5697).

I will read your *pidyon nefesh* at the holy gravesite.

Awaiting good tidings—and there is no "good" other than Torah and mitzvos—

With blessings,

**Menachem Schneerson**

## 890

B"H, 8 Shevat, 5711, Brooklyn

To my esteemed friend, the distinguished Chossid, G-d-fearing and learned, etc., R' Shneur Zalman, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

I received your letter dated Tuesday, Parshas Va'eira, and I have now also received the letter regarding Perezhitye that you requested your acquaintance to send to me. After reviewing it, I will return it to you, as you wrote in your letter.

The letter regarding the liberation of the Alter Rebbe was also printed in *Beis Rebbe*, but it was from a copy and is inaccurate.

I am enclosing here a booklet of *maamarim* on *hishtatchus* by the brilliant Gaon, the Tzaddik and Chossid, etc., R' Hillel of Paritch, of blessed memory. I have also sent you, in a separate package, the book *Maamarei 5627*, which was just published according to the instructions of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, before his passing.

In my conversation with the esteemed Chossid, etc., R' Shmuel Levitin, may he live, regarding the *maamarim* of my father-in-law, the Rebbe (Rashab), of blessed memory, he pointed out to me that the index which I arranged and printed does not include the *maamarim* that he heard himself. They are: from the year 5659 — *Ki Yishalcha*, *Chag HaPesach*; *Vayehi HeAnan VeHaChoshech*, *Shevi'i Shel Pesach*; *Hodu LaShem Kir'u Vishmo*, *Zimna Chada Itztarich Alma LeMita*, *Im Lo Brisi Yomam VaLaila*, and *Ish Ki Yimrot Rosho*, all between *Chag HaPesach* and *Shavuos*; the *maamar* *Se'u Marom Eineichem*, *Shivchi Yerushalayim Es Hashem*, *Az Tismach Besulah BeMachol* (Shabbos before the birth of my sister-in-law, the Rabbanit Chana, may she live), and *Hashem Berach Es Avraham Bakol*, *Az Tismach Besulah BeMachol* (both on the aforementioned birthday). From the year 5660 — *HaChodesh HaZeh*, *Parshas HaChodesh*; *Refuos Tehi LeSharecha*, *Parshas Emor*; *Refuos Tehi LeSharecha*, *Lag BaOmer*; *Gedolah Torah SheHi Nosenes Lecha Chayim*. He told me that you were also in Lubavitch at that time, and therefore I would like to ask you as well, if you recall that these *maamarim* were delivered at those times. Thank you in advance if you can answer me regarding this.

Perhaps there are other *maamarim* of the Rebbe Rashab, of blessed memory, preserved in your memory that were not included in the index? You surely have the index at hand; if not, please be kind enough to let me know and I will send it to you.

With blessing and regards to your wife, may she live,

**Menachem Schneerson**

## 991

B"H, 8 Shevat, 5711, Brooklyn

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, and pious man, who engages in communal needs, etc.,
R' Dovid Nosson, may he live.

Greetings and blessings!

I was distressed to read in your letter about the fire, *lo aleinu*, that occurred in your apartment. Since I do not know if you have at hand the *Sefer HaMitzvos* of the Tzemach Tzedek (end of page 228), I am copying here a passage from a letter of the Tzemach Tzedek regarding such matters. It reads as follows:

Copy from the holy handwriting of **my grandfather, the Rebbe** (the Tzemach Tzedek), may his soul rest in Eden:

"I heard from the mouths of holy men of old about the common saying that after a fire, one becomes wealthy. This is because the *hishtalshelus* of the holy supernal *midos* and their order is: *Chesed*, *Din*, *Rachamim*. Therefore, after the *midah* of *Din* in a fire, the *midah* of *Rachamim* is awakened, which is greater than the *midah* of *Chesed* that preceded it, as is known. This is the *midah* of Yaakov, an inheritance without boundaries, 'a bar reaching from one end to the other,' etc." — end of the golden words.

See also *Sefer Meah Shearim*, *Igros Kodesh* of the Mitteler Rebbe, letter 7, and of the Tzemach Tzedek, letter 5.

May it be the will [of Hashem] that the aforementioned ruling of the Alter Rebbe, based on the holy men of old, the Mitteler Rebbe, and the Tzemach Tzedek, be fulfilled in you completely, and may you report good news regarding this.

With blessings,

**Menachem Schneerson**

Enclosed is one letter (which you asked to have returned); the rest will be returned, *bli neder*, after they are copied.

## 496

21 Shevat, 5711

To the esteemed Rabbi and Chossid, G-d-fearing and learned, etc.,
Rabbi Shneur Zalman, may he live.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letters of the 15th and 24th of Teves and the 12th of Shevat:

Regarding the matter of Shmittah — according to the information received here, the Charedi settlements in Eretz Yisrael (may it be rebuilt and established) intend not to rely on leniencies, but to observe Shmittah according to Halacha.

It is surprising that you do not mention anything about the rains that finally fell, whether they saved the planting in its entirety or otherwise. Surely you will fill this in your next letter with good tidings regarding this and similar matters.

Regarding your question as to whether one should prevent the custom of delaying the Bris Milah until after Mincha so that it may take place before a large gathering:

While it is true that "the zealous hasten to perform mitzvos" and this generally overrides the principle that "the glory of the King is in the multitude of the people," as is evident from Rosh Hashanah (32b), seemingly, Milah is different. It is preferable that it be held in joy, as they accepted it upon themselves (Shabbos 130a; see also Megillah 16b, Kesubos 8a, and especially Niddah 31b: "**All are joyful**," etc.). This overrides the principle of "the zealous hasten," which is why on Tisha B'Av the Milah is delayed until after Mincha (Shulchan Aruch Orach Chayim, end of 559; the fact that if it falls on Tisha B'Av itself the law is not so, is because the difference in joy is not as great, whereas when it is delayed, he breaks his fast).

In Sdei Chemed (Klalei, Ma'areches Zayin, Klal 3), he cites from Birkei Yosef (Orach Chayim 61), Chayei Adam (Klal 68), Re'eh Chayim (Parshas Lech Lecha), and Lev Chayim (Vol. 2, sec. 27) that one should not delay the Pidyon Haben for this reason, and he writes simply that the same law applies to Milah.

In my humble opinion, they are distinct, as mentioned above. (One cannot argue that, on the contrary, for Milah there should be even greater haste, especially since every moment of delay he remains an *arel* and the *orlah* is repulsive—which would also make the delay on Tisha B'Av difficult—because here it is different: the Torah explicitly said "on the eighth day" and did not set boundaries within that day itself. However, according to this, for a Milah that is not in its proper time, there should be haste beyond that which applies to other mitzvos where "the zealous hasten" (see Sdei Chemed there). If so, the law of Milah on Tisha B'Av mentioned above would only apply to a Milah in its proper time, which is not the case. There is more to discuss here, but I will not elaborate.)

We see tangibly that the joy is dependent on the number of those gathered, and sometimes there is even sadness when some are prevented from coming.

In the case at hand, there is another matter dependent on this: the gathering of Anash, where they surely speak about matters of Torah, mitzvos, and Chassidus. Ultimately, Hashem commanded us to perform all these statutes in order to fear [Him], etc.

In any event, these reasons are sufficient, in my opinion, not to forcibly prevent those who follow the aforementioned custom.

Regarding the division of Shas and the division of Mishnayos: Since the Alter Rebbe exerted himself in the institution of the division of Shas, as brought at the end of Iggeres HaKodesh, and the Rebbe Maharash writes in his teachings that everyone must finish at least one tractate per year—if there is no room for both, the former takes precedence.

I enjoyed what you wrote regarding the conclusion of the Mishnayos, that there must be "strength" and also "peace," etc. (According to the simple meaning, it is as our Sages said, that the Holy One, Blessed be He, gives strength and power so that they may be able to receive His blessing—Sanhedrin 100b; therefore, the verse **preceded** "strength" to "bless with peace"). At a farbrengen here, the precision of the Mishnah's wording, "**not** found... **except**," was explained, for it should have said briefly that peace is the vessel, etc. The main point is how it is possible to have a vessel for a blessing that is infinite, for one answers the other, and surely there is a transcript. I will not elaborate.

With blessings and regards to your entire group, may they live.

**Menachem Schneerson**

## 897

B"H, 22 Shevat, 5711, Brooklyn

Greetings and blessings!

It was with joy that I learned that your daughter, Mrs. ... *tichyeh*, has become engaged to the *ben-gila* Rabbi ... I hereby express my blessings for a *mazal tov*, a *mazal tov*. May everything be at an auspicious and successful time, and may they build their home upon the foundations of Torah and *mitzvos*, as explained in the teachings of Chassidus.

I also thank you for informing me of the good news that your grandson ... *shiyeh*, has reached the age of three. Enclosed is a segment from a letter of my father-in-law, the Rebbe *ztzukulleh"h*, regarding the Jewish custom to cut the hair of the head at that time.

May it be His will that you always share only good news regarding yourself and your family *shiyeh*, as well as regarding communal matters.

With blessings for a *mazal tov* and success in all your endeavors,

**Menachem Schneerson**

The connection between *tzitzis* and the hair of the head is explained in *Pri Etz Chaim*, *Shaar HaTzitzis*, and in *Likutei Torah*, *Parshas Shelach* (47a). See also Rashi on the Torah, *Shelach* (15:38): "In the *tzitzis* of your heads."

The connection between *tzitzis* and marriage in holiness and purity is explained in the verse, "And you shall see them... and you shall not stray," and see also *Menachos* (44a): "His four *tzitzis* came... 'Acquire your purchase'..."

## 898

B"H, 22 Shevat, 5711, Brooklyn

To the esteemed and distinguished individual, active in communal affairs, etc., R. M. Tarn, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

Following your letter regarding the state of chinuch in Föhrenwald and my previous correspondence on the matter, I wish to inform you that I have now received a report from the Joint in Paris concerning the investigation they conducted into this issue.

According to this report, a series of improvements have been implemented: it has been agreed that only teachers who have a positive approach to religious matters shall teach Tanach; that during the hours of religion and Tanach, the children shall sit with their heads covered; and that the boys and girls shall be separated.

Furthermore, the report states that a special budget has been allocated for the rabbinate in Föhrenwald to maintain a mikveh and for the supervision of kashrus in the hospitals. Religious teachers have had their food rations increased from 5 to 12 this year, and the Joint has arranged for the religious teachers to receive their salaries from IRO as well. The necessities of the Rabbis and the religious requirements of the camp are being provided for to a greater extent than before.

Taking the above into account, the report concludes that the complaints are not so much aimed as criticism of the program, but rather, primarily, as a motivation for a group to create their own program.

I would be interested to know what the situation is now, and to what extent the aforementioned improvements are being upheld, etc.

With blessing and regards to the entire group, may they live,

**Menachem Schneerson**

## 899

B"H, 23 Shevat, 5711

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letters from the 11th and 17th of Teves, and the 4th and 15th of Shevat—although I have already partially replied and confirmed receipt of the lists and the *pan* (petition), which I read at the *tziyun* of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, during a time of favor.

I will begin with the main point, which concerns the health of the body. The Rambam rules in *Hilchos Deios* (4:1) that maintaining a healthy and sound body is a way of serving Hashem, etc. And in *Shulchan Aruch Orach Chaim* (571:2), it states: A *talmid chacham* is not permitted to fast, because it diminishes his work for Heaven, etc. Teachers and all those engaged in communal needs are considered like a *talmid chacham*. The Maggid of Mezeritch said (printed in *HaTamim*, Vol. 7, *ad loc.*): "A small hole in the body becomes a large hole in the *neshamah*." The Alter Rebbe rules in *Iggeres HaTeshuvah* (Chapter 3) that one may afflict oneself over one's sins only when one can estimate that it will **certainly** not cause any harm at all. After all these things, in my opinion, you should focus on improving your physical health through eating, drinking, and sleeping in a manner appropriate to the above. If it is necessary for this purpose to eat something before *davening*, and certainly to drink tea, milk, or the like, and you have been careful about this—you should increase this practice, and from now on, do as mentioned above without being stringent with yourself regarding this or similar matters. The Ribono shel Olam will surely grant you success in transforming *gashmius* into *ruchnius*.

I was very pleased with your thought to send students to the *beis medrash* in their camp to study *Chassidus* there, or to review a portion of a *maamar* of *Chassidus*. It is proper to do so in a way that the listeners will understand, and furthermore, that you should also draw their hearts through an introduction of a story or the like (taken from *sichos*, etc.). Beyond the benefit to the listeners and the great reward for those who review—which "illuminates the eyes of Hashem"—there is an additional benefit: the students thereby become accustomed to influencing others with *Chassidus* and influencing them in matters of fear of Heaven, even those who for the time being are not *anash*. After all, this is their role: to be **candles to illuminate**. Further elaboration on this is unnecessary.

Regarding what you wrote about the dream where you wanted to fast, etc.—in my opinion, you did well not to fast; your strength should be for *Torah* specifically. See what the *Taz* writes, whose words are cited in *Responsa Tzemach Tzedek*, *Shaar HaMiluim*, end of section 62; see there.

For the same reason you wrote regarding the benefit of studying a *masechta* for the sake of *le-migras* (that one gains at least a superficial knowledge of another *masechta*)—for that very reason, if I had the strength, I would also implement the study of *le-migras* in *Chassidus* (even though in *Chassidus*, the general study of its inwardness is more pertinent), such as a *Chassidishe sedra*, etc.

Regarding your good health, my hope is that if you conduct yourself as mentioned at the beginning of this letter, your situation will surely continue to improve, and you will bring me good news regarding this as soon as possible.

I await a letter bringing good news regarding the above, and especially regarding your good health. Give my regards to your entire group, may they live.

**Menachem Schneerson**

## 900

B"H, 24 Shevat, 5711, Brooklyn

Greetings and blessings!

I am happy to learn that your condition is improving, and may Hashem surely send you a complete recovery soon.

Regarding what you conveyed yesterday through your wife, the Rabbanit, may she live and be well, that your sleep is not as it should be: you should completely divert your mind from this and not be concerned by it, as you are surely following the doctor's instructions in this matter.

It would be appropriate to have a kosher mezuzah near your bed (not necessarily on the doorpost), provided, of course, that it is done as required—a vessel within a vessel, and the like.

Knowing your fondness for the words of the Rebbe, I will mention what I heard from my father-in-law, the Rebbe: that for several of the Nesi'im (I believe it is almost certain he specified the Rebbe Maharash), there was a note placed on his desk with the words: "I have set Hashem before me always" (*Shivisi Hashem l'negdi tamid*). And surely you are aware that on the writing and study desk of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, there was a mezuzah placed.

- It is worth noting the comments in Kelim 17:17 regarding those who would carry a mezuzah on a staff. See the Tosafot Yom Tov there. -

I look forward to hearing only good news from you, and I sign with a blessing for a speedy recovery,

**Menachem Schneerson**

If there are neighbors in your room, perhaps it is worthwhile to inquire about their standing regarding Torah and mitzvos, Chassidus, etc.

## 901

B"H, 26 Shevat, 5711

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter informing me that a shidduch is being proposed to you, and that the name of the young woman’s father is Avraham, and you are asking my opinion regarding the names.

One should consult the *Hagahos Mekor Chesed* to the *Tzava'as Rabbi Yehuda HaChasid*, which notes those who side with permitting this: *Chasam Sofer* (Yoreh Deah, 138; Even HaEzer, Vol. 1, 116), *Shu"t Moshe* (end of 60), *Divrei Chaim* (Even HaEzer, 68), *Imrei Esh* (Yoreh Deah, end of 60), *Tuv Ta'am V'Da'as* (Third Series, 263), *Kin'as Sofrim* (in the omissions, 26), *Yad Shaul* (Vol. 2, 240, 4), *Pischei Teshuvah* (Even HaEzer, 62, subsection 7; and 64, subsection 14), and others.

As for us, we follow only the ruling of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, the Tzemach Tzedek (*Shu"t Even HaEzer*, Vol. 1, 43; *Piskei Dinim* to Yoreh Deah, 116), that since "the names are not exactly identical, there is no concern whatsoever"—see there.

However, **it should be established** that he be called to the Torah and sign his name, etc., not only with the name Avraham alone, but also with his other names (both of them, or at least one of them).

With blessings,

**Menachem Schneerson**

## 812

B"H, 26 Shevat, 5711

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, and distinguished, etc., R’ S. [Librov], may he live.
Shaliach

Peace and blessing!

In response to your letter of 22 Shevat:

I have already written to the esteemed Chossid, etc., R’ B.G. [Gorodetzky], may he live, that in my opinion, he should immediately submit another request for entry into Morocco, and you should consult together as to the best way to proceed (to which city, whom to mention there, and the like).

May Hashem grant success so that everything happens in its proper time—that we may each of us fulfill our shlichus in this world, and with expansion.

If you also wish to occupy yourself with papers for Australia—provided that it does not distract from the work in Morocco—you may do so.

Regarding what you wrote about [Name]’s health—in my opinion, you must follow the doctors’ instructions regarding food, drink, and rest, and even rest from intensity in learning. Do not be stringent in this **at all**. The Rambam has already ruled (Hilchos De’os, Chapter 4) that maintaining a healthy body is one of the ways of Hashem. See also Iggeres HaKodesh, Chapter 3.

And especially, it is better to lose one hour now, and thereby add—when he returns to full health—many more hours, and with joy. Further elaboration on this is unnecessary.

I will conclude with a blessing for the time of the Bar Mitzvah of your son, may he live (a letter to him is enclosed), that you should have Yiddishe and Chassidishe nachas from him in all respects.

With blessing,

**M. Schneerson**

## 903

B"H, 29 Shevat, 5711, Brooklyn

Greetings and blessings!

...And may you increase your courage in setting fixed times for Torah study with the public, and in bringing the warmth and light of Yiddishkeit and Chassidus into the homes of the children of Israel. This is also a channel for increasing warmth and light in your own home — in spiritual matters, and consequently in material matters as well, for with all the children of Israel, the two are one; it is only that for the average person this remains hidden, whereas for Chassidim it must be revealed. And consequently, from Above, they give [blessings] in a revealed manner, so that one sees success in material matters and feels vitality in a word of Chassidus and in the fulfillment of a mitzvah, and all this with joy.

With blessings for a Mazal Tov and proper health,

**Menachem Schneerson**

## 404

B"H, 29 Shevat, 5711, Brooklyn

To the esteemed Rabbi and Chassid, G-d-fearing and distinguished, etc., our teacher Rabbi Mordechai, may he live, HaKohen.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of 17 Shevat, in which you request assistance in preparing speeches to deliver before your congregation, etc.:

It is difficult to suggest material for a sermon suitable for your congregation since you do not describe their nature (merchants, scholars, youth, elderly, and the like), nor what they are looking for in their Rabbi’s sermon. However, in general, you can find in *HaKriah VeHaKedushah* sufficient material for various types of our brethren in America. For example: *kashrus* (there is an article there in English as well), the role of women (in the "Call to Women"), the concept of *galus* and *geulah*, and so on. There is also a *hemshech* there on all the *sedros* and all the *haftaros* that you can use, at the very least, as a foundation and material for building a sermon.

If you have a specific topic in mind that you wish to speak about and are looking for sources and references pertaining to it, please be so kind as to inform me, and I will endeavor to assist you in this.

It is surprising that you do not mention anything regarding the religious life of your congregation, nor your activities to strengthen Yiddishkeit, or even to spread the *maayanos* of *Chassidus*. After all, "also" this is incumbent upon you, and surely you have been given the strength to fulfill this role; when you begin, you will succeed.

With blessings, awaiting good news,

**Menachem Schneerson**

#### 404

**Our teacher Rabbi Mordechai:** Fischer.

## 5105

B"H, 1 Adar Rishon, 5711, Brooklyn

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, and distinguished individual, who engages in communal needs, etc.,
R' A.L. may he live,

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of the 26th of Shevat, in which you inform me that you are considering honoring the activist R' Moshe Morgenstern, may he live, by inviting him as a guest speaker at the yeshiva's annual banquet, and you ask for my advice on this matter. You also request a blessing for success in your fundraising efforts, etc.

It is appropriate that you invite the aforementioned activist.

May it be the will [of Hashem] that you succeed in your efforts, both in material matters and in spreading the wellsprings of Chassidus outward.

I have already said several times that, in my opinion, you have become overly constricted within the "four cubits" (in both senses of the term).

When you spread out into the city and venture into the open—at least to some extent to begin with—this constitutes an expansion of the vessels and the limbs. Consequently, you draw down additional *oros*, which, in their descent downward, also result in an increase in the funds of the campaign—simply put, *mer gelt*—and this is a *mitzvah* for which no one else can fulfill your obligation and merit.

With blessings and regards to the entire group, may they live,

**Menachem Schneerson**

## 406

406

B"H, 2 Adar Rishon, 5711, Brooklyn

To the distinguished Rabbi and Chassid, G-d-fearing and learned, etc., Moreinu HaRav Ephraim Eliezer, may he live, HaKohen

Greetings and blessings!

I was pleased to receive your letter from Erev Rosh Chodesh Adar, and especially that you are not diverting your attention from the matter of the distinguished Chassid, etc., Moreinu HaRav Shmuel, may he live, the shochet.

- It is worth noting that the prohibition of diverting one’s attention is learned from the Kohen Gadol (Shabbos 12a), for "the lips of a Kohen" — all Kohanim, not specifically the Kohen Gadol — **shall guard** knowledge. See Zohar Vol. III, 146b, that this applies even in our time (unlike the tzitz), and it is proven there that specifically through this, he is able to bless the Jewish people. -

May it be the will [of Hashem] that the delay be for the good, in a good that is visible and revealed, the good for us. And whoever prays for another, etc., is answered first; may you, sir, bring good tidings soon regarding his matter.

With blessings,

**Menachem Schneerson**

## 907

B"H, 2 Adar Rishon, 5711, Brooklyn

Greetings and blessings!

...You surely remember, and I wish to emphasize here, that you should also fulfill what my father-in-law, the Rebbe, told you and reiterated: that one must always be *besimcha*.

You surely also remember our conversation, that the world is not, *chas v'shalom*, ownerless; rather, just as Hashem created it, so too does He conduct it now, at every moment and every hour. Nothing happens without *hashgacha pratis*. This is the *emunah peshutah* of all Jews, who are *ma'aminim bnei ma'aminim*.

Everyone also believes that Hashem is *tachlis hatov*, and consequently, it is certain that everything He does is for the good.

By remembering this, and from time to time reflecting upon it, it is easier to understand many occurrences in life. The main thing is that this provides true security in daily life, as Dovid Hamelech said: "Hashem is my shepherd—therefore—I shall not lack... for You are with me."

I would be pleased if you would find some free time to write me a few words about how you are feeling. I wish you a complete recovery, and I hope you will be able to report good news regarding this.

With blessings of all the best,

**Menachem Schneerson**

## 808

B"H, 2 Adar Rishon, 5711, Brooklyn

Greetings and blessings!

I have received various reports about your uncle... through our shluchim who are in Switzerland from time to time, and through your relatives here.

I have also had the opportunity to become personally acquainted with... and to see to what extent a character such as his is in need of friendship and friendly attention.

It is certainly unnecessary to draw your attention to this, or to emphasize the importance of the matter, both from the standpoint of humanity and from the standpoint of the Torah. I take the liberty, however, of underscoring the great mitzvah that you and your wife, may she live and be well, will have by showing your uncle... more than the usual attention and friendship.

According to a saying of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, that the Ribono shel Olam never remains a debtor, I am certain that the Ribono shel Olam will repay you with much hatzlacha, a happy life, and much nachas from your son, may he live and be well.

With blessings of blessing and hatzlacha to you and your household, may they live and be well.

**Menachem Schneerson**

## 8109

B"H, 3 Adar Rishon, 5711

Greetings and blessings!

I was pleased to hear the good news that a son has been born to you, mazal tov. I hereby send my blessing that you should bring him into the covenant of Avraham Avinu at the proper time, and that you should raise him to Torah, to the chuppah, and to good deeds, with abundance in both material and spiritual matters.

The mitzvah that you have accepted upon yourselves with joy will surely continue to bring joy into your home. I would point out the teaching of our Sages (Kesuvos 8b) and what is written regarding this in *Ois Chayim V'Shalom*, Siman 265, subsections 27 and 29. See also *Moed Katan* 9a regarding brothers who **derived pleasure**, etc.

In the *Shulchan Aruch* of the Alter Rebbe, *Mahadura Basra*, end of Siman 4: The beginning of the **entry**, etc., into the mitzvah of milah—and because it is the **beginning**, it must be done specifically with joy, so that it should not be a "forced declaration" (*moda'ah rabbah*). It is also like a sacrifice (Zohar Vol. I, 95, *Ra'aya Mehemna*), which must be brought specifically of your own free will.

With blessings of mazal tov, mazal tov,

**Menachem Schneerson**

## 511

B"H, 5 Adar I, 5711, Brooklyn.

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, and distinguished individual, who engages in communal needs with faithfulness, etc., R' Moshe HaKohen, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

I received in due time the *pidyon nefesh* that you sent for yourself, for your wife, may she live, for... and for your household, may they live. I read them on the day of the *hilula* of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, at his gravesite. He surely awakens, and will continue to awaken, compassion for those connected to him in general, and for your wife and those mentioned above, may they all live in goodness, especially regarding what they need. May Hashem fulfill the blessings of the *tzaddik* to their fullest extent, for "the *tzaddikim* are greater... even after their passing."

I look forward to hearing good news from you regarding the improvement of the health of those mentioned above.

It would also be kind of you to inform me of the situation of... regarding Yiddishkeit and the observance of *mitzvos*.

The saying of the Baal Shem Tov is well-known: that sometimes a soul descends to this world for seventy or eighty years for the sole purpose of doing a favor for a fellow Jew, whether in material or spiritual matters.

However, it is obvious that one should not be satisfied with doing a favor once or twice, etc., but rather, as is common in the language of our Sages, even a hundred times (see *Chullin* 106a: "Here it is written as a minority").

And if you are helping those mentioned above with health, livelihood, etc., you are surely also taking an interest in their spiritual state and helping them as much as possible in that regard.

As the verse in this week's *parsha* states: "And Aharon shall carry the judgment of the Children of Israel upon his heart before Hashem always" (and the deeds of the fathers are a sign for the children).

With blessing and regards to all your group, may they live,

**M. Schneerson**

## 812

B"H, 5 Adar I, 5711, Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

...It is told in the name of the Alter Rebbe that "without a plan, one does not get anywhere." However, since you write to me regarding your situation and your desire to be able to relocate overseas, in my opinion, it is far more appropriate to endeavor to move to one of the countries in South America than to the United States. According to the information received, it is easier to get settled there, as the majority of immigrants come here [to the U.S.]. For someone for whom the question of their children’s chinuch is not currently at the forefront, the primary obstacle to settling there is thereby removed.

I will conclude with wishes for proper health and a successful settlement in both body and soul.

With regards and blessings,

The work has only just begun, and large sums are needed to continue it, and Hashem Yisbarach will help with success.

With blessings and regards to those who pray, may they live.

## 414

B”H, 6 Adar Rishon, 5711, Brooklyn

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, and refined, R’ Kalman, may he live.

Greetings and blessings!

I was pleased to receive the detailed report from the Beis Rivkah school in Crown Heights, and I will note here a few comments regarding this report:

(a) Regarding what you wrote—that you are trying to accustom the children to learning various words in Lashon HaKodesh while speaking in the vernacular, which is the language of the country—accustoming a child to mix two languages in their speech is, on the face of it, something that contradicts such a habit.

(b) Regarding the Shacharis davening for the children, I do not understand the relevance of the hymn *Adon Olam* there. You surely have the *Brachos U’Tfillos* order that was published; please look there on page 2, at the morning blessings for young children.

(c) In the *Brachos HaNehenin*, you mention that the **standard** *Brachos HaNehenin* are missing, such as *Borei Pri HaEtz*, *Borei Pri HaAdamah*, etc., and likewise *Brich Rachmana*.

(d) It is not mentioned in the report whether you are accustoming the children to matters of *derech eretz*, such as conduct while eating, etc., helping a friend, etc.

(e) It would be appropriate to make a remembrance of the Mincha davening before dismissal, such as by reciting the verse *Poteiach es yadecha*, etc., and the verses after *Aleinu*—*Al tira*, etc.

It is surely known to you how much my father-in-law, the Rebbe, sacrificed himself for proper chinuch and for upholding Yiddishkeit, even in the most "simple" matters, despite the fact that he could have utilized those times for the study of the secrets of Torah and the secrets of secrets. This is a lesson for each and every one of us, and further elaboration is unnecessary. I am certain that you, too, will increase your strength in your educational work, in your influence upon your students and those you educate, and also in the homes of their parents, may they live, to illuminate them with the light of Torah and mitzvos in a manner that fits the words of our Sages: "Words that come from the heart." The meaning of this is also, in the literal sense, *hartzike reid* (heartfelt words).

With blessings for success in your work in proper chinuch and in your personal matters.

#### ***414***

**R’ Kalman:** Katlovitz.

## 915

B"H, 7 Adar I, 5711, Brooklyn

To our dear friends, Anash, the esteemed, G-d-fearing, and learned, etc., who are in the city of Paris, and the groups, may they live.

Peace and blessing!

Through our dear friend, the esteemed, G-d-fearing, and learned, etc., R' Binyamin, may he live, Gorodetzky, I learned of your good decision to establish a weekly shiur in Chassidus at the office hall, in two groups, in which Anash from all the groups will participate together. You will surely endeavor to fulfill the request that "your wellsprings be dispersed outward," with all the conditions pertaining to this, as explained in my letter of 10 Kislev last year, for this is a preparation, a readiness, and a vessel for the coming of Moshiach speedily in our days.

It is a good thing that you have discussed the matter of the shochtim—that those who have trained, as well as those who have not yet trained properly in this holy craft, both in the actual work and in the thorough knowledge of the halachos, should return to and continue their studies in this area—even those among them who already hold slaughtering positions. The rabbis of Anash should oversee this. It is well known that in addition to the knowledge of the halachos and the craft of slaughtering, the essential element in this matter (see Responsa of the Alter Rebbe, 69; see also Responsa of the Tzemach Tzedek, Yoreh Deah, 12, and Shaar HaMiluim, 15-18) is yiras shamayim, which is required of a shochet even more than of a rav. May we merit that which is destined for the day of the coming of the "Great Shochet," who is Hakadosh Baruch Hu, as our Sages of blessed memory state in Sukkah (52a).

I will be pleased to hear good news from all of you, may you live, in material matters, and that all of you, as one, fulfill and feel your responsibility—that you, your wives, and your sons and daughters are all attached and connected to the Nasi of the generation, who is my sainted father-in-law, the Rebbe, the head and the brains of this generation. And since you are all part of the stature of this generation, it is certain that the head ensures the well-being of the part (not merely the fulfillment of one of its individual needs), both spiritually and materially alike.

With blessing and regards to each and every one, may they live.

## 416

B"H, 7 Adar I, 5711, Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter of the 2nd of Parshas Mishpatim and the *pidyon nefesh*.

One must be strong in *bitachon* in Hashem, who directs the entire world without exception, that He will guard and protect you, and ultimately bring you to a good arrangement in both material and spiritual matters.

One must also have good *keilim* to receive all these blessings, and these are *Torah* and *mitzvos*. Specifically: reciting *Tehillim* every day as it is divided for the days of the month, studying every day a *parsha* of *Chumash* from the weekly *sedra* with *Rashi* (Sunday until *Sheni*, Monday until *Shlishi*, etc.), and the *shiur* in *Tanya* as divided by *K'vod Kedushas Moreinu V'Rabbeinu Admur* for the days of the year.

Why do you not mention anything regarding a *shidduch*?

May the *Ribono shel Olam* help you to soon report good tidings.

With blessings.

## 419

B"H, 9 Adar I, 5711, Brooklyn

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, and distinguished R' Chaim, may he live:

Greetings and blessings!

I have duly received your two letters along with the enclosed checks, which serve as a beginning for the printing of the sefer of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, as well as for the *maamad*. The receipts are enclosed herewith, with many thanks.

In accordance with your request, I have mentioned you and your wife, may she live, for whatever you may need, at the *tziyun* of my father-in-law, the Rebbe. Especially now, since you have received and taken upon yourself the *zechus* of printing a sefer of his *maamarim* or *sichos*, and thereby bringing light into many, many Jewish homes in all corners of the world—everywhere—you have surely earned that this should draw down light and warmth into your own lives as well. One only needs to open the doors and windows so that it may enter within, and this is done through *Tehillim*, Torah (*Chumash* with Rashi, *Tanya*, a *shiur* in the Rebbe’s *maamarim* or *sichos*, and the like), which opens the heart and the mind.

Regarding your question as to when to send the remaining funds—I do not wish to make things difficult for you. However, the sooner the money is here, the sooner the typesetters, printers, and so on, will be able to do their work.

I hope that in your next letter you will also write about an improvement in your mood and in the health of you both.

With blessings, and awaiting good news.

#### ***419***

## 920

B"H, Purim Katan, 5711, Brooklyn.

To our brothers and sisters of Israel, and to those in Greater New York in particular, may Hashem protect them and grant them life,

Peace and blessing!

Certain Jewish circles, where Torah and mitzvos are unfortunately, for the time being, in a neglected state, are exposed to the danger of intense propaganda from missionaries who aim, in either an open or a disguised manner, to bring about conversion, Heaven forbid.

They focus especially on children whose Jewish education has been neglected.

If it has always been true that "whoever sustains one soul of Israel, it is as if he sustained an entire world," then today, all the more so, when millions of our holy and pure brothers and sisters who were killed for the sanctification of Hashem’s name were suddenly taken from us, every single soul is an entire world. We must exert the greatest efforts to safeguard their connection to His Name, may He be blessed.

The responsibility is especially great regarding children, for they must build a *bayis b'Yisrael* in the future. Any negative influence upon them—and certainly an influence of *kefirah*, Heaven forbid—affects their generations and the generations of their generations.

I was therefore highly pleased to hear of a greater *hisorerus* that has begun in responsible Jewish circles to take **practical** steps to combat these seductive influences and to prevent Jewish *neshamos* from being severed, Heaven forbid, from their Jewish source.

I am especially pleased to support the *hatzalas nefashos* work of the **"Vaad Megini U'Marhivei HaChinuch HaKasher,"** founded by my father-in-law, the Rebbe, *ztzukulleh"h nbg"m zi"e*, under the supervision of "Merkaz L'Inyonei Chinuch," which has developed extensive plans in this area and is proceeding toward their implementation.

It is certainly the duty of every Jew, man or woman, to assist in this important and urgent work to the best of their ability, and the merit of the *mitzvah* of *hatzalas nefashos* will surely stand by them to be blessed with all good.

With blessing,

**M. Schneerson**

## 921

B"H, Purim Katan, 5711, Brooklyn

To our dear friends, Anash, wherever they may be, may they live:

Peace and blessing!

Kolel Chabad, the Rambah"n, which was founded by our holy Rebbe, the Alter Rebbe—may the merit of the righteous protect us—who established it with *mesiras nefesh*, and which was subsequently supported by our holy Rebbes—may the merit of the righteous protect us—who served as the Nasi of Kolel Chabad in every generation and exerted themselves to the utmost for its maintenance and existence, has in recent years been in a difficult situation.

The following are the words of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, among his other holy words in his final appeal in this world on behalf of the Kolel, nineteen days before his passing:

"Every single one of Anash has the obligation to remember at all times and at every hour that the mitzvah of the Tzedakah of the Rambah"n, which we were commanded by our holy Rebbes—may the merit of the righteous protect us—is a personal obligation (*chovas gavra*) for every man and woman. It applies in every place and at every time, and is established for all generations. Furthermore, the holy blessings... were designated by our holy Rebbes—may the merit of the righteous protect us—for all who support this holy Tzedakah, and they are fixed and endure forever."

Surely these holy words are engraved upon the hearts of Anash, may they live. I have written this only to encourage those who are already diligent, and to urge them to increase in holiness: those who, for whatever reason, do not yet have a Rambah"n Kolel Chabad *shofar* (charity box) in their homes should hasten to acquire one and affix it in their homes. And all who maintain the Rambah"n Kolel Chabad *shofaros*, the *gabbaim* of the Kolel, its members, its workers, and its supporters—each and every one of them—should increase their efforts in assisting Kolel Chabad, so that the Kolel may fulfill its mission and responsibilities in accordance with the demands of the hour.

Great is this Tzedakah in awakening supernal kindnesses, to draw down for each and every one of its supporters thousands of blessings, so that they and their households, may they live, may be blessed with everything they require, both materially and spiritually.

With blessings for goodness, materially and spiritually,

**M. Schneerson**

## 922

B"H, Purim Katan, 5711, Brooklyn

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter, via your family members—may they live—asking whether you should extend or shorten your travel schedule due to the concern regarding the rising exchange rate of the country’s currency, etc.:

In my opinion, you should not change your plans because of this matter. Any profit due to you in connection with your travels will undoubtedly come to you in full, whether through the exchange rate or in some other way. What difference does it make to you?

Seemingly, those who have merited the beautiful portion of standing close to matters of Torah and its support, and at a distance from matters of the world and commerce, why should they delve into and expend the energy of their minds on the machinations of business and the like? For regarding them, the requirement of the verse, "Hashem will bless you in all that you do," is fulfilled completely through engaging in the means of livelihood in the ordinary way. Their power of invention, comprehension, and depth—and certainly their *hiskashrus*—belong to matters of Torah and the ways of supporting it. And it is for the *Ribono shel Olam* to grant, through these ordinary vessels, abundant success in a revealed and manifest way, above the ordinary path, for that is the measure.

Enclosed is a letter to the *avreich* who wrote on your behalf, as I did not know his address. Many thanks for the trouble of delivering my letters.

Give my regards to "our Yidden," and as my father-in-law, the Rebbe, explained: "Our Yidden means Yidden who are connected to Torah and *mitzvos*" (and who among the children of Avraham, Yitzchak, and Yaakov is not connected to Torah and *mitzvos*?), and [I wish you] success in your affairs.

## 923

16 Adar, 5711, Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Rabbi, the G-d-fearing, learned, and wise, etc., R. Reuven, may he live.

Greetings and blessings!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your book, *Mishpetei Bnei Adam* (three volumes), as well as your letter dated 7 Adar.

Regarding what you noted in your letter, and likewise in your book (Vol. 2, *Erech* *Dalet*), concerning the words of the *Yam Shel Shlomo* (*Bava Kamma* 91b) regarding the law that it is forbidden to injure or shame oneself for the sake of monetary gain:

Specifically, that the words of the *Yam Shel Shlomo* are only applicable if one shames or injures oneself by way of mockery or the like, but if the shaming or injury occurs through [legitimate] labor, it is permitted.

From this, you find a difficulty with what is written in the *Shulchan Aruch* of our Rebbe the Alter Rebbe (*Hilchos Nizkei Guf V'Nefesh*, 6:4 in the *Kuntres Acharon*), that since Rav said to Rav Kahana, "Strip [the carcass]...," and from [the words of] Yaakov, "I was consumed by drought by day and frost by night," it is implied that it is permitted to endure shame and suffering for the sake of monetary gain.

I am astonished at your honor: From where do you derive the aforementioned distinction in the words of the *Yam Shel Shlomo*? And what does mockery and *bitul Torah* have to do with the case at hand of one who injures himself? (I do not have the *Yam Shel Shlomo* before me to examine his exact wording).

On the contrary, follow the reason for the prohibition against injuring oneself, which is because "a person has no **authority** over his body **at all** to strike it, nor to shame it, nor to cause it pain" (*Shulchan Aruch* of the Alter Rebbe). This means that regarding bodily pain, the law is the same as [the law regarding] the body of one’s fellow. The reason for this is explained more clearly in the *Radbaz* on the Rambam (*Hilchos Sanhedrin* 18:6): A person’s soul is not his own possession, but the possession of the Holy One, Blessed be He. See also Rambam, *Hilchos Rotzeach* (1:4).

Regarding the proof you brought for your opinion from what is written, "By the sweat of your brow you shall eat bread," "Man is born to toil," and the like:

It is simple that this depends on whether this is the "custom of the world," for then the Holy One, Blessed be He, has given permission to use His possession in such a manner, since He said, "Six days you shall labor." But if one adds to the aforementioned, he is injuring the possession of the Holy One, Blessed be He, without His permission. And from the very fact that Yaakov **boasted**, "I was consumed by drought by day and frost by night," and that Rav found it necessary to **warn**, "Strip the carcass," etc., it is proven that this is not at all a customary or standard practice. See *Bava Metzia* 93b: "Excessive guarding," etc. (Seemingly, this depends on the dispute between Rabbah and Rav Chisda there). See also *Tanchuma*, *Miketz*, on the verse "And G-d Almighty," [where it says] he fled from Esau to Lavan, "See how many **troubles** I had in the day, I was consumed by drought," etc. In the commentary of the *Tur* on the Torah (*Vayetzei* 30:39), he also explains that Yaakov did something he was not obligated to do.

You also noted what is written in *Tanya*, Chapter 1, and likewise in *Turei Even* to *Rosh Hashanah* (29a), that one who transgresses a minor prohibition of Rabbinic origin is called a *rasha*, and all the more so, *kal v'chomer*, one who neglects a positive commandment is called a *rasha*.

You raise a difficulty: Why is it necessary to learn this via *kal v'chomer* when it is explicitly stated in *Shevuos* (12b) and *Zevachim* (7b) that our Sages said, "What is the nature of this positive commandment? If he does not repent, 'The sacrifice of the **wicked** is an abomination'"?

This can be answered in two ways:

1) In *Shevuos* and *Zevachim*, he transgressed **two** positive commandments: the positive commandment of the transgression itself, and the positive commandment to perform *teshuvah*.

For from the language of our Rebbe the Alter Rebbe in *Iggeres HaTeshuvah*, Chapter 1 (91a), it is implied that he holds that *teshuvah* is a commandment from the Torah, contrary to those who say that the commandment is only that if one *wants* to perform *teshuvah*, it is a commandment to confess (see *Minchas Chinuch* 364; see also *Sefer HaMitzvos* of the Tzemach Tzedek, *Mitzvos Viduy V'Teshuvah*; the commentary of the *Rif* Perla to the *Sefer HaMitzvos* of Rav Saadia Gaon, *Parshah* 42; *Zohar* Vol. 3, 124a, and this is not the place to elaborate). And even according to this opinion, one could say that this applies all year round, but on Yom Kippur (which is what is being discussed in *Shevuos* there), it is different, for then everyone is **obligated** to perform *teshuvah* (Rambam, *Teshuvah* 2:7). Likewise, when one brings a sacrifice to atone for a sin (which is what is being discussed in *Zevachim* there), the positive commandment of *teshuvah* **takes effect** upon him automatically. However, in *Tanya* (and *Turei Even*), he brings proof that one is called a *rasha* immediately upon neglecting a single positive commandment. This requires further study.

2) It can also be said: From *Shevuos* and *Zevachim*, it is only proven that he is called a *rasha*, and one might have thought to say that this is a "minor *rasha*." *Tanya* brings proof that he is a "severe *rasha*," because it comes via an *a fortiori* argument, a *kal v'chomer*.

**Note:**

I saw in your book that you begin with the "category of kings" (which is based on the end of *Horayos*, that a king takes precedence over a High Priest, and a prophet, etc.), and in this very category—regarding the master of all prophets, Moshe Rabbeinu—I have a difficulty, for the greatness of Moshe Rabbeinu was his prophecy, not his kingship, as your honor yourself wrote there (272).

In the category of kings, the beginning—from above to below—should be King Moshiach.

For regarding prophecy, it is said in *Rosh Hashanah* (1st chapter) that among kings, there arose none like Moshe Rabbeinu. But from what is written in the Rambam (*Teshuvah* 9:2), that Moshiach is a great prophet, close to Moshe Rabbeinu, it is implied that he holds like the opinion in *Rosh Hashanah* there, that even among kings, there arose none [like him].

But regarding the level of a king—it is said that Moshiach "smells and judges" (*Sanhedrin* 93b, and they acted upon this, see there). Even according to the opinion that among kings there arose one like Moshe—namely, Shlomo—he was not permitted to judge except through witnesses, etc. It is obvious that "smelling and judging" is a law of a king, not a law of a prophet, for a prophet does not judge.

According to our version, it can be said that these are the two interpretations in *Tanchuma*, end of *Parshas Toldos*, regarding King Moshiach: "He will gain wisdom," etc., and "he will be exalted" from Yitzchak (and it does not specify from Moshe, because Moshe is greater than him in prophecy), etc., and "he will be exalted" from Moshe (because in kingship, Moshiach is greater than Moshe).

See the notes of Maharash Buber to *Tanchuma* (there, 34), that Maharatz Chayes raised a difficulty from here against what is written in the Rambam there, that Moshiach is only "close to Moshe." See also the *maamar* of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of Acharon Shel Pesach 5709 (printed in *Kuntres 60*), that in the future, Moshiach will bestow the inner dimension of Torah even to the Patriarchs, Moshe Rabbeinu, and Aharon, etc.—and this is also proven in *Likutei Torah* of our Rebbe the Alter Rebbe, *Parshas Tzav*, *D'H V'Heinif Yado*, Chapter 2.

With blessings for success in Torah study with Heavenly assistance, and from a position of tranquility in body and soul.

## 924

By the Grace of Hashem, 19 Adar, 5711, Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, learned in the ways of Chassidus, etc.,
Rabbi Avraham Dov, may he live.

Peace and Blessing!

In response to your letter inquiring about the Zohar, Vol. II:

1) Page 156a: "On a weekday, at the time of Mincha, judgment hangs in the world, and it is not a time of favor," end quote.

Seemingly, this is the opposite of what our Sages said (Berachos 6b): "A person should always be careful with the Mincha prayer, for Eliyahu was only answered during the Mincha prayer."

**Response:**

This difficulty is addressed in Chassidic thought, along with another difficulty from our Sages (Avodah Zarah 3b): "During the three fourth-hours, the Holy One, Blessed be He, sits and plays." The core of the resolution is: The time of Mincha is a time of judgment. If a person davens **then**, it means he is victorious in the Heavenly Court at the very moment that Gevurah holds sway. Therefore, he can accomplish great things, because there is no longer any opposition; on the contrary, even the opponent answers "Amen." This is not the case with the Shacharis prayer, when the attribute of Chesed holds sway. He may accomplish something **then** through his prayer, but it is not yet an *atafcha* (transformation). Therefore, when the attribute of judgment comes in its full force—when the shadows of evening stretch—it is possible that a new indictment could be found. Thus, in the case of Eliyahu, where they were "wavering between two opinions" **regarding the essence** of the faith, and an *atafcha* was required—he was answered during the Mincha prayer. The Mincha prayer transforms the time of the sitting of the Heavenly **Court**, for it is precisely then that the Holy One, Blessed be He, sits and plays. This is also what is written in *Kedushas Levi* at the end of Parshas Chayei Sarah, that the Mincha prayer is the prayer of Yitzchak, and "behold, camels are coming"—the Holy One, Blessed be He, bestows kindness upon Yisrael. As you copied in your letter, specifically **camels** (*gemalim*), based on our Sages (Berachos 56b): "One who sees a camel in a dream, **death** was decreed for him from Heaven, and they saved him"—an *atafcha* from one extreme to the other.

It can also be understood in terms of *avodah*. The superiority of the Mincha prayer is explained by the fact that one is in the midst of his business dealings in worldly matters (judgments, *birurim*, the *nefesh habahamit* is in a constrained state), and it is precisely then that he pauses, davens, and unites with his Creator—an *atafcha* from one extreme to the other. From this, there is proof that worldly matters will not divert him from the mind of his Creator, and the *nefesh habahamit* is **conquered**. This is not the case with the Shacharis prayer, which one davens before going to his business; it is possible that upon going out into the street, etc., he will stumble, G-d forbid, in his path and fall from his level.

See the *maamar* beginning "Nach Mitzvasah" (when the stars appear), the *maamar* beginning "Leolam Yehei Adam Zahir" (Kuntres 15), and elsewhere.

2) You are troubled by the fact that **night** is a time of judgment.

**Response:**

It is true that Mincha is a time of judgment relative to the morning, and night is a time of judgment even relative to Mincha (this is also proven in Yerushalmi Shekalim, Ch. 5, Halacha 4; see also Zohar Vol. III, 221a, *Pri Etz Chaim*, *Tefillas Arvit* 4a, in the notes of the Arizal there, and elsewhere). However, in the case at hand in the Zohar, it concerns the time of the sitting of the Heavenly Court, and "the upper world and the lower world are one in the same manner," and one does not judge at night (Sanhedrin, Ch. 4; *Shulchan Aruch Choshen Mishpat*, Sec. 65, and sources cited there). But the execution of the verdict and the like can take place even at night, and in fact, even more so.

3) In the Zohar (Vol. II, 156a), it says that Moshe passed away at the Mincha of Shabbos. This is difficult, given our Sages' statement that on the day of his passing, he wrote thirteen Sifrei Torah.

**Response:**

Many have already tread this ground—see *Tosafos* (Menachos 30a), *Rosh* (Pesachim, Ch. 10), *Mordechai* there, *Or Zarua* (Laws of Motzaei Shabbos), *Sefer Chasidim* (Sec. 356), *Kol Bo* (Law 40), *Shulchan Aruch Orach Chaim* (Sec. 292), *Bach*, *Taz*, and *Shulchan Aruch* of our Rebbe the Alter Rebbe there, *Asarah Maamaros* (by Rema Mi'Pano), Part 8, Ch. 13, *Responsa Chasam Sofer* (Vol. VI, Sec. 29), *Seder HaDoros* (Year 2488), *Taamei HaMinhagim* (citing *Sefer Ateres Tzvi*), and more.

The conclusion from all of the above can be summarized in three points: a) The Midrashim are divided, and this is the very dispute of the Tannaim in *Bava Basra* (15a); see there. b) The beginning of the passing was on Erev Shabbos, and its conclusion was at the Mincha of Shabbos (it remains difficult how it is written "and He buried him" before the event—what is written "and he died," etc., has already been explained as being because his *tzelem* departed; perhaps it can be explained according to what is written in Zohar Vol. II, 9a, that his burial was by the will of the Ancient of Days, and it speaks of his soul; see also Zohar Vol. I, 27b, and Zohar Vol. III, 280a). c) The writing of the Sefer Torah was done through a change: with tears (as mentioned there) or by adjuring the quill (*Chasam Sofer* there, in the name of the *Shelah*). Seemingly, it is a great innovation to say that such writing is valid, and if you say that this was the command: "Take this Sefer Torah," etc.—then we should learn from it for every place as well.

4) There, it says that because of the passing of Moshe, the doors of the *beis medrash* were locked. You are troubled that we do not observe public mourning on Shabbos, so why do we observe this even now?

**Response:**

If our Sages instituted this—that if a scholar dies, his *beis medrash* is closed—then they are the ones who said it, and they are the ones who said [the laws of Shabbos].

Regarding your reasoning, you should have rather questioned the saying of *Tzidkascha* [on Shabbos], which is like *Tziduk HaDin* (justifying the judgment), and our Sages there [forbid it]—and yet, *Tziduk HaDin* is forbidden even on Erev Shabbos after midday, etc.—but it is as mentioned above, that their enactment is a special matter.

## 925

B"H, 20 Adar Rishon, 5711, Brooklyn

To the esteemed Rabbi, the Torah scholar, the G-d-fearing man, the man of understanding and wisdom, the one who occupies himself with the secrets of Torah, the organizer and sharp-witted debater, possessor of noble character traits, who seeks the good of his people, etc., etc., Moreinu Harav R' Yitzchak HaLevi, Chief Rabbi,

Peace and blessing!

I have received reports from various sources regarding the possibility of elections in Eretz Yisrael, may it be rebuilt and established.

Considering the situation in Eretz Yisrael in general, and in particular the results of the municipal elections that were held not long ago, and based on the information I have received since then regarding what is transpiring in Eretz Yisrael—which, on the face of it, appears to be accurate—it seems that the religious parties and the Charedi Jewry there, in general, are not yet organized to the extent that if new elections were to be held in the near future, the situation in the Knesset would improve. On the contrary, and even more so, Heaven forbid.

Surely, since you are on the scene, these matters are known to you even more clearly, and you will also arrive at the conclusion that for the benefit and from the perspective of **all** Charedi Jewry (without considering a specific party that might **perhaps** gain from this)—the time is not at all appropriate for general elections.

I trust that the aforementioned rumors are nothing more than a tactic and a matter of intimidation, in order to achieve thereby the desired solution to the questions of kosher education, but they do not intend to actually hold elections at all. And surely this will be done without compromising on matters pertaining to religion.

According to reports, although they are not yet fully clarified, this is also the position of Mapai, and therefore it is to be expected that the elections will not take place.

It is surely superfluous to emphasize that if it is impossible to prevent elections, it is absolutely essential that there be a united religious front.

In accordance with the above, I have sent a telegram to your honor, and I thank you in advance if you will inform me of your perspective and actions regarding this matter.

With blessing.

As a matter of sharp wit, I would say that a united front—its necessity or the damage in it—is akin to the question of quantity and quality. And one should learn this from the measure of punishment. And according to what our Rabbeinu HaZaken wrote in Iggeret HaTeshuvah, Chapter 7 (97b): "For with a multitude, etc., they obscure, etc., **and more**." And the words of the Ran at the end of the second chapter of Yoma are well known, as is the ruling of our Rabbeinu in his Shulchan Aruch, Orach Chaim, section 328, subsection 16. And many examples were brought in Lekach Tov by the Mahar"i Engel, rule 15. It is understood that there are several distinctions in the matter. And this is not the place to elaborate.
