Greetings and blessings!

I received your letter, mentioning that there was supposed to be a meeting last week regarding your matters. Surely, if there is good news to report in this regard, you will inform me, and I too will rejoice.

With the blessing that the reading of this Shabbos be fulfilled in our immediate time: **"When you take (Ki Sisa)"** the head of the Children of Israel, in the year 5711 (Tisha), for "there is a mother to the reading" (a tradition of vocalization) and it is read as a full word (see the commentaries on Rashi at the end of Parshas Shelach; see also Tosafos, s.v. "Lo," Menachos 39a; Likutei Torah, Parshas Behar, discourse beginning "Es Shabbosai," end of section 1; and as stated in Zohar Vol. III, 267a: "And if the yud is missing, the chirik is in its place").

And with the blessing of a good Shabbos.

#### ***926***

**Moreinu HaRav Ephraim Eliezer HaKohen, may he live:** Yalles. Additional letters to him appear above, 906, and in the notes referenced there. **"When you take (Ki Sisa)... in the year 5711 (Tisha)":** In the dating of letters during the summer, it is customary to write "Tisha" (5711).

## 927

B"H, 24 Adar, 5711, Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Rabbi and Chossid, the G-d-fearing, learned, and distinguished, etc., our teacher Rabbi Moshe, may he live, and all those who join with him, may they live.

Greetings and blessings!

It was with pleasure that I read your letter regarding your gathering among anash to strengthen your connection with one another and your connection to the *ilana d'chaya*—the light of the teachings of Chassidus and the ways of Chassidus, the teachings of the words of the living G-d which our forefathers and our holy Nasi'im, the Admurim, have bequeathed to us, from the Baal Shem Tov, the Maggid, the Alter Rebbe, etc., until my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, may his merit shield us and all of Israel.

Our Sages said in Midrash Avkir, cited in Yalkut on the beginning of Parshas Vayakhel regarding the verse "And Moshe gathered": The Holy One, blessed be He, said (to Moshe), "Make for yourself large congregations and expound before them, etc., so that they may learn from you for future generations to gather congregations, etc., to teach and instruct the children of Israel, etc., so that My **great** Name may be glorified among My children."

From here we learn that when the "Moshe" of a congregation or group in Israel gathers members of his community and they learn there about the path in which they should walk, this is a glorification of His great Name, may He be blessed and exalted. As is known, the entire concept of a "name" in general is only necessary when there is an "other." So too, *kivayachol*, it is above: His Essence and Being, may He be blessed, is not hinted at by any letter or any stroke. His Names, may He be blessed, relate to the creation of the worlds. As our Sages said (Menachos 29b), with the *yud* (of the Ineffable Name—Havayah—) the World to Come was created, etc. He adds to them His "great Name," which refers to the **ability** to create worlds. But even before they were created, as our Sages said (Pirkei D'Rabbi Eliezer, ch. 3), before the world was created, He and His **great** Name alone existed. Even to such a level of G-dly holiness, one can reach a state of praise and glorification by speaking in a congregation and gathering about the words of Chassidus, which teach and demonstrate what is forbidden and what is permitted, and which is the path and the highway that ascends to the House of G-d.

Please convey my regards to all those who gathered, each and every one individually, and extend to them a blessing for success in their affairs, for livelihood, both material and spiritual, for each and every one in a manner appropriate for them in both material and spiritual matters.

With blessings for material and spiritual goodness.

***

**Rabbi Moshe:** Etter, Harrisburg.

## 928

B"H, 24 Adar, 5711, Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter informing me of the improvement in your wife’s health—may she live and be well—I am certain that you will continue to follow the doctors' instructions, and that she will remain strong in her trust in Hashem, that everything will be in its proper time and in good order.

I also suggest that before retiring to sleep (before *Krias Shema Al Hamitah*), she should recite the psalm *Yaancha* [Tehillim 20], and afterwards repeat the verse *Yaancha* once more. While reciting that verse, she should intend as if she had focused on all the *kavanos* associated with it.

With blessings that you should share good news.

## 929

B"H, 27 Adar Rishon, 5711, Brooklyn

Greetings and blessings!

I have already been distressed by your long silence, as I have received no news from you; therefore, I was all the more pleased to receive your letter with the news that, thank G-d, you are feeling an improvement in your condition. Naturally, I will read the *pidyon nefesh* you sent at the *tziyun* of my father-in-law, the Rebbe.

I will repeat once more: you should contemplate this in a way that anchors your thoughts firmly in the realization that Hashem is the One who leads His world, and each and every one of us individually. Consequently, this will remove worry from your heart, for it is surely clear that Hashem will manage matters in the best possible way, and the matter does not rest upon us. What pertains to us are only the matters of *Torah* and *mitzvos* that were given to us through free choice.

I do not mean to innovate here, for these matters are simple and known to all. However, if they remain merely as an encompassing concept, while in practice we behave as if things depend on us ourselves, we thereby make life burdensome—in the simplest, most literal sense, our physical life. This is not the case when one is permeated with the idea that "Hashem is my shepherd"; then, even the body and the *nefesh habehamis* feel the "I shall not want."

Heaven forbid that I am here to preach morality, but I am distressed by your distress and your anguish over reasons that have no foundation, and surely have no reality, as is known according to what is explained in *Chassidus* regarding the distinction between the matters of *nisyonos* and *birurim*.

I look forward to hearing good news from you regarding the improvement of your health and the health of your wife, may she live and be well.

With blessings.

## 530

530

B"H, 27 Adar Rishon, 5711, Brooklyn

To the G-d-fearing, honorable, and upright man, who conducts his business with integrity, etc.,
R' Yaakov, may he live, Hakohen

Peace and blessing!

In response to your letter of 23 Adar Rishon...

Regarding the situation in the shul, where you write that the financial state is critical and therefore the Rav, shlita, has not been paid his salary for two months, etc.—Mr. Levintansky, may he live, also spoke to me about this by telephone on Motzaei Shabbos. You are surely aware of this. I told him my opinion as well: that based on what I know of the attitude of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, toward your shul and your Rav, shlita, it occurs to me that in this instance, my father-in-law, the Rebbe, would have said that for the time being, the baalei-batim should cover the money, and at the first opportunity, you must conduct a drive, an appeal, or something similar to raise the funds to cover the deficit, and also establish a special fund for this purpose so that you do not have to rely on loans.

I am very surprised that you write nothing at all regarding the business of Mr. Yosef, may he live, Robinson. Hopefully, you will rectify this at the next opportunity.

I will conclude with a thought from the farbrengen of this past Shabbos, Parshas Vayakhel—in brief.

In Torah in general, and in Torah Shebichtav in particular, every word and even every letter is calculated. This is why we find that many halachos are derived from individual words or even individual letters. Nevertheless, we find that in the parshiyos of Vayakhel and Pekudei, the entire lengthy description of the kelei hamishkan and the bigdei kehunah is repeated, even though they were already described in minute detail in the parshiyos of Terumah and Tetzaveh.

Surely, one could have written briefly that the Yidden made the kelei hamikdash and the bigdei kehunah as Hashem commanded Moshe, and in doing so, saved dozens of pesukim in the Torah.

The answer to this is along the lines of the answer given to a similar question: Why are the offerings of the Nesi'im in Parshas Nasso repeated twelve times? The answer to that is that with the offerings of the Nesi'im, each Nasi achieved different things, as is hinted at in the Midrash to Parshas Nasso (Torah Or, end of Parshas Bereishis, 70, column 2; Likutei Torah, Parshas Berachah, page 98, column 3)[15].

In this same vein, one can answer the question regarding the sedras of Vayakhel and Pekudei:

When the kelei hamishkan and the bigdei kehunah were first described (Terumah, Tetzaveh), it was: a) from Hashem Himself, b) to Moshe Rabbeinu, to whom there arose none like him, c) when Moshe Rabbeinu was on Mount Sinai, when he stood on a level incomparably higher than when he was below, for there he ate no bread and drank no water. However, the kelei hamikdash and bigdei kehunah as they are described in Vayakhel and Pekudei are as they were actually made: a) by Yidden, b) down here below, c) from physical gold, silver, copper, etc. Nevertheless, despite this great difference between the potential and the actual, it was when the ultimate desire of Hashem was fulfilled and His promise of "I will dwell among them" was realized—specifically in the physical Mishkan of Vayakhel and Pekudei, and not in the spiritual Mishkan of the "that which you were shown on the mountain."

The lesson for us is that one should not feel dejected, thinking, "How can we possibly perform a deed of the Divine Will or align with the Divine intent?" especially when each of us knows the standing and state in which he finds himself, and in general, we find ourselves in the double and redoubled darkness of this bitter galus. But, even so, Hashem promises that if one is only a *nadiv lev*—meaning, if one does a deed with Yiddishe and Chassidishe warmth and heart—then the "I will dwell among them" is present, and **Hashem** helps to carry it out and align it with the Divine intent.

...Enclosed is a receipt.

Regarding the question of the shul, I have written in the same vein to Mr. Levintansky, may he live, as well.

His father replied that it is so that one may see the virtues of another with the right eye, and see one’s own shortcomings with the left eye.

I am enclosing an excerpt from my remarks at the farbrengen this past Shabbos.

## 432

B"H, 28 Adar Rishon, 5711, Brooklyn

...And if he will listen to my advice, he should endeavor to find a rabbinical position. Regarding what he writes—that until now he has been unable to remain in a community for long because a G-d-fearing Rav is not to the liking of the *baalei batim*—on the contrary, for that very reason he should remain in the community and influence them to strengthen themselves in the spirit of Yiddishkeit through the study of Torah and the performance of *mitzvos maasiyos*.

We have heard a general directive that the vessel for success in both material and spiritual matters is the study of Torah. It is highly appropriate that he also set aside times for the study of Chassidus, for it is the *pnimiyus haTorah* (inner dimension of the Torah) and provides light and strength to the "candle of the mitzvah and the light of Torah."

With blessings for a proper arrangement for him and his family *shiyeh*, with revealed good.

## 833

833

B.H., 28 Adar I, 5711, Brooklyn

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, and distinguished individual, a man of noble character, etc.,
R' Moshe, may he live.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter from Sunday, Parshas Tetzaveh, which was received with some delay, and my response has been delayed due to the press of many matters—please accept my apologies—as well as regarding your letter from Tuesday, Parshas Vayakhel...

Enclosed is the receipt for your contribution to the **"Ohalei Yosef Yitzchak Lubavitch"** institutions in North Africa, which, thank G-d, are continuing to develop. However, it is fitting that these institutions, which are named after my father-in-law, the Rebbe, should grow and expand much further, and that their development should not be hindered by financial obstacles or delays. Yet, the unfortunate reality is that a lack of funds is a hindrance, and hundreds and thousands of Jewish boys and girls in the cities and villages of North Africa are still growing up without Torah. But, thank G-d, our institutions—a teachers' seminary, a yeshiva, a yeshiva ketana, a Talmud Torah for boys, a Talmud Torah for girls, and evening classes for tradesmen and merchants—have already established a name for themselves and serve as an encouraging symbol of what can be accomplished in practice with the help of Hashem and the participation of friends who love Torah. If they could see with their own eyes how they are transforming their physical means into spirituality, they would surely volunteer more than enough with extra effort.

As you requested, tomorrow, G-d willing, on Erev Rosh Chodesh, when I am at the Tziyun of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, I will mention you, your wife, and your family, may they live, for blessings and long, good years.

Enclosed is what I wrote to someone regarding the topics of the day from the farbrengen of this past Shabbos.

I will conclude with a blessing that Hashem should grant you and your wife, may you live, long days and good years, with an abundance of Yiddishe nachas and Chassidishe nachas from all your family members, may they live, and from yourselves as well. May you be able to increase in tzedakah and good deeds for the strengthening of Yiddishkeit and the dissemination of Torah in general, and the teachings of Chassidus in particular. This is the intent of "long days and years" according to what my father-in-law, the Rebbe, explained: that it is not only that they are long in quantity, but that they are also long in quality—meaning they are filled and overflowing with Torah, mitzvos, and good deeds, and full of the light and vitality of the teachings of Chassidus.

With blessings.

## 434

B”H, 29 Adar Rishon, 5711, Brooklyn

Greetings and blessings!

I have been informed that your daughter, may she live and be well, has already had her engagement with her fiancé, may he live and be well. I hereby wish you a hearty Mazal Tov. May this union be in a good and auspicious hour, and may you and your wife, may you live and be well, derive from them and from all your other children, may they live and be well, much nachas and pleasure—an *iddishen un chassidishen nachas*.

However, on the other hand, I have been told that there is a concern that your daughter’s resolve to wear a *sheitel* has weakened. I do not know what influence caused this weakening of her resolve, but surely you are making the appropriate efforts, in a calm and gentle manner, to ensure that she fulfills her promise in this regard. As I said when they were here, this is not merely a question of wearing a *sheitel*, but rather *fun a gantzen shtel in lebn* (of one’s entire stance in life).

I am writing to her specifically regarding this.

And although it is surely unnecessary, I will repeat once again that through matters of closeness and speaking with gentleness, one *kanen gar a sach* (can accomplish a great deal).

Furthermore, your son, may he live and be well, told me that your daughter, may she live and be well, spoke with them regarding several details concerning the time of the wedding and its style.

I do not know to what extent she is firm on this matter, but in general, when one grants a concession in secondary matters, one succeeds in obtaining a concession in essential matters. And for someone like you, further elaboration on this is unnecessary.

To conclude with a matter of the day, I am enclosing a segment from the *farbrengen* of this past Shabbos, although it is recorded only in brief.

With blessings for proper health—and for your wife, may she live and be well, in particular—and with blessings of Mazal Tov to you both.

## 3535

B"H, Rosh Chodesh Adar, 5711, Brooklyn.

It is known from our Sages that even those who can justly say of themselves, "I am asleep in exile," their hearts are awake—especially when one awakens them with Chassidic warmth and with words that come from the heart.

With blessings.

With blessing and regards to the entire group, may they live,

## 938

B"H, Rosh Chodesh Adar Rishon, 5711, Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, and distinguished, etc., Rabbi Tzvi, may he live:

Peace and blessing!

In response to your letters of the 10th and 17th of the past month of Adar Rishon:

It is difficult to establish **rules** regarding your question of whether to speak at gatherings of non-Chareidi parties or organizations.

On one hand, it is correct to utilize every opportunity that arises to influence **various** circles of our fellow Jews, to bring them closer to Yiddishkeit, Torah, and mitzvos.

On the other hand, one must be careful that by participating in their gathering, it should not be interpreted—*oistaitzen*—as a form of validation for their ideologies, or at the very least, for their activities.

Regarding the practical application, one must preempt—*bavaren*—the latter concern, and speak in any place suitable for sowing a seed of Yiddishkeit and yiras shamayim. In the **overwhelming** majority of cases, such sowing leads to growth, whether on the spot or, at the very least, after some time.

I trust you are meeting with Mr. ... and his wife, may they live, and that you will diplomatically endeavor to ensure they practically fulfill what we discussed when they were here regarding taharas hamishpachah.

I hope you will share good news with me that the son of Mr. ... also began putting on tefillin. *Un vos darf er zich shpiln mitn Oibershten?* (And why must he play games with the Almighty?)

...As you requested, I mentioned you and your family, may they live, when I was yesterday—Erev Rosh Chodesh—at the Ohel of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, regarding what they need.

With blessing and regards to all his colleagues, may they live.

## 939

By the Grace of Hashem, Erev Rosh Chodesh Adar Sheni, 5711, Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, learned, and distinguished, etc., R' Ephraim, may he live:

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letters of 26 Teves, 7 Shevat, and 16 Shevat:

Regarding the third birthday of your son, may he live, I send my blessing that you may raise him, together with your other children, may they live, for Torah, for the chuppah, and for good deeds, in comfort and abundance. Enclosed is an excerpt from a letter of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, regarding the custom of cutting the hair at three years old (specifically then, and not before).

May it be the will of Hashem that very soon you will share good news regarding the good health of your wife, may she live, as well as the health of your sons, may they live, and their success—the older ones in their studies, and the younger ones in their development, both physically and in a soul of holiness. As is known, there are several levels of the entry of a soul of holiness that are dependent on time—

—and these precede those that are dependent on a person’s avodah, as the Sages say in *Zohar* (Vol. III, 94b): "If he merits more, they give him more, etc.; if he merits more, they give him more, etc."—

And these are: at the mitzvah of milah (and for a daughter, it is as if she is circumcised—*Avodah Zarah* 27a; this can be explained as being at the naming, just as for a son we give the name no later than the time of his milah, although we find instances even earlier, such as Rachel with Binyamin and the daughter-in-law of Eli the Kohen), when he reaches the age of chinuch, when he becomes obligated in mitzvos (see *Shulchan Aruch HaRav*, Orach Chaim, Second Edition, end of section 4), and at twenty years old (see *Likutei Torah*, Bamidbar, discourse starting *Mi Ben Esrim*)—which means nineteen years and thirty days, or twenty years minus thirty days (depending on the two opinions brought in *Shulchan Aruch*, Even HaEzer, section 155, subsection 12; see also *Hilchos Talmud Torah* by our Rebbe the Alter Rebbe, end of chapter 1, in the *Kuntrus Acharon*).

Thus, as he grows in years, he also approaches a higher level of the entry of a soul of holiness.

In response to your question: Since your avodah is in Lod and you are successful in it, it is appropriate that your family also move there and that you all be together...

Regarding your question about teaching Chassidus to Sephardim (adults or children):

In the *Ahalei Yosef Yitzchak-Lubavitch* yeshivos and Talmud Torahs that we opened in Morocco, they study Tanya, *Likutei Torah*, the *Kuntrusim*, etc., and we see success and the entry of a spirit of life into their Talmud Torah and their observance of mitzvos. Similarly, the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, learned, and distinguished, etc., R' Shmuel Levitin, may he live, relates that he once asked my father-in-law, the Rebbe (the Rebbe Rashab), of blessed memory, regarding the country of Georgia, and he answered him that they should study it. They did so in practice, and there are already great, great scholars from that study.

And if that was the case at that time, how much more so now, when we have drawn closer by decades to the coming of our Moshiach. We have seen tangibly from my father-in-law, the Rebbe, a great and vast effort in spreading the wellsprings of Chassidus in many different ways and in all circles that it is possible to reach—*dergreichen*—them.

May the knowledge of Hashem increase, and may the Master come to reveal the inner reasons of Torah, and "the earth shall be full of the knowledge of Hashem."

With blessings for success in your holy work, and abundant success in your personal affairs—in both material and spiritual matters.

...And regarding the cutting of the hair—*upsherenish*—it is a significant matter in the custom of Israel. Its essence is in the chinuch of leaving the *peios* of the head. From the day of the cutting and the leaving of the *peios*, it is customary to be diligent in accustoming the child to wearing *tzitzis*, the morning blessings, Grace After Meals, and the *Krias Shema* before retiring. May Hashem be their helper that you may raise him for Torah, for the chuppah, and for good deeds, with livelihood in abundance and peace of mind, both materially and spiritually.

## 940

940

B"H,

Our Torah, in all its parts, is a *Toras Chaim*—a living Torah—and it is eternal. My revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, explained that "a living Torah" means "a Torah that provides instruction for every individual in their daily life," in the life of the individual, and all the more so in the life of the collective. There are many matters in the Torah that, **at first glance**, one might assume have no relevance to practical life in these days, or to the situation in which we currently find ourselves. Yet, upon reflection, one can find in them a parallel to the present situation—whether in a subtle way or the opposite—and derive from these matters clear instructions and absolute directives regarding practical action: "Arise and do," or "Take heed, lest you do."

This is also the case regarding the *maamar* printed herein.

It demands with intensity that one stand "with *mesiras nefesh* in the actual fulfillment of Torah and *mitzvos*" and, in particular, regarding education—without concern for the enemy, "the enemy who fights openly," and without concern for the avenger, "the hidden enemy who devises schemes... regarding the matter of vengeance, which goes beyond the bounds of the law."

And it promises that these children—who will continue to be *tinokos shel beis raban*, or whom one will now make into *tinokos shel beis raban* despite all the decrees, intimidations, stratagems, and deceptions—their study and education are precisely what will silence these enemies and avengers. On the contrary, through this *mesiras nefesh*, they will merit the *Geulah*.

Even now, in every country, there are those—whether enemies who fight openly or avengers who fight with stratagems—whose intent is one and the same: control over the children. Their goal is the same as the goal of Achaz: "If there are no small ones, there are no adults... no students... no sages... no Torah... and the *Ribono shel Olam* will not cause His *Shechinah* to dwell in the world."

Just as it was promised then, so it is promised now: that through **mesiras nefesh and standing without fear** in the fulfillment of Torah and *mitzvos*, and in the matter of education in particular, all the stratagems and decrees "that Torah should be forgotten, *chas v'shalom*, from Yisrael, and to lead them astray, *chas v'shalom*, from *Elokus*" will not succeed. The children will be "for signs and wonders in Yisrael," and "the foundation for 'and your people are all righteous.'"

And great is the power of this *mesiras nefesh* to merit, through it, the complete and true *Geulah*, which will come speedily in our days through *Moshiach Tzidkeinu*.

**Menachem Schneerson**

7 Adar II, 5711. Brooklyn, N.Y.

## 941

B"H, 7 Adar II, 5711, Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, learned, and accomplished, etc., Rabbi Y. [may he live],

Greetings and blessings!

Enclosed is the *kuntres* for the upcoming days of Purim. I am certain you will share it with all those under your influence, so that they may study it, and learn and teach, observe and perform and fulfill the conclusion and the "therefore" (*uvchein*) of the *maamar* printed in the *kuntres*.

This is: despite the trials, distractions, and confusions—to stand firm in the actual fulfillment of Torah and *mitzvos*, and in particular, to add courage, with extra effort, in the *avodah* of proper *chinuch*—to teach the sons and daughters of Yisrael the *mitzvos* of Hashem and His Torah.

And if there are places where, through open decrees or deceitful stratagems, they wish to "seize the *batei knesios* and *batei medrashos*" in order to cause the children of Yisrael, *chas v'shalom*, to forget the Torah of Hashem and His *mitzvos*, and to lead them astray, *chas v'shalom*, from *Elokus*—

One must know that specifically during a time of decree, when the concealments and hiddenness have multiplied to the point where they "place darkness for light" (matters that should have been used to increase the light of holiness are being used to increase the darkness of the *kelipos* and *sitra achra*),

"At that very moment, strength is given from Above to transform the darkness into light that is good."

And when we guard—even to the point of *mesiras nefesh*—the young boys and girls, then, according to the language of the *Midrash*, when there are children, there are adults, there are sages, there are elders, there is Torah, there are *batei knesios* and *batei medrashos*. And the ultimate purpose of everything is that the Holy One, Blessed be He, causes His *Shechinah* to dwell in the world—in this lower, physical world—because the *sitra achra* is subdued and the darkness is transformed into light, so that the light of *Ohr Ein Sof* may shine.

With blessings for a joyous Purim and regards to the entire group,

**Menachem Schneerson**

## 943

B"H, 8 Adar Sheni, 5711, Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings to the esteemed Rabbi, the G-d-fearing man, a man of action, who leads his community with integrity, who illuminates and shines, whose words are pleasant and whose insights are clear, of distinguished lineage, etc., our teacher Rabbi Meir Abihatzira, leader of the holy community of Midelt, may it be established.

Greetings and blessings!

From time to time, I receive reports regarding what is transpiring in your camp through the esteemed Rabbi and Chassid, the G-d-fearing man, a man of many accomplishments, engaged in the work of Heaven, etc., our teacher Rabbi Michael Lipskar, may he live.

I am certain that you, too, will gladden me with good news that rejoices the heart regarding the expansion of the Torah institutions, "Ohalei Yosef Yitzchak - Lubavitch," in your pure camp—Torah that teaches the precepts of Hashem, which are upright and gladden the heart, and which produces Torah scholars from the very beginning.

I am writing now to express my profound gratitude for the book *Machsof HaLavan* that you sent. It is a significant matter; see Zohar Vol. I, 161b: "The white peeling, where the white is revealed over the red, and all this is in order to draw down to this level of the source of blessings from the Source of all," etc. And there, 162a: "And the white is engraved upon the colors and ascends above all the colors; this is what is written, 'the white peeling,' etc., and then, 'Hashem is my shepherd, I shall not want,' and it is written, 'He makes me lie down in green pastures,' etc." See there.

I am enclosing the *Kuntres* for the upcoming days of Purim, which we have just printed from the teachings of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, the tzaddik who is the foundation of the world, who awakens compassion to bestow blessing and success upon all of Israel, and especially upon those who provide *nachas ruach* to his soul in the Garden of Eden and in this world (Yevamos 97a) through supporting educational institutions for the sons and daughters of Israel in the spirit of our ancestors. For when there are kids, there are goats; when there are little ones, there are adults, there are sages, there are elders, there is Torah, there are synagogues and *batei medrash* (based on the language of the Midrash—cited in the *Kuntres*). And the ultimate purpose of all this is that the Holy One, blessed be He, causes His *Shechinah* to dwell in the world—in this lower, physical world—because the *sitra achra* is subjugated and the darkness is transformed into light, so that the light of *Ohr Ein Sof* may shine.

With blessings for a joyous Purim and regards to the entire group, may all of Israel be united, and peace to all his offspring.

## 944

B"H, 8 Adar Sheni, 5711, Brooklyn.

To the great Gaon, the G-d-fearing man, a man of Torah and noble lineage, a man of action and many accomplishments, a master of good deeds, who sits in judgment and leads his community beside still waters, our master, Rabbi Refael Baruch, may he live, the leader of the holy community of the city of Meknes, whose influence extends throughout the entire country.

Peace and abundant blessing!

From time to time, I receive reports regarding what is happening in your camp through the great Gaon and Chossid, the G-d-fearing man of action, who is engaged in the work of Heaven, etc., Rabbi Michael, may he live, Lipskar.

I am certain that you, too, will gladden me with good news that brings joy to the heart regarding the expansion of the "Ohalei Yosef Yitzchak - Lubavitch" institutions in your pure camp—Torah that teaches the upright statutes of Hashem which gladden the heart, and Torah scholars, Torah scholars from the beginning.

The reason for my writing at this time is to send herewith the Kuntres for the upcoming days of Purim, which we have just printed from the teachings of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, whose soul is in Eden. He is the *tzaddik* and foundation of the world, who awakens compassion to bestow blessing and success upon all of us, and especially upon those who provide *nachas ruach* to his soul in the Garden of Eden and in this world (Yevamos 97a) by supporting educational institutions for the sons and daughters of Israel in the spirit of the elders of Israel. As the Midrash states (quoted in the Kuntres), when there are kids, there are goats; when there are young ones, there are elders; there are sages; there are the aged; there is Torah; there are synagogues and houses of study—and the ultimate purpose of it all is that the Holy One, Blessed be He, causes His *Shechinah* to dwell in the world, in this lowly, physical world, for through *iskafya* of the *sitra achra* and *is'hapcha* of darkness into light, the light of *Ohr Ein Sof* will shine.

With blessings for the joy of Purim and regards to the group, may they live, who are friends in the one Torah of the one Hashem.

#### 944

**Rabbi Refael Baruch:** Toledano. Additional letters to him appear in Vol. 3, 742, and in the notes referenced there.

## 945

945

B"H, 11 Adar II, 5711, Brooklyn.

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, learned, and reliable man, who conducts his business with integrity and is involved in communal needs, etc., R' Y. HaKohen, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

I received your letters from Erev Rosh Chodesh Adar II and from Friday, Adar II, and due to a multitude of preoccupations, I have not had the opportunity to respond until now. Surely you will not take it amiss...

I acknowledge the *tzedakah* for my discretion that you sent, which I have divided into two parts: one half toward the obligation to print the *piskei dinim*, and one half for our joint work overseas. Regarding *kabbalos*, as long as you do not write that they should be sent, they are not sent.

Regarding the matters of our friend, the esteemed, G-d-fearing, learned, and reliable man, etc., R' Yosef, may he live, Robinson, it is a great wonder to me that you have not yet received the loan. I hope to be at the *tziyun* of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, on Erev Purim, and since the checks are still with you, perhaps you will hold them until after Purim.

Enclosed is the receipt for the donation of $3,535 for the *ilui neshama* of Ephraim, of blessed memory, Golub.

Perhaps you could inform me of the name of the mother of the deceased.

A heartfelt *yasher koach* for the good news regarding Mr. [Name], may he live. It surprises me that he has not written to me, as he promised to write the good news.

Did he convey to you the content of our conversation, when he committed to give $3,000 to print the *seforim* of my father-in-law, the Rebbe? I replied to him that he must ensure that his son begins to put on *tefillin* daily immediately. Only after he reiterated regarding the money did I tell him that three is not necessary; two and a half will suffice, and that will go toward the printing of the *seforim* as mentioned above. I hope he will keep both promises—both regarding *tefillin* and regarding the commitment for the donation—and may we be able to share good news with one another always, all the days.

Since I do not have the address of Mr. [Name], may he live, I would like to trouble you to deliver the enclosed letter and receipt, and I thank you in advance for the trouble.

With the blessing of *Simchas Purim* and all the best.

## 940

B"H, 11 Adar Sheni, 5711, Brooklyn

Greetings and blessings!

I was pleased to receive good regards from you through our friend, the G-d-fearing man, a man of truth, who occupies himself with the needs of the community and contemplates good things, etc., etc., R' Yaakov HaKohen Katz, may he live, as well as the check as a start toward your undertaking to print a sefer from the works of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory.

I hope that you surely remember our conversation when you were here, and that your son, may he live, puts on tefillin daily, as I spoke with you, and will continue to do so; this will bring blessing and success to him and to you in all matters.

Since Purim is approaching, which is associated with joy among Jews, I would like to conclude with a thought that my father-in-law, the Rebbe, explained in the sicha of Purim 5701, when the decrees of that time began:

The essence of Purim is that, notwithstanding the decree that Haman the wicked sought to carry out against the Jews because they were Jews, the Jews held even more firmly to their Yiddishkeit and were proud of it. Therefore, the decree was nullified and it became *v'nahafoch hu*—from sorrow to joy. So too in all times: when we Jews are proud of the fact that we are Jews and hold firmly to Yiddishkeit, regardless of the obstacles this brings, we will be liberated from all Hamans—both the Hamans in gashmius and the Hamans in ruchnius—and it will be "for the Jews, light and joy, and gladness and honor."

With blessings for a joyous Purim and regards to your son, may he live.

## 947

B"H, 11 Adar Sheni, 5711, Brooklyn

And may this be not only with physical tranquility, but also with spiritual tranquility.

The good deeds you have performed until now, especially the printing of "Sdei Chemed," as well as the fact that you have taken it upon yourself to work for the benefit of supporting the mosdos of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, should stand by you and all your family to continue to bring blessing and success in all matters. May you very soon be able to fulfill your promise to support the aforementioned mosdos with a generous hand, and have the ability to increase your assistance as the work requires and as your Jewish heart desires.

Please convey a blessing of mazal tov in connection with the bris to the parents of the newborn, your son R' Yisrael Zalman, may he live, and his wife, Mrs. Freidel, may she live, and to the grandmother, Mrs. Rachel, may she live, and the great-grandmother, Mrs. Breindel, may she live, for long and good years.

With the blessing of Simchas Purim.

## 944

944

B"H, 12 Adar Rishon, 5711, Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

Your letter of 4 Shevat and the accompanying list were received, and I read them at the tziyun of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, to arouse rachamei shamayim for what is needed for them...

Regarding your question about registering for immigration to Canada, since for the time being you are not being granted papers for the United States, and this registration does not disqualify your rights to apply for the United States later—accordingly, there is no contradiction here at all, and may it be with success.

However, in general, anash should take an interest in moving to Australia, for according to reports from there, it is a place of parnassah. It is to be hoped that with the help of Hashem, a Chassidic center will be built there. The sooner more of anash arrive there, the sooner the building and refinement of this center and the spreading of the maayanos will be advanced. For those who do not yet require a yeshiva for their children, it would be appropriate for them to move there, and it will be good in both gashmius and ruchnius alike.

You have surely already received the Kuntres for Purim and the general letter enclosed with it, and you have shared them with the public in an appropriate manner.

With blessings that you should report good news, and regards to the entire group.

## 949

By the Grace of Hashem, 12 Adar II, 5711, Brooklyn

To the members of the administration of the Yeshiva and Talmud Torah of the Russian immigrants, Lod, may Hashem grant them life,

Peace and blessing!

I received with pleasure your letter of 23 Adar I, along with the detailed report regarding the activities of the Yeshiva, both in the physical and spiritual realms. I was also pleased to see the list of students, including their mothers' names, which, G-d willing, I will read tomorrow at the holy resting place of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory.

Due to the pressures and preparations for the upcoming Purim, time does not permit me to respond at length to your request for my opinion regarding your letter and the aforementioned report. I will suffice here with a few general remarks, and first:

In days of old, the primary function of the Yeshivos and Talmud Torahs was the study of Torah and progress therein. The practical observance of mitzvos and the preservation of Jewish customs were understood as a matter of course for every Jewish boy and girl, through the education they received in their homes and in the environment where they spent the hours they were not within the walls of the beis medrash and the Yeshiva.

Times have changed in these days of ours. Now, the function of the Yeshiva and Talmud Torah is also, and primarily, to make the student, first and foremost, a yirei shamayim — a Jew who observes Torah and mitzvos — and only afterwards a scholar. In the Yeshivos founded by our Nesi’im, it is also to make them a Chassid.

There is no need to elaborate that the main thing is the actual observance of Torah and mitzvos, for "action is the ultimate," and the purpose of everything is the matter of yiras shamayim, as it is said, "And Hashem commanded us to perform all these statutes... to fear Hashem, our G-d."

As a direct result of these matters, it is incumbent upon every Talmud Torah and Yeshiva in general, and the Yeshivos founded by our Nesi’im, the Nesi’im of Chabad, in particular, to concentrate all efforts to achieve, first and foremost, the primary goal: that the students should be *frume erliche Yidden, varime Yidden, Chassidishe Yidden* (pious, honest Jews, warm Jews, Chassidic Jews). With this perspective in mind, in response to your request for my opinion regarding the curriculum of the Yeshiva and Talmud Torah, I offer these remarks:

(a) In the curriculum of all departments, one must include the study of *dinim* (laws) and Jewish customs, both in the lower and higher grades, and it is understood — each according to its level.

(b) Make the greatest effort regarding the arrangement of Shabbos, Yomim Tovim, Chol Hamoed, etc., in the students' lives, in such a way that the laws of Israel and its customs become ingrained in them as a matter of course, through their participation in the order and customs of the days of Shabbos, the celebration of Purim, the conducting of the Pesach Seder, etc., etc. It is known that what can be learned from *maaseh rav* (the conduct of a master) as a matter of course is sometimes much more than what can be taught to students through speech and instruction.

(c) Seemingly, the study of Gemara and the like should be in the morning at the beginning of the study session, and the study of Chumash, etc., which does not require such concentration of thought, can be in the afternoon hours, and not the other way around.

(d) It is proper to institute the study of Chassidus before davening. I am surprised that this has not been done yet; perhaps it was omitted from your report by mistake. As is known, this was the custom from days of old in all our Yeshivos, and even the custom of *baalei batim* in their homes.

(e) Surely there are groups of students among you who are also suited for the study of *poskim*.

(f) The study of Chumash with Rashi on their own — for those students who do not study this in the Yeshiva curriculum.

(g) To institute the recitation of Tehillim after davening.

We must learn a moral lesson, *halacha l'maaseh* (in practical terms), from the matters of the day, and according to what is written in the *Kuntres* for Purim of this year, which is:

Despite the trials, pressures, and confusions — to stand firm in the practical observance of Torah and mitzvos, and especially to add courage, with extra effort, in the work of proper education, to teach the sons and daughters of Israel the mitzvos of Hashem and His Torah.

And if there are places where, through open decrees or deceitful schemes, they wish to "seize the synagogues and houses of study" to "make the children of Israel forget, G-d forbid, the Torah of Hashem and His mitzvos, and to lead them astray, G-d forbid, from Elokus," one must know that precisely in the time of the decree, when the concealments and hiddenness increase, to the point where they turn light into darkness (matters that should have been used to increase the light of holiness are used to increase the darkness of the *kelipos* and *sitra achra*) — "it is then that power is given from above to turn the darkness into light, for it is good."

And when we guard — even to the point of *mesiras nefesh* — the young boys and girls, then, according to the language of the Midrash, when there are young ones, there are adults, there are sages, there are elders, there is Torah, there are synagogues and houses of study — and the purpose of everything — the Holy One, blessed be He, causes His Shechinah to dwell in the world, in this lower, physical world, for the *sitra achra* is subdued and the darkness is transformed into light, so that the light of the *Ein Sof*, blessed be He, may shine.

With blessings for a joyous Purim and regards to the entire group, may they live,

**M. Schneerson**

## 950

B"H, 12 Adar Sheni, 5711, Brooklyn

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, and distinguished, R' Avraham Chanoch, may he live:

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter from the 5th of Adar Sheni:

Our Sages have already ruled (Avos 3:5) that whoever accepts upon himself the **yoke** of Torah, the yoke of government and the yoke of worldly affairs are removed from him. All of the attributes of the Ribono shel Olam are measure for measure, and that which is written and recorded in the Tzeivos Hashem in actuality (and not merely in potential, which is the case for all Bnei Yisrael) naturally emerges with a high hand.

The concept of Tzeivos Hashem has already been explained in the *hemshech* of the *maamarim* of the *histalkus*.

I have received the package of copies of the letters of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, that you sent,

And although I have not yet had the opportunity to review them as required, nor the list of *sichos* included there, it is my hope to do so in the near future, and I will then inform you regarding those that are missing from the archive in my possession.

With blessings for a happy Purim.

**R' Ephraim Eliezer, may he live:** Yalles. Additional letters to him – see above 950 [sic], and the references in the notes there.

## 951

B"H, 12 Adar II, 5711, Brooklyn.

The illustrious Rabbi and Chossid, G-d-fearing, of noble lineage, etc., etc., Moreinu HaRav Efraim Eliezer, may he live, HaKohen.

Peace and blessing!

With pleasure and delight—*b'noam u'v'taanug*—I received (in the sense of *angerirt*, see *Likutei Torah*, beginning of Parshas Shemini, 18a, column 1, at the end) your letter, informing me that you were chosen at the conference of Rabbis convened by the heads of the city committee to serve as *Ra'avad* (Head of the Rabbinical Court).

May it be the will of Hashem that you succeed in this position to draw into the **Beis Din** (which represents *Gevuros*) the quality of **Av** (the Merciful One, the Compassionate, see *Likutei Torah*, *Drushei Rosh Hashanah*, *d'h Shehe'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he' 'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he'he

## 952

B"H, 12 Adar Sheni, 5711, Brooklyn.

To the illustrious Rabbi, the chossid, G-d-fearing, and refined, of the holy seed, etc.,
Rabbi Y.Y. shlita,

Shalom u’vracha!

I received your letter, along with the four pages from the sefer *Chakal Yitzchak*, in due time.

I have taken them and am responding by enclosing a *kuntres* that I published for the upcoming days of Purim. It contains the teachings of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, and you will surely find much of interest in it.

Thank you very much for the few details you wrote regarding the passing of the father of the *Tanya*. I would be most grateful if you could also share any other details you know regarding this from a reliable source, as the verified information we have on this subject is **extremely** scarce; even the year of his passing is unknown.

In any event, as a brief note regarding the pages from the sefer you sent, and in connection with the current time, one should examine the *Shaar HaPurim* by the Mitteler Rebbe, son of the author of the *Tanya*, in the *maamar* beginning "Yavi'u Levush" (page 92b). He explains, in his own way, the dispute between Beis Shammai and Beis Hillel, **as well as the opinion of Rashbi that they were created together**, which is not as clearly understood from the pages you sent. He brings that "Es HaShamayim V'Es HaAretz" (Bereishis 1:1) is an acronym for the Holy Name *Ahu"h* (Zohar Vol. I, 251a), and also an acronym for "the garment and the horse." Please see there.

With blessings for a happy Purim.

***

**952**

**Rabbi Y.Y.:** Weiss. **Regarding the passing of the father of the Tanya:** The elders of Szöllős told me that before he passed away, the *gabbai* of the *chevra kadisha* asked him for the addresses of his sons so he could notify them to say Kaddish. He told them he had three sons, but he only gave the addresses for two of them, saying, "My Zalman will already know on his own." It is also accepted that on the first yahrtzeit, which fell on the 8th of Tishrei—the thirteen attributes—the holy *Tanya* was in Szöllős, and on that holy day, he traveled to the city of Munkács.

## 953

953

B"H, 12 Adar Sheni, 5711, Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Rabbi and Chossid, G-d-fearing and Torah-learned, etc., etc., Moreinu Harav Sh.Y. (may he live),

Greetings and blessings!

My telegram and letter regarding the elections and their cancellation have surely been received, and you will respond to them...

**A note in passing:** The commentators on the Megillas Esther were puzzled as to the relevance of the homiletical interpretation (derashah), "Do not read [it as] 'your children' (banayich), but 'your builders' (bonayich)."

Seemingly, one could explain this by first addressing another difficulty: what is the proof from this verse that the **attribute of Hashem** is one of increase? The answer is that we interpret it as "bonayich" (with a kamatz under the nun), referring to Hashem, who made you and established you (yichonenecha) with every type of foundation. It is just that the printer followed the version found in Berachos, etc., and **mistakenly** printed "bonayich" with a yud.

Enclosed is the Kuntres for Purim and a copy of a letter pertaining to it, which I hope will be of interest to you.

I sign with blessings for a joyous Purim.

**Moreinu Harav Sh.Y.:** Zevin. Additional letters to him are found above, 913, and in the references noted there.
