## 995

B”H, 21 Adar Sheni, 5711, Brooklyn

Greetings and blessings!

I was distressed to hear from your husband, the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing man, active in communal affairs, etc., that you are feeling broken and are finding it difficult to recover from the situation that has occurred, *l’o aleinu*.

In general, all Jews—both men and women—are believers, the children of believers. This means that everyone believes, and understands intellectually as well, that Hashem, and He alone, directs the world.

Furthermore, all Jews believe with complete faith that Hashem is *tachlis hatov*, goodness itself.

You have surely also heard the teaching from my father-in-law, the Rebbe, *ztzuklalleh*, which he relayed in the name of the Baal Shem Tov: that every Jew, man or woman, is as precious to Hashem as an only child is to a father (in truth, even more so, but we use this example because we cannot imagine a love greater than that for an only child).

From all of this, it follows naturally that everything Hashem does is *letov*, for the good. And since Hashem desires that Jews have goodness not only in *ruchniyus* but also in *gashmiyus*, this good is certainly not limited to *ruchniyus* but extends to *gashmiyus* as well.

As mentioned, all Jews believe this, and one understands it intellectually.

However, it happens in some cases that this remains only in one’s belief and intellect, and unfortunately does not reach the feelings of the heart. Consequently, it becomes manifest to the person that certain events are a cause for brokenness and sadness, *chas v’shalom*. And since this is how it appears to them, while the true intent—that this is for the good—remains hidden in the intellect, it can also happen that the event which made a negative impression remains with its true intent—the *tachlis hatov*—hidden from the human eye, and it is not illuminated.

If, however, one works on oneself to bring this faith and understanding down into the feelings of the heart—to the point where one feels that it cannot be otherwise, that *kol man d’avid Rachmana* (everything the Merciful One does) is *l’tav avid* (done for the good) in a manifest way—until the heart feels this as well, then that person sees the good in a manifest way too. Hashem’s reward is *midah k’neged midah*—of the same nature: Hashem reveals to everyone, and especially to the person themselves, the good that was hidden within that event, and one sees it even with physical eyes.

Needless to say, this is difficult work to accomplish within oneself. However, this work is easier for those who were raised by Chassidishe parents, for those who married Chassidim, and for those who have established their home in a Chassidishe manner, so that it is permeated with the *ruach hachassidus* and the *minhagei hachassidim*.

I wish for you that very soon Hashem will reveal to you, together with your husband *shiy* and your son *shiy*, the *tachlis hatov* that exists in the various events in your life which you have not seen until now, and that you may all be happy together, in *gashmiyus* and in *ruchniyus*.

With blessings.

## Tiskenu

*[21 Adar, 5711]*

I have duly received your two letters, one undated and the second from the 22nd of Adar. Unfortunately, due to a multitude of preoccupations, I have not had the opportunity to answer them until now.

Enclosed, I am sending you the *kuntres* for Purim and the *kuntres* for the 2nd of Nissan. And now, to address your letters:

I was extremely pleased to read that you are working with your *koach hatziur* (power of artistic expression) and preparing for an exhibition, and that the press has written good reviews about you. Surely you will see yourself rising in this and utilizing the *kishron* (talent) that Hashem has given you to bring *chizuk* in *Yiddishkeit* and *yiras shamayim*.

Regarding the main point of your letter, where you complain about your status and situation, feel very broken, at times fall into despair, find no place for yourself, and the like—and for this reason, you wish to see me so that we might speak face to face:

While seeing one another is a fine thing for two good friends and brings spiritual satisfaction to both sides, to postpone everything until then, and in the meantime remain in the same state of despair, *chas v’shalom*, etc.—who among us can afford such a thing?

You do not write the reason that brings you to such a state of mind, and therefore I cannot enter into details to prove how these reasons are *inyanim medumim* (imaginary matters) that stem from the *eitzas hayetzer* (counsel of the *yetzer hara*). That is to say, even if the matter has some *achiza* (foothold), the fact that it is being utilized for despair and feeling down is not the truth; it is a trick of the *yetzer*, whom *k’k mo”ch Admur* (my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe) called "the clever one," because he approaches everyone with words that will catch them.

I must limit myself here to a general remark on the entire matter. Relying on the saying of the Baal Shem Tov, which *k’k mo”ch Admur* repeated many times—that every Jew can learn a lesson in *avodas Hashem* from everything he sees or hears—I want to illuminate your case specifically.

Surely you know that the primary art of a painter in the wisdom of painting is that he must be able to detach himself from the *chitzoniyus* (externality) of the object. Without looking at the outer form, he must be able to look "inside" the object and perceive there its *pnimiyus* and *etzem hadavar* (inner essence), and then be able to convey this in a painting. In this way, for the one who sees the painter’s work, that which he had not noticed before is revealed, because the *toch* (core) was hidden by *inyanim tefelim* (trivial matters). Thus, the painter reveals the *etzem* and *mahut* (essence and nature) of the object he is depicting, and the viewer sees it in a different, true light and realizes that he was previously in error.

Just as with all these things and this vision, this is one of the foundations in the *avodah* of man to his Creator.

As we know from Torah in general and from *Chassidus* in particular, the entire creation is brought into being by the *Dvar Hashem* (Word of Hashem), and this *Dvar Hashem* is what gives life and sustains it at every moment. However, due to the Divine power of *Tzimtzum* and *Gevurah*, the *Dvar Hashem* stands in *he'elem v'hester* (concealment and hiding), and only the *chitzoniyus* is visible.

The matter of *avodah*, which relies on the *emunah peshutah* (simple faith) that *ein od milvado* (there is nothing else besides Him), is that one should approach every matter in life with this standpoint. One should seek to bring out, each according to his ability, as much of the *Elokus* (Divinity) that is in every thing, and to diminish, as much as possible, the *he'elem v'hester* of the *chitzoniyus* over the *Elokus* within it.

The same applies to every individual specifically. Since "you are children to Hashem your G-d," the *Tanya* (Chapter 2) says regarding this: "Just as a son is drawn from the father’s brain, so too, *kivayachol*, the soul of every Jew is drawn from His thought and wisdom"—and He and His wisdom are one. Consequently, this is the essence and the entire *mahut* and *etzem* of all Jews, and of you as well.

Just as the *Oibershter* desired that the soul should not have to receive *nahama d'kisufa* (the bread of shame), He gave it the possibility of *avodah*—and not just any *avodah*, but *avodah* with *yegias nefesh* and *yegias basar* (toil of soul and body). Through this *avodah*, one should receive all good, up to the highest levels, and all of this **earned**.

And another thing the Rebbe warns (in *Tanya*): one should not think that there are those for whom this will not be accomplished. He says that this cannot be, for even "from *shelo lishmah* one comes to *lishmah*," and "none shall be cast away from Him" (*Tanya*, end of Chapter 39).

Consequently, one must guard against letting *inyanim tefelim* cover up the *ikar ha'adam* (the essence of man) and the *tachlis hakavanah* (ultimate purpose).

The fact that a person has difficulties, *nisyonos* (trials), and matters of *birurim* (refinements) are the means by which one arrives at the *tachlis hadavar* (the purpose of the thing). That is to say, the soul should be able to be what it was even before "You created it"—which then is, "the soul You placed within me is pure"—and reach even higher levels. For "one hour of *teshuvah* and good deeds in this world is better than all the life of the World to Come." Therefore, one must not let the difficulties of overcoming *nisyonos*, or even a failure if one has stumbled from time to time, overcome the joy one must feel from "My firstborn son, Israel," and from the promise one has from the *Oibershter* Himself, that "Your people are all righteous."

Therefore, when a Jew comes along—let alone one who has heard of the *Ohr HaChassidus*, let alone one who has studied *Toras HaChassidus*, and let alone one whom the *Oibershter* has purified with *yisurim* (afflictions)—and writes that he is, *chas v’shalom*, in despair and finds no place for himself, etc., this is not only against *emunah*, but against *sechel* (reason) as well!

The *Oibershter* promises with all strength and power that "none shall be cast away from Him," and He does not demand of a person that he do beyond his strength—for "the Holy One, blessed be He, does not act tyrannically with His creatures"—but rather that he do according to his strength. Furthermore, He tells him that it is enough if there will be "an opening for Me like the eye of a needle—**and I** will open for you like the opening of a hall."

The *Oibershter* says all this, and yet he comes along and says that the calculation is, *chas v’shalom*, different, and therefore comes the despair, the dropped hands, and the self-deception that things are getting lower?!

The question is: "The words of the Master and the words of the student, whose words do we listen to?" And this is a question you must ask yourself: It seems so to you, but the *Oibershter* says it is otherwise; is there any doubt as to who is correct?

So much regarding arguing with oneself.

Regarding *l'po'al* (in practice), you must know that you are one of the *kehal haChassidim*; **consequently**, you are *mekushar* to the *ilana d'chayei* (Tree of Life). And this connection is as the verse says: "You who cleave to Hashem your G-d are all alive today." The Rebbe brings down in the *kuntres* of the 2nd of Nissan the teaching of our Sages: "Even on the day when the whole world is dead, you are alive," and "Just as today you are all existing, so too in the World to Come you are all existing." Consequently, you have a personal promise from our Sages that "you are all alive today" and "you are all alive in the World to Come."

Therefore, one must utilize the time for Torah and *mitzvos* with *yiras shamayim*, and utilize the *kishron* with which the *Oibershter* has gifted you so that it should bring a benefit in *yiras shamayim*.

These are things that one must not postpone until tomorrow, because tomorrow the tomorrow-things must be done, and today the today-things. And in order to do all these things, one must know that **all** obstacles are *eitzas hayetzer*, and one must bring the *emunah* down into the *sechel* (mind), into the *lev* (heart), and into *po'al mamash* (actual deed) in thought, speech, and action.

When you take this upon yourself—even if it seems to you that you can only begin with "the eye of a needle"—the *Oibershter* will grant success and will open "like the opening of a hall."

I hope that you will not hold it against me that my answer has been so delayed, and that you will reply soon with a *besorah tova* (good news) that you are acting in the spirit of the above.

With blessing—waiting for your good news in the very near future.

## 597

B"H, 24 Adar II, 5711, Brooklyn

To the Temimim students, may they live, who have come from South America,

Shalom u’Bracha!

It gave me great pleasure to hear of your hisorerus and your decision to gather from time to time to strengthen the connection between yourselves regarding matters of study and conduct, and to prepare yourselves for practical activities in strengthening Yiddishkeit in general and kosher education in particular in the countries from which you come. It is also important to maintain a constant connection with your friends in those countries in order to inspire them to work there to strengthen Yiddishkeit, and to send as many children as possible to study here in the yeshivos, etc.

It is worthwhile that you also involve in your work students from other yeshivos who come from South America.

Regarding what you wrote about questions and answers concerning Yiddishkeit, it is not necessary for everyone to prepare questions and answers every week; rather, this should be done by one or two individuals.

Surely, you will continue to keep a record of everything you do, and I hope to hear good reports from you from time to time.

With blessings for diligence and perseverance in the study of Torah with yiras shamayim, and for success in influencing others in all of this.

## 9598

B"H, 24 Adar Sheni, 5711, Brooklyn.

To the distinguished Rabbi and Chossid, G-d-fearing and learned, etc., Moreinu Harav Ephraim Eliezer, may he live, Hakohen.

Peace and blessing!

I received your letters in due time, and I was pleased to read in them that the matter of the Rav Av Beis Din is proceeding and being resolved. May Hashem bless him and protect him, etc. (and according to the opinion of R' Yehuda Kahana, "a Kohen assists a Kohen," *Chullin* 49a), to lead his congregation in peace and uprightness, and—despite that—to turn many away from iniquity, especially in the field of kosher chinuch, where, according to reports, even the little that exists here and there is diminishing in an alarming manner.

It is well known what the Rebbe, my father-in-law, said in the early years of his arrival here: "There is hashgacha over what is put into the pots, why is there no hashgacha over what is put into the heads?!"

- To note from *Chullin* 45a: "That which is in the pot," and the language of the verse, "Your Torah is within my innards," and it is taught in the end of Chapter 5 [of Tanya] -

Regarding what you wrote concerning the number of chapters in Tehillim, see also the introduction to *Minchas Shai* on Tehillim, the introduction in the Redelheim Tehillim, and *Yefeh Einayim* to *Berachos* 9, bottom of the page.

Enclosed is the receipt for the funds you sent from the Machatzis Hashekel. One might say, by way of a witticism, regarding what you wrote in that same letter—that you felt you still lacked bitul, etc.—that your Machatzis Hashekel comes and nullifies this feeling. For a Kohen who weighs [the shekalim] does so because he is handing it over to the tzibbur; this is very appropriate, as nothing remains of his ownership or authority (*Shekalim* 4, 2), or at the very least, it is nullified (*Erchin* 4, 1, in Rashi).

And yet, "Kohanim are demanding," etc., for the very fact that he negates his ownership is also a form of connection. Therefore, Moshe requested, "Do not turn to their offering," even though it is a communal sacrifice. See my note in *Kuntres* 53, page 31, at the end.

As you requested, I will mention you when I am at the Tziyun on Erev Rosh Chodesh Hageulah, may it come upon us for good.

I am very distressed that, for the time being, the distinguished Chossid, etc., has not been settled in a suitable position, and Shabbos comes and Shabbos goes, a month comes and a month goes, etc.

I conclude with best wishes for all good.

## 949

949

B"H,

The saying of the Baal HaHillula regarding his students is well known: that their role is to be "candles to illuminate."

The words of Tzaddikim in general, and especially the words of the Nesi'ei Yisrael regarding their students and those who are connected to them, are precise—even in their details. This is also true of the title "candles to illuminate," which serves as a guide for those connected to him in several fundamental matters.

Among them are the following:

There are several characteristics of a burning candle: The candle itself is a **source** of light—a *ma'or* (luminary), albeit in *Ze'er Anpin*.

The candle is comprised of oil and a wick. In the analogy: the oil represents Torah and mitzvos. The wick represents the person—that is, the body, or more accurately, the part of his soul, the *nefesh*, which is the partner of the body; and on a deeper level, the *nefesh elokis* that is enclothed within the *nefesh habahamis*.

When the wick is lit and it unites with the oil, the candle shines with many lights.

Collectively, these are two types of light: *nehora ukma* (black light) and *nehora chivra* (white light)—*ha'ala'ah* (ascent) and *hamshacha* (drawing down).

Furthermore, there is a unique advantage to the light of a candle: it is specifically suited for searching and examining in hidden places, holes, and crevices—it searches all the chambers of the belly.

All these matters in the analogy are sufficiently understood and explained.

And the practical application is paramount: through fulfilling all the above according to the instructions of the Baal HaHillula, the candle illuminates the portion of the world that belongs to it, and all the more so its own *nefesh habahamis* and *nefesh elokis*. This is the purpose of the soul's descent into this world, and upon this depends the ultimate purpose of the days of Moshiach and the Resurrection of the Dead, which should happen speedily in our days, Amen.

**Menachem Schneerson**

25th of Adar, 5711. Brooklyn, N.Y.

## 960

B"H, 25 Adar Sheni, 5711, Brooklyn

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, and learned, etc., Moreinu Harav Y. [may he live],

Peace and blessing!

Enclosed is the Kuntres for the upcoming 2nd of Nissan, the yom hilula of my father-in-law, the Rebbe (the Rebbe Rashab), of blessed memory. I am certain you will merit the public by having them study it, especially on the holy Shabbos Parshas Hachodesh, Rosh Chodesh Nissan, and the following day, the yom hilula. For as stated in the sicha printed in this Kuntres:

The students of the Baal Hahilula, their children, and their children’s children, possess his power—the power of one who teaches Torah to his fellow’s son. Consequently, they bear a responsibility toward the teacher, the Baal Hahilula. Furthermore, even

Those who merely saw him—they, too, possess his power, the power of the teacher. And even

Those who did not see him, this power is within them—through the power of the sender, for through this power, a person’s agent becomes like him.

There are several levels in this:

1. The granting of permission and power to the agent to act as the sender, yet the action remains the agent’s own, for the agent is an independent entity in all his affairs, only that he **desires** to fulfill the mission.

2. The granting of power from the sender to the agent to act, to the point that the action is the action of the sender, for the agent’s activities (regarding the mission) have no independent existence; they are nothing but the power of the sender.

3. The granting of power from the sender and the bitul of the agent to the sender, to the point that the agent himself is nothing but the sender. Each and every one of us falls into one of these categories, and the responsibility corresponding to that category rests upon him.

In accordance with the words of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, at the conclusion of his aforementioned sicha: "One must know the powers that we possess, and may the Ribono shel Olam help" to bring these powers into actuality and reach the goal—to become, as the Baal Hahilula demands, a **shining lamp** in all the details explained in the introduction to the Kuntres.

With blessing and regards to the entire group [may they live],

**M. Schneerson**

## 961

B"H, 25 Adar II, 5711, Brooklyn

To the congregants and gabbaim of the Nusach HaAri Synagogue of Chicago, may Hashem grant them life,

Peace and blessing!

Your contribution to *maos chitim* has arrived through the esteemed and accomplished Chossid, Rabbi Shlomo Zalman Hecht, may he live, and the receipt is enclosed.

I ask that you convey my thanks and blessings to the donors and their families, may they live.

We are now in the time between Purim and Pesach, both of which our Sages refer to as *geulah*. The difference, however, is that the *geulah* of Purim brought about only the nullification of the decree, but the Yidden remained in *galus* at that time, whereas the *geulah* of Pesach brought about true freedom, which is why Pesach is designated as *zman cheiruseinu*.

The beginning of the celebration of Pesach commences with the proclamation, "Let all who are hungry come and eat; let all who are in need come and celebrate Pesach." This means that before we begin the *seder* ourselves, we declare that we will provide everything necessary to all who are in need. Only then do we proceed to the *seder*. This grants us the merit to experience a true *zman cheiruseinu*. This is one of the things accomplished through *tzedakah* in general, and *maos chitim* in particular: far more than what one accomplishes for the other person through this *tzedakah* or *maos chitim*, one accomplishes much more for oneself. For through this, one merits to be freed from material and spiritual anxieties, and each individual attains their own true *zman cheiruseinu*. And—speedily in our days—we will merit the general *zman cheiruseinu*, as the Ribono shel Olam takes us all out of *galus* through Moshiach Tzidkeinu, who will bring us the *geulah amitis v’sheleima*.

With blessings for a kosher and happy Pesach and all good, materially and spiritually.

Regarding the situation at the yeshiva, I have already told you several times that everything will surely be successful. The vessels for this—especially to hasten the matter—are to increase the number of students and to increase efforts to plant in their hearts yiras shamayim and the performance of mitzvos in practice.

Tomorrow, G-d willing, I will be at the Tziyun of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, and I will mention you for great success in your material affairs and in your holy work, as my father-in-law, the Rebbe, entrusted to you. He **surely** also gave you the possibility and the strength to bring this matter from potential into actuality.

With a blessing for success in your holy work, and may you feel the great nachas that is in this.

## 964

B"H, 27 Adar Sheni, 5711, Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

I am pleased to hear—from your letter—that everything is well with you, B"H, regarding your *kvius itim l'Torah*, and that your daughter, may she live and be well, is doing well in her studies.

Regarding your *Gemara* studies, for which you have given up your *kvius* because you find it difficult to delve into the material:

I believe you should renew your *kvius* in learning *Gemara*. The very anxiety and frustration that arise from the difficulty of learning and understanding—and yet one continues to learn regardless, because this is the *chochmah* and *ratzon* of the *Ribono shel Olam*—actually alleviates other worries and frustrations regarding *parnassah* and health.

Tomorrow, *im yirtzeh Hashem*, I will be at the *tziyun* of *kavod kedushas moreinu v'rabbeinu Admur* and will mention all of you for blessing and success in everything you all need.

I hope that you will continue to share good news with me, and I conclude with blessings for all that is good.

Enclosed is the *kuntres* for 2 Nissan.

## 965

B"H, 29 Adar Sheni, 5711, Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings,

An elderly, G-d-fearing Rabbi visited me. He is fighting for his community, defending matters of Yiddishkeit with *mesiras nefesh*, including issues pertaining to *kashrus*.

A battle has now erupted in his camp regarding meat, specifically concerning the *melichah* of meat kept for more than three days.

I was alarmed to hear that those opposing the aforementioned Rabbi are basing their position on the rumor that your honor, *shlita*, has given clear *heter* for frozen meat—and furthermore, that the time meat spends in a refrigerator (freezer) does not count toward the three-day limit.

The campaign against this Rabbi is being waged not only by laymen, but also by [others], etc.

As your honor, *shlita*, is aware of the situation, it is surely unnecessary to elaborate on the terrible breach that could arise from this rumor, especially in matters of *kashrus*, which are entrusted to women and cooks.

I take the liberty of suggesting that your honor, *shlita*, publish a denial of this rumor in a manner appropriate for this country. I would be most grateful if you would inform me of the steps you have taken regarding this matter.

With respect and blessings for the *Nasi* over his kingdom—for "who are the kings? The Rabbis"—and may his strength in the holy Torah be fortified.

***

**965**

**Frozen meat:** See *Sefer Teshuvos U’Biurim* (5741), p. 192; *Kovetz Yagdil Torah* (N.Y.), Issue 45, Section 18. **I would be most grateful:** *Va’ani toda* (lit. "and I am grateful").

## 967

B"H, 4 Nissan, 5711, Brooklyn

To the students of Yeshivas Achei Temimim
Pittsburgh, may Hashem grant them life

Surely you know that at the beginning of the *Seder*, the children take center stage with "Mah Nishtanah," and that the *Haggadah* speaks of four types of children: one wise, and so on. Children who study are generally not categorized as the "one who does not know how to ask" or the "simple one." However, in order to belong to the category of the "wise one," one must study Torah with *frumkeit* and be *frum*. But since there is no limit to *chochmah*, I wish for you that you should constantly ascend in your learning, so that one may derive much *nachas* from you.

Please convey to your parents my wishes for a *kosher* and *freilichen* *Pesach*, and the same to all of you.

With blessings for success in the study of Torah with *yiras shamayim*,

**M. Schneerson**

## 965

B"H, 6 Nissan, 5711, Brooklyn

To the Agudas Noshim Tzeirois Lubavitch, and at their head, the Chairperson, Mrs. Mindel Katz, may she live:

Blessings and peace!

It was with pleasure that I received your letter with the enclosed donations to be distributed to the various mosdos that were founded and led by my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory. The receipts are enclosed herewith.

Surely you will continue with your good work and make even greater efforts to generate as much assistance as possible for these holy mosdos. Through this, you also create for yourselves the channels through which the Ribono shel Olam sends you and all your loved ones blessing and success.

In this current time between Purim and Pesach, Jewish women must reflect especially on the importance of these Yomim Tovim and what they teach us.

Both Purim and Pesach are Yomim Tovim of salvation and redemption, with the distinction that the salvation of Purim occurred while the Yidden were in golus, and even afterward they remained in golus for a certain time, whereas the redemption of Pesach was from slavery to freedom—from bondage to complete liberty. However, in both cases—and this is what I wish to emphasize here—the redemption came about due to the participation of Jewish women: on Purim, it was Esther; and on Pesach, our Sages, of blessed memory, tell us that it was in the merit of the righteous Jewish women that the redemption came, for they strengthened the spirit and maintained the courage of their husbands, and they raised a young, devoted Jewish generation, despite all the difficulties and obstacles of golus.

Jewish women must see to it, with all their strength, to maintain the golden chain that their mothers and grandmothers forged throughout all generations, so that through their participation, they may hasten the complete redemption through Moshiach Tzidkeinu, speedily in our days.

With blessings for a kosher and happy holiday,

**M. Schneerson**

## 971

B"H,

It is well known that the exodus of our forefathers from Mitzrayim was their departure from the status of Bnei Noach to receive the Torah and to receive the presence of the Shechinah—whether it was the beginning of the exodus or the exodus in its entirety—which is why our Sages learned the laws of conversion from that event. It is understood that this also points to their spiritual state, where the evil within the souls of Yisrael was still in its full strength within the left chamber [of the heart]; their goal and desire, however, was for their neshamah elokis to emerge from the galus of the Sitra Achra, which is the tumah of Mitzrayim, and to cleave to Him, may He be blessed.

And so it is every single day, that a person is obligated to view himself as if he went out of Mitzrayim today—as is brought in the maamar in the Kuntres—and especially during the days of Pesach, for the themes of every chag and moed are aroused each year at their appropriate times, as is known.

Every single person, and especially those who have not yet reached the level of the Beinoni—which is the measure for every person, and toward which every person should strive—must bring out and elevate their neshamah elokis from the galus of the body and the nefesh habehamis. On the contrary, they must elevate the neshamah elokis above the body and the nefesh habehamis, higher and higher, and cleave to Him, may He be blessed, through the Torah and mitzvos that they study and fulfill.

All the days of Pesach (and certainly the first night of Pesach) are changed for the better compared to the rest of the year and even compared to other Yomim Tovim. For then, Yisrael are nourished by the eating of matzah, which contains a semblance of the essence of the greatness of Abba—the essence of Elokus. This means that one’s physical body becomes connected to the vitality of his soul, such that he lives even physical life from the consumption of food that is the essence of Elokus. Therefore, besides the effect it has on the neshamah elokis, it also acts upon the nefesh habehamis—which is the Yetzer Hara—so that it will not incite as much, and so that it will begin to be refined and allow the neshamah elokis to believe with perfect faith even in that which it does not grasp through the intellect.

* * *

And in the words of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, in his sicha in the Kuntres: **These hours are so precious!**

**Menachem Schneerson**

11 Nissan, 5711
Brooklyn, N.Y.

For

What is stated (in the *sicha* from Chol Hamoed Pesach in the *Kuntres*) to the *Roshei Yeshiva* and administrators, and regarding America—is a clear instruction for each and every person who possesses influence. In the words of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, *ztzuklalleh"h, nbg"m, zy"a*, in this *sicha*:

"You must make clear to yourselves the responsibility that Divine Providence has placed upon you...

"If there is a *yungerman*, a *ben Torah*, in a city, it must be felt there that there is a Yid in the city...

"You must take the youth into your hands." [End quote].

And all four types of sons and daughters are included in this: the *chacham*, the *rasha*, the *tam* (the simple one), and the one who does not know how to ask—none are excluded, as it is written, **"And I will multiply** (*ve'arbeh*) His seed."

And through this "taking" (*nemen*) and the approach suited to each and every one of them, the blessing at the conclusion of the aforementioned *sicha* is drawn down and fulfilled: that the *Ribono shel Olam* grants success in the fulfillment of this *shlichus* and *avodah*.

With blessings for a kosher and joyous Pesach, and regards to the entire group, may they live,

**M. Schneerson**

Since it is impossible to encompass all those in need of a kosher education—in our current situation—it is understood that the law of priority applies to those where there is no *sircha* (such as the mixing of holy and secular studies together, and the like), and to those who have no education at all.

- And special attention should be given to the training of teachers and guides through appropriate courses and the like.

The division of Pesach is like the sacrifices, where the eating of the person is the primary element. *Po'el v'omed* (acting and standing), and to influence the physical body in its physical life. And similar to what is written in the introduction to the *Kuntres* regarding *matzah* from the *hemshech* "And thus the great one."

## 973

B"H, 11 Nissan, 5711, Brooklyn

To the esteemed Rabbi, G-d-fearing and distinguished, etc., Moreinu HaRav Aryeh Zev, may he live:

Greetings and blessings!

I received your telegram asking about the conduct regarding the second day of Yom Tov in the Diaspora. It is somewhat surprising, as this is a question for a *moreh hora’ah* (halachic authority); however, since you have asked, I will answer you. I have seen people conduct themselves like a resident of Eretz Yisrael, since their families are in Eretz Yisrael and thus they have the intention to return. However, one must be careful that this not be done in public. This is contrary to what is written in the beginning of *Shaar HaKollel*.

It should be noted that I did not hear this ruling explicitly from my father-in-law, the Rebbe, but I have seen several people from Eretz Yisrael who came to his holy court who conducted themselves in this manner, and it was with his knowledge.

Enclosed is the *Kuntres* for the festival of Pesach and the general letter pertaining to it.

I will conclude with a blessing for a kosher and joyous Pesach, and success in your holy work.

With blessings,

## 974

974

B”H, 11 Nissan, 5711, Brooklyn

Greetings and blessings!

In honor of the festival of Pesach, the season of our freedom, which is approaching us and all of Israel for good, I send you my best wishes for a kosher and happy Pesach.

Every year, at the time of our freedom, every Jew must experience and relive the Jewish meaning of the "season of our freedom." The inner intent of this was—"When you bring the people out of Egypt, you shall serve Hashem on this mountain": the giving of the Torah. The effect of this must be felt in daily life throughout the entire year, in the study of Torah and the fulfillment of mitzvos in general, and with a deep sense of responsibility for kosher education in particular, for children have always been, and remain, the guarantee for the existence and true freedom of our people.

With blessings for a kosher and happy holiday for you and your family, may they live and be well.

## 975

975

B"H, 11 Nissan, 5711, Brooklyn

Greetings and blessings!

In anticipation of the upcoming Pesach holiday, I hereby extend my blessing for a kosher and joyous Pesach.

Our Sages have said that one of the reasons that hastened the redemption from slavery to freedom was the severity of the bondage—specifically, that they would place the children of Yisrael into the walls of the buildings whenever the Bnei Yisrael fell short of their quota of bricks, and the children, buried alive, would cry and scream with no one to save them, and their cry ascended to Hashem.

Now, beyond the literal meaning, there is also an allusion here to spiritual life: to the children who are severed from a Jewish home and life, which are filled with the light of Torah, and are placed into the homes of strangers—the homes of Mitzrayim, where darkness can be felt.

And if the bondage of the body is bitter, the bondage of the soul is all the more so.

As we come to celebrate the time of our freedom, each and every one of us must liberate ourselves from being sunken, Heaven forbid, in the matters of Mitzrayim, and must strive—each according to their ability—to liberate the sons and daughters of Yisrael from this terrible bondage of the soul, and to bring them out from darkness into a great light through kosher education, based on the purity of holiness.

With blessings for a kosher and joyous Pesach.

* * *

The esteemed Rabbi, the G-d-fearing, the distinguished, etc., our teacher Rabbi Shimshon Raphael, known as Dr. Weiss,

I enjoyed reading your article in the journal *HaKerem*. See the sefer *Gulos Aliyos* regarding these Mishnayos.

#### ***975***

Printed in *Likkutei Sichos*, Vol. 4, p. 1297, and completed based on the secretariat’s copy. A similar version was sent to several others.

**"HaKerem":** The Adar I 5711 issue, p. 46, regarding the subject of *mei gaba*, *Mikvaos*, Chapter 1.

## 979

B"H, 11 Nissan, 5711, Brooklyn

To the esteemed Rabbi, the pious and G-d-fearing, distinguished in Torah and mitzvos, etc., etc.,
Rabbi Aharon Chaim Halevi, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

In due time, I received your gift, the monthly journal "Kerem," which is published under your direction, and many thanks for this.

May it be the will of Hashem that your strength increases in Torah, to magnify Torah, to glorify it, and to disseminate it.

It would be highly appropriate to set aside a special section in a Torah journal such as this, and others like it, for the Giver of the Torah as well. For although our Sages of blessed memory said that since the Beis Hamikdash was destroyed, Hashem has nothing in His world but the four amos of halacha, and even more so: "Hashem conceded [on idolatry, immorality, and bloodshed] but did not concede on the abandonment of Torah... 'If only they had forsaken Me but kept My Torah, the light within it would have returned them to the good,'" nevertheless, one should not rely on the reader finding that light and being returned to the good on his own, nor on his recognizing that the four amos of halacha are the dwelling place of Hashem. Rather, one must provide the light within the Torah—that is to say, the pnimiyus haTorah—in a ready-made fashion, to assist the reader so that he may recognize with complete clarity that the four amos of halacha are truly the dwelling place of Hashem.

It is known from our Sages of blessed memory in Nedarim (81a) regarding the verse "Because they have forsaken My Torah," that they did not recite a blessing over the Torah beforehand. The Ran explains that they were certainly engaged in Torah constantly... but they did not recite a blessing over the Torah beforehand, meaning that it was not so important in their eyes that it was worthy of a blessing, for they were not engaged in it lishmah.

This means they did not "walk in it"—that is, with its intention and lishmah. These are the words of the Rav HaChassid, of blessed memory. End quote. It is also worth noting the explanation of the Rambam (in his introduction to the Commentary on the Mishnah) regarding the aforementioned statement of our Sages that Hashem has nothing, etc.—for from halacha we learn wisdom and action. "And the most honored of intellectual concepts is to picture in one's soul the unity of Hashem."

With blessings for a kosher and happy Pesach.

Enclosed is the Kuntres for the festival of Pesach, which has just been published.

## 977

977

B"H, 11 Nissan, 5711, Brooklyn

Greetings and blessings!

I have received your letters, one from the 24th of Adar II and the second undated. In accordance with your request, while at the Ohel of the Rebbe, my father-in-law, of blessed memory, I mentioned you for good for everything you are in need of. Please send me his mother’s name.

In general, if my response is ever delayed, it only means that the reply has been held up, but I fulfill the request as soon as possible. The actual writing, however, depends on the many pressures that limit my time.

You ask about a *segulah*. It is generally not my way to provide *segulos*, but, as in every Jewish home, one should have the *mezuzos* checked and ensure that the person in question recites *Tehillim* every day.

You are certainly correct in what you write in your letter, that one has already suffered enough troubles, and it is time for everyone to be helped in everything they need, especially regarding proper health. I hope that you will be able to share good news with me in this regard.

The observation I would like to make here—though I am not entirely certain if it is fully applicable to this case—is as follows:

In general, a person’s sense of security often depends on something outside of and higher than themselves. Simply put, it depends on their feeling of *emunah* and *bitachon* in the *Borei Olam* in general, and in the *Borei Olam Katan*—which is man—in particular. After the great upheavals of our generation, which have shaken various spiritual foundations and severed many people from deeply rooted family and communal traditions, it has affected many people in such a way that they feel as if they are hanging in mid-air. I mean this even for those among them who are believers; for them, *emunah* has become something disconnected from their practical lives. One thinks about it, and one recites *Shema Yisrael* or *Modeh Ani*—often even with an understanding of the words—and yet, one goes about the entire day with the thought that one is alone, and everyone draws conclusions from that according to their own nature and the inclinations of their soul.

In order to bring these people back to their equilibrium, the most realistic way is to reveal to them the family tradition and the tradition of the fathers that is currently also hidden within their own *neshamah*. They will then see that a person is not alone, and even more so, that a person is the master of their own fate only up to a certain point, and that the main thing depends entirely on the *Ribono shel Olam*. Consequently, one does not have to drag everything on one’s own shoulders, feel an overwhelming responsibility for everything, and certainly not feel a sense of despair regarding specific matters or specific circumstances.

When one connects these people with the feeling of *emunah* and *bitachon*, which is undoubtedly deeply rooted within them, it brings them tranquility and helps them pass through the "against your will you live" in a healthier way, and to better fulfill the *tafkid* that every person has in life.

It goes without saying that for everything, and especially in matters connected to the *pnimiyus hanefesh*, one needs *siyata d’shmaya*. Here, the *zechus avos* helps—the fact that one descends from such a family and such parents who were permeated through and through with *emunah* and *bitachon*. This will eventually resonate with the children, so that they, too, will arrive at this.

I hope you will share good news with me, and I conclude with the wish for a *chag kasher v’sameach* for you and all your family.

With blessings that you should share good news soon.

I would be interested to know about the composition of your family, etc.

## 978

B"H, 12 Nissan, 5711, Brooklyn

To my dear friend, the chossid, G-d-fearing, and learned, etc., Rabbi Yosef Chaim Shlomo, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

In response to your notification regarding the wedding of your granddaughter, Mrs. Rivka, may she live, I wish to extend my blessing of Mazal Tov, Mazal Tov. May they build their home upon the foundations of Torah and mitzvos as explained in the teachings of Chassidus, and may her parents and her grandfather, may they live, see from them much nachas, both materially and spiritually.

With blessings for a Mazal Tov and a kosher and happy Pesach.

Enclosed is a gift certificate for a package, as a wedding gift.

Regarding your questions:

a) Is there a source for the Tzemach Tzedek’s instruction regarding wearing a watch on Shabbos? I have not heard of this. It seems to me that it is not mentioned in his printed seforim. Perhaps there is an oral tradition from him.

b) How is it possible for Shabbos to bless the days that precede it? This is along the lines of how the holiness of Shabbos begins—in several respects—from Erev Shabbos, and in some matters even before midday. Regarding this specific topic, see *Mishnas Chassidim*, Maseches Yom Revi’i, Chapter 3, Mishnah 2, and the appropriate places in *Shaar HaKavanos* in *Pri Etz Chaim*, etc. See also the *Siddur Yaavetz* regarding why we do not recite *Vayehi Noam* when a Yom Tov falls during that week, because the holiness of the Yom Tov protects **those that precede it**.

#### ***978***

**Rabbi Yosef Chaim Shlomo:** Schneersohn.

## 979

979

B"H, 12 Nissan, 5711, Brooklyn

Greetings and blessings!

I have been informed that you are not feeling in good health and are suffering from an ailment in your leg. I am hereby sending you my blessing for proper health in general, and specifically regarding your ailment, and I hope you will be able to share good news in this regard.

Surely you are aware of what is explained in Tanya, Iggeres HaKodesh, Epistle 1, that faith is called by the name "loins and feet," which support the entire body. Now, the festival of Pesach is approaching, during which our ancestors were redeemed from Egypt in the merit of faith, and for this reason, we eat matzah, which is the "food of faith." It adds strength to the faith of all Yisrael, and since the Jewish body and the Jewish soul are bound together (see *Kuntres L'Chag HaPesach*), both the body and the soul are nourished by the matzah, the "food of faith"—especially the physical and spiritual loins and feet. I wish you a speedy recovery.

With blessings for a kosher and happy Pesach and for a good arrangement in all matters, both revealed and hidden.

Enclosed is the *Kuntres L'Chag HaPesach* along with the *Michtav Klali* pertaining to it.

## 980

B"H, 13 Nissan, 5711, the Hillula of the Tzemach Tzedek, Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, and distinguished individual, engaged in communal needs, etc.,
Rabbi Y. [Gordon], shlita, Shochet and Bodek

Greetings and blessings!

I observe the involvement in the many matters that the Rebbe, my father-in-law, of blessed memory, placed upon your shoulders, and I take pleasure in seeing that even now you continue in these good activities. Surely you will add even greater effort in them, and without a doubt, Hashem will grant you the necessary strength for this, for the Holy One, blessed be He, does not deal tyrannically with His creatures.

It is known that the health of the Jewish body is dependent upon Torah and mitzvos. Engaging in them not only does not harm one’s health, Heaven forbid, but actually strengthens the health of the one who engages in them and all the members of his household, shlita.

It is known from our Sages (Bava Kamma 92b), "The wine belongs to the master, but the thanks go to the one who pours it." The author of this day’s Hillula, the Tzemach Tzedek, explains that regarding those who lack free choice—who are merely like an axe in the hand of the one who hews with it—the concept of "the thanks go to the one who pours it" does not apply. This is why the service of [idolatry] is forbidden, as they are merely like an axe in the hand of the hewer. This is not the case, however, with a Jewish person, who possesses free choice; the "thanks" go to the one who pours it, even if the other person would have performed the mitzvah regardless of his intervention (see this at length in *Derech Mitzvosecha*, Mitzvas Milah, end of Chapter 3).

How much more so is this true regarding the mitzvos in which you are involved, such as the *maamad*, *maos chitim*, the gabbai-ship at the Lubavitcher shul, and printing. In matters of Heaven, every individual can influence his fellow. If so, the one who "pours" is not merely an intermediary, but also an influencer who brings his fellow to perform a mitzvah, for which his reward is exceedingly great. This is even more true regarding matters of *tzedakah*, which is called "the act of *tzedakah*," for "the act is greater than the one who does it." Its concept is related to the word *kefiyah* (compulsion), as is known from our Sages, "We compel [one] to give *tzedakah*" (see in *Kuntres Chag HaShavuos 5708*, discourse *VaAvdi David*, p. 27). If regarding the one who performs *tzedakah* it is said that he eats its fruits in this world while the principal remains for the World to Come, how much more so is this true for the *act* itself, which is a vessel prepared to draw down and receive the blessing of Hashem—the promise of the Holy One, blessed be He, "Test Me now in this... and I will pour out for you a blessing until there is no room for more"—and in its literal sense: with children, life, and ample sustenance.

May Hashem bless you and your wife, tichyeh, with proper health and livelihood, with tranquility and much *Yiddishen un Chassidishen nachas* from all your descendants, shlita.

With blessings for a kosher and happy holiday and proper health,

[Signed by the Rebbe]

## 981

B"H, 13 Nissan, 5711, Brooklyn

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, and learned R' Shneur Zalman, may he live:

Greetings and blessings!

It was with pleasure that I received your letter from the evening after Shabbos, the 9th of this month, informing me of your safe arrival in Canada and your commencement of settling in. May it be the will of the Master of Will, the Almighty, that things arrange themselves in a manner suitable for you, both materially and spiritually, and that you may be able to set times for the study of the revealed Torah and the teachings of Chassidus with expansion, peace of mind, and physical tranquility, and may you also add strength in the area of tzedakah.

However, it is not advisable to wait until you are fully settled before establishing fixed times for study. For the Torah—and specifically the study of Torah with consistency—is the very vessel that draws down and receives material and spiritual good. The sooner you prepare this vessel, the sooner the blessing will arrive, and the larger you make the vessel, the greater will be the drawing down and reception of the blessing.

In due time, the mishloach manos—a bottle filled with Benedictine—was received, and I thank you for it.

Enclosed is the Kuntres for Pesach, along with the general letter pertaining to it. I will conclude with the blessing of a kosher and happy Pesach, and that you may be properly settled, both materially and spiritually, very soon.

With blessings,

#### ***981***

**R' Shneur Zalman, may he live:** Gurevitch.

## 982

B”H, 13 Nissan, 5711, Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and Blessings!

It was with pleasure that I heard from our friend, the esteemed Rabbi, Chassid, and G-d-fearing man, who occupies himself with communal needs, Rabbi Binyamin, may he live, Gorodetsky, regarding his vigorous and devoted work for the strengthening and dissemination of Torah in general, and his participation in our educational work in the **"Oholei Yosef Yitzchak Lubavitch"** institutions in particular.

I am hopeful that you, may you live, will continue to gather strength in your holy work to magnify and glorify Torah.

It is known from our Sages in the Zohar (Vol. III, 183b) regarding the eating of matzah: "It is like a king who had an only son who was ill. One day, the son desired to eat. The king said, 'Let my son eat healing food...' So too, when the Jewish people left Egypt... the Holy One, Blessed be He, said, 'Let the Jewish people taste healing food.'"

Now, as the upcoming festival of Pesach approaches, when every person in Israel, at the beginning of their Seder, calls out and proclaims, "All who are hungry, let them come and eat," the intent is not only in the literal sense, but also to provide "healing food," "food of faith," for the "only son" who is ill and desires to eat. Great is the *nachas ruach* (spiritual satisfaction) that is caused by this to our Father in Heaven, may His name be blessed and exalted. And how great is the good that is hidden in this world and the next for all those who work and involve themselves in the work of education—to educate the sons and daughters of Israel with proper education—and especially for those who stand at the head, as our Sages say, "The High Priest takes the first portion."

With this, I wish you and all those who join you a kosher and happy holiday, and all the visible good, from soul to body. May our request be fulfilled speedily and in our days: "Next year in the Land of Israel, as free men," through Mashiach Tzidkeinu.

He who seeks your peace and well-being always, throughout all days.

#### 982

Similar content to several rabbis and communal activists in Morocco.

## 983

B"H, 13 Nissan, 5711, Brooklyn

To the congregants and Gabbaim of the Nusach HaAri Beis Medrash in Montreal, may Hashem protect them and grant them life,

Peace and blessing!

I received your letter of 29 Shevat in due time, and I was pleased that the words of inspiration brought to you by the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing and learned, Rabbi Moshe Chaim Sapotshinsky, may he live, found a warm response. I had no doubt that this would be the case, for as our Sages of blessed memory say, "I sleep, but my heart is awake"—I sleep in exile, but my heart is awake to Torah and mitzvos. I also wish to hope—and this is the main thing—that this inspiration will be translated into concrete action in all three areas that my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, so often emphasized: ahavas Hashem, ahavas haTorah, and ahavas Yisrael.

As we now stand in the days of Pesach, you are surely aware of what our Sages tell us: that in order to leave Mitzrayim, all six hundred thousand of the Jewish people had to be present, and had even one been missing, it would have, G-d forbid, hindered all the rest. A lesson for us in these words, especially during the days of Pesach, is that we must all remember and exert our greatest efforts to bring every single person in Israel—man, woman, young, and old—closer to Torah and Yiddishkeit. This is relevant not only to the one being brought closer, but to all of us.

This is also one of the allusions in the beginning of the Pesach Seder; before we begin to conduct the Sedarim, we proclaim and announce, "Let all who are hungry come and eat, let all who are in need come and celebrate Pesach." This is meant both literally—help in material matters—and help in spiritual matters. Only after that can we say, "This year we are here; next year in the land of Israel. This year we are slaves; next year we will be free men."

I wish you all and your families, may they live, a kosher and happy Pesach, and I hope to hear good news from you in all matters. May we very soon merit the fulfillment of the request we make and pray for: "Next year in the land of Israel, as free men," through Mashiach Tzidkeinu, speedily and in our days.

With the blessing of a kosher and happy holiday.

## 984

984

B”H, 13 Nissan, 5711, Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and Blessings!

I received your letter in due time, but due to many preoccupations, I have not been able to answer until now. In truth, it does not require an answer from me, as you already received an answer from my father-in-law, the Rebbe, when you were here.

In any event, I wish to reiterate what I have already spoken about a number of times:

Once and for all, one must know that emunah is not something that should remain merely in one’s thoughts, but must permeate one’s entire life.

There is no doubt that you are a believer. The first principle of emunah is that Hashem runs the world. And if He has the power to manage one and a half billion people, it is certainly a sure thing that regarding your own affairs, what is stated in the pasuk will be fulfilled: "I have made, and I will carry, and I will sustain, **and I will deliver**" (Yeshayahu 46:4).

Now, consider this yourself: Hashem promises that "I will sustain and I will deliver," yet you are reconsidering whether a gentile from this or that country could, chas v’shalom, prevent Hashem from fulfilling His promise. And as a result of this, consider yourself: does Hashem need you to worry about how He should manage your business affairs and solve your problems, or will Hashem be able to find the good path even without your worries?

Ultimately, you must remember that the Rebbe, my father-in-law, of blessed memory, blessed you, and a blessing from a tzaddik will certainly be fulfilled; consequently, your blessing will also certainly be fulfilled. The only question is, you have been given two choices: Either, until you see the fulfillment of the blessing, you can walk around worried that perhaps, chas v’shalom, the blessing will not be fulfilled—and then, when it is fulfilled, you will have an additional worry: why you had to waste so much life-energy worrying for nothing. Or, you can be strong in your bitachon and emunah in Hashem, that He will lead you on the correct path and will fulfill all the blessings with which you were blessed. Then, when you see how they are fulfilled in actual reality, you will be able to say to yourself: "See how well I acted, that I did not worry about things that there was no reason to overthink."

This is one of the meanings of my father-in-law’s blessings to you—not only as a blessing, but also as a command: you must be in a state of simcha. For with Hashem’s help, the problems that seem difficult to you will be solved, and you have nothing to worry about; you can be in simcha and fulfill the command of "Serve Hashem with joy."

I wish you a kosher and happy Pesach, and to be healthy and happy always, and I look forward to hearing good news from you soon.

Enclosed is the sicha from Pesach 5703, which will surely interest you.

## 895

B"H, 13 Nissan, 5711, Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and blessings!

In anticipation of the approaching festival of Pesach, I hereby wish you that you may celebrate the holiday in a kosher and joyous manner together with your entire household. May you merit to influence your entire environment to ascend in holiness on the path that leads to the House of Hashem.

Especially during the days of Pesach, which was the beginning of our people’s liberation—and every year, at the appointed times of the year, the matters pertaining to that event are awakened—the festival of Pesach, which is the time of our freedom, is a freedom not only from physical servitude but also freedom from the *yetzer hara*, etc. The moral lesson of the day is to increase courage and effort in these matters. This is why matzah is called *michla d’asvusa* (Zohar Vol. III, 183b), and it strengthens faith, as is written there on page 41a.

Enclosed is the *kuntres* that was published for the festival of Pesach, which I am sure will be of interest to you.

I would like to point out something I noted in my introduction regarding the eating of matzah: that during the days of Pesach, the body is nourished by food that strengthens faith in *Elokus*. It is worth noting in this regard that the *korban Pesach* is distinct from other *korbanos* in that its primary purpose is for eating—specifically for the eating of the owners, rather than the eating of the *mizbeach* and the *kohanim*.

With blessings for a kosher and joyous holiday,

**M. Schneerson**

Printed in *Likkutei Sichos*, Vol. 7, p. 248. A similar copy was sent to several others.

## 896

B”H, 24 Nissan, 5711, Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

... This is the content of the message I requested your son, may he live, to convey to you:

"L’chaim! May the father be a Chassid in the open (*b’galui*); he is already a Chassid in concealment (*b’helem*). Thank G-d, he has Chassidic children, but when he becomes a Chassid in the open, he will be able to assist his children to be Chassidim in the open."

The explanation of these words:

Knowing my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, I know for certain that he was a *tzaddik*, and the words of *tzaddikim* and their actions are truth; they are alive and endure forever, and it is obvious that **nothing** of them is ever lost.

I heard several times from my father-in-law, the Rebbe, how he spoke about you and your wife, may she live, and how much effort he invested in you and your wife—both directly in conversations with you, and indirectly in his own way, with a chapter of Tehillim, etc. I also heard from my father-in-law, the Rebbe, regarding the hopes he had for your children, may they live, and what one sees even with physical eyes is that they are gradually being fulfilled more and more.

Based on the above—that the action of a *tzaddik*, and especially of a Rebbe, is never lost—I am certain that all the good things that the father-in-law, the Rebbe, wanted to see in you will come down into actuality. A portion of this has already come into actuality, and I am certain that everything will be in the open, one hundred percent.

It goes without saying that this does not refer to the fulfillment of *mitzvos* in the simple sense, which has always been present in you and your home. Rather, it refers to matters of *lifnim mishuras hadin* (going beyond the letter of the law), in which there is no limit; no matter how much a created being attains, he can always ascend further.

However, "a prisoner cannot free himself from jail"—one needs assistance from another. As the Mitteler Rebbe (son of the Alter Rebbe) said, at that moment, it is two *nefesh elokis* against one *nefesh habehamis*. This is especially true when one has the assistance of someone like my father-in-law, the Rebbe, whose own merit is great, in addition to the merit of his holy ancestors who assist him.

And this is the explanation of what I meant: "He is a Chassid in concealment, and he should be a Chassid in the open," in a conduct of *lifnim mishuras hadin* to the ultimate degree. My father-in-law, the Rebbe, gave you the *kochos*—as I have already written—not only in the words spoken to you face-to-face, but also while he was alone in his room, with a chapter of Tehillim, etc. But you have not yet utilized **everything** in the open, for it is impossible to exhaust a blessing of a *tzaddik* to its very end and ultimate conclusion.

Therefore, I wished that the blessings with which my father-in-law, the Rebbe, blessed you—both in his presence and in his absence—should be fulfilled in their entirety.

The greatest blessing for every person, and especially for Jews, is *nachas* from children, as our Sages say, "A person is jealous of everyone except his son, etc." I explicitly stated **this** and clarified it: that the blessing of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, should be fulfilled in you, that your children should be Chassidim in the open.

B

The reason I conveyed this blessing through your son, may he live, **during the farbrengen**, is because it is written in the *sefarim* that when a Jew says a word of blessing and ten Jews are present and answer "Amen," the word of blessing becomes a blessing of a *rabim* (a multitude). And a *rabim*—"where ten are gathered, the *Shechinah* rests" (Sanhedrin 39a). Especially when there are dozens of groups of ten present, and it is a time of a Shabbos or Yom Tov meal, which is a *seudas mitzvah*. And in particular, when this is in a holy place, a *beis knesses* and *beis medrash*, I did not want to let the opportunity pass. Seeing that those present were among good friends and Jews who were in a state of *hisorerus* (spiritual arousal), I utilized the opportunity so that it would be with the agreement of all the Jews present, who were in a state of Shabbos and Yom Tov, and at a time of *Seudah Shlishis*, which is the time of *Reva D’chol Revin* (as we say in the *zemiros* of Shabbos, with its source in the holy Zohar). I wanted them all to agree that the blessings which my father-in-law, the Rebbe, gave should be fulfilled in their entirety. And one of the essentials is that one should be a Chassid, act *lifnim mishuras hadin*, and do a favor for another, even when it might be a loss for oneself, G-d forbid—as Tosafos explains the definition of a *Chassid*, etc. (Niddah 17a, and see also Shabbos 120a)...

With regards to all your household, may they live, and with blessings.

B"H, 25 Nissan, 5711, Brooklyn

By the way, I have protested for some time, and I protest now as well, against a most strange custom: when the blessing of Gomel is recited, those present do not answer "Amen" to the blessing itself, but instead respond, "He who has bestowed upon you..." [with the rest of the response]. It is astonishing that this custom has spread; I have seen this several times in the shuls where I have davened, that they do not answer "Amen."

## 988

B"H, 25 Nissan, 5711, Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and blessings!

Our Sages of blessed memory included the statement "against your will you live" among the things that are "against your will." This means that life is not a series of pleasures, or at the very least, not a sequence of tranquil matters or even minor hardships.

However, from time to time, one must return to oneself with strength and consistency, remembering that "against your will you live," and that "everything the Merciful One does, He does for the good."

See also the *Kuntres* 5708, from the letters of my father-in-law, the Rebbe (12 Tammuz 5708).

But we see tangibly that to a significant and great extent, the impression that life’s events leave on a person depends on the person himself—on the intensity with which he receives them and reacts to them. Who is greater than the Rambam, whose external life was filled with troubles, adventures, hardships, and disasters, Heaven forbid, beyond the ordinary measure? Yet, his outlook on life, as explained in his *Moreh Nevuchim*, was of the highest quality—optimistic, as they say in the vernacular. Conversely, we have seen many people whose external lives are seemingly successful, yet only very rarely does one see any sense of satisfaction in them.

This same distinction exists in the natural character traits of human beings. Chassidus helps every individual in this regard. From the time of the Baal Shem Tov, they proclaimed the concept of "Serve Hashem with joy." Even at the time of *teshuvah* for sins that one has undoubtedly committed and transgressed, this does not have to contradict the "joy fixed in the heart" from the other side, as explained at length in *Tanya*.

Especially regarding matters that are not dependent on one's own choice, Chassidus certainly provides the ability to find within them—even through human intellect—some aspect of joy, or at the very least, some aspect of rectification for matters of the past. Consequently, this should greatly diminish the agitation, bitterness, and—needless to say—the sadness that arise from these events. See *Tanya*, Chapter 26. We have already been promised in the books of our Sages and in *Iggeres HaKodesh*, Chapter 21: "And then Hashem will also give what is good, and He will shine His countenance upon him in a manner of revealed love, which was previously clothed and hidden within revealed rebuke, and the *Gevuros* will be sweetened at their root and the *Dinim* will be nullified, etc." (This is despite what we heard from my father-in-law, the Rebbe, in one of his *sichos* regarding what is written there at the beginning of the passage: "And like a merciful, wise, and righteous father who strikes his son, etc." He explained that it does not say "and pious" (*chassid*) here, as it says later—"before his merciful, righteous, and pious father, etc."—because since this is a father striking his son, even though it is from hidden love, the title "pious" is not applicable here, so to speak.)

It is understood that all that has been said above is not, Heaven forbid, a way of delivering moral rebuke. Moreover, it is difficult to say this to another, knowing what that person has gone through. I have come only to point out to you some matters from our Torah that may be able to lighten the burden of the load for you and calm your spirit, at least in some measure, until the promise mentioned in the aforementioned *Iggeres HaKodesh* is fulfilled in you: that Hashem, who is good, will give what is good and shine His countenance upon you in all that you require.

I am certain you will inform me when there are any changes in all the aforementioned matters, and especially when you have good news regarding one or more of these matters.

With blessings for proper adjustment soon.

## 889

B"H, 26 Nissan, 5711, Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and blessings!

I received your letters in due time. When I was at the Tziyun of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, I also read your Pidyon Nefesh and the matters recorded within it. I was pleased to read in your letter of 13 Nissan that, at least regarding some of these matters, a rectification has already occurred, and you yourself acknowledge this. Surely, regarding the remaining matters as well, you will see an improvement in the situation in a way that is good, visible, and revealed.

...Regarding what you feel—that you are suffering from heart palpitations, etc.—it is almost certain that this is nothing more than a matter of imagination, or at most, merely nerves. To set your own mind at ease, you should certainly visit a specialist in this field and follow their instructions. This is regarding the natural path. 

As for the inner dimension of these matters, you should firmly anchor your thoughts in the simple faith that every Jew possesses—as believers, the children of believers—that the Ribono shel Olam, who created the world 5,711 years ago, is creating the world at every single moment and guiding it according to His will, which is the ultimate good, and it is the nature of the Good to do good. If so, it is simple that your own affairs are also included in this; that in your life and your affairs, the **Ribono shel Olam** is the Master, and He will guide you to your desired destination (the inner will of every single Jew, which is why, when one is compelled until he says "I want to" regarding things that are according to Torah, it is truly his own will). 

May it be His will that He guide you with revealed love, with kindness and mercy. And you should get all these things about nerves out of your head. A Chossid must be healthy, not only in spirituality but in physicality as well, so that he, and through him, the mission for which his neshamah descended into this low, physical, and material world, will be fulfilled.

With blessings that you will soon bring me good news regarding all of the above.

[Signed]

## 990

B"H, 26 Nissan, 5711, Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and blessings!

I received your letters in due time, as well as regards from you through the esteemed Chossid, a man of integrity who occupies himself faithfully with communal needs, Rabbi Yosef Weinberg. On one hand, I was pleased to receive regards from you, but on the other hand, it pains me to hear that you are finding it difficult to adapt to your new situation, and that you are taking the circumstances in which you find yourself (with the help of Hashem, only **temporarily**) with such intensity.

Surely you also take into account the situation in the place from which you were saved, and you reflect from time to time on the kindnesses that Hashem has performed for all Jews, and for us in general, in that they were saved from all the terrible things that Jews have endured in recent years.

Regarding your current situation, there is no doubt that in time you will settle in, to the point where you will be able to have not only what you need materially, but also satisfaction in your spiritual state. You will be content not only with yourself, but also be able to influence your surroundings so that it is evident that a Jew has arrived—a Chossid who has merited to have a connection for many years with my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, and who has drawn from him so much strength, not only to carry his own burden, but also to influence those around him in the spirit of Chassidus. This means spreading the three loves: Ahavas Hashem, Ahavas HaTorah, and Ahavas Yisrael. In the simplest terms: making life easier for yourself and those around you through the light and warmth of Torah and mitzvos in general, and according to the path of Chassidus in particular.

Therefore, you must not, Heaven forbid, be discouraged that things are moving slowly for the time being. I am certain that little by little, the situation will improve, and you will be able to report good news—that your bitachon and courage have grown stronger, and that your material situation has improved and continues to improve.

I wish you all the best and extend my blessing that **very soon** you will be able to report good news regarding all the aforementioned matters.

Needless to say, when I am at the Ohel, I will mention you for what you need, and my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, will surely arouse mercy so that you may have what you need, both materially and spiritually.

Awaiting good tidings.

You are surely more or less familiar with the state of Yiddishkeit in your city; seek to influence and acquaint those with whom you come into contact with the warmth of Torah and mitzvos.

## 991

B"H, 27 Nissan, 5711, Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the organizers and donors of the Maos Chittim campaign in Fall River, Mass., may Hashem grant them life.

Peace and blessing!

Through the esteemed Chossid, man of many accomplishments, Rabbi Meshulam Zalman HaKohen Schachter, your contribution to Maos Chittim was received before Pesach, and the receipt is enclosed.

I ask that you convey my thanks and blessing to the donors, the organizers, and their families, may they live.

Maos Chittim is connected to the declaration of "Let all who are hungry come and eat, let all who are in need come and celebrate Pesach," which is the beginning of the Pesach celebration. This means that before we begin the Seder ourselves, we declare that we will provide everything needed for all who are in need. Only then do we proceed to the Seder. This grants us the merit to experience a true *zman cheiruseinu* (time of our freedom). This is one of the things accomplished through *tzedakah* in general, and Maos Chittim in particular: far more than what one accomplishes for the other person through that *tzedakah* or Maos Chittim, one accomplishes much more for oneself. For through this, one merits to be freed from material and spiritual worries, and one attains a true *zman cheiruseinu* for each individual. And—speedily in our days—we will merit the general *zman cheiruseinu*, as the Ribono shel Olam takes us all out of *galus* through Moshiach Tzidkeinu, who will bring us the *geulah amitis v'hashleimah*.

With blessings for all that is good, materially and spiritually.

Great is the satisfaction that is caused thereby to our Father in Heaven, may He be blessed and exalted. And the measure of good is abundant, with much goodness stored away in this world and the next for all who perform and engage in the work of education to raise the sons and daughters of Yisrael with a proper chinuch.
