## 994

B"H, 1 Iyar, 5711, Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed and diligent activist, R' Mordechai Cohen, may he live:

Greetings and blessings!

I have received your report regarding the state of education in the country of Tunisia, and I thank you for it. It gives me pleasure to hear from time to time of your good work in the field of educating the sons and daughters of Israel there.

As per your request, I have instructed the office of the Merkos L’Inyonei Chinuch to send a package of books to the address of the Rav in Mabrouk, shlita. I trust they have been received in good order, and I look forward to confirmation of their receipt.

Regarding the festival of Pesach, which we have just celebrated, and also in connection with the spring days that are now approaching in all their splendor: the festival of Pesach is marked in Scripture as needing to occur in the month of spring. In nature, with the appearance of spring, the forces of nature that were hidden throughout the winter—to the point where, to the observer’s eye, it seemed that vitality, creation, growth, and development had ceased—suddenly, in the month of spring, reveal to all that this was merely a period of gathering strength, so that later, blossoming trees and fields draped in green might appear. As our Sages of blessed memory said, one who goes out during the days of Nissan and sees trees blossoming must recite the blessing, etc.

There is a moral lesson in this for all of us: if there is a period in our lives where one might mistakenly think that it is not a time of creation, growth, and development, it is almost certainly a mistake on our part. The pause serves only to add strength, and to use the language of the analogy, to bring forth blossoms and yield fruit.

We can find a hint of this in the matter of Pesach: after the bitter period of the exile of Mitzrayim—the exile of the body and the exile of the soul combined—to the point where the minister of Mitzrayim argued, "How are these different from those [the idolaters]?"—within a short time, the refinement that the exile of Mitzrayim had wrought was revealed in them. In fifty days, they ascended from the forty-nine gates of impurity to receive the Torah from the mouth of the Ribono shel Olam Himself.

With blessings for success in your work to bring the sons and daughters of Israel closer to our Father in Heaven.

## 995

B”H, 1 Iyar, 5711, Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, and pious individual, who conducts his business with integrity, etc.,
Rabbi Y. HaKohen, may he live:

Peace and blessing!

Following our telephone conversation, I am enclosing the copy of my letter to Mr. Yosef Robinson, as well as the 20 checks made out to Mr. Simon and Mr. Kaplan, which are post-dated sequentially, beginning two days after Mr. Robinson’s check, and starting with the sixth check, in accordance with your instruction that tzedakah takes precedence.

In this regard, I would also like to emphasize what the Alter Rebbe writes in Iggeres HaKodesh, Siman 21: that regardless of how great a mitzvah may be, the alacrity with which one performs it carries immense significance. The Alter Rebbe writes this specifically regarding the matter of tzedakah, and these are his words: “The alacrity of Avraham Avinu, peace be upon him, is what stands forever for us and our children for all time, etc.” He adds that, especially regarding “the act of tzedakah, which surpasses them all, etc., how much more so is it good for us, even in this world, to prioritize it as much as possible.”

I would like to conclude with the wish that the teaching of the Gemara be fulfilled: “Tithe (aser t’aser) — tithe so that you may become wealthy (titasher).” And [the teaching that] “the one who facilitates the act is greater than the one who performs it,” meaning that the merit of one who exerts himself to ensure that tzedakah reaches the treasury is greater than that of the one who gives the tzedakah. May your participation in the work that my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, established in Africa serve as a channel to draw down revealed and manifest goodness, in good health for you, your wife, and your children, may they live, and much success in your business affairs, both material and spiritual. And just as we ascend in matters of holiness, may you also merit to increase your participation in my father-in-law, the Rebbe’s work, and may it be a process of constant growth, higher and higher.

I hope to hear good news from you at all times. With great blessing, both materially and spiritually.

***

995

Rabbi Y. HaKohen: Katz. Additional letters to him appear above in 822, and in the notes referenced there. 1) Explained at length in the discourses on Sefiras HaOmer. See also the discourse *Ani L’Dodi* (Kuntres 57, Lag B’Omer 5708).

## 996

B"H,

Among the many pearls present in the printed sicha mentioned here, one of the most essential is (see section 15):

**"In the past, people knew that one had to be a Yid who is a yirei shamayim, a Chassid. Today, one must be able to learn Chassidus. He and the matter are two separate things"** (the Rebbe’s words, slightly abridged).

This is also one of the concepts of Sefiras HaOmer — the drawing down of the *mochin* into the *midos* — that one should conduct himself according to the instruction of the *mochin* and the intellect. That which he **knows** (in his mind) — to learn *nigleh d’Torah* and Chassidus (*pnimiyus haTorah*) — he should **be** in his daily life. That he and his knowledge should be one thing.

And, in truth, this is also among the concepts of *pnimiyus haTorah* — the revelation of which is Lag B’Omer (see below, section 21) — to unify and demonstrate that everything is a unity: materiality is nothing more than an external thing that must be refined, making it devoid of materiality, and from the *gashmiyus* itself, bringing out its *pnimiyus*, which unifies with *ruchniyus* and the *neshamah* of the thing.

And then the person becomes — his *neshamah*, his body, and all his affairs — **one thing**.

**And the path to this is through *pnimiyus haTorah***, which demonstrates within the Torah itself that everything is one. *Pnimiyus haTorah* demonstrates how within the Torah, the *razei Torah* and the *Torah haNigleh* — the *levusha d’Oraisa*, the *gufa d’Oraisa*, the *nishmasa d’Oraisa*, and the *nishmasa l’nishmasa* *d’Oraisa* — are one thing. Especially on Lag B’Omer, for the revelations of Lag B’Omer are those which the *baal hahillula* — Rabbi Shimon bar Yochai — revealed, *razei d’razin*. "Holy words that were not revealed until now... for He (the *Kudsha Brich Hu*) and all His holy entourage come to hear with joy these hidden words."

**Menachem Schneerson**

2 Iyar, 5711, Brooklyn, N.Y.

## 997

B"H, 9 Iyar, 5711, Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter asking whether you should purchase a business in partnership with someone who does not observe Shabbos, in such a way that the business itself will also not be Shabbos-observant, but rather that [the violation] will be on the portion of the other partner.

Surely you know that money connected with the desecration of Shabbos, G-d forbid, does not only go to waste itself, but also drags other money along with it. If so, what business does he have with such commerce, which is very, very close to loss and far from profit?!

And the Ribono shel Olam, who feeds and sustains everyone, will surely provide your livelihood in abundance, in a kosher manner, and in a way that you will be able to use your earnings for healthy things and Jewish things.

I would be happy to hear that you have established regular Torah study sessions in a group, and you will surely gladden me by informing me of an increase in the number of participants in these studies, and that you will also establish a study session in the teachings of Chassidus.

With blessings and regards to the participants of the shiurim, may they live.

Enclosed is the sicha of Lag B'Omer of this year, and surely you will share it with the public.

## 998

B"H, 10 Iyar, 5711, Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and blessings!

I received your letter in due time, and just now I received your letter from the 4th of Iyar. It is a pity that, as is apparent from your letter, your spirits have fallen. This is certainly a tactic of the *yetzer*, for all of *Am Yisrael* has long been accustomed to ups and downs throughout their history—especially those who are G-d-fearing, and in particular the *Chassidim*, who from time to time have faced various obstacles, concealments, and obstructions. Yet, despite all this, in the end, *didan notzach* (we are victorious). As the Alter Rebbe said, he accomplished through his *mesiras nefesh* that *Chassidim* should be successful.

You should strengthen your resolve to be a fitting vessel and a suitable conduit for fulfilling the *shlichus* of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory—which is to disseminate the light of Torah and the "Light within the Torah," namely the teachings of *Chassidus*, in your location and country at this time. If you do so, everything will surely be successful, and with extraordinary success. As I have written previously, this will also serve as a conduit for a happy life for you and your wife, may she live and be well, both materially and spiritually, and may you be blessed with upright offspring.

Awaiting good news, with blessings and regards to your *siyata d'shmaya*,

**M. Schneerson**

Enclosed is the *sicha* for Lag B'Omer, along with a general letter pertaining to it.

## 999

B"H, 10 Iyar, 5711, Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and blessings!

I trust you will forgive me for writing to you regarding a private matter of yours.

Many times I heard from my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, that the concept of *ahavas Yisrael* extends even to a fellow Jew who is in a distant place, and even to one whom one has never met. Our holy Torah has commanded us regarding this as well: "Love your neighbor as yourself." If there is hope that one can assist someone who is in a distant place and whom one does not know, it is a sacred obligation for every person to strive for the benefit of their fellow, for **all** of Israel are friends.

I have been informed that several distinguished proposals have been suggested for you, and for various reasons, you have declined to accept them.

Naturally, it is impossible to offer an opinion regarding a private proposal from a distance, but I will permit myself to offer a general observation on this matter.

Marriage is the most significant event in a man or woman’s life, leaving its mark on their entire existence. Consequently, it requires careful deliberation, and it cannot be done in haste.

However, at the same time, as with all events in a person’s life, both small and great, it is impossible for a human being to take every detail into account to its ultimate conclusion. For, after all, a person is extremely limited, and their intellect and thought cannot encompass all the causes and effects of every single thing. To a certain extent, in every matter and affair, one must utilize the quality of *bitachon* in Hashem, who directs the matter for the best in every detail.

This is also true regarding a *shidduch*. It is impossible to find something that is absolutely perfect in every respect, and it is impossible to calculate all the outcomes to their final end. If the essential matters are in order, it is often correct to forgo secondary issues that appear or seem to be not as they should be—especially since it is possible that this is merely an imagination, and in truth, they are also suitable.

Some say that this is merely a private matter of the individuals involved, but the truth is not so. For all of Israel are responsible for one another, and the well-being of each and every person—or the opposite, *chas v'shalom*—influences their family, their friends, and even those who are distant in place. If this was true in ordinary times, it is certainly true in these times of ours, after the terrible destructions that took from us tens of thousands of our brethren, *Hashem yinkom damam*. Consequently, the value of every home built in Israel is all the greater—and then some—especially when there is hope that this home will be built upon the foundations of Torah and *mitzvos*.

I hope you will be able to share good news with me regarding the above, and I will conclude with a blessing for a good arrangement soon, one that is good in both material and spiritual terms.

I would be interested to know if you participate in the public life of your community, and in what manner.

## 1000

B"H, 10 Iyar, 5711, Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter from Motzaei Shabbos Tazria, in which you ask whether you should accept the proposal of Agudas Yisrael to travel, together with a principal-teacher also from Bais Yaakov, during the vacation period as a shlichah on behalf of Bnos Agudas Yisrael to the countries of Western Europe for the purpose of organizing branches of Bais Yaakov, Bnos, and Bnos Agudas Yisrael, as well as to collect money for this cause, and you ask for my consent.

Regarding the goal of organizing branches of Bais Yaakov and so on, this is a proper thing. However, regarding the collection of money, if possible, you should avoid it.

As for your question regarding whether I consent to flying by airplane if there is no possibility of traveling by ship, surely the flight will be at a suitable time regarding the weather, and also on a large airplane.

Regarding the matter itself, I am somewhat puzzled, knowing the situation in Eretz Yisrael (may it be rebuilt and established), where there are many, many boys and girls in need of a kosher education in Torah and fear of Heaven. Certainly, every educational resource is precious on the spot, especially given the situation where, at every moment, every hour, and every day, boys and girls are being snatched away from their source and origin, and it is subsequently difficult to return them to a kosher education. Consequently, on the face of it, instead of traveling abroad on a doubt (whether the work is needed, and if one were to say there is suitable work there, perhaps there are already forces on the spot to handle it), at a time when hundreds and thousands of boys and girls are on the spot in danger of spiritual destruction, Heaven forbid—it is a great and holy obligation for all who are on the spot to do everything possible for them in the saving of souls, and to influence others to participate in this work. For whoever sustains one soul of Yisrael is as if he sustained an entire world, and especially tens, hundreds, and thousands.

I would be interested to know if the circle of teachers and friends who gather from time to time to discuss matters that interest them also bring up the history of Chassidus and relevant topics in the teachings of Chassidus, and your part in this specifically.

With warm regards to your parents, may they live, and with blessings of all the best to them and to all that is theirs.

## A-A

B"H, 10 Iyar, 5711, Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of 13 Nissan, which arrived with some delay, in which you inform me that several shidduch proposals have been suggested to you, but you are unable to decide for yourself due to a lack of sufficient satisfaction, and likewise regarding the current proposal for which preliminary outlines have already been made.

When I was at the Tziyun of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, I mentioned you for a blessing regarding what you need, and he will surely arouse mercy so that you may be blessed with a suitable arrangement very soon.

Regarding your doubts, you should surely take to heart how a physical home is built: even though one may beautify its exterior, the main thing is that it be built upon a strong foundation and with strong materials that are suited to the needs of the people who are to live in it, and not for the eyes of those passing by in the street.

And all the more so is this the case regarding the building of a home in Yisrael. The main thing is that it be built upon a strong foundation—which is Torah and yiras shamayim—for our Torah is called Toras Chaim, a "Torah of life," and a Torah of life in the literal sense as well, in that it serves as a guide for daily life. The opinion of the "passersby in the street" regarding "external beauty"—while it is human nature for this to be a measure of whether one is happy with their lot or, G-d forbid, the opposite—is nevertheless merely secondary to the aforementioned essential part.

Being a daughter of a Chassidic family, and having surely been raised in this spirit as well, it is certainly superfluous for me to elaborate and emphasize these matters, which are surely already known to you. Contemplating them will surely clarify for you, too, your position and your opinion regarding the honorable matters discussed with you. May Hashem guide you on the straight path to build a home in Yisrael upon the foundations of Torah and mitzvos, as they are explained and illuminated in the teachings of Chassidus.

I hope you will bring me good news regarding what is happening with you.

With blessings.

102

102

B"H, Pesach Sheni, 5711, Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, learned, etc., Rabbi Y. [may he live],

Greetings and blessings!

Enclosed is the booklet for the upcoming Lag B’Omer. May you merit to share it with the public in an appropriate manner.

Many reasons have been given for the joy and celebration of Lag B’Omer. However, we rely only on what is stated in the writings of the Arizal and brought in Chassidus: that this day is the day of the passing of Rabbi Shimon bar Yochai—**the Hillula of Rabbi Shimon**—who "reached at that hour the beginning and head of all his levels... and this was the content of his learning with his colleagues at that hour... and there shone within him an aspect of... the illumination of the light of Moshiach."

And every year, on this day, this state is awakened once again, as is known.

There is an advantage in these generations of ours: although the generation has become "fit" (in its entirety), nevertheless, in the earlier generations, permission was granted to reveal [these secrets] only to Rashbi and his colleagues alone. But in these final generations, it is permitted—and indeed a **mitzvah—to reveal** the inner dimension of the Torah. And it is specifically through this study that we will emerge from exile with mercy.

Happy is the person who, on this auspicious day—the day of the revelation of the inner dimension of the Torah—will strengthen himself and increase his resolve to establish regular study sessions in the inner dimension of the Torah: for himself, in gatherings with friends, and also to influence others, to the best of his ability, to do the same.

And it is through the light of this study specifically that we will also live in our engagement with the external dimension of the Torah, and "in all our ways we will know Him"—**that we will know Hashem and what Hashem demands of us**, whether in tefillah, in the study of Torah, in the fulfillment of mitzvos, or in the **conduct of our entire day in every detail of our actions.**

With blessings and regards to the entire group, may they live.

**M. Schneerson**

## 104

16 Iyar, 5711, Brooklyn

Greetings and blessings!

...You write that you are a student of the late Rabbi Yosef Dushinsky, and that you have named your son—may he live a long and good life—after him.

Surely you are doing everything in your power to follow the paths that Rabbi Dushinsky desired, and also to have an *ayin tovah* (a good eye) regarding others, in order to bring them closer to *Yiddishkeit*. I am interested to hear about this in detail.

Regarding what you write, that *Yiddishkeit* in your area is very weak: this in itself is sufficient reason for one who finds himself in a place where *Yiddishkeit* is weak to strengthen it.

As for your writing that better *shluchim* are needed for this, it is well known what my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, used to say: that Hashem brings a Jew to a certain place not only so that he should have material *parnassah* there, but also for the sake of spiritual *parnassah*—so that he should illuminate the place where he has settled and finds himself. If you begin to act in this regard, and do so with enthusiasm, Hashem will grant you success, and I look forward to hearing good news in this matter.

Enclosed is the *sicha* for Lag B’Omer from my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, which has just been printed. Surely you will read it, and it will bring you benefit in your *avodas Hashem*.

Awaiting good news, with blessings.

## 105

105

B"H, 16 Iyar, 5711, Brooklyn

Greetings and blessings!

I was distressed to hear—by chance—that you are not in good health and are in the hospital, and I hope to hear good news regarding the improvement of your health.

In my humble opinion, since you were privileged to be educated in the Yeshiva Tomchei Temimim Lubavitch and to be in the presence of the light of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, and the Rebbe Rayatz for many years, you should immediately undertake, for the improvement of your health, to teach Chassidus in public on Shabbos, and at the very least on one other weekday. Do not concern yourself at all with whether the number of listeners is large or small, nor with the level of their understanding.

Especially since, as we have received from our Nasi and our holy Rebbes, the teachings of Chassidus "awaken the souls of the listeners." Furthermore, there is a wondrous quality to it: the teachings of Chassidus purify the atmosphere. When the atmosphere is purified in one place, even a small one, it acts—by way of a *davar mashal*—upon the atmosphere of the entire world. Through this added strengthening of your *hiskashrus* to the *ilana d'chaya*, this will surely be the conduit for added vitality and the improvement of your health, also in the literal, physical sense.

With blessings for a speedy recovery, awaiting good news.

Under separate cover, I have sent the booklet for Lag B'Omer that was just published, along with the *Michtav Klali* pertaining to it.

## 106

106

B"H, 16 Iyar, 5711, Brooklyn

To the esteemed and distinguished Rabbi Mordechai HaKohen, may he live and be well,

Greetings and blessings!

I received your letter in due time for your birthday. May the one who blesses be blessed with Hashem’s blessing, which is far greater than the original, for a complete and pleasant life, with tranquility of soul and body.

Much is discussed in the teachings of Chassidus regarding the virtue of those engaged in business, specifically in two respects:

First, the person who conducts business with integrity and engages in significant activities in the field of tzedakah.

Second, the importance of setting fixed times for Torah study despite the pressures of business and commerce. Even though the duration of his study is less than that of those who sit in the tents of Torah, because it comes about by "tearing oneself away" from one’s business, it is exceedingly precious.

I am certain that you, too, have fixed times for study—not only in the revealed Torah but also in the teachings of Chassidus. May it be His will that this serve as a channel to bestow upon you success in your business and goodness, both materially and spiritually.

Enclosed is the booklet for Lag B'Omer that has just been published.

With blessings to you and your household, may they be well.

## 107

B"H, 16 Iyar, 5711, Brooklyn

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, and learned R' Shmuel, may he live.

Greetings and blessings!

I was pleased, at the time, to hear regards from you through the esteemed, G-d-fearing, and learned R' Eliyahu Simpson, who is involved in communal needs, that you spent time together sharing memories of days gone by—those luminous days when you were within the walls of the classrooms of Yeshivas Tomchei Temimim in Lubavitch.

Surely you are aware of the saying that my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, said in the name of the holy Baal Shem Tov: that everything that happens to a Jew occurs through *hashgacha pratis*—it is not a coincidence or a matter of chance.

Therefore, it is certain that the fact that Hashem orchestrated your meeting and time spent together will, I hope, have a positive effect—not only on R' Eliyahu Simpson, but also on you yourself. The proof of this is if it succeeds in bringing one closer to the source of life for all Jews, which is Torah and *mitzvos*.

Those who have merited to learn also of the *ohr hachassidus* and the conduct of *darkei hachassidus* possess a warmth for doing a favor for a fellow Jew, as well as a warmth for studying a *parsha* of *Chumash*, *Ein Yaakov*, *Gemara*, *Tanya*, and *sifrei chassidus*. Whoever engages in these things even once leaves an impression for their entire life; it depends only on one's will, and if he truly wills it, he will certainly be able to do so.

Enclosed is the *sicha* for Lag B'Omer from my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, which has just been published. Reading this *sicha* will surely do you much good.

I hope to hear good news from you, and I conclude with blessings for you and your family, may they live.

## 109

109

B.H., 16 Iyar, 5711, Brooklyn

To the esteemed Chossid, distinguished, G-d-fearing, etc., R’ Yehoshua, may he live:

Peace and blessing!

Thank you for the gift to my library, your book in Yiddish, *Fargangene Velten* (“Bygone Worlds”). It is a collection of memoirs describing the environment of Chassidim during special days, Shabbos, Yomim Tovim, and even weekdays.

I took a moment—as time permitted—to leaf through it, and I enjoyed seeing the warmth (*warmkeit*) with which the chapters of the book were written. Furthermore, I also enjoyed the warmth that, I assume, they will inspire in the reader.

However, I must also point out something in which others who write on similar topics have also stumbled. Their attitude toward this is as you wrote on the cover of the book, *Fargangene Velten*, which leaves the reader with the impression that what is written here is a sort of memorial for something that has, G-d forbid, already passed from the world. G-d forbid, and G-d forbid to say so! For just as the Ribono shel Olam is eternal, so too are Bnei Yisrael eternal, and as it is said, Yisrael, Torah, and the Ribono shel Olam are all one.

So too, the teachings of Chassidus, the ways of the Chassidim, and Chassidus itself are eternal. There may be a change of place, but never, G-d forbid, an end, Heaven forfend.

It is true that at certain times, the avodah becomes more difficult, and conducting oneself in the ways of Chassidim and Chassidus requires additional strength. But our Sages have already said, "According to the camel is the load," and they further said, "The Ribono shel Olam does not deal tyrannically with His creatures," and when He makes a demand, He only demands according to their strength.

Since we have been promised that eventually the *maayanos* of the Baal Shem Tov will spread outward, and this is also a prerequisite and a vessel for the coming of Moshiach Tzidkeinu speedily in our days, it is beyond any doubt that the matter is ongoing. If it seems to us that the darkness now is double what it was for the previous generation, then it is one of two things: either this is merely an illusion and a tactic of the *yetzer*, or we have been given the strength for this. Consequently, the great responsibility is placed upon us to gird ourselves with all our strength to push away the darkness through the advantage of light. Then, the promise of our Sages will certainly be fulfilled: "One who comes to sanctify himself a little below, they sanctify him much from above," and "One who comes to purify" (with a *patach* under the *tes*—openly), meaning to purify others and his environment, "they assist him"—in the plural—meaning the avodah itself and the mitzvah he performs assist him (as explained at length in *Likutei Torah* by the Alter Rebbe in the *maamar* for Shemini Atzeres, *d.h. Hashem Li B'Ozri*, Chapter 5) to complete the supernal intent to illuminate the darkness of the world and thereby hasten the destiny: "And it shall come to pass at evening time there shall be light," and "The night shall shine as the day," where the darkness of the golus itself is transformed into light. Then it will be said: "I will thank You, Hashem, for You were angry with me," meaning the gratitude will be not only for "Your anger has turned away and You comforted me," but also for the "for You were angry with me."

With blessings to add warmth and the light of Chassidim within Bnei Yisrael.

Enclosed is the booklet for Lag B’Omer that was just published.

***109***

**R’ Yehoshua:** Shpetman, London.

## A.I.

#### ***A.I.***

Published in Likkutei Sichos, Vol. 18, p. 438. Yagdil Torah, N.Y., Issue 2, p. 11, and completed according to the secretariat's copy. **R' Shmuel Menachem Mendel, may he live:** Libarov. 1) Berachos 22a. 2) Likutei HaShas by the Arizal on Moed Katan. In the printings I have seen (Koretz 5745, Livorno in the year *HaMiSHRaH*, Krakow in the year *KeVuTZ GaLioT*—and this omission was also copied into the sefer Ohr Einayim by the holy Rebbe, etc., etc., Moreinu HaRav Tzvi Saprin of Komarno, Ohr Sheni, Ma'areches Eimah—and it is puzzling that he did not notice this omission.) The beginning of the commentary of **Z.E.A.** is missing—but it seems clear to me that this is merely an obvious printing error. The text **should have read**: **"Shebeshem. Z.E.A. in the external forces, in the mystery of Hashem that is in the Name, a garment, etc."**—and the words between the first and second instance of the word "Shebeshem" were omitted in the printing, and the conclusion there: **"the external garment of all the King's garments"**—belongs to the commentary of **Z.E.A.**—and see also Eiruvin 54, top of side a. Tanya, beginning of Chapter 32. 3) In Pirkei D'Rabbi Eliezer, Chapter 41: The dead who are in Sheol were alive, and all those who are destined to be created until the end of all generations stood with them at Har Sinai. And see also Zohar Vol. 1, 91a. 4) Torah Or, Parshas Vayeitzei, explanation of the maamar beginning "V'shavti B'Shalom," and in Torah Or, ibid. And see also Derech Chaim, maamar beginning "Domeh Dodi," Chapter 6. Boneh Yerushalayim, Siman 106.

## 11

B"H,

It is known that our Sages of blessed memory stated: "And you shall make them known to your children... the day that you stood before Hashem your G-d at Chorev; just as there it was with awe, fear, trembling, and quaking, so too here (in every place and at every time) it must be with awe, fear, trembling, and quaking."

The Arizal explains: "Awe" refers to the mind of a person; "fear" to the heart; "trembling" to the internal organs; and "quaking" to the external limbs.

This means that when a person reads, reviews, or studies Torah, his entire being—his mind and heart, his internal and external self—must be in the same state that he was in at the time of the Giving of the Torah at Chorev.

And even though at that time they "saw the sounds and the torches," etc., and "Hashem spoke with you face to face," etc., how can every person draw this fear upon himself at all times? The answer is: when a person takes to heart that the Torah he is studying is an extension of *Chochmah Ila'ah*, and that the light of the *Ohr Ein Sof*—which is far above the parameters of *Seder Hishtalshelus*, where "before Him darkness is as light," and where above and below, spirituality and physicality are equal—is present and **revealed** there, then "just as there it was," etc., so too here, everything is **equal**.

And this [state] will be here below, in absolute revelation, to hear from the essence of the *Matzil* Himself, "I am Hashem your G-d," etc.—that even here it is just as it was then. The possibility and the capacity for this were granted at the time of the Giving of the Torah, for at that time the decree was nullified that "the heavenly beings shall remain in the heavens and the earthly beings shall remain on earth," and "Hashem descended upon Mount Sinai," and to Moshe He said, "Ascend to Hashem."

This matter recurs, and this empowerment is awakened every single year during the days of the festival of Shavuos, the time of the Giving of our Torah, by the "Giver of the Torah"—the word "Giver" being in the present tense.

As a preface to this, it is incumbent upon us, upon each and every one of us, to accept upon ourselves that we will **"do" and "hear"**—to prioritize "doing" over "hearing"—as the meaning of this is well explained in the teachings of the **D**ivrei **E**lokim **C**haim.

**Menachem Schneerson**

21 Iyar, 5711. Brooklyn, N.Y.

## 112

B"H, 22 Iyar, 5711, Brooklyn

Greetings and blessings!

I have received your *pidyon nefesh* in which you request a blessing for the healing of your eye condition and for your wife, *tichyeh*.

When I visit the *tziyun* of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, *ztzukul-l-h-h, n-b-g-m, z-y-a*, I will mention both of you for a *refuah*, and I hope that you will be able to share good news with me in this regard.

Every Jew must create *keilim* to receive the blessings of the *Ribono shel Olam*. Therefore, if you have not done so until now, you should begin from now to recite *Tehillim* every day, the *shiur* of *Tehillim* as it is divided for the days of the month, so that you complete the entire *Tehillim* over the course of the month. You should also study a portion of *Chumash* every day, completing the *sedra* over the course of the week. Furthermore, you should participate in *shiurim* in public at the *beis medrash*—specifically those *shiurim* to which you feel an attraction. Your wife, *tichyeh*, should give *tzedakah* to the *kupah* of Rabbi Meir Baal HaNes—*Rambahen*—before lighting candles every *erev Shabbos* and *erev Yom Tov*.

I hope to hear good news from you. I am enclosing the *sicha* for *Lag B'Omer* that was printed recently; please study it and delve into it.

With blessings for a speedy *refuah*.

## 13

B.H., 22 Iyar, 5711, Brooklyn

Greetings and Blessings!

...You ask in your aforementioned letter regarding the fact that you have submitted papers to immigrate to Canada, and you ask for my opinion on this.

In general, according to the information available regarding the prospects for material livelihood in Canada, it is not so easy. Some time ago, I wrote to one of our anash from France that it would be very appropriate for them to endeavor to move and settle in Morocco (naturally, in one of the two cities where our institutions are located, namely Meknes or Casablanca), in Australia, or in South America. According to the information we receive from those places, it is possible to establish oneself there with a material livelihood, and there is also a vast field there for spiritual livelihood. The time has already arrived when—in the words of my father-in-law, the Rebbe—anash must deeply contemplate the matter of *hafatzas hamaayanos chutzah* and know that this is truly directed at us. Even though the question arises for everyone within themselves, "Who am I and what am I?" the truth is that it is not our business to think that way. Since we have been placed in this generation—which is "standing behind our wall," waiting for the completion of the matter of "when the feet reach the feet"—to bring the *maayanos* of *Da"ch* even into the *chutzah* where they had not been until now, then through the power of the *Atzmus u’Mahus* of the *Ein Sof*—who entrusted His word to us through His holy servants, the Rebbes—we will go forth on this *shlichus* and we will succeed.

Of course, the above does not contradict the effort to obtain papers for Canada or any other place.

With regards to the whole group and a blessing for a successful settlement soon.

## 114

B"H, 22 Iyar, 5711, Brooklyn

To the renowned Torah scholar, a man of profound insight, possessor of noble character, who engages in communal needs with faith, our friend, the honorable Rabbi Avraham Yitzchak, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

I have heard much about you from our friend, the chossid, who engages in communal needs, the honorable Rabbi Moshe Leib Radstein, may he live, regarding your activities in strengthening Yiddishkeit in your city in general, and especially regarding your participation in the affairs of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, and his holy institutions in particular. I was pleased to hear that you will continue to strive in this, notwithstanding the great loss that the Jewish people have suffered—the passing of their captain, my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory.

Or more accurately, not *notwithstanding* the loss, but rather the opposite: after such a great loss, the responsibility placed upon each and every one of us has increased many times over—to stand firm with even greater intensity against all the concealments and hiddenness. Especially this concealment and hiddenness, for the passing of the righteous is **more** difficult than the destruction of the Beis Hamikdash. This obligates and grants merit to each person who recognizes the needs of the Jewish people, especially in these days of double and redoubled darkness, where they call light darkness and darkness light, to stand firmly at one’s post. Anyone who has influence over a certain environment, and especially a rabbi and leader of a community, must strive all the more in strengthening Yiddishkeit and in disseminating Torah.

We have already been promised that "whoever adds, they add to him." One of the interpretations of this is that whoever adds strength to his avodah in Torah and mitzvos, they add to him strength and ability to go from strength to strength. This is especially true for "your heads, your tribes"—the rabbis of the communities—for the merit of the many depends on them to lead them on the path that ascends to the House of Hashem.

May Hashem grant that you lengthen your days at your post, the holy post, in tranquility and abundance, and may you lead your congregation in peace. And there is no peace but Torah, as our Sages of blessed memory said (Sanhedrin 99b): "Whoever occupies himself with Torah for its own sake brings peace to the heavenly entourage and the earthly entourage." May you turn many away from iniquity, to draw their hearts closer to our Father in Heaven.

Enclosed is the booklet for Lag B'Omer that was published recently, along with a copy of the general letter pertaining to it, which I hope will interest you.

With blessings for success in your holy work and all the best in your personal matters.

#### ***114***

**Rabbi Avraham Yitzchak:** Perlstein, Chicago.

## 15

B"H, 22 Iyar, 5711, Brooklyn

Greetings and blessings!

I received your letter in due time regarding the health of your son, may he live and be well, about whom you are worried due to the opinion of one doctor who discouraged you and weakened your hope for his complete recovery.

Surely you are aware of the statements of several of our Rebbeim regarding the teaching of our Sages, "And he shall surely heal," that permission is granted to the doctor **to heal**. This is the only power and authority the doctor possesses—**to heal** in matters of medicine. In particular, since the second doctor does not agree with the pessimistic opinion, you have no reason whatsoever to weaken your positive hope. This is even more true in our days, when new medications and new methods in the field of medicine are being discovered every single day.

At a time of favor, when I am at the Tziyun of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, I will mention your son, may he live and be well, for a recovery. My hope is strong that in time you will be able to bring me good news regarding this. However, it is self-understood that, Heaven forbid, you must not weaken your trust in Hashem, for He is the Healer of the sick, and there is no obstacle for Him to save, whether through much or through little. Through an increase in strength in your trust—**both on your part and on the part of your wife, may she live**—this will undoubtedly hasten the improvement of your son’s health, may he live and be well.

It is appropriate that you take upon yourself additional study in Torah in general, and in the teachings of Chassidus in particular, as well as giving to tzedakah—even if only small amounts, but consistently and frequently—in the merit of your son, may he live and be well. I will await good news from you regarding the above.

With regards to your father-in-law, the esteemed Chassid, etc., Rabbi... may he live and be well, and with a special blessing for your son... may he live and be well.

## 116

B"H, 22 Iyar, 5711, Brooklyn

One should not be anxious about this, as there is generally a standstill in business right now. 117

B.H., 22 Iyar, 5711, Brooklyn

To the esteemed and distinguished chossid, who toils in the vineyard of Hashem, etc.,
Rabbi Chaim Hillel, may he live.

Greetings and blessings!

I received your letter of 12 Iyar in due time, in which you describe the nature and manner of your avodah in the Talmud Torah in your camp, as well as regarding the learning with the students whom you visit to teach in their homes.

It would be appropriate to send here a list of the students—both those who learn in the Talmud Torah and those with whom you learn in their homes—along with their mothers' names, so that they may be mentioned at the Tziyun during an *eis ratzon*.

It is unnecessary to elaborate on the value of this lofty avodah, and it is also unnecessary to explain that the effort regarding the number of students has no limit. One should not be satisfied with those who are currently enrolled, as our Sages have said regarding the verse, "In the morning sow your seed, and in the evening do not withhold your hand." It is also well known that whoever sustains one soul, it is as if he has sustained an entire world. Surely you are doing everything possible in this regard, but "one only encourages those who are already diligent," and therefore I have written these lines.

Surely you have heard the saying of the Rebbe Maharash, "If it is good, it is good; if it is better, it is not better." The time has already come to seek counsel on how to guide the students and teach them—especially those who come to the Talmud Torah—not only the "light of Torah" and the "lamp of mitzvah," but also the "source of light" within the Torah, which is the study of Chassidus and conduct in the ways of Chassidus. This should, of course, be done for each individual in a manner appropriate to his current standing and situation, as is also explained in the Sicha for Lag B'Omer, which is enclosed.

I ask you to convey my blessing for success in your work to all those who participate with you in the aforementioned matters. May the saying of our Sages be fulfilled in them: "He who comes to purify himself is assisted," and he is granted the strength whereby the Torah and the mitzvos assist him (see Likutei Torah, Drush Shemini Atzeres, s.v. *Hashem Li Be'ozri*, Chapter 5). And "to him who adds, they add more"—may they be granted an addition of vitality and light, both in general matters and in personal ones.

Regarding your note on Tanya, Chapter 2, concerning the phrase *mima'al mamash* (literally from above):
a) The Alter Rebbe would refer to Atzilus as "the supernal Atzilus"—see the Maamar s.v. *Oteh Or Kasalmah* (5672).
b) *Mima'al* (from above)—see *Sefer HaKitzurim L'Tanya*, p. 73, that it refers to the supernal worlds—and consequently, it is understood that this is above Atzilus. The word *mamash* (literally) is not needed for this.
c) In a letter from the Rebbe Rayatz (from the year 5698, which will be printed in due course), he relates at length how the Tzemach Tzedek delved into these words. For *mima'al* means "higher than anything one could conceive of," implying there is nothing above it. If so, what is the meaning of *mamash*? *Mamashus* (tangibility), the sense of touch—this is a contradiction! The Alter Rebbe answered him: *Mima'al* is *ratzo* (ascending), *mamash* is *shov* (descending). The meaning of this, in my opinion, is that through the *shov*, one reveals two opposites within the soul: 1) *Mamashus*, a connection to matters of the sense of touch; 2) A loftiness greater than all ascents, as is known regarding the superiority of *shov* over *ratzo*. See also *Biur Tanya* by Harashag (Kupfer), p. 144.

With blessings for success in your work and for good health.

## 118

B"H, 22 Iyar, 5711, Brooklyn

Greetings and blessings!

... [You] have begun thinking about traveling here in order to study at the Tomchei Temimim Yeshiva and to be in the midst of the Chassidim:

In my opinion, there is no reason to rush this. It is worthwhile that you continue your work in the garden or in other work—physical labor—and in your spare time, set fixed times for Torah study to learn on your own, and also strive to disseminate Torah in your surroundings. For we do not know which is greater (both in terms of the matter itself and regarding the worker himself): whether to be in an environment of Chassidim and absorb it, or to fulfill the shlichus of spreading the wellsprings outward, even if it **seems** that through this, your portion of knowledge in Torah or in the conduct of the ways of Chassidus and Chassidim is diminished. This doubt is even greater according to what is explained in Iggeres HaKodesh, Epistle 69, that in these generations, the primary avodah is along the line of tzedakah.

It goes without saying that G-d forbid to despair of traveling here, but for the time being, it is good and proper that you take part in the development of the yeshiva in your location in a manner suitable to your ability and strengths, and strengthen your health as it should be through your work in the garden and the like, until you are in robust health.

Enclosed is the sicha from 13 Shevat, in which you will see what was discussed at the farbrengen then, regarding the self-improvement that is incumbent upon each and every one, which depends specifically upon his own standing and situation, and one should not always learn from one person about another.

With blessings and regards to the entire group.

## 19

B"H, 22 Iyar, 5711, Brooklyn

Greetings and blessings!

In response to the *pan* you sent me: when I was at the *tziyun* of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, *ztzukulleh"h, navgam, zya*, I mentioned you for what you need. Surely he is arousing Divine mercy for you and your wife, that you should be in good health, with peace of mind and peace of body. This is especially true since, as you write, you possess a letter from my father-in-law, the Rebbe, with his holy blessing to be settled in a life of goodness.

In your letter, you **write** that you are suffering from an ailment—though you do not specify what the ailment is—but that you are liable at any moment to a serious heart attack, *chas v'shalom*. (In my opinion, this is not the case, and you are greatly exaggerating—if you will forgive me for saying so.) You also write that an iron partition separates you, and that your *tefillah* and *tzedakah* have not been effective, etc.

Surely you yourself understand that these are merely figments of the imagination. For even if there were an iron partition, we have been promised by our Sages, of blessed memory, quite simply that not even an iron partition separates the Jewish people from their Father in Heaven. Furthermore, regarding what you write—that your *tefillah* and, most importantly, the *tzedakah* you distribute have not been effective—I have seen in a small book, the *Tanach*, and it is written there (*Malachi* 3:10) that the *Ribono shel Olam* says: "Test Me now with this"—with the *mitzvah* of *tzedakah*—that if you only give *tzedakah*, then "I will pour out for you a blessing, etc." The same applies to *tefillah*, as is explained in many places in the words of our Sages.

The essence of the matter is as explained in the books of Chassidus: this is one of the tactics of the *yetzer hara* to cause a person to fall into a state of sadness. If one must be extremely careful even regarding sadness that stems from spiritual matters, then certainly regarding sadness that comes from elsewhere—there is nothing worse than that.

Strengthen your trust firmly in what all the Jewish people believe, even the simplest of the simple: that the *Ribono shel Olam* is not only the Creator of the world, but also its Guide—and not only in the past, but He guides it every day, every moment, and every hour. And He does not only guide the "great world," but also all the affairs of the "small world," which is man. Since the *Ribono shel Olam* is the ultimate good, He will surely, in the end, show even to physical eyes that everything will be for the good, even in a revealed and manifest way. However, this requires strengthening your *hiskashrus* to the living *Elokus* through setting fixed times for the study of the "Torah of life," through the *avodah* of *tefillah*—by which one performs an act of kindness for the living soul—and through strengthening the fulfillment of *mitzvos*, and in particular the *mitzvah* of *tzedakah*, which is truly "charity for life."

I hope that in the near future you will inform me of an improvement in your situation materially, and also an improvement in your situation spiritually—meaning that all thoughts regarding the existence of a partition, etc., have been nullified. You should strive and strengthen yourself in fulfilling the command of the *Ribono shel Olam*: "Serve Hashem with joy."

Enclosed is the *sicha* from Lag B'Omer that was recently distributed; please study it deeply.

Awaiting good news.

## 120

B.H., 22 Iyar, 5711, Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, and distinguished R' Dovid Aryeh, may he live:

Peace and blessing!

Enclosed is a receipt for your contribution, which I have directed toward our educational work in Africa. This assistance comes at a most opportune time, as our work has, thank G-d, expanded significantly and must continue to expand further.

For many years, the state of education in the countries of North Africa was severely neglected due to the great poverty prevailing there, as well as a lack of active workers and communal leaders in this field.

However, with the help of Hashem, the situation has changed for the better over the past year through the educational institutions we have established there: yeshivos, yeshivos ketanos, Talmud Torahs for boys and for girls, evening courses for workers, and a beis medrash for teachers to train instructors and melamdim from the local youth.

Our program in North Africa envisions establishing Talmud Torahs and yeshivos in all the cities and towns. This work, which is also connected with providing material aid such as food, clothing, and the like, naturally requires large sums. Yet, it is a great and rare zechus to have a share in this holy work, which began with the initiative of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory. I hope that lovers of Torah in general, and anash in particular, will exert themselves to give and to generate as much assistance as possible, through which they will also create great and broad channels for blessing and success in both material and spiritual matters.

I am sending a message to your son, Mr. Zalman Yaakov, may he live, and I wish him a safe journey home.

With blessing,

## 121

B"H, 23 Iyar, 5711, Brooklyn, N.Y.

It will surely please you to hear that our work in North Africa is continuing to expand, B"H. Our institutions—the yeshivos, yeshivos ketanos, Talmud Torahs for boys and Talmud Torahs for girls, evening courses for workers, and also a *beis medrash* for teachers—have made a name for themselves, and the number of students increases daily. Furthermore, we are being approached from various cities and countries in all parts of North Africa to extend our work to places it has not yet reached.

This is truly a work of *hatzalas nefashos*, because due to the great poverty on one hand, and the influence of the *le'umas zeh* on the other, thousands upon thousands of children in those countries find themselves in great danger of being severed, *chas v'shalom*, from Yiddishkeit.

Therefore, everyone must exert themselves to take an ever-greater part in this work, and also influence friends and acquaintances to have a share in this endeavor, through which one opens channels to receive Divine blessings in both material and spiritual matters.

With blessings,

It may be only for a few minutes to wear the tefillin, but he must absolutely put on tefillin every day. Hashem Yisbarach will protect him, and he will return home safe and sound. I am sending a message enclosed here, and she should forward it to her son, may he live.

With blessings.

## 1:24

B"H, 25 Iyar, 5711, Brooklyn

Greetings and blessings!

Since we met in the beis medrash, I have not had the opportunity to see you again. I am writing to you now to send my blessing to you, your daughter, and your son-in-law, yichyu, that you should derive nachas from your grandchild and their son, sheyichyeh, and that you should raise him to Torah, to the chuppah, and to maasim tovim.

As we now stand before the Yom Tov of Shavuos, the time of the giving of our Torah, it is brought in the Midrash that Hashem requested guarantors, and only after the Yidden provided guarantors—that their children would fulfill the Torah—did Hashem agree to give the Yidden the holy Torah.

This must serve as a lesson for us all: that anyone who wishes to receive the Torah as it ought to be received must exert effort to ensure that his children and grandchildren, as well as the children of other Yidden, are educated in the way of Torah. One must assist the mosdos and all those who are involved in the proper chinuch of Jewish children—boys or girls—so that they may be good, frum Yidden.

With blessings for a Chag Sameach, and regards to your son-in-law and daughter, yichyu, with wishes of Mazal Tov.

## 25

B.H., 25 Iyar, 5711, Brooklyn

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, and distinguished individual who engages in communal needs with faith, etc.,
R. Yom Tov, may he live.

Greetings and Blessings!

It was with pleasure that I read your letter, in which you write about the progress and success in the work of the Yeshiva Achei Tmimim in Boston, and of your constant work and assistance for the Yeshiva.

I still remember your warm words when we met a short time after the histalkus of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, regarding the institutions of my father-in-law, the Rebbe. I am certain that you will continue your good work for all the institutions of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, and that you will also influence your acquaintances and friends to join in this work. This in itself—as is brought down in seforim—will bring success in your private affairs.

Regarding your question and proposal to renovate and add a few more rooms in the same Yeshiva building, since the current space is too cramped and cannot accommodate all the students who wish to come to the Yeshiva, but it will cost several thousand dollars and some members are doubtful whether this should be done:

Turning away children who wish to enter the Yeshiva to learn is something that, aside from the fact that it should not be done in and of itself, will also cause damage, G-d forbid, to the good name of the Yeshiva, and consequently, a loss in the Yeshiva's income as well. According to the situation as you present it—that there is no other choice but to renovate the rooms of the current Yeshiva building—it is certain that the other members will also agree to this. May Hashem Yisbarach grant that it be with success.

We are now standing close to the days of Shavuos, the time of the Giving of the Torah. It is brought down in the Midrash that before the Giving of the Torah, the Almighty asked for *arvus*—guarantees—and did not accept the *arvus* of the holy Patriarchs, nor that of the shepherds of Israel, until the Jews said that their children would be the guarantors, that they would teach them Torah and educate them in Yiddishkeit. Only then did Hashem agree to give the holy Torah. This must be a lesson for us all: that one of the preparations for receiving the Torah is intensified work in the chinuch of Jewish children.

I ask that you convey my greetings and blessings to all the melamdim of the Yeshiva and all those who assist the Yeshiva, both materially and spiritually, and in particular to the esteemed Rav and Chossid, the G-d-fearing and distinguished individual who engages in communal needs with faith, etc., etc., Rabbi Zuber and Rabbi Kastel, may they live.

With blessings for receiving the Torah with joy and inwardness.

Enclosed is the sicha from Lag B'Omer, which was recently printed, and which I am sure will interest you.

***

**R. Yom Tov:** Priluk, Canton, Mass.

## 126

B"H, 25 Iyar, 5711, Brooklyn

To the distinguished Rabbi, the G-d-fearing, who occupies himself with communal needs in faith, etc., Moreinu HaRav Shlomo Zalman, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

In due time I received the *pidyon nefesh* on behalf of Mr. ... and surely he took his *tefillin* with him, and likewise gave him the message from my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory. It is necessary to warn him double and triple to put on *tefillin* every day—excluding, of course, *Shabbos* and *Yom Tov*—and if it is impossible for him in the morning, then he should put them on during the day until sunset. In any event, he should put them on even for a short while, even if he is forced to remove them immediately. Explain to him that this *mitzvah* is a special *segulah* for long life and years, as our Sages of blessed memory said: "Whoever puts on *tefillin* lengthens his days." Consequently, this is not merely a matter of religion, but also a protection from danger. He must be careful in this, regardless of his standing and situation regarding the observance of *Torah* and *mitzvos* while at home. Surely you will find the appropriate words for him, and if he needs it, you may transcribe for him what is written here in the English language...

Awaiting good tidings.

***

**Moreinu HaRav Shlomo Zalman:** Hecht. Additional letters to him: above, Vol. 3, 468, and in the references noted there. Below, 138, 114.

## 127

B.H., 25 Iyar, 5711, Brooklyn.

To the esteemed and distinguished, etc., Rabbi Yehuda Leib, may he live:

Peace and blessing!

I was pleased to hear greetings from you through the esteemed and distinguished, etc., who engages in communal needs with faith, etc., Rabbi Eli Simpson. He also told me about the farbrengen you had together in a warm Chassidic environment, and how my father-in-law, the Rebbe, used to say that a Chassidic farbrengen warms the head, the heart, and right down to the soles of the feet. When one returns home from such a farbrengen, one brings light and warmth into the house, so that the home becomes brighter and warmer than it was before.

You surely know what my father-in-law, the Rebbe, told many times in the name of the Baal Shem Tov: that everything a Jew hears and sees, he can learn a moral lesson from for his own personal avodah to Hashem. This is especially true regarding one’s source of livelihood, which one is connected to for a long time—many days of the year and many hours of the day.

Your business, which you are about to begin in a good and auspicious hour with this new patent, consists of taking used sacks. Because they have been used, bacteria have taken hold in them, which not only provide no benefit, but on the contrary, can ruin whatever one puts into them. One seeks ways to eliminate these bacteria, and one of the methods is to place the sacks in a closed space and increase the heat there more than usual, which the bacteria cannot withstand. Consequently, the sacks are freed from the bacteria, and they can be used once again.

It is the same in our own lives. When the yetzer tov comes to a person at the age of thirteen, the person has already been "used" by the yetzer hara, who arrived before the age of thirteen. The yetzer hara claims a *chazakah* (presumptive right) over the body of the person and over his thoughts, speech, and actions, claiming to be the firstborn. There is a remedy for this, so that foreign thoughts, ulterior motives, or improper intentions from the yetzer hara do not easily take hold in one’s thoughts, speech, and actions. The remedy is to seclude oneself for a certain time from the outside atmosphere, to enclose oneself within the *daled amos* of a shul, yeshiva, or beis medrash, and there to warm oneself more than usual with *ahavas Hashem*, *ahavas haTorah*, and *ahavas Yisrael*. The "sack" itself is then freed from the bacteria of the yetzer hara, and whatever one puts into it then is healthy and useful. And just as with the literal sacks, a one-time disinfection is not enough for it to be perfect, so too with the "sack of man": when one rises from sleep, one must once again absorb within oneself Jewish, Chassidic warmth, and then one can be certain to be an *oved Hashem*, a student of Torah, and one who fulfills mitzvos.

I wish you success in your endeavor, and may Hashem help that what my father-in-law, the Rebbe, told in the name of the Alter Rebbe, the author of the Tanya, be fulfilled in you: Hashem gives Jews physical livelihood in abundance, and Jews turn that physicality into spirituality, using it to provide for themselves and their households in a kosher manner, for the strengthening of Yiddishkeit and the dissemination of Torah.

I hope to hear good news from you.

With the blessing of a happy holiday and the receiving of the Torah with joy and inwardness.

## 1,028

B"H, 25 Iyar, 5711, Brooklyn.

To the esteemed and distinguished individual, who occupies himself with communal needs in good faith, etc., Moreinu Harav Elyakim Getzel, may he live.

Greetings and Blessings!

Through the esteemed and distinguished Chossid, who occupies himself with communal needs in good faith, etc., Moreinu Harav Ben Zion Shemtov, may he live, I was happy to receive regards from you and from your entire family, may they live. He also delivered your *pidyon nefesh* to me, and I read it at the *tziyun* of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, when I was there this past Lag B'Omer.

Surely you know that the day of Lag B'Omer was called by Rashbi—as it is the day of his passing—his day of joy. It is also known that "joy breaks through barriers." The reading of a *pidyon nefesh* on the day of Rashbi’s joy at the *tziyun* of our Nasi—who is the one who reveals the secrets of Torah in this generation of ours, and through whose Torah we are all connected to the *ilana d'chaya*, which is the inner dimension of the Torah, and through which there is connection and *dveikus* to the living Elokus—this reading has the power to break through concealments and obstructions, and to draw down for each person what they require in terms of children, life, and abundant sustenance. I hope that you will be able to bring me good tidings regarding the matters about which you wrote in your *pidyon nefesh*.

Enclosed is the *sicha* from Lag B'Omer that was recently printed. May you study it and delve into it, and through it, you will be able to quench your soul's thirst regarding many matters that require resolution.

I look forward to hearing good news from you, both regarding yourself and regarding your family, may they live. I will conclude with a blessing for a joyous Chag Shavuos and for the receiving of the Torah with joy and inwardness.

## 29

B"H, Erev Rosh Chodesh Sivan, 5711, Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, and distinguished [name],

Shalom u’Bracha!

Enclosed is the Kuntres for the upcoming Chag HaShavuos. It is intended to be used to bring merit to the many in an appropriate manner.

"And whoever has the ability to..." and the merit of the many depends on him; therefore, [Hashem] will also assist him in this very matter, to succeed in this influence.

***

It is known that during the festivals and holidays of every year, the matters associated with them are aroused—on Chag HaMatzos, the matter of the Exodus from Egypt; on Lag B’Omer, the revelation of the inner dimension of Torah, etc.—and that time is a uniquely opportune moment for the internal drawing down and absorption of these matters in particular.

And these days, the time of the giving of our Torah, are days of *segulah* (special virtue) for the *am segulah* (treasured people) to receive the *segulah*—which is the Torah—with joy and inwardness.

However, the Holy One, Blessed be He, said to Yisrael: "Bring Me good guarantors that you will keep the Torah, and I will give it to you." And the guarantee He accepts from them is only the guarantee of the children. When the recipients of the Torah said, **"Our children are our guarantors"** (that we will educate them in the way of Torah), the Holy One, Blessed be He, said: "These are certainly good guarantors; through them, I will give it to you." 

**And as it was then, so it is now.**

It is incumbent upon each and every one of us, as we prepare ourselves for the upcoming time of the giving of our Torah, to do everything in our power now regarding the education of our sons and daughters in the way of Torah, and to resolve and take upon ourselves to strive with greater intensity and greater strength in this regard for the days that follow the receiving of the Torah.

**And all Yisrael are responsible for one another.**

The aforementioned effort, if it is only for the education of one’s own sons and daughters, is not sufficient at all.

Each and every person **certainly** has the ability to influence—to a certain degree, at the very least—the education of the sons and daughters of Yisrael in his immediate vicinity, and sometimes even the education of those who are in a distant place, or even in another country.

And if everyone is obligated to strive to strengthen and expand proper education in the place where it already exists, and to strive to introduce it in a place where it is not yet recognized,

Then how much more so must one rise with all his might and fight against any action or matter that is liable to disconnect a son or daughter being educated in the way of Torah from this education of theirs, and which is liable to distance them from the Torah of the living G-d, and certainly if it is liable to bring them to the point of *kefirah* (heresy), *chas v’shalom*.

And the promise of our Sages is known: Everything for which Yisrael have sacrificed their lives is maintained in their hands. 

With blessings for receiving the Torah with joy and inwardness,

**M. Schneerson**

## 130

B"H, Erev Rosh Chodesh Sivan, 5711, Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the brilliant Rabbi, G-d-fearing, a man of exemplary character, wise and understanding, known for his praise, etc., etc., Moreinu HaRav Ben-Zion Meir Chai Uziel, may he live, Rishon LeTzion.

Greetings and blessings!

Approaching the time of the giving of our Torah, may it come upon us for good, I wish to express my blessing that we may celebrate the festival of the receiving of the Torah with joy and inwardness, "on the morrow of the seventh Shabbos"—both in its deeper sense and in its literal sense, according to the calendar of this year.

It is known how Chassidic teaching explains (Likutei Torah by the Alter Rebbe, author of the Tanya, Parshas Emor, discourse beginning *Veheineif*, ch. 28) "on the morrow of the Shabbos"—meaning above the (holiness of) Shabbos, the *makifim* of Imma. This provides the strength for the *Sefiras HaOmer*, as explained in the Zohar (Vol. III, 96a, and elsewhere).

Knowing the holy affection that your honor, may he live, holds for the words of Torah and the holy *sichos* of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, I am sending herewith the **Kuntres Chag HaShavuos** of this year, which has just been published.

With holiday blessings and great respect.

1031

B"H, Erev Rosh Chodesh Sivan, 5711, Brooklyn, N.Y.

The brilliant Rabbi, G-d-fearing, wise and understanding, who occupies the seat of Torah, who organizes and clarifies, possessing noble character traits, who seeks the good of his people, etc., Moreinu HaRav Yitzchak Isaac HaLevi, may he live, Chief Rabbi.

And according to the calendar of this year, it is for everyone "seven complete Shabbosos" (Menachos 65b), and not merely complete days.

- Regarding what the Rambam writes: that that Pesach occurred on Shabbos, as **the foolish imagined** (Hilchos Kiddush HaChodesh, ch. 7, halacha 11), it can be said that he calls them foolish because their excuse is no excuse, as the Rambam concludes there. And he writes regarding this **"imagined,"** because Moshe, who passed away on the 7th of Adar, this occurred on Shabbos or Erev Shabbos (noted in the commentaries on Shulchan Aruch Orach Chayim 292, and in the introduction of the Rambam: **the entire** Torah was written by Moshe Rabbeinu before he died **in his own handwriting** and he gave, etc.). And if so, the day after the Pesach of the year they entered the land was on a Tuesday (and they had not yet received the general rule that Pesach cannot fall on a Monday, Wednesday, or Friday, and these are ancient matters), or a Wednesday. -

I hope that the health of your honor has improved as it should, and I pray that Hashem will send you a speedy recovery and that you will return to your full strength very soon.

Knowing the holy affection that your honor harbors for the words of Torah and the holy sichos of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, I am sending the **Kuntres Chag HaShavuos** of this year, which has just been published.

With regards and with the blessing of the festival, with honor and appreciation,

**M. Schneerson**

## 132

B"H, Erev Rosh Chodesh Sivan, 5711, Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, refined in character, public activist of many accomplishments, of noble lineage, etc., Rabbi Yitzchak Meir HaKohen, Minister of Social Welfare,

Shalom u’Bracha!

As we approach the time of the giving of our Torah, may it come upon us for good, I wish to express my blessing that we may celebrate the festival of the receiving of the Torah with joy and inwardness.

My soul is deeply pained by the situation prevailing in Eretz Yisrael, may it be rebuilt and established, as every day brings most distressing news from there. Furthermore, the fragmentation among the Chareidim themselves is a most painful affliction.

Yet, my hope remains strong that, in the end, a unified religious front will be organized, especially following my conversation regarding this with Mr. Moshe Shapira, the Minister of the Interior.

As I have written previously, it is clear to me that the elections in Eretz Yisrael at this time will, G-d forbid, cause a stumbling block for the entire Yishuv, as well as for every enterprise connected to it in other countries, particularly in the U.S.—such as the Bond drive, the United Jewish Appeal, the U.N., and so forth. Since it is hidden from no one—and especially not from the Yishuv on the ground—that the matter is close to a loss and far from a gain, it is not inconceivable that even at this late hour, there is still a possibility to cancel the elections through appropriate efforts. However, if despite all this it does not succeed, then if there is at least a possibility to postpone the elections for a time, it would seem that this, too, is worth every possible effort; even a small rescue is still a rescue.

Knowing the holy affection that you, sir, hold for the words of Torah and the holy sichos of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, I am sending you herewith the **Kuntres Chag HaShavuos** of this year, which has just been published.

With regards and wishes for success and a happy holiday.

## 133

133

B"H, Rosh Chodesh Sivan, 5711, Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the crew members and their officers at their head,
Of the ship "Misgav," on their visit to the United States

Greetings and blessings!

It was with pleasure that I heard from your colleague, the avreich Mr. Yitzchak Gittelsohn, regarding your visit to the United States. Through him, I wish to send you my greetings of "welcome in peace," along with my regards and best wishes.

It is self-understood that one of the goals of a visit to the U.S. or other countries is to acquire honor and acclaim for the settlement in our Holy Land—may it be built and established—by serving as an example and symbol of the development of life in Eretz Yisrael, and by representing before all the best strengths of our people, the important and the exalted within it.

And what is the important and the exalted among us in the eyes of all the nations?

Ever since the Children of Israel became a nation—that is, from the time of the Giving of our Torah, an event we celebrate on the upcoming festival of Shavuos, may it come upon us for good—the Children of Israel have been the fewest of all peoples, the fewest in quantity. But from that very time, they have served as a model and a guide to the entire world in quality, in spirituality: the dissemination of the idea of the oneness of Elokus, and the observance of the way of Hashem to perform charity and justice, and so on.

From then until now, in every generation they have risen against us, yet despite all this, the Children of Israel live and endure, at the very same time that those who rose against them—Assyria and Babylon, Greece and Rome—met their end in destruction, leaving no remnant or survivor.

It is clear from the above that the secret of our people’s existence does not depend on quantity, but rather on quality. Not on the strength of the arm, but on the eternal spiritual values that our people have absorbed into their essence, becoming one with them.

In the language of the verse: **"And you who cleave to Hashem your G-d are all alive today."**

The same applies to the purpose of your visit wherever you go. In your desire to represent what is characteristic of Jewish life and the primary line of the Jewish people—that which distinguishes them, that in which they excel, and that which constitutes their greatness—you must hoist high and emphasize the spiritual strengths of the Jewish people, their elevation of form over matter. As in the saying of our prophet: "Not by might, nor by power, but by My spirit, says Hashem Tzeva-os."

With blessings for a happy holiday and success in fulfilling your true mission and your essential role in this world.

#### ***133***

Printed in Likkutei Sichos, Vol. 13, p. 162, and completed according to the secretariat's copy.

## 1,034

B"H, 1 Sivan, 5711, Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, and distinguished, etc., R' Zalman Shimon, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

It was with pleasure that I received your letter informing me that the date for the wedding of your niece, may she live, has been set for Thursday, the 10th of Sivan, upcoming. Please convey to her my blessing that the wedding take place at a favorable and auspicious time, and that they build a home in Israel upon the foundations of Torah and mitzvos as explained in the teachings of Chassidus, and may they be blessed with a righteous generation.

With blessings of Mazal Tov, Mazal Tov.

I was pleased to read in your letter that you intend to record your memoirs from the years 5680–5686, when you were in Rostov. You should certainly record them in detail, in accordance with the statement of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory: "When one recounts a story, one must relate it with the entire context—the time, the place, and the surroundings." This is as brought in the sichos of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, that his father, the Rebbe (Rashab), of blessed memory, would accustom him to the question, "What do you remember?" so that through this, all the matters he had seen or heard would be engraved in his memory. In these times, when forgetfulness is more prevalent in the world, it is very necessary that every story in general be written down, along with all its details. For just as the first Tablets and the second Tablets were both [inscribed by] the Divine (though the first Tablets also had the power to ensure there would be no forgetfulness in the world). See the maamar beginning *Lech Lecha* 5666, *Yud-Tes Kislev* 5689, and elsewhere.
