## 1031

B"H, 1 Sivan, 5711, Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

I received your letter of 2 Bamidbar, in which you write that you are being offered a promising match, but the young woman in question is still hesitant. It is possible that she—and her father—will come to me to ask for my opinion.

You do not mention the name of the young woman in your letter, nor is it clear whether you are asking for advice or whether you simply want me to be aware of your perspective before she and her father come to see me.

Regarding the matter itself, in such situations one usually seeks out acquaintances or relatives who might be able to influence the other side in the desired manner. It seems from your letter that you are unable to clarify the reason why they have not yet reached a decision regarding this proposal. Surely, when you have good news to report in this regard, you will inform me.

I am interested to know whether you have a set time for Torah study in general, and for the study of Chassidus in particular. If in previous years the necessity of studying Chassidus was clear, in our times it is an absolute requirement—for many reasons. In your specific case, it is superfluous to elaborate, since—as you mention in your letter—your grandfather traveled to the Rebbe. To use the language of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory: if you turn to me with a question regarding a shidduch—which is among the most difficult matters, comparable to the splitting of the Red Sea, as our Sages have said that the Holy One, Blessed be He, sits and makes matches—and I am neither an expert shadchan nor even a non-expert shadchan, yet you still wish to hear my opinion, then surely you should also heed my opinion regarding the necessity of having a set time for studying Chassidus. May the Almighty grant you success in your life’s path; through connecting yourself to the inner dimension of Torah—which is the "light" within the Torah—it will illuminate your conduct, so that you find the correct path and the decision that is most appropriate for you, both materially and spiritually.

Enclosed is the sicha from Lag B'Omer that was published recently, along with the general letter related to it, in which the study of the inner dimension of Torah is also discussed.

With blessings for receiving the Torah with joy and inwardness.

## 137

B"H, 1 Sivan, 5711, Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

I received your letter from Lag B'Omer. Yesterday, when I was at the Tziyun of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, I mentioned you for a *refuah*, and I hope you will share good news regarding this.

Regarding your concluding request—"I ask that you revive me with a good *teshuvah*, at the very least a *teshuvah tata'ah"—I have already answered others among *anash* (may they live) that we are currently in the time of *ikvesa d'Meshicha*, the very heels of the heels. As my father-in-law, the Rebbe, said and repeated several times, there is nothing left to refine but the small vessels. It is also a received tradition that the vessel for the coming of Moshiach is the *hafatzas hama'ayanos chutzah* (spreading the wellsprings outward). You, too, should exert yourself in *hafatzas hama'ayanos*; surely, even in Jerusalem (may it be rebuilt and established), you can find people who fall into the category of "outward." Warm them and illuminate them with *Chassidishe* warmth and light. When one is immersed in light, the darkness is naturally removed. If it is necessary to nullify and uproot letters of *machshavah, dibbur, u'ma'aseh* (thought, speech, and action) that are not as they should be, this too can be accomplished through the "line of the right"—that is, through tears of joy, as explained in the commentary on "Let tears stream down like a river" (*Eichah 2:18*; see also *Derech Mitzvosecha* 11a). As for matters of intellect and *midos* that are not entirely aligned, this is achieved through the three loves: love of Hashem, love of Torah, and love of Israel, and through engagement in Torah—specifically the "light" within the Torah, which is the teachings of Chassidus. Through this, there will be an *atahpcha chashucha l'nehora* (transformation of darkness into light).

It is difficult for me to intervene from here in the *kollel* regarding the matter of providing a monthly stipend for your grandson (may he live). In its stead, I am enclosing a certificate for a package. I sign with a blessing for a speedy recovery and that you may share good news regarding your health, your personal matters, and the happenings among *anash* in general.

With the blessing of receiving the Torah with joy and inwardness.

## 39

B"H, 3 Sivan, 5711, Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and blessings!

In anticipation of the festival of Shavuos, the time of the giving of our Torah, which approaches us for good, I hereby send you my blessing: may you have a joyous festival and may you receive the Torah in its inwardness.

The Torah, which is the wisdom of the Creator, may He be blessed and exalted, is longer than the earth and broader than the sea. When Hashem gave it to us on Mount Sinai, it was, as is well known, given according to the capacity of each and every individual, and each person grasps it according to the power of their intellect.

There are those who grasp the Torah as the aspect of "choose life" in its literal sense—that its reward is great in this world and the next, and that the Torah protects and saves one from punishments, both severe and minor.

And there are those who possess the insight to understand that the Torah is a guide, showing the path upon which people should walk and the deeds they should perform, both as individuals and as a community, for "its ways are ways of pleasantness and all its paths are peace."

Yet, even these two perspectives, which relate only to the *nigleh* (revealed) aspect of the Torah, are not yet complete.

The teachings of Chabad engage also with the **inwardness** of the Torah, revealing the light within it and its essential purpose, in accordance with the statement of the Zohar: "Three levels are bound one to the other: Yisrael, the Torah, and the Holy One, blessed be He." The Torah is the central bond that connects the creation with the Creator, may He be blessed.

The matter, in brief, is that creation is *yesh me'ayin* (something from nothing), and not by way of cause and effect (as explained at length in the teachings of Chabad). Therefore, there is no inherent value or connection between the "something" and the "nothing." In this regard, there is no difference between the lowest of the inanimate and the highest of the speakers, since all—inanimate, vegetative, animate, and speaker—are created beings. Even the most perfect human being cannot grasp Him at all, for even the intellect is a created thing, as it is well known that there is no comparison whatsoever between the limited and the Unlimited.

However, the Creator, may He be blessed, who is the ultimate good, desired to give man the possibility to emerge from the boundaries and constraints in which he finds himself, being a created being, and to ascend higher and higher—not only within his created world, but even beyond it—in order to unite with his Creator in a complete union. Therefore, in His great goodness, He gave us the Torah of truth and sanctified us with His mitzvos, through which and by means of which a person can emerge from his narrow world and unite with the Creator in a complete union and cleave to Him, as it is written: "And you who **cleave** to Hashem your G-d are **alive** all of you **this day**."

With blessings for the receiving of the Torah with joy and inwardness.

## A.M.

A.M.

Blessings for receiving the Torah with joy and inwardness, and surely you will hold a Chassidishe farbrengen.

**Menachem Schneerson**

#### ***A.M.***

General telegram to Anash.

## 101

B"H, 9 Sivan, 5711, Brooklyn.

To the distinguished Rav, the esteemed and G-d-fearing, etc., R' Kalman Nachum, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

It was with pleasure that I received your regards, and I am satisfied with your involvement in communal affairs in our camp, and with your kindness in conveying regards and blessings to all those who have participated and will participate with you from here on. May Hashem grant each and every one of them success in all that they need, and may they be able to share good news in this regard.

Sent in a separate package is the *Sefer HaSichos* of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory. Surely, during a time of favor (*eis ratzon*), such as *Seudah Shlishis* of *Shabbos* or on *yomei d'pagra* and the like, you will find an appropriate way to merit the public with the holy *sichos* printed therein. These contain matters suitable for every type of person, from the greatest scholars to the simplest of the simple. As is known, this is a matter of the "line of truth," and especially in our Torah, the Torah of truth, where the truth must extend from one end to the other, as explained briefly in *Tanya*, end of Chapter 13.

I am interested to hear about the public study *shiurim* that take place in the *beis medrash*. Surely, the *takanah* of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, is also practiced among you: to recite *Tehillim* every day after *davening*, according to the monthly division. This is in addition to the *shiurim* that are equal for every soul to study individually: the study of the *Chumash* portion with *Rashi* every day (on Sunday from the beginning of the *sedra* until *Sheni*, on Monday from the *Sheni* portion until *Shlishi*, etc.), and the *Tanya* *shiur* as divided for the days of the year (as printed in the *Moreh Shiur*).

With regards to the entire group, and a blessing for material and spiritual good. Awaiting good news, and there is no good other than *Torah* and *mitzvos*.

#### ***101***

**R' Kalman Nachum:** Fisher, Shebagin.

## 142

B”H, 9 Sivan, 5711, Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

I have just received your letter dated 25 Iyar. You have surely received the Kuntres and the Sicha by now, along with my letter. At an auspicious moment, I will mention you and your wife, may she live, at the resting place of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, for whatever you may need. I stand by what I have written to you previously: I do not understand your agitation and your mental anguish at all. For even the appointment of a minor official is decreed from Heaven; how much more so for a Rav in Israel. It is obvious that he must be aware of the responsibility placed upon him, but it is even more obvious that if such thoughts cause him sadness and mental anguish, they certainly come from the *sitra d’le’oiz*—or as my father-in-law, the Rebbe, called it, "the clever one." Every hour and every moment that he thinks about this, these are thoughts originating from the chambers of the *sitra d’le’oiz*. Regarding them, it is said that **immediately** upon their ascent there (into his mind), he must push them away with both hands, divert his attention, and not accept them willingly. This applies to every person, for the level of *beinoni* is the level of every person, and every person can attain it. (There is no contradiction here with the statement in *Tanya* that a *beinoni* has never committed a sin, nor with the statement in Chapter 14 that every person can be a *beinoni* at any time and at any hour; for the meaning of this is that, given his current state, it is not relevant for him to commit a sin, neither in the future nor in the past—but this is not the place to elaborate.)

It is understood from all the above that regarding what you write in your letter—that you are requesting a different position—I am not at all pleased with this. You must remain in your position and be strong in your trust in Hashem, that He will guide you on the path of truth and grant you success in your holy work. If doubts arise for you in this, it is not a doubt in your ability, but rather a weakness in your *bitachon*. The advice for this is to study *Shaar HaBitachon* in *Chovos HaLevavos*, and in general, to be connected to the "Tree of Life"—which is the study of Chassidus—and to participate in *farbrengens* of Chassidus with true Chassidic joy, frequently, to rejoice and to bring joy to others.

And since you have already moved into your new home, you should have arranged a *Chassidishen farbrengen* as it ought to be, and recalled the old times—when we would spend time at a *farbrengen* without calculating what so-and-so might say, or what the "left side" or the "right side" might say. They knew only that a *Chassidishe hitva’adus*—to hear Chassidus, a *Chassidishen vort*, and a story about our Nasi, may his merit protect us—brings light, and a little light pushes away much darkness. Furthermore: why must we think about the darkness? Let us think more about the light, especially since we are standing at the time of the giving of the first Tablets, *charut* (engraved)... "Do not read *charut*, but *cheirus* (freedom)..." May it be Hashem’s will that in your new home, a change of place will bring a change of fortune for the good. May your home be a warm home, a joyful home, filled with the candle of the *mitzvah* and the light of Torah, and the "light of Torah"—which is the teachings of Chassidus, the ways of Chassidus, and the customs of Chassidim. From time to time, you should host a *Chassidishe hitva’adus* there.

I look forward to hearing good news regarding the improvement of your state of mind, and that, finally, you will accept the yoke upon yourself—that from now on, you will fulfill the command of our holy Torah to serve Hashem with joy and a glad heart.

## 143

143

B.H., 9 Sivan, 5711, Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed and distinguished activist, a man of many accomplishments, etc., R' Moshe Shapira, Minister of Interior and Immigration

Shalom and blessing!

I received your telegram, and in response, I sent you a telegram today, which reads as follows: "I was alarmed by your telegram regarding the dissolution of the Religious Front. Many are blaming Hapoel Hamizrachi. Certainly, if the parties forgo party gains, the establishment of the Front will be possible—which is necessary not only for the collective but also for each of the parties individually. I have strong hope that at such a critical hour, every party will recognize its responsibility toward the collective and will bring about the establishment of the Front. In accordance with our conversation here, I am confident that you will exert yourself in the above, and I thank you in advance for the good news you will share with me regarding this. With blessing, awaiting the mercies of Heaven."

The news in your telegram was a surprise and a bitter disappointment to me, after you had promised me that there would certainly be a united front and that you would inform me if there were any change in the situation. Therefore, I had hoped with certainty that there would be a front, despite the rumors to the contrary, as I had not heard from you about any change.

My hope is strong that you will exert all your energy toward the realization of the matter of the Front, even if it is necessary to make party concessions, especially since a concession in this regard is close to a reward.

I wish you success in the aforementioned efforts and thank you in advance for good news regarding this.

With regards and blessing.

I am sure you have already received the telegram regarding the necessity of the united Religious Front that was sent to you signed by the representatives of the Religious Front here, as well as the telegram from Mr. Moshe Feuerstein on this matter.

## 444

444

B"H, 9 Sivan, 5711, Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, and distinguished individual, who engages in communal needs, etc.,
Mr. Yosef, may he live, Burg

Greetings and blessings!

Relying upon our meeting in Paris in the year 5707 and the impression that remained with me from that encounter—which, according to the law of the Torah, establishes a Jew in the presumption of his integrity—I am writing these lines.

It is a pity that while you were here, we did not have the opportunity to meet. I will suffice here with a brief written note, as it is unnecessary to elaborate on the responsibility of the hour in connection with the elections in our Holy Land, may it be rebuilt and established.

I had hoped that the elections would not take place at all, as the time is not appropriate for them, or at the very least, that there would be complete unity within the Chareidi Judaism of Eretz Yisrael to create a united front for the elections.

It is unnecessary to elaborate to one such as yourself that in a matter concerning the good of the collective, every party must forgo partisan gains that run counter to the good of the collective. It is unnecessary to elaborate to a Chareidi person that matters concerning Chareidi Judaism take precedence over all calculations of material gain—even if that gain is certain, and certainly if it is imagined and doubtful—especially when this imagined gain could also be close to a loss.

I refer to the united front within the religious Judaism of Eretz Yisrael, which is a necessity not only for the good of the collective but also for each of the parties themselves. I appeal to you as a Chareidi person to exert all your efforts and influence to create a united religious front, even if the matter involves partisan concessions. I am confident that you will place the matter of Chareidi Judaism in its entirety at the forefront and exert influence in this direction wherever your influence reaches.

Awaiting your notification of good news in this regard,

With regards and blessings.

With best regards and blessings.

## 147

B”H, 13 Sivan, 5711, Brooklyn.

To the Poalei Agudath Israel (Pagi) Organization
in Eretz Yisrael

Greetings and Blessings,

I had hoped that the elections in the Holy Land—may it be rebuilt and established—would not take place at this time, or at the very least would be postponed, as for several reasons the time is not appropriate for them. In any event, I hoped there would be unity within the Charedi Jewish community in order to establish a united front for the elections.

I was greatly alarmed to receive the news of the dissolution of the Religious Front.

It is surely unnecessary to elaborate before you that in a matter such as this, every party must forgo partisan gains that run counter to the good of the collective. Regarding matters that concern Charedi Jewry as a whole, priority must be given over any material gain—even if that gain is certain, and certainly if the gain is illusory, doubtful, or—in particular—if it could potentially lead to a loss.

For these reasons, and relying upon your letter to me from the 12th of Adar II, I believe that further elaboration on the above is unnecessary. I am certain you will exert every effort to ensure that the Religious Front continues—a matter that is truly essential, not only for the good of the collective, but for each of the parties themselves.

I thank you in advance for informing me of good news regarding this.

With regards and blessings,

#### ***147***

**Your letter to me from the 12th of Adar II:** To the Rebbe, Rabbi Menachem M. Schneerson, Admur of Lubavitch, New York: The telegram and letter from the Rebbe were a subject of discussion among us, and we are pleased to inform the Rebbe that we found in his words great strength and encouragement for our position. Anyone who knows and recognizes the abysses between one person and another in this land—and the partitions that divide—cannot help but be alarmed by the horror of the elections. Furthermore, we do not have, nor have we ever had, any intention or desire to appear in the elections with a separate list, even though we were filled with hesitations regarding the drawbacks involved in establishing a "Religious Front." These hesitations, which this is not the place to detail, have only grown over the two and a half years of the Front’s existence and its participation in the government. But since the Religious Front has already been created, the threat of division is so great that the fear of it is sufficient to tip the scales in favor of a unified appearance. In the first elections, we expressed this position explicitly, but that unified appearance failed due to the rigid stance of people who place questionable matters above public interests. We were forced then to act against our spirit, and even today, there exists the full possibility for a unified appearance if those who were responsible for the first failure do not sabotage it.

May the Good Hashem spread the shelter of His peace over us, over all of Israel, and over Jerusalem.

Yehuda Blau, Poalei Agudath Israel (Pagi) Organization, Eretz Yisrael, Central Committee

## 448

B"H, 15 Sivan, 5711, Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and Blessings!

I was happy to learn through my dear friend, the esteemed and pious chossid, R' Chaim Mordechai Isaac Chadakov, may he live, that your affairs have been arranged for the best. May Hashem grant that in the future as well, matters will be arranged—both in physicality and in spirituality—in a manner befitting the body of a Yid and the soul of a Yid. And, naturally, there can be no peace between them unless the body heeds the voice of the soul, or more accurately, unless the *nefesh habehamis* heeds the voice of the *nefesh elokis*.

The path to this is as our Sages have said: "Whoever engages in Torah *lishmah* makes peace in the heavenly retinue and in the earthly retinue." The "earthly retinue" refers to the *nefesh elokis*—and the body and the *nefesh habehamis* (see *Likutei Torah*, *Parshas Matos*, the *maamar* beginning *Hechaletzu*). I am certain you are keeping the *shiurim* we spoke about.

Enclosed is a receipt for the sum you sent for my attention. I have delivered it to the *Lishkas Chashaim*, the *tzedakah* fund from which assistance is given discreetly and without publicity. It is well known that *matan beseser* (giving in secret) is one of the highest virtues of *tzedakah*.

With blessings for success in both physicality and spirituality.

## 149

B"H, 15 Sivan, 5711, Brooklyn.

To the Rabbi, the Gaon, the G-d-fearing, the distinguished scholar, the master of order, etc., etc., Moreinu Harav [Margolios] shlita,

Peace and blessing!

I received your letter in due time, and just now your book has also been received—Sefer HaBahir with your notes and illuminations. Thank you, thank you for this.

Regarding what you wrote asking for my opinion on this: It is a great thing you have done and are doing with your *nitzutzim* (sparks) and notes on the Zohar, Tikkunei Zohar, HaBahir, and Zohar Chadash. There is wisdom here, and there is craftsmanship here.

The Sages’ teaching is well known: "He taught knowledge to man—that He taught him the signs of the cantillation marks" (Eruvin 21b). Scripture uses this as a preface to "He pondered and investigated, and composed many proverbs" (referencing the various examples of this in the beginning of Shir HaShirim Rabbah). This is especially true regarding the Zohar, etc., a field where room has been left for one to distinguish oneself. I have seen, firsthand, the great benefit of your *nitzutzim* during my own study and review of these books, and the blessing of the many who will use the Zohar with your notes upon it shall come to you.

It is only a pity that you were brief in every place, even in places where it is said one should elaborate. But it is a wonder, and indeed a cause for surprise, that except for a few places—a mere handful—you do not bring in your commentary anything from the books of Chabad Chassidus that relates to the subject matter of your books. This is especially so given that in Chabad Chassidus, a unique explanation is provided for the matters of the wisdom of Kabbalah and the mysteries of our Sages in the Zohar. The wonder is even greater in these days of ours, when these books are becoming increasingly widespread and the opposition of the past has ceased, etc., etc.

As you requested, the Haggadah has been sent to you in a separate package, and your name has been recorded on the list of those who receive the *kuntreisim*.

With the blessing that the strength of your Torah may increase in the "garment and body of Torah," and also in its "soul and the soul of its soul" (Zohar III, 154a).

**P.S.**

As is my custom, I immediately leafed through the pages of the book out of affection for the matter, and in my haste, I noted:

**In Section 1:** Regarding what is brought in *Ohr Bahir* from Sefer HaTziyoni, "Here you have clear proofs **that the light** was created"—in the Lemberg 1882 edition that I have, it is indeed so. It should be verified in earlier editions, for in my opinion, it is clear that it should read "**that the darkness** was created." Regarding the matter of whether darkness is a creation in itself, see the note at the beginning of the *Kuntres* for 12 Tammuz 5708.

**In Section 200:** One should note the Midrashic teachings brought in *Torah Sheleimah* on Bereishis, Chapter 3.

Sefer HaBahir is cited in *Torah Ohr* (the Kehot edition, which is the Vilna edition) 18c, 114c (twice). In *Likutei Torah*: Parshas Beshalach 2a, Vayikra 35b, Bamidbar 51a, 63c, 64a, 94a.

See there in all the aforementioned places.

## To Anash

## 1

B.H., 15 Sivan, 5711, Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the graduating students and their parents, may Hashem grant them life,

Peace and blessing!

On the occasion of your graduation, I greet all the graduating students who are moving on to higher grades and divisions in their path of *chinuch al taharas hakodesh*.

The summer vacation is beginning—days of rest and refreshment of one’s strength, and for gathering new strength for the new *zman* that is approaching for us and for you for the good.

You must know, dear children, that vacation does not mean a *hefsek*—a break—from learning and from *chinuch*. A Jewish child must not be without Torah study and proper *chinuch* even for a single day, summer or winter. On the contrary: taking into account the abundance of free time that students have during the long summer days, you must utilize it to thoroughly review what you have already learned and to prepare yourselves for your continued path, the path of Torah and *mitzvos*.

In this way, you will—together with gathering fresh physical strength—also draw upon fresh spiritual strength. Both together, and especially the spiritual strength, make a person whole and healthy.

And you, Jewish parents, who always carry the responsibility of parents and educators at the same time, must remember that especially during the summer months, almost the entire responsibility rests upon you.

I send you my blessing, that Hashem Yisbarach should grant you, dear children, and your parents, as well as your *melamdim* and educators, *shichyu*, health in *gashmius* and in *ruchnius*, with much *nachas*, Jewish *nachas*, with *menuchas haguf* and *menuchas hanefesh*.

With a blessing for a healthy summer—in *gashmius* and in *ruchnius*.

**M. Schneerson**

## 53

53

By the grace of Hashem, 17 Sivan, 5711, Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

I received with pleasure the book *Kocho D’Rashbi* which you sent me. I offer you my thanks for this, in accordance with the Sages’ teaching: "The wine belongs to the owner, but the thanks belong to the waiter" (Bava Kamma 92b).

Since the principle that "the thanks belong to the waiter" applies only if he is a *baal bechirah* (a person of free choice)—as explained in the *Sefer HaMitzvos* of the Tzemach Tzedek, Mitzvah of Milah, Chapter 3—it follows that this applies only if the waiter is a member of the Jewish people. This is not the case for an angel or one who is not a *ben bris*; see *Likutei Torah*, Parshas Emor, *Biur V’Heinif*, Chapter 3. This requires further study.

Please convey my thanks to the author of this book for the gift. If it is possible to send his other books to our library, or to exchange them for books published by Kehot, I thank you in advance. May the author’s strength be fortified for printing a book that pertains to the *nistar* of Torah in general, and to the *Zohar* in particular, for "through it, the Jewish people will emerge from exile **with mercy**," speedily and in our days.

However, I am surprised, for as it appears in many places in this book, the author draws his reasoning from the teachings of the Baal Shem Tov and his disciples, yet I have not found—as of now—any citations from the books of Chabad Chassidus, even though the matters he deals with in his book are explained therein.

There were days of old when, in certain circles, they were wary of studying the teachings of Chabad, based on the principle of "Do not inquire into what is too wondrous for you," and that one should only occupy himself with "the faith of Hashem all the day," as is found in the books of the Rebbe of Zidichov and others.

This is exactly like the situation several generations prior to that time, when many of the great figures of Israel were wary of the dissemination of the general Chassidic teachings—the teachings of the Baal Shem Tov. And several generations before that, they were wary of the dissemination of the *Zohar*.

But as decades passed after the *Zohar* was publicized, and then decades after the revelation of the Baal Shem Tov and his teachings, and then the six luminaries of the Chabad Nesi’im shone—and continue to shine even now—from the Alter Rebbe until the Rebbe Rayatz, the matter has been decided by living proof.

For when one contemplates the results of studying the *Zohar*, the results of studying the teachings of the Baal Shem Tov, and in our generation, specifically the results of diligent study of Chabad Chassidus—it is beyond any doubt that the *Zohar* is the "Tree of Life," the teachings of the Baal Shem Tov are the "fountains" of which Mashiach spoke to the Baal Shem Tov, and the study of Chabad Chassidus is the very path to understand the *Zohar* now. This is the manner in which the "fountains will spread outward," for only then will "the Master come"—this is King Mashiach.

And all of us, who have merited (even though we are not of the stature of the previous generations) that now they have revealed, and revealed **clearly**, many of the hidden matters in the teachings of the *Zohar* and Chassidus, to the point that they have become understood in the *chabad* of the soul (at the very least—their existence, if not their essence), whereby the power of the intellect in the soul also **becomes empowered** with the knowledge of Hashem—how He fills all worlds and encompasses all worlds, and "all is considered as nothing before Him," etc., and not merely the power of faith—if someone does not "seize and eat, seize and drink" from this, even though he has become aware, **through Divine Providence**, of the existence of these Chassidic teachings, it should arouse great astonishment. Furthermore, since it is within his ability to engage in this area of Torah and he does not do so, he has not fulfilled his obligation of *Talmud Torah* to the best of his ability, etc. See *Hilchos Talmud Torah* by the Alter Rebbe, Chapter 1, end of the last section, regarding the aforementioned: "And so said the Sages of Truth... and they further said..." and it concludes: "Everything that his soul is capable of attaining from the knowledge of Torah... this is the rectification of perfection, and it is impossible for it to be rectified and perfected in the 'bundle of life' with Hashem, in its source from which it was hewn, without this knowledge."

The length is unnecessary for a matter that is understood, and also simple (after the fact).

I will note here some of the places, though not all, where this is discussed in *D’rachim* of Chassidus (that are printed) regarding the Rashbi: **Iggeres Kodesh**, Section 19, etc. **Torah Or**, 23c. **Likutei Torah, Vayikra**, 18a (there is a gloss there by the Tzemach Tzedek that the Baal Shem Tov was also in this category), 28a (and regarding what is written there, "in every chapter," it requires study). **Bamidbar**, 84c, 87d.

**Devarim**, 12b, 43a (seemingly the meaning is that even less than sixty [years] is also not [the case]. And if so, this is higher than the level of King David, and it requires study). **Shir HaShirim**, 19c. **Siddur**, *Shaar* of Lag B’Omer. *VeHecherim*—5631, p. 52 and onwards, and in many places. In the *Maamar* "Va’Eileh Shemos" (of the year 5612, now in print) by the great Rabbi, the great Gaon, the great Chassid, etc., R. Hillel of Paritch, it states: "In the name of the Alter Rebbe, that before lofty souls like the Rashbi, the Beis Hamikdash was not destroyed at all," and a word to the wise is sufficient.

I will conclude with what can be said, by way of possibility, regarding the Sages’ teaching that serves as the opening preface to the book *Kocho D’Rashbi*. It is in the *Yerushalmi*, Sanhedrin, Chapter 1, Halacha 2: When Rabbi Akiva ordained Rabbi Meir and the Rashbi, he said, "Let Rabbi Meir sit first." The face of the Rashbi darkened. Rabbi Akiva said to him, "**It is enough for you that I and your Creator recognize your strength.**" There are many wonders here, among them: **The content of the response:** Since He recognizes your strength, why did He not have him sit first? And if the Rashbi’s strength is not sufficient for this, he should have said so; it makes no difference that "I and your Creator recognize your strength." And what is written in the commentary *Pnei Moshe* there, that it is because Rabbi Meir was older than him—according to this, the answer is **entirely** missing from the book. **The style of the response:** The precision of the term "your Creator," when he should have said "the Holy One, blessed be He," "the Merciful One," or similar, as is customary in the words of our Sages. Especially since the acquisition of Torah comes to the Sages not through creation, but through the forty-eight qualities that they **strive** for. The precision of the word "**your strength**," when he should have said "**your wisdom**," since we are dealing with the ordination of elders—one who has acquired wisdom. **The arrangement of the response:** He should have said "your Creator and I," and not the reverse, as is understood.

The matter in brief, for time does not permit the necessary length: The entire Torah is in the supernal *Atzilus* (see *Torah Or*, *Chayei Sarah*, *Maamar* beginning "Lashon Adoneinu"). It is then enclothed and drawn down—the Talmud (the reasons for the *halachos* in their entirety, etc.) in *Beriah*; the Mishnah (the bodies of decided *halachos*, whose reasons are enclothed and hidden within them) in *Yetzirah*; see all this in *Tanya*, Chapter 53. And Kabbalah is in *Atzilus* alone (see there in the aforementioned *Torah Or*, *Tanya* end of Chapter 50 in the gloss, *Kuntrus Acharon* *Maamar* beginning "Lehavin Mah Shekasuv B'Pri Etz Chaim").

Now, the Rashbi was the "Master of the Secrets of Torah," and the intermediary to draw this down also to the other mighty *Tannaim*, to draw the inner dimension of Torah into the revealed Torah openly. As explained in the aforementioned *Hemshech VeHecherim*.

Now, the order of the seating of the elders—regarding the debate and analysis, there is not much difference between who sits first or who comes after. But regarding the **ruling** of *Halacha*, in monetary cases, the debate begins from the great one who sits first, and in capital cases, they begin from the side (Sanhedrin, Chapter 4).

Based on all the above, the *Yerushalmi* statement is understood—that when Rabbi Akiva came to seat Rabbi Meir and the Rashbi according to the order, which pertains to the matter of **ruling** *Halacha*, he seated Rabbi Meir first, who was the one who "illuminated the eyes of the Sages in *Halacha*" (Eruvin 13b). The face of the Rashbi darkened, knowing his strength in the analysis of Torah (Shabbos 33b) and that he was the "Master of the Secrets of Torah," and the intermediary for the other *Tannaim* as aforementioned—(even if one were to say that some of these qualities came to the Rashbi long after he was ordained by Rabbi Akiva, some of them were present even before this, and the main thing is that he knew his ability in this, what he could attain, for "a gourd is known by its blossom").

Rabbi Akiva said to him—"It is enough for you that I (the *Shechinah*, from the word ***Atzilus***—see *Zohar* I, 6b, and in many places. And see also *Sukkah* 53a: 'If I am here,' etc., for that is the place of Kabbalah, as aforementioned) and your Creator (the Talmud in ***Beriah***, drawn from the *Shechinah* that is in *Beriah*, as aforementioned) recognize your strength (even though it has not yet been revealed so much in practice regarding the ruling of *Halacha*, which is in *Yetzirah* as aforementioned. And therefore he said 'your Creator' and not 'your Former'), (and see the explanation of the concept of 'strength' at length in *Likutei Torah* for the three *parshiyos*, 56c). And all these are wonderful qualities, and therefore it is enough for you, even though in decided *halachos*—*Yetzirah*—Rabbi Meir sat first."

—And all the aforementioned wonders are explained, and a word to the wise is sufficient.

With blessings for good in all matters.

## 154

B"H, 17 Sivan, 5711, Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Rav and Chossid, G-d-fearing and learned, etc.,
Rabbi Mordechai Avraham, may he live, HaKohen

Greetings and blessings!

I received your letter with the note regarding what is written in the *Kuntres Chag HaShavuos 5711*, page 278: "The Rebbe makes the Kohen Gadol." In my note there, I left the precise intent of this statement as requiring further study (*tzarich iyun*). You wish to explain this based on what is written in *Avodas Yisrael* (by the Maggid of Kozhnitz) in the *maamar* for Yom Kippur, that the *tzaddikim*, through their holiness, elevate the Kohen Gadol and the *shaliach tzibbur*.

This does not seem correct to me, for we do not have a Kohen Gadol at this time, and if your intent is regarding the *shaliach tzibbur*, then the essential point is missing from the text. In my opinion, the intent is that the Rebbe, *k'vod kedushas admoreinu* (the Rashab), *nuch nafshei*, explained what these tasks are now in terms of the *avodah* of the individual—what one must accomplish within one's own soul. When he reached the matters of the Kohen Gadol, he said that in order to reach a level akin to that of a Kohen Gadol **regarding the aforementioned spiritual avodah**, "the Rebbe makes the Kohen Gadol," and only afterwards can the person who has been influenced perform the *avodah* of a Kohen Gadol in a spiritual sense.

If this is the intent, then there are two contradictory novelties in the matter: a) that every person is **obligated** also in the *avodah* of a Kohen Gadol—obviously in a spiritual sense (see *Iggeres HaKodesh*, section 27: "Apart from the mitzvos that are incumbent **upon the King**," and he does not list the Kohen Gadol; see also *Shaar HaGilgulim*, Introduction 11, 16; *Shelah*, *Chelek Torah Shebichtav* at the beginning; *Toldos Yaakov Yosef* in the introduction). b) That it is **impossible** for him to begin this *avodah* until he is first assisted to become a Kohen Gadol—this remains in need of further study (*tzarich iyun*).

With blessings for a speedy recovery.

#### ***154***

Printed in *Likkutei Sichos*, Vol. 16, p. 618, and completed based on the secretariat's copy. **Rabbi Mordechai Avraham, may he live:** Friedman.

## 155

155

B"H, 17 Sivan, 5711, Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, learned, and distinguished R' Yaakov, may he live:

Greetings and blessings!

In connection with your visit to me, I would like to express my blessing once again that you and your wife, may she live, should be granted long and good days and years.

For a Jew, "truly good, long years" means filling them—with peace of mind and body—with good deeds. This means filling the days and years with actions connected to Torah and mitzvos, which express in actual practice the three loves: *ahavas Hashem*, *ahavas haTorah*, and *ahavas Yisrael*. Such a life brings success and blessing both in one’s own home and in the homes of one’s children and grandchildren, may they live.

As I told you in person, the Rebbe, my father-in-law, of blessed memory, would often repeat a teaching from the Baal Shem Tov: from everything a Jew sees or hears, one must learn a lesson in how to serve the Ribono shel Olam. Naturally, one must also learn from one’s constant occupations.

Before one wears clothing, it is completely clean, neatly pressed, and everything is in its proper place. However, after wearing it for a while, it becomes wrinkled, dusty, or stained.

Nevertheless, one does not throw such clothing away; rather, one sends it to a laundry or a cleaner. The launderer places the item into a vessel or machine where there is a warm or high temperature—hot water—as well as various chemicals or soap. All of this removes the dust and stains. Afterward, it is pressed by applying a weight or pressure to the item, and then the garment can be worn again.

The same is true for a Jewish *neshamah*. When the Ribono shel Olam gives a Jew his *neshamah*—man and woman alike—the *neshamah* is pure, pressed, and perfectly suited to the individual, as we say every day in the *brachos* of *davening*: "The *neshamah* that You have placed within me is pure."

With time, however, as one uses it for worldly matters, the *neshamah* becomes wrinkled when it is not used for what the Ribono shel Olam desires. It can happen that dust or stains adhere to it when one fails, *chas v'shalom*, to perform a *mitzvah* that one should do, or when one commits, *chas v'shalom*, an *aveirah* that one must not do.

Nevertheless, the Torah teaches us that one should not, *chas v'shalom*, lose hope for the purity of the *neshamah* and its suitability for a human, Jewish life. Rather, one must place it into a warm temperature—that is, to warm it with the warmth of Torah and *mitzvos*, so that it "cooks" in them and gains vitality. This warmth must be a moist warmth; it should have moisture and adhesiveness to all holy things. This is achieved through heartfelt *davening*, regarding which it is written: "Pour out your heart like water" (*Eichah 2:19*); and through heartfelt learning, as it is written: "Ho, everyone who is thirsty, come to the water" (*Yeshayahu 55:1*)—and "water" refers only to Torah.

To this, one must add various elements: giving *tzedakah*, observing *kashrus*, and other *mitzvos*. Through these, the *neshamah* becomes completely pure once again. And if one places upon it the "weight" of Torah—even though it may seem like a burden—it not only does not ruin the garment, but it presses it out, putting every detail in its place, in its proper form and shape. This means that through Torah and *mitzvos*, the *neshamah* becomes what it is meant to be.

I conclude with the wish for long and good days and years for you and your wife, may she live, and that you should have much *Yiddishe nachas* from all your children, may they live.

With blessing.

## 154

B"H, 21 Sivan, 5711, Brooklyn.

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, and scholarly R. Menachem Mendel, may he live:

Greetings and blessings!

I was pleased to receive regards from you through the esteemed, scholarly, G-d-fearing, and faithful communal worker, R. Shlomo Zalman Hecht, may he live, and also to receive your contribution for tzedakah to be distributed at my discretion.

I have distributed it as follows: three portions to Kollel Chabad in Yerushalayim, three portions to Yeshiva Toras Emes in Yerushalayim, and three portions to Yeshiva Olei Russiya in Lod. The remainder I have deposited into the fund of the central office for the work being done in North Africa—about which you have surely heard from Rabbi Hecht, may he live. I will briefly relay the matter to you:

Two weeks before the histalkus of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, he mentioned that it was necessary to begin kosher chinuch work in North Africa, where there is a large community of Jews—may they increase—who are observant and desire a religious education for their children, but due to their great poverty, a large portion of them lack the means to provide it.

In accordance with the wish of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, a special shaliach was sent to North Africa a short time after his histalkus to familiarize himself with the situation on the ground.

Today, nearly a year later, a number of yeshivos, yeshivos ketanos, Talmud Torahs, and chadarim for boys and girls have been opened there. Thank G-d, everything is proceeding with great success; the children are very happy, they are learning well, and they are succeeding in their studies. The only obstacle to expanding this chinuch work as required is a lack of financial resources. The pain is all the greater because the cost of living there is low, and a few dollars a month is enough to bring another child into kosher chinuch. With every dollar brought into the central office, the possibility is created to raise another Jewish child, to strengthen his connection to Torah and mitzvos, and to ensure that he remains a true Jew for his entire life.

I am interested to know whether you have a set time for Torah study, and which seforim you study. I am certain that you observe the takanah of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, to recite the daily Tehillim after davening, bli neder.

I sign with a blessing for long days and good years, that you may ascend in Torah and mitzvos—specifically in the mitzvah of tzedakah—and that we may hear good news from you.

With blessing.

B"H, 22 Sivan, 5711, Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, and distinguished, etc., Moreinu HaRav Yosef, may he live:

Peace and blessing!

I received your letter from Wednesday, Parshas Shelach, along with the *pidyon nefesh*. When I am at the *tziyun* of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, I will read the *pidyon nefesh*, and he will surely arouse Divine mercy so that Hashem may fulfill the requests of your heart for the good.

I will repeat here once again what I have written to you previously: that you must set fixed times for Torah study and also be careful to recite the daily *Tehillim*—as it is divided according to the days of the month. Regarding what you wrote to me once in a letter, that you are extremely busy, this is the very remedy for that: by showing Hashem that despite the constraints and the pressure, you nevertheless set fixed times for Torah study, then Hashem fulfills what is stated, "If you walk in My statutes," which Rashi explains to mean that you should **toil** in Torah with effort and labor. Then, "I will give your rains in their time." It is known what the inner meaning of this is: that *gishmikechem*—your physicality—means that even all your physical needs will be "in their time," without distractions, and you will be able to serve Hashem with peace of mind and peace of body.

With a blessing for a suitable arrangement in both spiritual and material matters.

## 151

B.H., 22 Sivan, 5711, Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

I received your telegram and your letter upon your safe arrival. I was pleased to hear that, thank G-d, the trip went well and that you found everything in good order. However, I was pained to discern from your letter a brokenness of heart that is neither appropriate nor timely.

It is unnecessary to elaborate that when it is said, "The sacrifices of G-d are a broken spirit," it does not refer to a broken spirit—and certainly not a brokenness of heart—which is harmful, G-d forbid, to one's health and affects the nerves. Furthermore, because of this brokenness of heart, one perceives matters as sharper and more difficult than they are in reality. My father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, related in the name of his father, the Rebbe Rashab, that he once said to him: "See how precious the Jewish body is, that for its sake so much Torah and mitzvos were poured out." Now that He gives everyone such a precious thing as a body, one must exert effort—effort for one's own sake—to ensure the body is healthy, so that one can naturally fulfill what Hashem desires of it. As the Rambam writes in Hilchos Deios, chapter 4, "Maintaining a healthy and sound body is among the ways of Hashem." In the letter of the Maggid of Mezritch to his holy son, the Malach (printed in *HaTamim*), he writes: "A small hole in the body makes a large hole in the neshamah." I do not intend this as a sermon, but rather my hope is that perhaps this will have an effect on you, and through you, on your husband, the Rav, may he live (even though the Zohar uses the expression "the strength of the neshamah is the weakness of the body," this should be interpreted as the weakening of the body's demands, but not, G-d forbid, the weakening of the body's health. We see this in practice: when the body is healthy, one can accomplish incomparably more in all matters, and especially in the love of Hashem, love of Torah, and love of fellow Jews).

I hope to hear good news from you regarding your health and the health of your husband, the esteemed Chossid, etc., may he live. May Hashem grant us all the merit to share only good news with one another, both in material and spiritual matters.

With blessings for true health and to see Yiddishe nachas, Chassidishe nachas, from all your children and family members, may they live.

**M. Schneerson**

## 152

B"H, 23 Sivan, 5711, Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and Blessings!

On the occasion of your Bar Mitzvah, which is being celebrated this Shabbos, Parshas Shelach, I would like to reiterate the blessings I gave you personally when you were here with me: that the day of your Bar Mitzvah should be the beginning of a full Jewish life in Torah and mitzvos. For on this day, you become a full, mature Jew, with all the privileges as well as all the obligations in the study of Torah and the fulfillment of mitzvos that are incumbent upon a Jew.

One of the first Bar Mitzvahs we know of is described in the Midrash (Bereishis Rabbah, Parshah 53). This was the Bar Mitzvah of Yitzchak Avinu. As the Midrash relates, Avraham Avinu made a great feast, to which he invited many people. Since Avraham Avinu was a ruler, he invited the other rulers of his time, among them Og, King of Bashan.

The Midrash continues that upon seeing the joy of the elderly Avraham Avinu—who was then one hundred and thirteen years old—and his only son, Yitzchak, the mighty Og, King of Bashan, said: "What can Avraham and Yitzchak, and everything they represent and fight for, possibly accomplish? They are so few and weak in number; I could crush them with a single finger."

The Ribono shel Olam responded to this: "A time will come when Og, King of Bashan, will see the tens of thousands of Jews who will descend from this child, and they will be victorious over him!"

From this, every one of us must learn for himself: if it ever crosses one's mind that Jews among the nations are a small and weak people—in a material sense—and especially that the things for which Jews are prepared to give their lives do not have many adherents, and that in every generation there are "Ogs"—that is, great heroes and giants in physicality and materialism who laugh at them and say, "What can you achieve? We can crush you and your ideas with a single finger"—

Our Avos, Avraham, Yitzchak, and Yaakov, taught us not to be intimidated by them.

"Avraham was one" (*Echad hayah Avraham*)—he was one in the world when he began to teach Elokus, and he was not ashamed, nor did he hide. He walked with his head held high, and wherever he went—*vayikra shem b'shem Hashem*—he taught everyone about the Ribono shel Olam and showed them how to walk in His ways.

Therefore, when his only son, the only son of Sarah, became a Bar Mitzvah, despite the fact that all around them were so many children of other nations, with other beliefs and other ways of life, Avraham Avinu nevertheless made a *mishteh gadol* (a great feast) and used the opportunity to spread Elokus.

And so that one should not think that mesiras nefesh ends, chalilah, without success, the Midrash relates that when one possesses the proper strength not to be intimidated by those who mock, and not to hide one's Torah and mitzvos, in the end, one is victorious—not only morally, but also materially. Just as Og, King of Bashan, fell in the war he waged against the Jews, the children of Avraham, Yitzchak, and Yaakov.

I hope that you, too, will proceed with the proper strength in the fulfillment of Torah and mitzvos. Then, Hashem Yisbarach will grant you success, and you will also have a positive influence on your surroundings, bringing them closer to Torah and mitzvos and illuminating your environment all around.

With the blessing that your parents, as well as your grandparents, shichyeh, should have much nachas from you—true Jewish nachas.

## 163

B"H, 23 Sivan, 5711, Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and Blessings!

I received your letter dated Thursday, 15 Sivan, and I reiterate the heartfelt wishes I expressed to you while you were here: that you may derive much *nachas* from your grandson, the *bar-mitzvah* boy, as well as from your other children and descendants, may they live.

It is unnecessary to emphasize to someone like yourself that true *nachas* is *nachas* that is connected with Torah and *mitzvos*.

In my opinion, you should utilize your influence over your sons, may they live, to strengthen them in Torah and *mitzvos* more than you currently do.

It goes without saying that in such matters, the rule is, according to our Sages (as cited in *Shelah*, *Shaar HaOsiyos*, end of letter *Kuf*; *Shaar HaPesukim* of the Arizal based on this), that "the words of the wise are heard when spoken gently." I will rely on your own understanding regarding the methods and manners in which to increase your influence over them.

However, this must be emphasized: there are many parents who do not properly appreciate the extent of their influence over their children and think that their efforts are in vain. Consequently, they lose much of the influence they could have exerted over their children. This is a mistake on their part, for parents can influence their children much more than they imagine. When they make the effort, they will certainly accomplish a great deal—perhaps not one hundred percent, but certainly to a great degree.

Enclosed is my letter to the *bar-mitzvah* boy, may he live. Since you did not write to me in which language to write to him, and since you mentioned that he wishes to read it aloud before all those gathered to bring benefit to the many, I am writing the letter in *zhargon* (Yiddish).

With blessings for a healthy summer for you and your entire family, may they live.

## 154

154

B”H, 24 Sivan, 5711, Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed members of the Executive Committee of Agudas Chassidei Chabad in the Holy Land, may they live:

Greetings and blessings!

I read your letter of 21 Iyar with pleasure. Due to several reasons, my response has been delayed until now, and I ask for your forgiveness.

I was happy to read that you feel the magnitude of the responsibility resting upon you, and that you have undertaken to expand the scope of your activities and to bring to fruition the goals of Agudas Chabad in the Holy Land. If time is generally precious—for "days are fashioned, and not one of them is [merely] a day"—its value is all the greater in our generations, the footsteps of Moshiach. As the saying of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, goes, he is standing right behind our wall. This is especially true in our Holy Land, upon which the eyes of Hashem your G-d are from the beginning of the year to the end of the year. As explained in Iggeres HaKodesh, Epistle 14, a new and renewed light descends and shines from the level of *Chochmah*, a light that has never shone before, from a higher level, and this is true in every detail, every single day.

(1) Regarding your proposal to add members to the administration of Agudas Chabad in the Holy Land: with the agreement of all, you propose to add as representatives from Jerusalem, Rabbi Azriel Zelig Slonim; from Kfar Chabad, R. Zalman Sudkevitz; and from the younger *Temimim*, R. Yitzchak Ginsburgh. It is appropriate to include these individuals, and I hereby approve your proposal. May it be His will that it be successful. After further consideration, I would suggest that it is worthwhile to add one more representative from the younger generation.

(2) Regarding the present, I wish to emphasize (as it appears, unfortunately, that there will be elections in the near future) the holy duty and privilege that every G-d-fearing person who trembles at the word of Hashem must participate in the elections, both personally and by influencing others, to vote for the most *chareidi* lists, so that not even one vote is lost.

I hereby grant permission and authorization to publicize my opinion with all possible force and strength: that every G-d-fearing person who reveres His name must do everything in their power to increase the number of voters for the most *chareidi* lists.

(3) In my opinion, Agudas Chabad should organize a special department for women. This means two things: first, to organize the wives of Chassidei Chabad and all those for whom the spirit of Chabad is dear to their hearts and souls; and second, for work among women **in general**, as this work naturally requires a specific character, a specific approach, and specific tasks.

(4) In my opinion, the time has come to organize a special department among the youth of *Anash* and those close to the spirit of Chabad. The intention is twofold: to strengthen their own resolve, and for work among wider circles of youth, as this work naturally requires a specific character, a specific approach, and specific tasks.

Regarding sections (3) and (4), I will not enter into details here, as much depends on the local situation, and I rely on your understanding. I am certain you will propose a detailed plan of action in this regard, in accordance with the demands of the place and time. I look forward to your proposal, and I thank you in advance.

Note: It goes without saying that regarding the elections, the campaign must also reach women and the youth. However, one should not wait for the organization of the aforementioned departments, as time is short, and surely the experience gained in the election campaign will assist in preparing the proposals for their organization.

With blessings for success in your holy work—and to draw inspiration from the name "Agudas" (Association), chosen by our Nasi, as explained in *Likutei Torah*, the *maamar* beginning "For the mountains shall depart" (end of page 29), and in the *maamar* "And you shall take for yourselves a bundle of hyssop" by the Tzemach Tzedek (found in print)—

May it be His will that we all together merit to fulfill the will of our holy fathers, the Rebbeim, the Nasi’im of Chabad—and that which is closer to us, the will of my father-in-law, the Rebbe—with expansion and without concealment or hiddenness.

And in our days, may we see the fulfillment of the prophecy, "The King Moshiach comes," for the wellsprings have already spread outward, and my father-in-law, the Rebbe, will lead us to the complete and true Redemption.

With personal regards to all the members of Agudas Chabad, and the Committee at their head,

**M. Schneerson**

## 165

B"H, 24 Sivan, 5711, Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Rabbi and Chossid, G-d-fearing and distinguished, etc., R' Shalom [Rivkin]
May he live.

Greetings and blessings!

I received your letter of 11 Sivan, and it is pleasant to see that you have at least partially organized your study schedule, and also that you have made arrangements regarding the mikveh, the magnitude of which is difficult to estimate. It is well known what is written in *She'eilos U'Teshuvos Min HaShamayim*, in *Likutei Torah*, in the *maamar* beginning with the words "Tachas Asher Lo Avadta" (see the collection in *Siman Meah She'arim*, p. 45), and in many other places...

It is a very correct approach that you are exerting effort with your outstanding bochurim to convince them to go into exile to a place of Torah. It is understood that if it is not possible to arrange for them to travel to New York, it is certainly worthwhile, in order to "break through the path," that they travel at least to the yeshiva in Chicago. Afterward, it will certainly unfold that some of them will also come to New York...

With blessings for the fulfillment of your holy mission with success and in a state of expansion, and for a suitable shidduch in a good and auspicious hour, speedily in our days,

**M. Schneerson**

## 156

B"H, 27 Sivan, 5711, Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

...I hope that when you are, G-d forbid, unable to go to shul, you are maintaining your shiurim in learning while at home. This in itself is an eitzah and a segulah that you should be able to return to shul as soon as possible to learn your shiurim b'rabim.

You are surely aware of the Chassidic custom introduced by the Baal Shem Tov, to serve Hashem Yisbarach with simchah. Through this, one can accomplish more than through avodah in the opposite manner, for simchah breaks through barriers. And when that simchah is in accordance with the ratzon of Hashem Yisbarach—in ahavas Hashem, ahavas HaTorah, and ahavas Yisrael—then the Aibishter gives from His full, open, holy, and expansive hand, so that there should be cause for satisfaction without excessive calculations.

I hope to hear good news from you that your health has improved and that you have resumed going to shul, as is your minhag hatov.

I will conclude with a blessing for long days and good years, which has a twofold meaning: literally, long and healthy years, and furthermore, that those years are truly good, filled with tov—and there is no tov other than Torah and mitzvos.

With blessings.

## 1,067

B"H, 27 Sivan, 5711, Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

I received your letter in due time, as well as the *pan* [Pidyon Nefesh] for your son, Mr. [Name] *sh’yihyeh*. It is difficult for me to read his *pan* as it is written, because he writes that if some suffering is decreed upon him, *chas v’shalom*, then he accepts it, etc. It goes without saying that this is **not at all** the proper phrasing, and it is incorrect. One begins with a request to arouse *rachamim rabim* (abundant mercies); these *rachamim rabim* nullify the suffering, etc. It is not worthwhile to enter into a *shakla v’tarya* (debate) or a reckoning regarding matters of exchange or acceptance through others, etc. Therefore, I will read the *pan* while omitting those lines. May it be the will of Hashem that you will soon be able to share good news regarding your son, Mr. [Name] *sh’yihyeh*, about an improvement in his situation. If matters beyond the natural order are required for this, then nothing is withheld from Hashem, and who can say to Him, "What are You doing?" Especially since, even within the natural order, he has already been in prison for some time, and as for the fact that a verdict was rendered, etc.—when the judgment is not a true judgment, the verdict is of no consequence. The main thing, as mentioned above, is that since we are arousing *rachamim rabim*, we are not in need of [human] reckonings, etc.

Regarding what you wrote about moving to Brazil and asking how it is possible to obtain papers from there: as far as I know, they are very interested there in expert *shochtim*, especially in the capital city, Rio de Janeiro. Surely, our refugee office in Paris has the address of Rabbi Singerovitch there (he is a wealthy merchant, but he also fulfills a rabbinic role out of respect), and it would be worthwhile to speak with him.

Awaiting good news.

## 168

B"H, 27 Sivan, 5711, Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter from the 2nd of Tammuz, informing me that the Canadian consul is prepared to grant you visas for that country: I have already written to several members of anash that, according to the information being received from Canada—and you surely have this information as well—arranging one's livelihood there, as well as here in the United States, is not so simple. This is in contrast to the countries of South America or Australia. Therefore, it is somewhat surprising that there is no interest in relocating there, even though obtaining a visa for those places is not so easy. In any event, wherever you may relocate, may the Ribono shel Olam grant that your journey proceeds properly and that you settle there in a manner that is suitable for you, both materially and spiritually.

Regarding your question concerning the proposal being made for your daughter, Mrs. [Name]—may she live—and your question since the name of the person in question is Avraham, while his name is [Name], but he only uses the name Avraham when called to the Torah and for signing documents: Since the other matters are suitable, there is no need for there to be an impediment on this account. (See Responsa Tzemach Tzedek, Even HaEzer, Siman 143, that in such a case, this is not considered a situation where their names are identical at all, and there is no room for concern. See also Piskei Dinim of the Tzemach Tzedek to Yoreh Deah, Vol. 1, Siman 116).

With blessings and regards to your family—may they live.

## 159

159

B"H, 27 Sivan, 5711
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

I received your letter with pleasure—though it was undated—regarding your engagement to the young woman, may she live.

I hereby wish to express my blessing that your engagement should be in a good and auspicious hour, for good fortune and a good sign. When you set the date for the wedding, may it be for good fortune, and may you build a home in Israel upon the foundations of Torah and mitzvos, as explained in the teachings of Chassidus. For especially in this time of double and redoubled darkness, when people make darkness into light and light into darkness, it is essential that every single person occupy themselves with the teachings of Chassidus. Through the "light that is in the Torah," he will find illumination in the revealed aspects of Torah as well, and through this, in all other details of both physicality and spirituality.

When you see [the young man], may he live, please convey my regards to him, and also convey to him what my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, used to say. It is based on the well-known principle that from every single matter one must learn a moral lesson in the service of Hashem, may He be blessed. The lesson from Pesach Sheni is that "it is never too late" (*es iz keynmol nit farfallen*). Even if at the time when all of Israel offered the Pesach sacrifice, a person was impure or on a distant journey—or even if it was "for you," meaning it was by his own choice—it is still not lost. A special appointed time is made for him, so that after he purifies himself, he may draw near to the Beis Hamikdash and enter within the threshold, etc.

## 1070

B"H, 27 Sivan, 5711
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, and distinguished individual, occupied with communal needs, etc., R' Boruch, may he live:

Peace and blessing!

I was pleased to read in your letter that you have taken a deep interest in, and have also familiarized yourself with, the situation of our brethren, the Children of Israel, in the Holy Land, may it be rebuilt and established. This is, after all, one of the consequences of Ahavas Yisrael: "that another’s situation should truly concern you."

It would be a pity if the information and impressions you gained were to be lost. You have likely written them down, or at least the main points. If so, I would be grateful if you could send them to me (with the intention that they be returned).

In any event, I would ask you to answer me, if possible, regarding the following questions (which I have listed in the order of the points you raised in your letter):

a) The impression from your visit to Kfar Chabad.

b) The spirit in which the students of the various educational institutions are learning.

c) Data regarding the number of children who are under the influence of the various political parties.

d) Information regarding the spiritual life in the ma'abarot in general, and regarding the education there in particular.

e) You have surely reflected upon the Sedra that we just read yesterday morning: (Bamidbar 14:8-9) "If Hashem desires us, He will bring us... and give it to us" (and **He** will give it to us, that is when it is) "a land flowing with milk and honey" (but an eternal condition accompanies this:) "Only do not rebel against Hashem." (And when they cried out—ibid., verses 40-42—"Here we are, and we will go up... and Moshe said... Do not go up" [and do you know why?] "for Hashem is not in your midst.")

And this is the main point I am seeking to discover regarding the situation there: do you have information about this? Not the situation in the land of Canaan, not even the situation in Eretz Yisrael, but the situation in the Holy Land—which will be built and established speedily in our days, literally, through Moshiach Tzidkeinu—if Jews, wherever they may be, whether in the exile here or in the exile there, will fulfill what Moshiach said, that he is coming **today** (if only) "if you will listen to My voice" (Sanhedrin 98a).

With greetings to your family members, may they live, and with blessing.

## 171

B"H, 27 Sivan, 5711
Brooklyn.

I am interested to know if, aside from what you write regarding Epsom salts and magnesia, you are also aware of any recommendations regarding radiation or surgery. For although Hashem is the Healer of all flesh and performs wonders, nevertheless, it is customary to have some foothold in nature as well, even if it is the slightest bit. As I once heard from my father-in-law, the Rebbe: A very ill person, may we be spared, once came to the Alter Rebbe, and he healed him with a piece of matzah shemurah and half a glass of water. This shows that, at the very least, there must be some foothold in nature. May Hashem hear your prayer and request, and may you be able to share good news.

You surely received my previous letter in due time. I am interested to know how your daughter, may she live and be well, has settled with her husband, the Rabbi, may he live, and whether he remains in the "tent of Torah," etc.

With blessings for good tidings.

## 172

B"H, 29 Sivan, 5711
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the distinguished Rabbi and Chassid, G-d-fearing and learned, etc.,
Rabbi Yechezkel Shraga, may he live,

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of Wednesday, Parshas Beha'aloscha, regarding your efforts in the matter of *hachnasas kallah* for Rabbi... may he live,

Enclosed is my contribution toward the expenses associated with this *hachnasas kallah*.

May it be the will of Hashem that the union take place in a good and auspicious hour, and may they build a home in Israel upon the foundations of Torah and *mitzvos*.

Please convey my blessings to the *mechutanim*, may they live.

With blessings of *mazal tov*.

A note regarding the matter of *hachnasas kallah*:

I was asked about what is written in the text of *Birchos HaShachar*: "These are the things... and *hachnasas kallah*... and *Talmud Torah* is equivalent to them all." The difficulty is that one must interrupt *Talmud Torah* for *hachnasas kallah* (and one may note the *Sdei Chemed*, *Asifas Dinim*, *Chosson V'Kallah* 22 — and I found this question in *Responsa Maharam Schick*, *Orach Chaim* 62).

However, this matter is explained beautifully according to what the Alter Rebbe writes in *Hilchos Talmud Torah*, Chapter 4, Section 3: "And if it is impossible... he should interrupt his study and perform the *mitzvah*... for he is obligated to interrupt his study in order to fulfill them... and if he does not do so, it turns out that he studied not to perform... end quote." This means that if he does not interrupt for the aforementioned *mitzvos*, he is diminishing his **Talmud Torah**, and he must interrupt so that his **Talmud Torah** may be elevated. Based on this, the fact that *Talmud Torah* is equivalent to them all is not related to this issue.

#### ***172***

**Rabbi Yechezkel Shraga:** Apparently Lipshitz-Halberstam; see letter 170 below.

## 175

B"H,

In his letter regarding the first celebration of 12-13 Tammuz—in the year 5688—my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, explained the significance of this redemption, stating that "The Holy One, Blessed be He, did not redeem me alone on 12 Tammuz, but also all those who love our holy Torah, those who observe the mitzvos, and even those who are merely called by the name of Yisrael."

This includes all types of Jewish men and women: those who possess both Torah and mitzvos, those who possess either Torah or mitzvos, and those who possess neither Torah nor mitzvos, but who are nevertheless **called** by the name of Yisrael.

As is known, a "kinui" (a moniker or nickname) is something that conceals and covers the essence of the person being called by this name. It may not be their actual name, nor an abbreviation of their name, nor an explanation of their name; it might not even be in the language of their name, and it might not be a name they chose for themselves, but rather a name they are called by solely because of their family.

Yet, despite all this, they are still called by the name **Yisrael**. For, in the language of the aforementioned letter, "Every Jewish person (regardless of their individual status regarding the observance and fulfillment of mitzvos) has a heart that is perfect with Hashem and His Torah."

**To all** of these types, a redemption was drawn down on that day in that year (5687), and this influence is reawakened every year at this time.

Redemption means an exodus from the straits, the measurement, and the limitation of material and physical matters, and of the body and the animal soul.

However, we must prepare ourselves to be a vessel to receive this influence, to absorb it internally, and consequently—to bring it into practice, in thought, speech, and action, in the days that follow this festival of redemption.

And then, the redemption will be ours, for all of the Jewish people—the complete and true redemption, speedily in our days, Amen.

**Menachem Schneerson**

Motzaei Shabbos, 3 Tammuz, 5711, Brooklyn, N.Y.
