## 178

B"H, 4 Tammuz, 5711
Brooklyn

To the esteemed *avreich*, G-d-fearing, etc., R' Meir, may he live:

Greetings and blessings!

I received your letter of 1 Rosh Chodesh Tammuz in good time, and I am pleased to hear that the *shiur* in the *shul* has been renewed. Thank you for the regards you conveyed to the *baalei batim* in the *shul* regarding the *seder* of *Shabbos Mevarchim*. I hope that you will also be able to succeed in introducing the other *sedarim* of *Shabbos Mevarchim* among them, such as reciting *Tehillim*, and so on.

Surely you will also convey to them what was discussed on *Shabbos Kodesh Parshas Shelach* regarding the sin of the *meraglim*. They were, after all, righteous—*kesheirim*—as Rashi explains, and yet they did not want to enter *Eretz Yisrael*. In *Chassidus*, it is discussed that the error of the *meraglim* was that, while in the *midbar*, they were occupied solely with *Torah* and spirituality. For food, they had the *man*; for drink, they had the *be'erah shel Miriam*; and their garments grew with them, as Rashi explains on the verse, "Your garment did not wear out upon you." Consequently, they did not want to deal with the affairs of *olam hazeh*. Entering *Eretz Yisrael* would have required them to enter a different *seder*: to work the land, engage in commerce, and the like. Even though this itself must be done *al pi Torah*—to guard against theft, *lashon hara*, *hasagas gevul*, etc., and to fulfill the *mitzvos* of *maaser*, *sheviis*, and *terumah*—it would have left little time for learning and *davening*. The *meraglim* argued: why should they exchange the refined work they had in the *midbar* for the work of *Eretz Yisrael*, where one must occupy oneself with the fruits of the land (not the *man*) and with the "people who dwell therein" (not as in the *midbar*, where "the people shall dwell alone")? Consequently, they felt it would be a "land that consumes its inhabitants," consuming the spirituality and *kedushah* of the Jewish people.

Yet, they were mistaken in this. As the *Torah* says, "The land is very, very good." Even though the *avodah* involves simple and mundane matters, this is what the *Ribono shel Olam* desires: that even in these simple things, it should be evident that a Jew is acting as he ought. This is more precious to *Hakadosh Baruch Hu* than the study of *Torah* in the *midbar*.

This should serve as a *mussar haskel* for all of us. When finding ourselves in such a difficult *galus*, where, due to various circumstances, one cannot learn eight hours a day, and one only participates in *shiurim* in public at the *shul*, and these *shiurim* are not even in the deep concepts of *Torah* but are merely the study of the laws of the *Kitzur Shulchan Aruch*, *Aggados Chazal*, or *sipurei tzaddikim*—nevertheless, one should not feel discouraged. Always remember that "the land is very, very good." If one is not *nispael* by all these difficulties and conducts oneself as a Jew ought to conduct himself, one can also fulfill the *ratzon elyon* through this, just as one did by learning *Torah* in the *midbar*. And when one does this with *simcha*, it is even more precious.

I would like to ask you to convey my regards to all those who participate in the *shiurim*. May *Hashem Yisbarach* help that the study of the *shiurim* should be successful, and that they should take with them *Yiddishe* warmth and bring it into their homes.

With blessings,

## 179

B"H, 4 Tammuz, 5711
Brooklyn

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, and learned, etc., R' Aryeh Dov, may he live, Shochet and Bodek.

Peace and blessing!

I received your two *pidyonos nefesh*. When I am at the *tziyun* of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, I will read them. He will surely arouse Divine mercy for the fulfillment of your heart’s desires for the good, and you will surely bring me good news regarding all those you wrote about in the *pidyon nefesh*.

Regarding your trip to Ireland: In general, it is appropriate that you find a way for this trip to also include *parnassah ruchnis* (spiritual livelihood). It is understood how significant the matter of *parnassah gashmis* (material livelihood) is, as explained in the *nigleh* of Torah, and especially as explained in the teachings of Chassidus. Nevertheless, there is something precarious about it: a *minyan* of Chassidim and *Temimim* travel once, twice, or three times, they slaughter hundreds of animals, they get paid in pounds or francs, and they return home. In the eyes of flesh, at least, one does not see in this a fulfillment of a *shlichus* (mission) in the simple sense, nor, in general, a sense of refinement.

It is told that in the time of the Mitteler Rebbe, there was an instruction to all the Chassidim who came to Lubavitch that when traveling back—or more accurately, when returning—they should review Chassidus in all the places they passed through, even in very small towns along their route home. Even though the purpose of their traveling or walking to Lubavitch was to be in Lubavitch and return home, and all the places they passed through were not, for them, a *makom hamafsik* (a place of interruption), but rather a *davar hamachaber* (a connecting element).

I am confident that after the "strong look" (*histaklus*), as explained in the writings of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, regarding the nature of *histaklus*, etc.—that despite the fact that the purpose of the trip to Ireland is to earn a livelihood for yourselves and your families, may they live, and to return to your place of residence—surely, even in the places and matters in between, there is something to be accomplished. It should be evident that this was the work of Chassidim, *Temimim*, and those connected to my father-in-law, the Rebbe.

May it be the will of Hashem that you find appropriate work and an appropriate manner so that even on this trip, you will add, at the very least, a little light into the darkness of the world.

With a blessing for a proper journey and successful work, and regards to all his colleagues, may they live.

## A'P

Consequently, you must be strong in *bitachon* that through being connected to Chassidim and the ways of Chassidus, one is thereby also connected to the *ilana d'chaya*—the source of life. Therefore, one need not be anxious; rather, be strong in the *bitachon* that Hashem Yisbarach will lead you and send you everything you need. When one is strong in this *bitachon*, one brings about the reality of seeing this with physical eyes in daily life.

I hope that you will be able to bring me good news regarding an improvement in your health, and I conclude with the blessing of a *refuah kerovah*.

## 182

B”H, 5 Tammuz, 5711

To the students arriving from South America,
May Hashem grant them life,

Shalom u’Bracha!

In response to your letter, I was pleased to hear of your correspondence with various communities in South America, and that some good results are already visible from your work. Surely you will continue to maintain contact with those you have already begun to reach, and you will strive to expand your activities to the extent possible for you, while still maintaining your study schedules.

And certainly, you should endeavor to utilize every opportunity so that those you influence in the various cities will themselves become "moist enough to moisten others," by exerting their own influence upon their surroundings.

The aspiration to translate various publications from the *Melach* [Merkaz Le’inyonei Chinuch] into the languages spoken in South America is good and correct. It is worthwhile for you to put effort into this, initially using a mimeograph (stencil) once you find a skilled typist, and to copy only individual *maamarim* and the like.

Regarding the specifics, you should discuss this with the *Merkaz Le’inyonei Chinuch*, who are well-versed in these matters.

It is also worthwhile to consult with Dr. Greenberg as to whether it is possible to print some of these *maamarim* in a general periodical there, or one affiliated with the school.

You should also clarify if there are study *shiurim* in the *beis knesses* and the like, especially on *Shabbos*, and if it is possible to arrange such *shiurim* if books are sent from here (naturally, only a few copies, not for every single listener), such as *Chumash*, *Kitzur Shulchan Aruch*, *Ein Yaakov*, etc.

Keep me informed of the development of your activities. May the pleasantness of Hashem be upon you and your handiwork, and may you be blessed with everything you need, both materially and spiritually.

With blessings for success in your studies and in your work to illuminate the darkness of the world with the light of Torah and *mitzvos* in *yiras shamayim*.

From a copy. For its content, see letter 957 above.

## 183

B"H, 5 Tammuz, 5711
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of the 25th of Sivan and the *pidyon nefesh* enclosed therein:

I will read the *pidyon nefesh* when I am at the *tziyun* of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, and he will surely arouse Divine mercy for each person for whatever they require.

Regarding your question concerning *tikkun*: You should increase the recitation of the letters of Torah and the letters of *tefillah*, which is, of course, in addition to the three daily *shiurim* in *Chumash*, *Tehillim*, and *Tanya* that are incumbent upon everyone.

By "increasing the letters of Torah and *tefillah*," I mean that you should also articulate them with your mouth. Furthermore, you should endeavor to take a part in the education and the drawing of the youth toward *yiras shamayim*. And thirdly—you should divert your mind from this matter for the time being; that is, not only from the matter itself, but also from contemplating the magnitude of the sin and the necessity of the *tikkun*. You should divert your mind from all of this entirely, and focus your mind with strength on study and *tefillah*. It is understood that all of the above must be done with joy (even though it is explained in the *sefarim* in a different manner, this is the path you should follow for the next few years; for now, divert your mind from the entire matter and strengthen yourself to serve Hashem specifically through joy).

I trust you are careful that your body remains healthy, and that you do not eat or drink for an hour and a half or two hours before sleep, *bli neder*. It is understood that this refers to a substantial meal, but it does not apply to very light eating or drinking.

You will certainly continue your studies for a few more years.

With blessings for success in your studies and in *yiras shamayim*.

**M. Schneerson**

This network of chinuch institutions includes everything from the teaching of the alef-beis to a beis medrash for teachers and Rabbonim. Even though we are not in a position—for the time being—to send large sums from here, I can surely find a source for the small expenses required for the initial period, provided that this is a matter of substance. Not only in reality, but also in accordance with the inner intent. I am sure you will inform me of the details regarding this.

It is understood that if it is impossible to establish an institution along the lines mentioned above, then the proposal to participate in the work of a Charedi chinuch institution, even if it is connected to a party, is a correct proposal.

I hope that you will fulfill what you write in your letter, that you are exerting the appropriate energy regarding a shidduch. May Hashem arrange your match for you soon, in a manner that is suitable for you, both materially and spiritually.

With blessings for a suitable arrangement for your personal affairs, in both body and soul.

B"H, 6 Tammuz, 5711
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, and distinguished, etc., R' Y. [shiyichyeh],

Greetings and blessings!

Enclosed is the Kuntres for the upcoming Chag HaGeulah, 12-13 Tammuz. I am certain that you will merit to share its light—the light within it and the Luminary within it—with the many.

Just as the soul of the Baal HaSimcha was redeemed in peace—because "there were many with him," for the sake of the many, and because he did good for the many—so too may we merit to receive and internalize this redemption through a "double good": good for Heaven and good for mankind.

For through the dissemination of Torah in general, and the dissemination of the teachings of Chassidus in particular—through which darkness is transformed into light—just as he [King David] redeemed his soul in peace because "there were many with him," even the men of Avshalom, so too will each and every person redeem his soul in peace. This is because "there were many with him"—the angels that guard a person, the Yetzer Tov and the Yetzer Hara—will be with him. Through the aforementioned [dissemination of Torah and Chassidus], one strengthens the Yetzer Tov over the Yetzer Hara and sweetens the Gevuros, and then even the Yetzer Hara turns back and becomes a "guardian of the fruit."

And then—even though "there were many with him," in the multitude of his distress, "He redeemed my soul in peace," for His word was with me in my support.

With blessings for Chag HaGeulah—awaiting good tidings from your farbrengens during these days of redemption, for the strengthening of brotherly love, the dissemination of Torah, and the bolstering of Yiddishkeit,

**M. Schneerson**

## 489

B"H, 6 Tammuz, 5711
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, learned, and distinguished individual, a man of many talents, engaged in communal affairs, etc., etc.,
Rabbi Y. [Fleyer], may he live.

Greetings and blessings!

I gratefully acknowledge receipt of your letter dated 1 Tammuz, along with the enclosed checks. As the saying goes, "The wine belongs to the master, but the credit goes to the one who serves it" — thank you for your dedicated efforts on behalf of the Kolel in Eretz Yisrael, may it be rebuilt and established. I am certain that you will continue to gather strength to increase and expand these efforts in accordance with the demands of the hour. Especially since, as you noted in your letter, less than half of the expected amount has been collected this time, you are certainly justified in appealing to all those who participated with smaller sums this year, or who did not participate at all. On the contrary, in matters of life, one must always be "increasing and growing," and never, G-d forbid, "decreasing." Growth and expansion are signs of vitality, whereas contraction and Tzimtzum are the opposite. "Whoever adds, they add to him," and regarding Tzedakah, our Sages have said that "the one who causes [others to give] is greater than the one who gives," which is an even higher level than the aforementioned "the wine belongs to the master, but the credit goes to the one who serves it."

Incidentally, there is a well-known question: if we say that "the credit goes to the one who serves it," then why is Avodah Zarah forbidden, given that through the sun and moon, influence is also drawn down below, as it is written, "with the best fruits of the sun and the best yield of the moons"? The answer is simple: the sun, the moon, and all the hosts of heaven do not possess free choice; they are merely like an axe in the hand of the woodcutter, and there is no place to offer thanks to an axe. This is not the case if the one who "serves" possesses free choice; when he becomes a vessel for our good Creator to bring goodness into actual reality, he is indeed deserving of thanks. It follows from this that since angels do not possess free choice — as brought in Tanya, Chapter 39, at the beginning — and among created beings below, free choice is found only in the Jewish people, the concept of "the credit goes to the one who serves it" applies in its true sense only to the Jewish people.

— It is understood that absolute free choice exists only in the Creator Himself, for there is nothing that compels Him, G-d forbid, and therefore His choice is truly free. This is not the case with any created being, for it is impossible for them to be entirely free, since ultimately their nature, intellect, or desires and cravings compel them to perform one action rather than its opposite. Even if the compulsion comes from within, it is still not free choice. And since free choice pertains only to the Essence and Being of the Ein Sof, blessed be He, who is the ultimate perfection, it has no place below except in man, who is created "in our image, after our likeness," for you alone are called "man." —

Thank you for the few lines you wrote regarding the Keren Hatzalah. As you are aware, this year they gave nothing to the institutions of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, whereas in previous years, their entire support went to those institutions. This year they did not give a single penny, even though they did provide aid to Europe, in the country of Romania... It is my hope and trust that you will endeavor to rectify this as soon as possible, so that these institutions will not suffer any lack. These are the institutions of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, and he surely watches over them with an "open eye" even now, takes an interest in their welfare, and arouses great mercy from Above so that all their affairs may be successful.

May it be His will that we may share only good news with one another.

With blessings.

190

B"H, 8 Tammuz, 5711
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the administrators, Roshei Yeshivos, and teachers
in the Yeshivos "Achei Temimim" in the city of...
May Hashem keep them alive.

Peace and blessing!

In response to your letter, request, and inquiry:

In accordance with the changes in the schedule in several of the Yeshivos during the summer months, I wish to draw your attention to the following matters:

(a) Even during the days when the students are in the Yeshivah and diligent in their studies, the obligation rests upon their educators not to divert their attention from their students even during the hours they are outside the walls of the Yeshivah, and to strive with all their might that their conduct and ways of life should at all times and at every hour be as they ought to be.

This is all the more true during the summer vacation days, when extra interest in the students is required—to know about each and every one of them, where they are, and what they are occupied with—and to assist them with all kinds of support to walk in the correct and straight path. As our Sages of blessed memory said, even when one is not visible to the students, one must supervise and ensure that one’s mind is upon them (Bava Basra 8b, and in Chiddushei Aggados there).

(b) There is no end to growth. Therefore, even the most expert teachers should utilize the vacation days to add to their knowledge in matters pertaining to their work, which is the "work of Hashem" (Bava Basra 21b).

(c) It is worthwhile to arouse the baalei batim and the activists in the Yeshivos to strive, while they are in pleasant pastures for rest, to utilize every opportunity when they meet new faces to draw them closer to assisting the Yeshivos, and to explain to them that "it is a tree of life to those who grasp it, and its supporters are happy (me'ushar)." And do not read it as *me'ushar* (happy), but rather *me'rosho* (from its head), for they draw down from the "head" of all the draw-downs and influences (Zohar Vol. III, 53b; Maamar *Eitz Chaim* 5799).

(d) One should not be satisfied with the number of students in the Yeshivos as long as there are children who are suitable for Yeshivah but do not attend due to the weakness of their parents' recognition of the necessity of the matter. Therefore, it is an obligation to organize in every place a systematic campaign, conducted with the necessary energy and enthusiasm, to increase the number of students in the Yeshivos. There are not enough words to describe the greatness of the merit of saving even one soul in Israel, physically, and all the more so, spiritually (Bava Metzia 30a).

I am interested to know about the good activities being done in accordance with the above, and also whether you have organized a summer camp. I hope to receive good news in this regard.

And approaching the days of redemption, 12-13 Tammuz, the redemption of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, and the redemption of all "those who engage in spreading Torah"—in the words of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, "May it be His will that his blessing be fulfilled in its entirety—that Hashem will open His good treasury and bestow upon all lovers of Torah, its students, and those who teach classes in public, within the entirety of our brethren the Children of Israel, may they live, an abundance of life and abundant blessing without limit."

With a blessing for success in your holy work and an abundance of good, physically and spiritually,

**M. Schneerson**

## 1092

B"H, 8 Tammuz, 5711
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

I received your letter in due time—a response to my letter—and seeing your interest, I am enclosing the *kuntres* for 12-13 Tammuz that has just been published, along with the general letter pertaining to it.

Regarding what you wrote in your letter, that you are one of the "chicks that have wandered from their nest," etc.—it is worth noting (perhaps with a touch of humor?) the principle in Torah that "living creatures are not pushed aside" (*Yoma 64a*; see *Lekach Tov* by the Mahar"i Engel, *Klal 6*), and that there is no "pushing aside" (*dichuy*) regarding *mitzvos* (*Chullin 87a*; see the *Acharonim* in *Shulchan Aruch Orach Chayim 546* and *Yoreh Deah 328*). This is especially true in spiritual matters, where "there is nothing that can stand before the will."

As for your observation that the obligation to become *tamei* for a *meis mitzvah* proves that the *mitzvah* of burial is *min haTorah* (from the Torah), see the Ramban in *Sefer HaMitzvos*, *Shoresh 1*. However, Rashi in *Berachos 19b* explains it as being due to *kevod habriyos* (human dignity), and in that *sugya* there, he compares it to one who removes a garment in the marketplace, where there is no *mitzvah* involved, only *kevod habriyos* **alone**. In any event, there are **Rishonim** who hold that there is no *mitzvah* of burial *min haTorah*. These include the Rav Saadia Gaon in his *Sefer HaMitzvos*, *Parshiyos 134* (that it only applies to those hanged by order of *Beis Din*), the Radbaz, Vol. 1, *Siman 311* (that for ordinary deceased there is only the negative commandment of "do not leave overnight," but no positive commandment of burial), and according to the *Baal Halachos Gedolos*, it is merely part of the general positive commandment of "walking in His ways" (Ramban, ibid.). The *Yereim*, *Siman 253*, holds similarly. The Rambam, in *Hilchos Avel*, end of Chapter 12, states that it is a positive commandment *midivrei sofrim* (rabbinic) and included in "love your neighbor as yourself" (though it has already been noted that this contradicts what he writes there at the end of Chapter 14 and in *Sefer HaMitzvos*, *Mitzvah 231*). See also *Shulchan Aruch* of our Rebbe, *Siman 395*, *Kuntres Acharon*, *Seif Katan 3*, and beginning of *Siman 527*, where he holds that it is a positive commandment *min haTorah*. See also *Shu"t Shaagas Aryeh HaChadashos*, *Siman 6* and *12*, and the *Pe'er LaSefer HaMitzvos* to the *Sefer HaMitzvos* of Rav Saadia Gaon, *Mitzvah 19*, which discusses this at length; *Sdei Chemed*, *Klalei Ma'areches Kuf*, *39*. I will not elaborate further.

With blessings to engage in Torah study with tranquility and expansion, in both body and soul.

#### ***194***

**Study of Toras HaChassidus:** See also the letter that follows.

## 105

11 Tammuz, 5711

I was pleased to learn from the letter of his father, the learned Chossid, etc., that he is studying Torah and has a desire to learn and flourish in Torah. He will surely hold fast to this stronghold—which is also the stronghold of Hashem—as our Sages of blessed memory state in Sanhedrin (99b) regarding the verse, "Let him take hold of My strength, that he may make peace with Me," which the text says refers to one who occupies himself with Torah for its own sake. As is explained at length in Tanya and in Chassidic teachings in general, Torah is the wisdom and will of Hashem. Since He and His wisdom are one, then through Torah and the study of Torah, the concept that "Yisrael, the Torah, and the Kudsha Brich Hu are all one" is realized.

However, the difficulty is that through the sin of the Tree of Knowledge, death was introduced into the world. As the Bachya states, from the moment an infant is born, he begins to wither—meaning that at the very moment the infant’s life begins, his death also begins. This is also the meaning of the verse, "On the day that you eat of it, you shall surely die."

So far, this applies to the physical realm.

Since "the Kudsha Brich Hu looked into the Torah and created the world," every matter found in the world must have a source in the Torah. (This explains the question of our Sages in Chullin 139b, "Where is Haman alluded to in the Torah?"—meaning it is understood simply that it is impossible for something to exist in the world if it does not have a source in the Torah.)

Similarly, the sin of the Tree of Knowledge (and subsequently the sin of the Golden Calf—for as is known, when the Jewish people stood at Mount Sinai, their impurity ceased and they were free from this, but after the sin of the Golden Calf, it returned) brought about the phenomenon of forgetfulness in Torah, as explained in Maseches Eruvin (54a): "Were it not for the sin of the Golden Calf, Torah would not have been forgotten by the Jewish people."

In the spiritual sense, this forgetfulness is the equivalent of death.

Just as in the physical realm, the process of death reaches its completion only after seventy years, or eighty years if one has the strength, and one’s days are one hundred and twenty years—yet why does the process of death reach its completion then? Because it begins immediately at the moment the infant is born, as the aforementioned Bachya states.

So, too, with the study of Torah: the reason it is possible for there to be total forgetfulness later on is that at the beginning of the study, the learning was not as it should have been. This is along the lines of what our Sages say in Eruvin (54a): "If it is arranged in all 248 limbs, it is preserved." See the beginning of Chapter 32 of Tanya, where this refers to the manner of Torah study. Within the Torah itself, there are two parts: what the Zohar calls the "body of the Torah" (and in the language of our Sages in the Mishnah, "these are the bodies of Torah") and the "soul of the Torah," which is the hidden dimension of Torah.

It is understood that one who deals only with the human body also has a connection to the person. Nevertheless, in order for that connection to be full of vitality, for him to have a desire for it, and for it to bear good fruit, he must know the structure of the body, all its details, and its functions. It is essential that he contemplate the reality and essence of the human soul, its matters and details; only then can he properly direct everything concerning the human body.

And as with all these things, so it is in the analogy:

In days of old, the majority of the Jewish people were healthy in Torah and mitzvos. Since the Torah speaks of the majority, and according to the principle established by the Rambam, just as with a healthy body, all of the Jewish people were necessarily occupied with the "body" of Torah—that is, the study of the revealed, literal Torah. Only those who were occupied with the internal limbs of the complete stature of the Jewish people, and specifically with the heart and the brain, also occupied themselves with the inner dimension of the Torah.

But as much time passed, and because of our sins, we were exiled from our land. In the world itself, the darkness increased more and more, to the point where hearts were diminished and minds were confused. As the prophet says, "From the sole of the foot to the head, there is no soundness in it." It is impossible to suffice with the "body" of Torah alone; one must also find medicinal remedies. As the darkness grows, so does the danger—the danger of the sick—and the necessity for medicinal remedies continues to grow.

The essential thing in these remedies is to strengthen and awaken the vitality within the soul—the inner dimension of the Jewish soul. Only then will they be able to stand firm without looking at the trials, the concealments, and the hiddenness. And since the Torah speaks of the majority, as mentioned above, the necessity for all of us to study the inner dimension of the Torah—the teachings of Chassidus—is great, for it is that which brings healing to the world, as explained in the Kuntres Eitz Chaim by the Rebbe (Rashab), of blessed memory.

The conclusion from all the above is as our Sages say in Shabbos (31a) regarding the verse, "And there shall be faith in your times, etc., the fear of Hashem is His treasure." Even one who has studied all six orders of the Torah, if "the fear of Hashem is his treasure," then yes; if not, then no. It concludes there that it is better not to learn if there is no fear of Hashem. This was said regarding that time and place where it was possible to attain Torah without excessive toil, and even without effort, etc. How much more so in these days, when we see tangibly that when people occupy themselves with the teachings of Chassidus, the inner dimension of the Torah, the vast majority remain G-d-fearing. This is in contrast to those among the youth who say, "I have only Torah"—in most of them, the statement of our Sages in Yevamos (109b) is fulfilled, G-d forbid: "Whoever says, 'I have only Torah,' does not even have Torah."

All the above applies to all the Jewish people.

And how much more so for those who have merited that their fathers are Chassidim—meaning they are in an environment where they know, thank G-d, about the teachings of Chassidus and the conduct of the ways of the Chassidim. This is a sign from Above that Hashem has placed him on the path of the good without his own toil in this, for it comes to him by birth, and He says to him, "Choose this for yourself, and go and occupy yourself with the teachings of Chassidus." It is understood of itself that his success in this will be of an entirely different nature. Furthermore, this also gives vitality to the study of the revealed Torah, so that his study of the revealed Torah will be without concealments, hiddenness, confusion, or difficulties. Most importantly, the study will be with inner vitality, and by default, the concept that "Yisrael, the Torah, and the Kudsha Brich Hu are all one" will be fulfilled in him.

I am interested to know what his study of the teachings of Chassidus is, for he is surely continuing in this and adding to it. As our Sages of blessed memory ruled, which according to many opinions is a matter of Torah law, "We elevate in matters of holiness and do not lower."

Awaiting good news—and there is no good other than Torah and the light of Torah—I sign with a blessing for success in study and in fear of Heaven.

**Menachem Schneerson**

## 199

B"H, Yom HaGeulah, 13 Tammuz, 5711
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, and distinguished, etc.,
Moreinu HaRav Eliyahu Shmuel, may he live, HaKohen, Shochet u'Bodek

Greetings and blessings!

I was saddened to hear of the passing of your wife.

May the Omnipresent comfort you among the other mourners of Zion and Jerusalem.

It is known that one of the reasons why a *taanis chalom* (fast for a dream) is effective on Shabbos is that since it is a time of *taanug* (delight), it is impossible to endure sorrow in the world, and consequently, all *dinim* (judgments) are nullified thereby, etc.

And inasmuch as today is a day of joy—the day of the rejoicing and redemption and the deliverance of the soul of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe—who, as he writes in his letter, "The Holy One, blessed be He, did not redeem me alone on 12 Tammuz, but also all those who love our holy Torah, those who observe the *mitzvos*, and also those who are called by the name of Israel"—surely on this day of joy, all matters of *dinim* and *mochin d'katnus* (states of constricted consciousness), etc., will be nullified, and you shall sorrow no more.

With blessings of comfort.

## 101

B.H., 14 Tammuz, 5711
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

Through the esteemed [name], I have received your donation of five dollars, which I have transferred to the *Lishkas Chashaim* fund. This is a fund from which we assist people or causes without publicity. The merit of such *tzedakah* is very great, and I hope that this *tzedakah b'sesser* (charity given in secret) will help ensure that the request for [the person for whom you gave the *tzedakah*] will be answered, and that he will begin to feel better in his health.

The Gemara tells us that one who prays for his fellow while he himself is in need of that same thing is answered first. Since, in general, in these times, everyone has something they are lacking, I would like to wish you that Hashem Yisbarach should fulfill whatever you are lacking, and that your home should be a true Jewish home of Torah and *mitzvos*. I will be pleased to hear from you about this.

As I understand it, you attend *shul* frequently. I would suggest that you take upon yourself—*bli neder*—to keep the *takanah* of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, to recite each day after *davening* in the morning a *yom* of *Tehillim* (as the *Tehillim* is divided according to the days of the month). I would also suggest that you accustom yourself to giving *tzedakah* every day before *davening*—*Shacharis* and *Mincha* (the amount is not the point, but rather the consistency, that every time before *davening*, the act of giving *tzedakah* should not be missing).

In the *parsha* that was read this past Shabbos, the *parsha* begins with the verse, "This is the statute (*chukas*) of the Torah." It is explained in *Toras HaChassidus* that the word **chukas** also carries the meaning of **chakikah** (engraving). The difference between engraving and writing is that with writing, the ink is one thing and the material upon which one writes is another; only later—after it is written—do they become one. However, with *chakikah*—when one carves letters into stone—the letters are of the very same stone itself. So too, in studying Torah and fulfilling *mitzvos*, it must be in a manner of **chakikah**, where the person and the Torah and the *mitzvos* that he fulfills are one. And then the Torah tells us, "If you walk in My statutes (*chukosai*)"—from the root of *chakikah*—"then I will provide your rains in their time, and the earth will yield its produce," etc.

I hope to hear good news from you, and I sign with a blessing.

## 101

B"H, 14 Tammuz, 5711
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

I was pleased to hear from Mr. [Name] regarding you and your good work for matters of Yiddishkeit, and Mr. [Name] also writes to me that you are currently in need of a refuah.

When I was at the Tziyun of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, last Monday, 12 Tammuz, I mentioned you for a refuah. I hope that you will be able to share good news with me that you are already feeling better, and I will be grateful to you for such good news.

I wish to encourage you regarding the takanah of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, to recite the daily portion of Tehillim every day after davening in the morning (as Tehillim is divided according to the days of the month), so that in the course of the month one will have recited the entire Tehillim at least once. Also, to study a parsha of Chumash with the commentary of Rashi every day. I hope that, bli neder, you will see to fulfilling this—reciting Tehillim and studying Chumash with Rashi—from now on, as both of these shiurim draw down blessing and success into the life of a Yid.

In the sidra of last week that was read on Shabbos, the first verse is, "This is the statute (chukas) of the Torah." In Toras HaChassidus, it is explained that the word **chukas** has an additional meaning, from the term **chakikah** (engraving). This is a hint that Yidden must study Torah and fulfill mitzvos in a manner of **chakikah**, not like writing, where the ink is one thing and the material upon which one writes is another, and they are only later joined and connected to one another. Rather, the study of Torah and the fulfillment of mitzvos must be in a manner of engraving, like carving letters into stone, where the letters are of the same stone itself, not something added from the outside. So too, in the fulfillment of mitzvos and the study of Torah, it must be a matter of engraving, such that he and the Torah and the mitzvos are one thing. And then the Torah says, "If you walk in My statutes (bechukosai)—from the term chakikah—then I will provide your rains in their time, and the land will yield its produce," etc.

With blessings for a speedy refuah.

## 104

19 Tammuz, 5711
Brooklyn

Greetings and blessings!

I have received your letter asking about the fact that in many places the *taamei ha-mikra* (cantillation marks) do not align with the simple, literal interpretation of the verses. You ask which path to choose: whether to read according to the *taamim*, or to read with pauses and word groupings that align with the simple meaning of the verses (and you noted that you have given each person the authority to decide whether to make a major or minor pause, etc.).

**Response:**

1) According to the tradition of our nation, the *taamim* were given *mi-pi ha-gevurah* (from the Almighty). As stated in the *Pardes* of the Ramak at the beginning of *Shaar* 28 (regarding the vowel points), he writes: "It is well-known among all the sages of Israel, by tradition from mouth to mouth, from Ezra the Scribe, who received it from mouth to mouth until Moshe Rabbeinu at Sinai, *mi-pi ha-gevurah*, that the vowel points and their variations are..." See there in *Shaar* 29, where it is proven that even the names of the *taamim* are based on Kabbalah, and therefore, many deep concepts are hinted at within them as well.

This is contrary to the view of R' Eliyahu Bachur and others who wished to say that the *taamim* and vowel points were established at a later time. This discussion has already been addressed at length in many books (see also *Piku'at Sadeh* by the author of *Sdei Chemed*). However, once the *Zohar* and *Tikkunei Zohar* were revealed, anyone who believes in what is written therein will naturally believe that the vowel points and *taamim* were given *mi-pi ha-gevurah*. See also *Likutei Torah*, *d.h. Shir HaShirim*, end of chapter 2, where this is noted.

2) The *taamim* were given so that the words could be chanted through them. In the language of the *Zohar* (Vol. I, 15b): "The letters are the body, and the vowel points are the spirit; they all move in their movements following the *taamim*, and they stand in their place. When the melody of the *taamim* moves, the letters and vowel points move after them; when it pauses, they do not move and they stand in their place." See also similarly in the introduction to *Tikkunei Zohar* (8a) and in many other places.

3) Seemingly, based on the above, it is difficult to understand why in many places the *taamim* do not align with the simple meaning of the verses, as you questioned in your letter.

This can be explained in several ways: a) We do not have a complete understanding of the laws of the *taamim* and their essence. The vast majority (and perhaps all) of the rules of the *taamim* brought in the books are merely the work of human beings who compiled these rules as an attempt to understand the order of the *taamim* in the Tanach. When there is a contradiction between the rules of the *taamim* and the simple meaning of the verses, it is possible that at times, the *taamim* were given precedence. b) In line with the above, one must take into account the rules of musical intonation, the length of one's breath, and the like. c) Just as the written text (*kesiv*) hints at an interpretation that transcends the simple, literal understanding (see *Iggeret HaKodesh*, Epistle 19), it is possible that in many places the *taamim* also hint at such interpretations. However, the *kesiv* exists only in writing and not in the reading, whereas the *taamim* do not. This is also understandable, as melody in general is more connected to the inner dimension of the soul, which transcends intellect and comprehension; see *Likutei Torah* there.

4) Based on the above, the statement of our Sages (Yoma 52a) that "there are five verses that have no definitive punctuation" requires study. In *Bereishis Rabbah* (ch. 70) and in the Jerusalem Talmud (*Avodah Zarah* 2:8), they added another one. However, the early authorities (*Rishonim*) have already addressed this and offered resolutions: a) That in truth, the verses were indeed resolved through the punctuation of the *taamim* that Ezra established (Ritva, Yoma ibid.; Rosh in his Tosafot; *Yad Malachi*; *Chiddushei Aggadot* of the Maharsha). b) That there is a dispute regarding the *taamim* of those specific verses, and therefore they remain without a definitive resolution (Beis Yosef in *Responsa Avkat Rochel*, end of section 4). See regarding all this in *Sdei Chemed*, *Kelalim* 8, 28.

See also *Shaarei Ephraim*, *Shaar* 3, paragraph 15.

The conclusion from all the above is that it is **obvious** that one must read the *mikra* according to its *taamim*, and one must not change them or establish *taamim* of one's own, Heaven forbid. See the *sicha* of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of 24 Shevat 5696, section 5, regarding how much they were particular about this.

I trust you are continuing your work in the field of proper education. I would be interested to hear the details regarding this, and I thank you in advance.

## 106

106

B.H., 20 Tammuz, 5711
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and Blessings!

I was pleased to have the opportunity to become acquainted with your two sons, may they live, who visited me. They made a good impression, and I am certain that if you speak with them from time to time a little more regarding Yiddishkeit and the performance of practical mitzvos, it would receive the proper resonance with them. It would also find expression in them and their households, leading them to draw closer to Torah and mitzvos even more than until now.

In our conversation, they told me that you are suffering from the prostate, and that there is an opinion from a doctor that it would be worthwhile to undergo an operation, but that you are deliberating about it, as you feel you are not strong enough for it.

My suggestion would be that you consult the opinion of two specialist doctors, and that you also share your own perspective with them. If it is their conclusion that you should have the operation, you should proceed with it in a good and auspicious hour, following their instructions. The Ribono shel Olam will grant that it should go well and successfully, and that you should have long life and good years. This means, quite literally, many long, good, and calm years; but it also has an inner meaning—that the years should also be long and good in terms of ruchniyus. That is to say, filled with Yiddishkeit—Yiddishkeit for yourself, and also through influence upon those around you, and especially upon your children and grandchildren, that they should conduct their homes and their lives according to the path of Torah and mitzvos.

Now, during the "Three Weeks," which remind us of the time of the Churban, one must also remember what the Gemara tells us: that the primary cause of the Churban was sinas chinam. Since we all desire and hope for the complete and true Geulah, immediately, we must exert special effort to remove the cause that brought about the Churban—that is, we must exert special effort in ahavas Yisrael. This is especially relevant to Kohanim, who say in Birkas Kohanim, "to bless His people Israel with love." As my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, related in the name of one of the tzaddikim nistarim, these words also contain the intention to bless His people Israel with the trait of love—that they should have love for one another, and that they should express this through actual deeds, in gashmiyus, and even more so in ruchniyus.

I hope to hear good news from you. I ask that you convey my regards to your sons, may they live, and I hope to hear good news from them as well.

With blessings,

## 107

[20 Tammuz, 5711]

In response to the notification that you are becoming a Bar Mitzvah and your request for a blessing,

I hereby express my blessing that, in the words of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, you should be a G-d-fearing person, a Chossid, and a scholar, and that you should provide much *chassidishen nachas*.

My father-in-law, the Rebbe, related that the Bar Mitzvah *maamarim* used to be started (by the Nesi'im) with the words *Na'aseh Adam* ("Let us make man")—though when the *maamar* was given over to be transcribed, the beginning was sometimes omitted.

This means that the Bar Mitzvah must know that he has attained the status of *Adam*—which is the most exalted of the four titles: *Adam*, *Ish*, *Gever*, *Enosh* (see *Kuntres Toras HaChassidus*, Chapter 7; *D'H Vayavo Amalek 5709*, *Kuntres* 62, Chapter 2). He must begin this *avodah* immediately and not postpone it for later, and then he is assisted from Above to truly become an *Adam* (see *Sefer HaToldos*, page 64).

I am sure you recited a *maamar* of *Chassidus* on the day of your Bar Mitzvah, and that you will keep up your daily *shiurim* that are incumbent upon everyone: *Chumash*, *Tehillim*, and *Tanya*.

With blessings for success in your Torah studies and in *yiras shamayim*.

## 111

[23 Tammuz, 5711]

...It is certainly superfluous to remind you regarding a special program for the vacation days, which must be prepared well in advance. As the saying of our Rebbes goes: "As one sets out, so it goes," and this applies equally to the conduct during the vacation days. For several reasons, it is appropriate to arrange that the vacation should manifest only in a reduction and a minimum of studies, and nothing more, in accordance with the custom of Israel from time immemorial. And if such conduct was advisable in all cities and all settlements, how much more so in a settlement of Anash.

## 112

112

B.H., 26 Tammuz, 5711
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, and learned R. Menachem Nachum, may he live:

Peace and blessing!

Through the esteemed Rabbi and Chassid, who engages in communal needs with faithfulness, R. Shlomo Zalman Hecht, I received your *pidyon nefesh* on behalf of your son, Meir Zev ben Esther, who is currently in Korea.

When I am at the *tziyun* of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, I will read the *pidyon nefesh*. May it be His will that he be able to bring me good news regarding this soon.

I see on the bulletin of the Bnei Yisrael synagogue that you are their secretary. Surely, as is the custom of those who love Hashem, the secretary is the life-force of the synagogue, and the quality of the synagogue’s vitality depends on him. Most important are the matters of the synagogue’s spiritual life—whether there are public *shiurim* and how the conduct of *davening* is managed on *Motzaei Shabbos* and *Yom Tov*, etc. Although it is surely superfluous to call your attention to the importance of this matter, I rely on the words of our Sages, "One only urges those who are already diligent."

I would like to take this opportunity to call your attention to the great importance of reciting the daily *Tehillim* (as divided by the days of the month) each day after *Shacharis*, and to strive to ensure that *Maariv* on *Motzaei Shabbos* is conducted in such a way that it does not, G-d forbid, lead to a desecration of the holiness of *Shabbos*. Also, emphasize the great importance that mourners, may we be spared, who come to say *Kaddish* should also put on *tefillin*; often, this is the way to accustom them to putting on *tefillin* for the rest of their lives. There are many other such details that you, in your honor, will be able to find on the spot, knowing the conditions of the place and the nature of the congregants in the synagogue. Through all these details, you can add vitality to the synagogue and its congregants, to make them "living Jews." According to the saying of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, "The Almighty does not remain a debtor," and He repays measure for measure, granting long life and an increase in life to all those who work in the aforementioned matters. May they and their families live and be blessed through the "candle of a *mitzvah* and the light of Torah," and a way of life for all that they require.

I am sure you will inform me of good news regarding your son, may he live. I will conclude with regards to all the congregants, may they live, and tell them that the synagogue is called by our Sages a *mikdash me'at* (a miniature sanctuary). Through conduct that is appropriate for a *mikdash me'at*, this serves as a preparation and a prelude to hasten the building of the Third *Beis Hamikdash* by *Mashiach Tzidkeinu*, speedily in our days.

With blessing.

Enclosed is the receipt for your donation, which was delivered to the secret charity fund (*lishkat chashaim*), which is one of the most important levels of the *mitzvah* of *tzedakah*.

B"H, 26 Tammuz, 5711
Brooklyn.

May it be the will of Hashem that speedily and in our days, He will lead you out from the straits into the expanse—from physical straits and limitations into an expanse in the physical sense, as literally understood. Furthermore, from your side, you should also lead yourself out—in matters that depend on you—from the straits into the expanse in spiritual matters as well. Surely you have heard the saying of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, in the name of his grandfather, the Rebbe (Maharash), of blessed memory: "The world says that if you cannot go under, you must go over; but I say that from the outset, one should go over." This depends solely on one's own strength, as we spoke about at the farbrengen of the Chag HaGeulah, 12 Tammuz: that strength and bitul of self are the very vessels to overcome all concealments, obstacles, and obstructions. Then one sees that it is nothing more than a **test**, and it is self-understood that this makes the avodah enjoyable...

## 115

B"H, 26 Tammuz, 5711
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, learned, and distinguished R' Elkana, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

Through the esteemed Rabbi and Chassid, G-d-fearing, learned, and distinguished individual who engages in communal needs with faithfulness, R' Shlomo Zalman Hecht, may he live, I received his *pidyon nefesh*. When I am at the *tziyun* of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, I will read it, and he will surely arouse great mercy upon him, that he and his wife, may she live, be blessed with all that they require and that their hearts' desires be fulfilled for the good, in general and in particular...

Furthermore, Rabbi Hecht, may he live, mentioned that he now has an opportunity to enter into a business venture. May it be the will of Hashem that it be successful, and may there be fulfilled in him what my father-in-law, the Rebbe, related in the name of the Alter Rebbe, the author of the Tanya and Shulchan Aruch: "The Almighty gives Jews *gashmius*, and Jews make *gashmius* into *ruchnius*."

I will conclude with a matter relevant to the day, from the *parsha* of Matos, albeit briefly, as time does not permit me to elaborate, and for one such as you, this will suffice.

It is known that the subject of vows (*nedarim*) is distinct from other commandments in the Torah in that they begin with a minor who is **close** to adulthood—that is, at twelve years of age, rather than thirteen as with other Torah commandments. According to many *Rishonim*, this is *mid'oraisa*. The moral lesson here is that the entire concept of vows is in the category of a "fence," as our Sages said, "Vows are a fence for abstinence." That is, one makes a vow upon himself so as not to stumble in the fulfillment of *Torah* and *mitzvos*. Even though our Sages said in the *Yerushalmi* (Nedarim, end of chapter 7), "It is enough for you to abstain from what the Torah has forbidden you," and one could therefore argue that this is merely a matter of arrogance—and furthermore, that there is even a concern of prohibition involved, due to "you shall not add or subtract"—the Torah comes and points out that the opposite is true. For in the fulfillment of *Torah* and *mitzvos* alone, it is possible—as the Ramban states at the beginning of *parshas Kedoshim*—to be a "scoundrel within the bounds of the Torah." It is therefore necessary for one to "make a safeguard for My safeguard." The Torah comes with the *mitzvah* of vows to hint that in some way, one must obligate a person when he reaches the age of thirteen for *mitzvos* through the **preparation** of adding a fence and abstinence beyond what the Torah has forbidden. This is the matter of vows, which begin as a preamble to the fulfillment of *Torah* and *mitzvos*—namely, with a minor **close** to adulthood. It is understood by itself that this is not a matter that is equal for every soul, for the areas in which one person needs to abstain are not the same as those for another, and there is no room for concern in the case of another person. For example, our Sages said, "An *am ha'aretz* is forbidden to eat meat," whereas the opposite is true for a *talmid chacham*, as our Sages said, "In a place where vegetables are available, meat should also be available." Therefore, the *parsha* of vows was specifically stated to the "heads of the tribes"—that is, regarding the stature of the *Nesi'im*—because the annulment of vows and their fulfillment depends on the heads of the tribes. That is, regarding what to vow and what it is better not to vow—since it is not a matter equal for every soul—this must be done through the *Nasi*, who can say "**this** is the matter," with a clear vision (*aspaklaria hame'irah*). And the wise will understand.

With blessings for proper health and all good.

## 1116

B"H, 27 Tammuz, 5711
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed and distinguished, etc., R' Yosef, may he live,

Peace and blessing!

I have received your letter of Thursday, Parshas Balak. I am very pleased that you have accepted my suggestion, which I made while at the Tziyun of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, regarding contributing one thousand dollars toward the Rebbe’s work in Africa. Naturally, this will be credited toward the total of your participation in the sum of fifty thousand dollars.

The fact that you made an effort to send the thousand dollars at this time, despite being short on cash, makes your merit even greater. This is also in accordance with the verse, "Fortunate is he who considers the poor; Hashem will save him on the day of evil" (Tehillim 41:2). The interpretation of this is that even at a time when one is short on money and is, in that sense, himself "poor" (*dal*), he nevertheless disregards this and gives charity beyond his current means. Then, the continuation of the verse will certainly be fulfilled: "And as for me, in my integrity You uphold me, and set me before You forever."

I also hope that what is written in the Prophet Malachi will be fulfilled, where Hashem says, "Test Me now with this"—test Me in the mitzvah of charity—and you will see, "if I will not open for you the windows of heaven and pour out for you a blessing without limit." May Hashem grant that you should see this in actual, tangible reality with outstanding success, and that you should be able to fulfill all your obligations and even exceed them.

With blessings for success and tranquility.

## 118

B"H, 1 Menachem Av, 5711, Brooklyn.

Yalles – Philadelphia

Shalom u’Bracha!

I received your letter of 28 Tammuz a short while before I traveled to the Tziyun of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory. I mentioned you and your family, may they live, for whatever they need, as you requested in your letter. Surely, "a tzaddik who has departed is found in this world more than during his lifetime" will arouse Divine mercy for success in both material and spiritual matters.

As you requested, the donation you sent in connection with the yahrtzeit of your father, the holy Rav, etc., etc., of blessed memory, has been delivered, and the receipt is enclosed.

In the *Kuntres Eicha* that has just been printed—the vast majority of which is being published for the first time from manuscripts—you will find on page 44 a discussion regarding the equivalence between Yom Kippur and Tisha B'Av, in that on both days one does not wear leather shoes. Although it is written there that this is for opposite reasons, it is nevertheless known that the "depth of the height is connected to the depth of the lowest," and from this it is understood that on Tisha B'Av as well—may it be transformed speedily in our days into joy and gladness—there is the concept of removing the shoes, which is a state that transcends the "shoe." I see that this year, the yahrtzeit for the soul of your father, the holy Rav, etc., etc., of blessed memory, is also a day on which wearing leather shoes is prohibited, and surely everything is by Divine Providence. This is especially true for those connected to Torah and mitzvos; as is known, the day of a yahrtzeit is a matter of ascent, and this is also the concept behind the prohibition of wearing shoes on Yom Kippur, etc., which is also present on Tisha B'Av, and this year on the tenth of Av. May it be the will of Hashem that very soon we will see with physical eyes the fulfillment of the prophecy, "I will turn their mourning into joy," and all the matters of Megillas Eicha will be interpreted in terms of ascents, as written in the aforementioned *Kuntres Eicha*.

With blessings.

119

2) Regarding your question as to whether to reveal to your children, *shiy*, the passing of their mother, *a"h*: In my opinion, you should explain to them, little by little, that Hashem has now brought her to a place that is free from all illness and disease—a place that exists in Heaven. From there, she can also influence all her children and ask Hashem that they succeed in their studies and their conduct. Furthermore, even now, a mother’s compassion for her sons and daughters remains, and she yearns for them to conduct themselves in a manner befitting the sons and daughters of Yisrael, which brings her the greatest *nachas ruach*. When they do so, she is also able to act so that their affairs will be successful. The only change is that she is no longer seen with physical eyes, etc., etc. It is understood that the words you use when speaking with the older children will not be the same as those used with the younger ones, but the content, according to their level, can be the same for all of them, based on the above.

With blessings for a proper adjustment, in body and soul, very soon.

#### ***121***

**R' Chaim Yaakov:** Gass, Greensboro.

## 1,122

[4 Menachem Av, 5711]

...Regarding your question concerning a woman for whom, according to the doctors, pregnancy poses a danger, and whether it is permissible for the woman to employ methods to prevent this:

Our Rebbes, of blessed memory, are among the lenient authorities, and they permitted it in certain ways during or after the act of *tashmish*. See the *Responsa Tzemach Tzedek*, *Even HaEzer*, section 89, where he permits it, and there is also a document in the holy handwriting of his son, the Maharil, permitting it.

(I have since also found in the *Responsa Maharsham*, Vol. 1, section 58, that his opinion is also to permit it), and this is contrary to the rabbis, etc., who are stringent in this matter (cited in *Sdei Chemed*, *Asifat Dinim*, *Ma'arechet Ishut*, subsection 1, and in *Pe'at HaSadeh* there). We follow only the ruling of our Rebbes, and I have also heard in the name of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, that in certain ways he permitted it. You should turn to one of the elder *anash* rabbis who is a *baal hora'ah* and knows how this is practiced. Naturally, all the aforementioned methods are those that the woman performs, not the husband.

#### 1,122

Printed in *Likkutei Sichos*, Vol. 12, p. 179. **The lenient authorities:** See also above, Vol. 3, letter 625. Above, 828.

Below, 1,165.

## 1223

1223

B"H, 4 Menachem Av, 5711, Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

I received your letter (though it lacked the date of its writing) along with the *pidyon nefesh* enclosed within. When I am at the *tziyun* of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, I will read it. He will surely arouse Heavenly mercy for you, for the proper health of you and your wife, may she live, and for all that you require in both material and spiritual matters.

I have already written to you my opinion: your thinking is incorrect, and there is no basis for your concerns. This is surely nothing but a tactic of the *yetzer*. It would be best for you to minimize thinking about yourself—even regarding what you imagine needs fixing in your own affairs—and replace this focus with thoughts concerning others. Even better is to focus on thoughts of the *Ribono shel Olam*, as is explained in countless places in *Chassidus*, and as is also explained in Rambam, *Hilchos Yesodei HaTorah*, chapter 2: "How does one come to love and fear Him..."

This is especially true regarding what is explained in the books of *Chassidus* concerning one of the differences between the path of *mussar* and the path of *Chassidus*. Generally, the path of *mussar* emphasizes introspection and contemplation of one’s own shortcomings, negative character traits, and improper matters, along with the necessary rectifications. Consequently—even if one succeeds in actually implementing these rectifications, which is good—one has still spent his time thinking about and contemplating evil, or at the very least, that which is not good. This is not the case in the path of *Chassidus*, which emphasizes introspection and contemplation of "looking into the glory of the King," or at the very least, contemplating the nature of man as **"I shall be like the Most High,"** and matters of *ahavas Yisrael*. In this way, even if one does not reach the appropriate conclusion—meaning, even if one does not succeed in actually rectifying one’s own affairs—one has still spent his time fulfilling the *mitzvah* of "know the G-d of your father," by looking at the good, at the level of holiness, and so on.

The same applies to your specific situation: your preoccupation with matters that are not appropriate—who is to say that this is not merely an imagination? And even if your concern has a basis and requires rectification, it has already been explained in *Tanya* that this should be done at specific, designated times. Furthermore, who is to say that even after such contemplation and bitterness (for sadness, Heaven forbid, is not even a topic of discussion), there is no doubt that you will reach the correct conclusion one hundred percent? By contrast, if you occupy yourself with contemplating the greatness of the Creator—who brings into being, enlivens, and sustains everything at every single moment, and therefore, the power of the Creator must always be within the created—then, first of all, you have spent your time fulfilling the *mitzvos* of "know," of the greatness of Hashem, that "Hashem is the G-d," and "you shall love Hashem your G-d." And all the more so, if this leads to an actual improvement in your situation, you gain from every perspective. In a few words: why occupy yourself with the path of *sur meira* (turning away from evil) when you have the choice to occupy yourself with the path of *asei tov* (doing good), through which you will naturally also arrive at *sur meira*?

May it be the will of Hashem that these days be transformed for us and for all of Israel into joy and gladness, speedily in our days, in our immediate time. May joy and gladness be bestowed upon each of us, and may we fulfill the general command, "And you shall serve Hashem your G-d with joy and a good heart, from an abundance of everything" (see Rambam, end of *Hilchos Lulav*).

With blessings for proper health and that you should know of this.

## 124

B"H, 4 Menachem Av, 5711, Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

...In these recent days, everyone is reminded of the statement of our Sages, of blessed memory, that the *Churban* occurred because of the sin of *sinas chinam*—that is, not loving another person without any reason or basis. We, all Jews, surely want to emerge from *galus* as soon as possible; consequently, we must remove the cause that brought about the *galus*. The *tikkun* for this is *ahavas chinam*—that is, to love a fellow Jew without a reason. This applies even to a Jew from whom the Jewish people derive no benefit, and one does not even know if any Jew derives any benefit from him at all. There is even a doubt as to whether one can apply the commandment of "love your neighbor as yourself" to him, because he is not, G-d forbid, a "neighbor" (*rei'acha*)—he does not study Torah and does not observe *mitzvos*. Yet, *ahavas chinam* dictates that one must love even such a Jew. When one conducts oneself in this manner, one removes the cause that brought about the *Churban* and *galus*. By doing so, a Jew illuminates his own corner, thereby bringing light into his portion of the world and adding more light, until, in the end, we will illuminate the *galus* and merit the complete and true *Geulah* speedily in our days, through *Mashiach Tzidkeinu*.

With blessings for a good summer, in good health and prosperity.

## 128

B"H, 8 Menachem Av, 5711, Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Rabbi, the Chassid, G-d-fearing, and learned, etc., R' Avraham Eliyahu, may he live:

Peace and blessing!

It was with sorrow that I learned of the passing of his wife, the Rabbanit, Mrs. Bracha Niesha, a"h. May it be the will of Hashem that from here on you shall know no further grief or sorrow, G-d forbid. In these days of old mourning, which will surely be transformed speedily in our days into joy and gladness, may the new mourning also be forgotten from the earth, and may those who dwell in the dust awaken and sing.

Just now, the *Kuntres Reshimot* on *Megillas Eichah* by the Tzemach Tzedek, n"e, has arrived from the bindery. Included in it are a *maamar* by the Rebbe Maharash, n"e, a *maamar* by the Rebbe Rashab, n"e, and a *maamar* by my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe. May it be the will of Hashem that in the merit of your efforts in bringing the "Light that is in the Torah" and the "Light of Torah" into thousands of homes of the Children of Israel, that in accordance with the measure of the Holy One, Blessed be He—which is measure for measure—He will also illuminate you with a revealed and manifest good light, and that you will see much *nachas* from your daughter and son-in-law, the Rabbi, may they live.

Enclosed are two *kuntresim*; you will surely inform the office how many more to send to you.

May it be the will of Hashem that speedily in our days we will merit the fulfillment of the promise, "I will turn their mourning into joy," and may these days be transformed into joy and gladness, amen, may it be His will.

With blessings for true health and for success in all matters.

P.S. Your letter of 3 Tammuz was received in due time, and you have surely already received all the shipments from the office as listed in your aforementioned letter.

**R' Avraham Eliyahu:** Axelrod. Additional letters to him appear above, 870, and in the notes referenced there.

## 129

By the Grace of G-d
11 Menachem Av, 5711
Brooklyn

To the esteemed Rabbi, the Chassid, G-d-fearing, learned in Torah and meticulous in mitzvos, who engages in communal needs, etc., R’ Shlomo, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

I received your letter in due time, dated Erev Shabbos Kodesh, 23 Tammuz. Surely, in the meantime, the letters for Mr. Almaliach, Grass, and Davila have also arrived. However, since I wrote them in connection with the days of the Chag HaGeulah, they may require further clarification, and I rely on your understanding in this matter.

Regarding what you write—that concerning 12 Tammuz there is no one to talk to in your location—this is not correct. Surely there are those, and more than those; were it not so, you would not have come there. It is simply that a search is still required. The measure of good is greater than the measure of retribution; just as our Sages, of blessed memory, elaborated at the beginning of Maseches Pesachim on the methods of searching for chametz—that it must be done even in holes and crevices—then how much more so is this true regarding the search for the good, which every Jew must strive to uncover. When one does so, there is no doubt that one finds much more than one initially estimates, and certainly much more than is visible to the naked eye before beginning the process.

It is often necessary here to know **exactly** the number of institutions, and approximately the number of students—boys and girls—in each one. Since, according to the state of your avodah, the number of institutions increases from time to time, please be kind enough to inform me immediately whenever a new institution is added, and include any details you may have regarding that institution. Thank you in advance.

Regarding the financial matters from the Joint, there is much distress in the matter, but my hope is strong that even now, the Rebbe, my father-in-law, who is the one managing these affairs—and even more so now than during his lifetime—will bring about success, as explained in the Kuntres for 12 Tammuz for the days of Geulah of this year, regarding success that is natural yet transcends nature.

When I was at the Ohel of the Rebbe, my father-in-law, of blessed memory, on Erev Rosh Chodesh Menachem Av, I mentioned you and your wife, may she live, regarding what you need, and may you be blessed very soon with children.

It is somewhat surprising that you do not mention in your letter the state of your wife’s health, may she live. According to the custom of the older Chassidim, this is a sign that all is well. Surely in your next letter you will write about this explicitly. May your heart be confident, as well as the heart of your wife, may she live, that the Rebbe, my father-in-law, bestows blessing and success upon those who engage in fulfilling his shlichus, and may you both share good news in this regard.

Enclosed is a copy of what I said to the students, may they live, who are traveling to the provincial cities on a shlichus to strengthen Yiddishkeit. Perhaps you can utilize this for your own avodah in your location in an appropriate manner.

It would be proper to investigate whether there is a newspaper in your location where it would be possible to publish articles related specifically to our avodah, or regarding Torah and Chassidus in general. It is understood that it does not matter if it is in the local language; on the contrary, there is an advantage in this, as it will increase the number of readers, etc.

With blessings, and awaiting good news.

**M. Schneerson**

Just now, your letter from Rosh Chodesh Menachem Av was received. Thank you for sending the books via registered mail. A great request for the future: please strive to do this, both with books of Kabbalah and with Nigleh. The more one does, the more praiseworthy it is. And this applies not only to old books, but to everything printed in Africa, Asia, etc.

## 132

B"H, 15 Menachem Av, 5711, Brooklyn.

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, and faithful businessman, R’ Y. HaKohen, may he live:

Peace and blessing!

I have just received your letter from yesterday, and I am hastening to respond regarding another *mofes* (miracle) of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory:

It has been weighing on me this entire time that on Erev Rosh Chodesh Menachem Av, I was unable to bring to the Ohel the fact that you had sent your usual check for the Rebbe’s causes. However, since the Rebbe once told me that I should not pressure you regarding money—as I have already conveyed to you—I could do nothing about it. Now, I see that the Rebbe directly placed this thought into you, or, in the language you used, that "my heart pricks me." This is akin to the *kruzim* (proclamations) from Above that instill in a person good thoughts and resolutions that were not prepared by him beforehand, as explained in *Likutei Torah*, Parshas Teitzei (36d), and at length in the *maamar* "Az Yashir" from the year 5700. You surely have that *maamar*...

May Hashem help you not only to not diminish, Heaven forbid, from your good customs, but to add to them, as our Sages of blessed memory said: "We ascend in matters of holiness."

In particular, the *hashgacha pratis* is evident, as all of the above occurred on the fifteenth of Av, a day regarding which our Sages of blessed memory say (end of *Taanis*): "From here on, he who adds, will have added to him"—regarding Torah. It is therefore understood that Torah effects the same order and conduct in *mitzvos* as well, especially in the *mitzvah* of *tzedakah*, which is called "the *mitzvah*" (without qualification) and is equivalent to all the *mitzvos* (see *Tanya*, Chapter 37; *Iggeres HaTeshuvah*, end of Chapter 3; *Iggeres HaKodesh*, Chapters 3, 4, end of 5, 6, 8, 9, 10, 12).

With blessings for success in your private business affairs, and may you, with joy and a glad heart, transform the material into the spiritual.

## 133

133

B"H, 18 Menachem Av, 5711, Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the Rabbis, the pious, the G-d-fearing, who sit in judgment in the great city of Dublin, the Chief Rabbi, Moreinu HaRav Yisroel Jakobovits, and the Dayan, Moreinu HaRav Zalman Yosef Aloni,

Greetings and blessings!

I have received your letter dated Tuesday, Parshas Pinchas...

I will conclude with what I said in the continuation of Shabbos Nachamu, regarding our Sages' statement that it is a "double comfort." This means double not only in quantity, but also in quality. That is to say, the comfort will be such that it does not merely remove the pain, but actually transforms the pain itself into pleasure. This means that a person sees, even with physical eyes, that the suffering he endured—a) has a reason behind it. However, that cannot be called a "double comfort," for it is merely comfort. The prophet adds that the comfort is double, meaning b) that he sees that the suffering itself was not suffering at all, but rather an outpouring of hidden good, which, due to its immense magnitude, was drawn down in such a form.

The explanation of this matter is understood from what is written briefly in Tanya, Chapter 26, and as is also related in the Gemara, that there is one version of the saying, "Everything the Merciful One does, He does for the good," and a further, superior version: "This, too, is for the good." This is like the distinction between the incident of Rabbi Akiva and the incident of Nachum Ish Gam Zu. In the case of Rabbi Akiva, because his candle was extinguished, his donkey was eaten, and his rooster was taken, he was saved from physical harm. He saw that, in the end, through the pain he suffered, good came to him; however, the incident itself was a matter of pain. That is merely comfort. Not so in the case of Nachum Ish Gam Zu, when they exchanged the precious stones and pearls for earth, and a miracle occurred with the earth. They were not satisfied with the fact that through the pain he was saved from harm; rather, on the contrary, it was proven to him that this was not pain at all, but a very great good.

May it be the will [of Hashem] that in the present case as well, it will not only be a matter of "Everything the Merciful One does, He does for the good," but also a matter of "This, too, is for the good"—that the Almighty will reveal the inner intent, and then it will be seen that "this, too, is for the good, only it is not revealed and visible to physical eyes, because it is from the *alma d'itkasi* (the hidden world) which is above the *alma d'itgalya* (the revealed world)."

With blessings for success in your holy work, awaiting the mercies of Heaven, and for good news in general and in particular.

#### ***133***

For the content, see also Likutei Sichos, Vol. 2, p. 393, from the sicha of 20 Menachem Av.

## 134

B"H, 18 Menachem Av, 5711, Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the Administration of Yeshivas Tomchei Temimim Lubavitch, Lod, may they live,

Shalom u’Bracha!

In response to your letters of 27 Tammuz and 5 Menachem Av.

Regarding what you write about your intention to send a special shaliach to Belgium, Holland, Switzerland, etc., with the goal of collecting funds for the benefit of the yeshivah: In my opinion, this is **in general** the correct thing to do, but with two conditions: 

a) That you coordinate this with the other Lubavitch institutions that are also sending shadarim to various countries, so that there will be no confusion or grievances between one another. It might even be worthwhile to organize a joint fundraising campaign with some of them. 

b) That the shaliach or shluchim you send, in accordance with the instruction of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, should not occupy themselves merely with collecting money, but rather, as the saying goes, "take gashmius and sow ruchnius." We have seen tangibly that the success of the first part of this avodah depends on the success of the second part...

With blessings and regards to your group, may they live.

**M. Schneerson**
