## 135

135

B"H, 19 Menachem Av, 5711, Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the Administration of Kfar Chabad, may Hashem protect them and grant them life,

Peace and blessing!

In response to your letters of 7 Menachem Av and Friday, Erev Shabbos Parshas Devarim,

...You inform me that you have decided to send a special shaliach here as a representative of Anash from Kfar Chabad, but you do not state the purpose of the shlichus. Furthermore, I could not discern from the wording of your letter whether this is an announcement of a decision or a question as to whether it is advisable to do so. If it is an announcement of a decision, please be kind enough to inform me further regarding this soon, and you should exert yourselves in obtaining the necessary papers.

However, if this is intended as a question, I am not at all comfortable with this proposal. I do not see any great benefit in it, especially at a time when—during the month of Tishrei in particular, and at the beginning of the Shmittah year and the changes in your settlement in general—it is not at all an appropriate time for an active and influential person to travel away from there for several weeks. Surely, a large portion of what can be accomplished by coming here can also be accomplished through letters, etc.

4) During the next two weeks, the heads of the United Jewish Appeal here, the heads of the appeal for Eretz Yisrael, and the Joint Distribution Committee will be visiting Eretz Yisrael. In my opinion, it would be highly appropriate to: (a) endeavor to have them visit the Kfar and arrange a suitable reception for them; (b) afterwards, when the aforementioned individuals are in good spirits, etc., representatives of Anash from the Kfar should visit them. To strengthen the matter, there should also be representatives of Agudas Chabad and the Anash shuls, etc., in order to show them that this is a significant force in Eretz Yisrael. (If representatives from various institutions do not visit, then at the very least, you should authorize the delegation that visits the aforementioned individuals to speak on their behalf as well.) After a suitable presentation, you should demand from them with full force—though, of course, calmly and quietly—special assistance for the Shmittah year. In the course of the conversation, it might also be worthwhile to subtly mention that they are surely aware that it is possible to conduct a public campaign from Lubavitch for the Shmittah fund in the United States.

However, we are holding back from this, because it would surely result in a deficit in their general campaign fund. Consequently, they must recognize the validity of the claim for Shmittah assistance; it is not a deficit in their fund, but rather the opposite, etc., etc. Of course, all of this is only relevant if no other party or institution is already speaking in the name of the Kfar regarding assistance for Shmittah.

With blessing.

137

B"H,

It was with pleasure that I accepted, in its time, the proposal of the esteemed Chossid, a man of stature and accomplishment, etc., R' Menachem Zev, may he live, that he compile a collection of dinim and minhagim that pertain to daily life, but which do not receive sufficient attention—some people because they do not know the severity of these dinim and minhagim, and others because they are not aware of them at all.

And with great satisfaction regarding the appearance of this first collection, I write these few lines as a greeting and a blessing.

A blessing that the *devarim hayotzim min halev* (words that come from the heart) of the esteemed Chossid who compiled and edited this work, may the promise be fulfilled in them that they will *nichnasim el halev* (enter the heart) of those to whom this collection will reach, so that they may bring it into *b'poel mamash* (actual practice), fulfilling these dinim and minhagim, each according to his situation, in both *kum v'aseh* (positive commandments) and *shev v'al taaseh* (prohibitions).

This will certainly be aided, and to a very great extent, by the appropriate excerpts from the sichos of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, and from his letters, etc., which the esteemed compiler has included.

* * *

In many places, we have been pointed toward how important it is to be careful in these matters, which many people regard as light things. We have been warned that this can lead, Heaven forbid, to falling off the path entirely: "Woe to those who draw iniquity with cords of vanity" (Yeshayahu 5:18)—which one treads upon with his heel and does not fear, but later it strengthens and becomes like a wagon rope, and that sin strengthens and leads him astray in this world and in the World to Come. We have been warned regarding the punishment: "Why should I fear in the days of evil, when the iniquity of my heels—the light mitzvos that people do not pay attention to, but rather cast under their heels—surrounds me?" (Tehillim 49:6). However, we have also been promised regarding the greatness of the reward:

"And it shall come to pass, because [eikev] you hearken [tishme'un]—if you will observe the light mitzvos that a person treads upon with his heels—that Hashem your G-d will keep for you the covenant and the kindness which He swore to your fathers, and He will love you, and bless you, and multiply you, etc." 

**Menachem Schneerson**

Eve of Wednesday, Parshas V'hayah Eikev Tishme'un, 20 Menachem Av, 5711
Brooklyn, N.Y.

## 138

B"H, 21 Menachem Av, 5711, Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of 17 Menachem Av, where you write that your father, *shichyeh*, is demanding that his children, *shichyu*, provide him with the opportunity to travel to Eretz Yisrael, *t.v.*, and your mother, *shichyeh*, does not wish to accompany him...

I would like to share with you a story that I heard from my father-in-law, the Rebbe, *ka"k Admur*: A Chassid of the Tzemach Tzedek wanted to travel to Eretz Yisrael. The Tzemach Tzedek said to him: "Reb Hillel does not lack Eretz Yisrael, but you lack Eretz Yisrael; make Eretz Yisrael here." (From this story, we see that the Tzemach Tzedek addressed even his contemporaries as "Reb Hillel.") I hope that you will have good news, and that you will write to me about it.

Yesterday, in honor of the *yahrzeit* of my father, *z"l*, I was at the *Ohel* of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, *ka"k Admur*, and I mentioned you and your family for whatever they may need.

I assume that you have likely already received the *maamar*—in English—regarding Africa, as well as the booklet on *askanus tziburit*, and you will inform me of this.

With blessings.

## 101

B.H., 22 Menachem Av, 5711, Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter—the reply to which was delayed for several reasons—in which you inform me of an incident that occurred with your wife, *tichyeh*, and request a *tikkun* for yourself and for her:

1) You should set aside for *tzedakah* two-thirds of a *sela* of Torah for yourself, and the same amount for *tzedakah* on behalf of your wife, *tichyeh*. It is not necessary to give this all at once; you may pay it off little by little. It would be best if you could give it in forty installments. The measure of a *sela* of Torah can be determined in your local *beis medrash* based on the amount given for *pidyon haben*, which is five *selaim*.

2) You should exert the greatest possible effort regarding the matter of *shalom bayis* between you and your wife, *tichyeh*. That is to say, you must be extremely careful in this regard. It is known from our Sages that women are sensitive, and a woman’s tears are readily shed; therefore, it is good that you be the one to concede in order to fulfill her wishes, especially in worldly matters. If our Sages always emphasized the virtue of *shalom bayis*, how much more so on *Erev Shabbos*. We are all currently in the *Erev Shabbos* of history, after midday, for the end of our exile and the coming of our *Mashiach* is near.

3) You are surely aware that the *Tikkunei Zohar* is divided into forty sections, beginning from *Rosh Chodesh Elul* until *Yom Kippur*. You should recite the portion allocated for each day during these days.

4) It is self-understood that until after *Yom Kippur*, you must be especially careful to fulfill the three daily study portions—*Chumash*, *Tehillim*, and *Tanya*—as instituted by my father-in-law, the Rebbe.

One can assume that the greatest concealment and hiddenness will be for you regarding the second point, namely, *shalom bayis*. For it is known that "great is peace," and "all the Torah is pleasantness and all its paths are peace." This is especially true in this final exile, which, as our Sages state in *Yoma 9b*, came about because of a lack of peace. The closer we get to the end of the exile, the more the struggle from the "other side" intensifies, specifically to prevent peace from being made in the world at all, and particularly between a husband and wife below, who are in the likeness of the husband and wife above. However, "according to the camel is the burden," and surely the strength is granted to withstand this trial. See also the *kuntres* *Hechalotzu*.

Through all the above matters, surely "the iniquity shall depart," etc., and "his sin shall be forgiven." Especially since, as it appears from your letter, it is merely a matter of doubt.

It is appropriate to convey the general content of my letter to your wife, *tichyeh*, as her heart is surely also saddened by the incident that occurred to you both. May the *Ribono shel Olam* grant that you bring me good news regarding all the above in particular, and regarding your situation in general. As you requested, I will mention you at the *tziyun*.

With blessings.

## 142

B"H, 22 Menachem Av, 5711, Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of 11 Menachem Av, in which you inform me and ask for my opinion:

1) Regarding your involvement... as a guide and teacher, about which you explained the details in one of your previous letters, and you ask for my opinion:

This is a very proper endeavor. If at all times and in all eras this work was considered "work of Heaven"—and our Sages of blessed memory expounded upon this the verse, "And those who are wise shall shine like the brightness of the firmament, and those who turn the many to righteousness..."—how much more so in our present time, when the end of the galus is near and we must prepare the Jewish people for the coming of Moshiach. Just as it was at the time of the giving of the Torah, where our Sages of blessed memory say that had there been six hundred thousand minus one, it would have been a delay, Heaven forbid, in the giving of the Torah, so too regarding the exodus from galus, it is known from our Sages of blessed memory that the entire nation must be worthy, and the merit of those who involve themselves in this is immeasurable.

2) You ask for a tikkun regarding your personal matters: You should certainly keep the daily study cycles that are appropriate for everyone—Chumash, Tehillim, and Tanya—which were instituted by my father-in-law, the Rebbe. In addition to this, you should set aside money for tzedakah each day—excluding, of course, Shabbos and Yom Tov—three times in the morning and three times before Mincha. All of this is **without a vow** and should be observed until after the upcoming Yom Kippur. Furthermore, you should accustom yourself to reciting more words of Torah or tefillah while walking in the street...

With blessings for success in all the above.

## 143

143

B”H, 24 Menachem Av, 5711, Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Rabbi, the G-d-fearing, Torah-learned, etc., R’ Zalman, may he live:

Greetings and blessings!

It was with pleasure that I received the news of the birth of his son, mazal tov. I hereby express my blessing that he and his wife, may she live, raise him to Torah, chuppah, and maasim tovim, together with their other children, may they live, with peace of mind and physical well-being.

It is a well-known saying of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, based on the words of our Sages that the attributes of the Holy One, Blessed be He, are measure for measure: that for all those who involve themselves in proper chinuch, the Holy One, Blessed be He, repays them measure for measure, so that they will raise their own children, may they live, with the "candle of mitzvah and the light of Torah" and a "way of life," etc. May it be His will that you be able to bring me good tidings of the fulfillment of these blessings frequently.

Enclosed is an excerpt from what I said at the farbrengen regarding the month of Elul, which I am sure will interest you. The main thing is that it should be translated into good action, for as our Sages said, "The study is not the main thing, but the action."

I sign with the same sentiment as the opening, a blessing of mazal tov to him and his wife, may she live.

#### ***143***

**R’ Zalman:** Drori.

## 144

*Gevald*, R'...!

## 145

B"H, 24 Menachem Av, 5711, Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, and distinguished scholar, R' Shlomo Chaim, may he live, Shaliach.

Peace and blessing!

...I am writing now with a general observation, and I ask that you kindly convey this to all the students:

I do not know the reason for it, but it seems there is a trend among them to want to travel to the United States. I do not view this favorably, as they can surely continue to advance significantly in their studies where they are now. Perhaps there is an exception for whom this is not beneficial, but in general, this "running to America" to learn specifically in Brooklyn—I fear that an element of vanity is mixed into this. The spiritual administration of the students must root this out and explain to them the responsibility involved in leaving Eretz Yisrael, may it be rebuilt and established, which is only permitted for the sake of Torah study or to marry. Consequently, it must be the kind of Torah study that **the Torah** defines as Torah study, and as a student of Tomchei Temimim, this must also be in accordance with the **Torah of Chassidus**, which defines what that study is.

Furthermore: Given the current situation in Eretz Yisrael, may it be rebuilt and established, there is a vast field there for the salvation of hundreds and thousands of Jewish boys and girls. Therefore, there must be an institution on the ground that is in a position to declare: **"See** the great ones I am raising," rather than having to say that the students were sent elsewhere and expecting people to take it on faith that this is indeed the case. Moreover, I have a strong hope that a certain portion of the students could be utilized as educators and guides, at least for several weeks or months, even during their time of study in the Yeshiva. The magnitude of the value of this work is beyond measure.

...I have just received your letter stating that you also wish to come here for the seventh month—that is, the time that is "satiated with all good." Every moment that one can influence the students in this direction is more precious than anything else. And in exchange for this, you wish to leave your flock to fend for themselves, etc.—it is difficult for me to preach morality in general, especially since I do not know if what you wrote in your letter regarding the trip here is a question or merely a statement of fact, in which case there is no room for rebuke or the like—but I could not believe my eyes when I read that in your letter.

It is understood that this opinion of mine does not concern the matter of obtaining the papers. If you wrote this only as an announcement of a final decision, write directly to the Secretariat regarding this, and they will endeavor to assist as much as possible.

But my opinion is, quite simply, as stated above.

With blessings for success in teaching and for yourself.

## 1447

B"H, 24 Menachem Av, 5711, Brooklyn.

To the esteemed and distinguished scholar, our teacher Rabbi Chaim, may he live, Shochet and Bodek.

Peace and blessing!

I had already been thinking about the fact that I have not heard from you in a long time, and therefore I was very pleased to receive greetings from you through the esteemed and distinguished Rabbi, the scholar and chossid, who is involved in communal needs, our teacher Rabbi Meir Ashkenazi, may he live, that thank Hashem, all is well with you.

I was also pleased to hear that you visited Mr. [Name], may he live, and I calculate that if you visit him from time to time, you will gradually influence him to become closer to Yiddishkeit. I also believe that if ways are found to assist him in material matters, this will naturally help him listen more to what he is told regarding spiritual matters.

I am surprised that you do not mention anything about Chassidishe farbrengens, a Kiddush, or a Melaveh Malkah taking place in your city. Surely, when there are even one or two people who are interested in this, eventually they will draw a crowd to it. It is difficult to estimate at the beginning what such farbrengens can accomplish in bringing the hearts of Yidden closer to their Father in Heaven.

I hope that these few words will stir you to influence your acquaintances to arrange such hisvaaduyos. It likely does not require much effort or toil, and I am certain that this will bring good results.

With blessings, awaiting good tidings.

Enclosed are the receipts for those who sent them.

## 148

B"H, 25 Menachem Av, 5711, Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of 22 Tammuz, in which you write that for several reasons you wish to come to study at the Tomchei Temimim Yeshivah in Brooklyn, and that this is also the opinion of the Mashpia of your yeshivah, the esteemed and G-d-fearing Rabbi Shlomo Chaim Kesselman, may he live and be well:

You surely know the halachic ruling that one is permitted to leave Eretz Yisrael only for the purpose of Torah study (or to marry). Consequently, your study of Torah must be as it ought to be. If you take upon yourself such a standard of conduct, then it is appropriate that you come to study here. You must arrange in advance, either yourself or through the administration of the yeshivah where you currently study, with the administration of the yeshivah here regarding the necessary paperwork. May it be the will of Hashem that He grant you success in your studies and in your fear of Heaven, and that you become a Chassid, a G-d-fearing person, and a scholar.

I trust that you keep the daily *shiurim* incumbent upon everyone—Chumash, Tehillim, and Tanya—which were instituted by my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, and that from time to time you review *maamarim* of *Chassidus* by heart.

With blessings.

## 150

B"H, 25 Menachem Av, 5711, Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

Through the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, and learned man, who engages in communal needs, R' Shlomo Chaim Kesselman, I learned that you served as a shamash in the beis hachaim and that your health is currently not as it should be. You also sent a pidyon nefesh on your behalf, which I read at the tziyun of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory. Surely, he will awaken great mercy for you for a speedy recovery.

In my opinion, it is advisable that you ask for forgiveness from those who dwell in the dust at the beis hachaim where you served as shamash. If it is difficult to arrange this before ten people, you should do so before three. That is, they should enter the beis hachaim with you, and you should say in their presence that if there was any action that, G-d forbid, offended the honor of any of those resting in that beis hachaim, you ask for forgiveness before three (or ten) Jews, and that your intent was only for their honor.

Of course, you should only do this when the doctors permit you to walk in the street and go to the beis hachaim to perform the aforementioned.

Likewise, you should strengthen yourself in the observance of the three daily shiurim—Chumash, Tehillim, and Tanya—which are a takanah of my father-in-law, the Rebbe. During the month of Elul and the Aseres Yemei Teshuvah, you should also recite the additional Tehillim instituted by my father-in-law, the Rebbe.

My hope is strong that you will soon be able to bring good news of your health improving, continuing to improve until you return to your full strength.

It is understood that you must follow the instructions of the doctors, as our Sages have said that the Torah gave permission to the physician to heal.

Awaiting good news and signing with a blessing for a speedy recovery.

## 1,151

B"H, 25 Menachem Av, 5711, Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

I was alarmed to hear that you are engaging in many fasts and afflicting yourself by not eating for many hours before davening, and other such practices.

It is clear to me that this is a path that weakens one’s health, which is the opposite of the ruling of Chazal cited in the Rambam, Hilchos Deos, Chapter 4, that maintaining a healthy and sound body is among the ways of Hashem. It is also well known what the Baal Shem Tov said to his student, the author of the *Toldos Yaakov Yosef*, that "my stomach churns" (*HaTamim*, 1:7-8) when he heard that he was fasting, etc. If this was said regarding "cedars" like the author of the *Toldos Yaakov Yosef*, then how much more so for people like us. Furthermore, according to the ruling of the Alter Rebbe in *Iggeres HaTeshuvah*, Chapter 3: "This applies to a strong and healthy person for whom the frequency of fasts does not harm his physical health **at all**, as was the case in earlier generations. However, for one for whom frequent fasting is harmful, such that it could lead to illness or physical distress, chas v'shalom—as is the case in our generations—he is forbidden to increase his fasts, etc."

Therefore, if you will listen to my voice, you will immediately cease this practice. If you have a good custom of having done this three times, perform an *hataras nedarim* (annulment of vows), and eat before davening—including *mezonos*. If, according to the state of your health, you require more than that, then eat more, and do not rely on your own judgment in this matter. Instead, consult with the spiritual director, the esteemed chossid, G-d-fearing and learned, etc., Moreinu HaRav Sholom Chaim שי' Kesselman.

Regarding your question about your method of study—that it occurred to you to study exclusively in solitude, because it is possible that studying with peers might negatively influence you due to the nature of peers—our Sages have already stated in the Mishnah that Torah is acquired through the company of peers. While it is not necessary that all study be done in a group, as there are frequent times when depth is required, and there may be a mood or state of mind that necessitates studying in solitude—as is discussed similarly regarding the deliberations of the Sanhedrin, whether they were in pairs or each one individually—nonetheless, after that, you must have at least one or two peers with whom you have fixed times for study, and from time to time, you should also discuss with them the *Toras HaNigleh* and *Toras HaChassidus*. Consult with the administration and the *Rosh Yeshivah* regarding which peers to choose.

I hope that by return mail you will put my mind at ease and inform me that you have abandoned the path of fasts and self-affliction, and that the interpretation of the Baal Shem Tov on the verse, "If you see the donkey of one who hates you crouching under its burden... you shall surely help him," will be fulfilled in you, as the interpretation is transcribed in *Hayom Yom*.

With blessings for success in Torah and avodah with yiras shamayim, awaiting good news from you and to hear of the improvement of your health, both physically and spiritually.

## 152

B"H, 25 Menachem Av, 5711, Brooklyn, N.Y.

Rabbi, G-d-fearing, distinguished scholar, etc., Moreinu HaRav Shlomo, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

...On this occasion, I wish to stir your honor, as you are the Rav of Be'er Sheva. In this city and its surroundings, many new settlements have recently been established. According to the information received here, the state of Yiddishkeit in these places is cause for concern for several reasons, and a word to the wise is sufficient. It is incumbent upon everyone located in that region, and especially upon the Rav who leads the community, to strive with every effort and do everything in his power regarding the strengthening of Yiddishkeit in all its details. The saying of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, is well known: "One action is better than a thousand sighs."

Surely your honor is also aware of this. It is a presumption that a shaliach—and every Rav who serves with distinction in his community is a shaliach of the Merciful One—will fulfill his mission. However, our Sages have already said, "One only urges those who are already diligent," which implies two things: a) that it is permissible to urge, and b) that this urging brings benefit. And the urging is only for the sake of increasing [one's efforts]. The practice from the 15th of Av onwards is well known: that whoever adds, is added to.

I conclude as I began, with a blessing that you should share good news regarding the improvement of your wife’s health, may she live.

I saw on the margin that you are the author of the sefer *Birchas Shlomo*. Since it is not in my library, I would be interested to know if it is possible to obtain it.

In a separate package, I am sending you the *Kuntres* that was published for 12 Tammuz, the *Chag HaGeulah* of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory.

#### ***152***

**Moreinu HaRav Shlomo:** Tanvitzky.

## 153

B"H, 25 Menachem Av, 5711, Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of the 27th of Tammuz, in which you describe your situation and the matter of your scattered mind and lack of mental focus, to the extent that you stop in the middle of a pleasant conversation, and regarding various other matters, and you request good advice and a blessing for this.

In general, you should consult about this with the Mashpia, the esteemed Chassid, G-d-fearing and scholarly, who engages in communal needs, etc., Rabbi Shlomo Chaim Kesselman. Regarding the matter of a scattered mind, for a few weeks you should accustom yourself to davening from the Siddur. Likewise, when studying—whether in Nigleh or Chassidus—have the book or the maamar you are thinking about in front of you. As soon as you begin to feel your thoughts wandering, look at the letters in the book, for the letters illuminate and disperse the darkness and confusion, as the interpretation of the verse, "And when she came before the king, he said with the book, let his evil thought return."

Furthermore, memorize the beginning of Chapter 41 of Tanya, and from time to time repeat the lines aloud: "And behold, Hashem stands over him," etc., "if he serves Him as is fitting."

I trust you are keeping up with the daily study portions that are equal for every soul—Chumash, Tehillim, and Tanya—and that you review Chassidus by heart from time to time. Accustom yourself to thinking in the letters of Torah and the letters of Tehillim, especially when walking in the street.

It is understood that all of the above must be done without any ostentation, for as is known, chametz (pride and self-centeredness) is forbidden even in the smallest amount.

With blessings for success in your studies and in yiras shamayim.

## 154

B"H, 28 Menachem Av, 5711, Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your notification regarding your birthday, I hereby bless you that your *mazal* should be strengthened, that you should find your livelihood with ease, and that you should be able to provide for your wife and all your children—may they live and be well—with peace of mind and physical tranquility. May Hashem also strengthen your *neshamah elokis*, which currently finds itself in a constricted state, so that you may be able to act "below ten *tefachim*" to arrange your *shalom bayis*. I am utterly astonished—time and again—at how you do not see what is tangibly apparent to everyone: that this is the counsel of the *yetzer hara*, which is growing stronger in this matter.

I have already told you this many times, and I repeat it once more: you must exert the greatest possible effort regarding *shalom bayis* between yourself and your wife—may she live and be well—whose *shidduch* was approved by my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe. It is known from our Sages that women are of a "light mind" and that a woman’s tears are readily shed; therefore, you must be the one to concede, especially in worldly matters. If our Sages always extolled the virtue of *shalom bayis*, how much more so on the eve of Shabbos. And we are all now, within the collective of *Klal Yisrael*, on the "eve of Shabbos after midday," as the end of our exile and the coming of our righteous Moshiach draws near.

It is understood that the concealment and hiddenness are greatest regarding *shalom bayis*, for it is known that peace is great, and the entire Torah—its ways are ways of pleasantness and all its paths are peace. This is especially true in this final exile, which, as our Sages state in *Yoma 9b*, came about because of a lack of peace. The closer we draw to the end of the exile, the more the struggle from the "opposing side" intensifies, specifically in its attempt to prevent peace from being made in the world in general, and between a husband and wife below—which corresponds to the *Ish* and *Ishah* above—in particular. However, "according to the camel is the load," and you are certainly being given the strength to withstand this trial. See also *Kuntres Hechalotzu*.

With blessings for *yiras shamayim* and *shalom bayis*.

## 1055

B"H, 28 Menachem Av, 5711, Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and blessings!

I have received your letter, and I was pleased to hear that your son, may he live, is recovering from the operation. I hope that he is feeling well. You also write that your daughter, may she live, had an accident and you are requesting a blessing. I hope that your daughter is also feeling better, and that you will be able to report good news regarding this.

On this occasion, I would like to point out that just as a mother worries about the physical health of her children, she must also worry about the health of her children's neshamah. I hope that you are utilizing your influence upon your son and daughter, may they live, so that their homes will be as Jewish homes ought to be.

There are mothers who calculate that their children will not listen, so they do not speak with them about Yiddishkeit; others are embarrassed to speak. But both of these are incorrect, for it is not appropriate to be embarrassed when it concerns the neshamah-health of one's children. I am also certain that when one speaks with children once and then a second time, and explains to them with appropriate words that the one and only way for Jews to be truly happy and to have truly happy homes is only the Jewish way of Torah and mitzvos, then in the end, one succeeds in influencing them.

In the hope of hearing good news from you, with blessings.

## 156

B"H, 28 Menachem Av, 5711, Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

I received your letter of 22 Menachem Av, in which you inform me that your wife, may she live and be well, has been offered a position in London, that you also have hopes of settling there, that you are receiving letters from Australia suggesting you come there, and that the Joint is working on your transfer to the United States.

In my opinion, as long as you have the ability to bring the hearts of our fellow Jews in France—and especially in Paris—closer to their Father in Heaven (the intent here is to support the Tomchei Temimim Yeshiva and the Talmud Torah there), you should not move from your place. For the holy work is "carried upon the shoulder"—and the simple explanation of this is known: that they would not carry the holy vessels on animals or wagons. In our case, even if the *nefesh habehamis* cannot bear or understand the "what" and the "why" of this, since it is holy work—the Ark, the Table, the Menorah, etc., which represent the revealed and hidden aspects of Torah, and the *Amor* in Torah—they are the ones who are close to Hashem. They must fulfill their *shlichus* in the place where the Higher Intent brought them. The power of the *Meshaleach* is with them—the Rebbe, *k'vod kedushas moreinu v'rabbeinu*, who is found in this world even more than during his lifetime—and a person’s *shaliach* is like the person himself.

It is understood that these words of mine are directed not only to you, but to all those involved in the administration of Tomchei Temimim, **both physically and spiritually**. They have been given the strength to illuminate the entire country with the candle of *mitzvah* and the light of Torah, and the *maor* (the source of light) of Torah.

Together with this, it is worthwhile that you begin the efforts for a trip to Australia, since, according to your letter, this process is expected to take a long time. May Hashem grant you the desire and will that align with the Higher Will, and may you make a decision that is appropriate for you in both physical and spiritual matters alike.

Enclosed is an excerpt from the *farbrengen* of this past Shabbos Parshas Eikev.

With blessings.

P.S. Give my regards to your wife and to all your household, may they live and be well, both the small and the large, and please inform me of this explicitly. Thank you.

One can only imagine the pain of a single moment in Golus, or the [value of a] single additional moment in the time of Geulah, and the taanug [Hashem] has in it.

## 159

B"H, 1 Elul, 5711, Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, and distinguished, etc., our teacher, Rabbi Avraham, Shochet and Bodek, may he live:

Peace and blessing!

It was with pleasure that I learned you are continuing the good custom established according to the instruction of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, which is to organize a class each year of students for the craft of *shechitah*. You stand at their head, teaching them knowledge in this craft, and you are approaching this work again this year with desire and willingness. May it be His will that for many more years you will be able to influence the younger generation in the study of this craft, which according to the law is bound up with the highest level of *yiras shamayim*. As is known, the *chazakas kashrus* of a *shochet* must be exceptionally strong—even more so than that of a Rav, etc.

According to the words of our Sages that even a minor appointment is decreed from Heaven, and all the more so regarding the study of Torah and matters connected to it—since this appointment is from Heaven, it will naturally reveal within you a treasure of *yiras shamayim* in even greater measure than you have possessed until now.

Enclosed is an excerpt from the *farbrengen* of Shabbos Mevarchim Elul, in which is explained the concept and the allusion that *Elul* is an acronym for *“Anah Lecha Vesamti Lecha”* (Shemos 21:13)—the concept of the cities of refuge.

Regarding the cities of refuge, our Sages state (Makkos 10a) that one should only teach Torah to worthy students, for if a student is sentenced to exile, his teacher is exiled with him. As is explained in the *sicha* in section 6, in your specific case, my heart is confident in Hashem that since the students are students of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, and are studying in his *yeshivah*, you can proceed with confidence, and may it be His will that you derive much *nachas* from them, both in the study of the craft of *shechitah* and in *yiras shamayim*. May we merit soon the coming of the Great Shochet, the Holy One, Blessed be He, who will come and slaughter the *tzfoni* (the northern one), as explained in Sukkah 52a. As per the saying of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, this will be with *chesed* and *rachamim*—with the *chesed* of the attribute of Avraham Avinu, and with the *rachamim* of the attribute of Yaakov, according to what is written regarding Yaakov, who "redeemed Avraham" (see Tanya, end of Chapter 45). Between these two, there is naturally no concern from the attribute of *gevurah* of Yitzchak Avinu. This is also explained regarding the *tekiyos* in the Zohar, which is also an allusion to the Day of Judgment, for on Rosh Chodesh Elul we begin to blow the *shofar*, at which time the Holy One, Blessed be He, rises from the throne of judgment and sits upon the throne of mercy.

With blessings for success and for a *kesivah v’chasimah tovah*, and especially for proper health for you and your wife, may they live.

## 1061

1061

B”H, 1 Elul, 5711, Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

I am surprised and concerned that for a long time I have heard nothing from you, both regarding the health of your wife, *tichyeh*, and regarding your own situation and that of your son and your family, *sheyichyu*. Surely all is well, in accordance with the custom of the Chassidim of old, who would not write or provide updates when everything was peaceful. However, perhaps it would be worthwhile to set aside this custom and provide updates even when all is well. May the *Ribono shel Olam* grant us the merit to share only good news and kindness, *kohamachah yishaleinu*.

Enclosed is the *Kuntres HaReshimos* on Megillas Eichah and an excerpt from the *sicha* of the *farbrengen* of Shabbos Elul. Please distribute it appropriately among the widest possible circles.

I sign with a blessing for proper success, both materially and spiritually, for good health, and for all that is good. Please convey my regards to the congregants of your *beis medrash* with the blessing of *Kesivah V’Chasimah Tovah*.

## 162

B"H, 1 Elul, 5711, Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Rabbi and Chossid, G-d-fearing and distinguished, etc., Moreinu HaRav Yaakov Chaim, may he live.

Greetings and blessings!

I received your letter from the beginning of the month of Menachem Av, and I have been in correspondence with your representative in Paris. A few days ago, I received word that the matter has been settled. Surely, from here on, there will be peace for Yisrael.

I have already spoken at the farbrengen regarding the teaching of our Sages (Yoma 9b) that the reason for our current galus is that "its iniquity was not revealed"—which means that it was caused by sinas chinam (baseless hatred). Therefore, our rectification for a near geulah must be the opposite: ahavas chinam (baseless love). The explanation is as follows: just as sinas chinam means that there is no foundation for the hatred and no reason for it—neither in the intellect of holiness nor in human intellect—the rectification for this must follow the principle written by the Rambam at the beginning of Hilchos Deios: that one who has strayed to one extreme is rectified not by the middle path, but by grasping the opposite extreme. Thus, ahavas chinam must also be practiced even when there is no basis for it, not only in human intellect but even in the intellect of holiness (where it seems to him that his judgment is based on holiness). This means that even if he cannot find a merit in his fellow to justify loving him, and cannot find such a merit despite all his efforts—based on what appears to him—he nevertheless loves him. He persists in this love until he no longer sees the other’s fault; this is true love. Through this rectification of the extreme of ahavas chinam, the galus that came about through sinas chinam will be rectified, and we will merit the true and complete geulah, speedily and in our days.

I wrote this some time ago to the esteemed Rabbi and Chossid, the G-d-fearing and distinguished, etc., Moreinu HaRav Shmuel Yaakov Rubinstein, may he live, and he surely received my letter along with the enclosed kuntres in due time.

I sign with the blessing of Kesivah Vachasimah Tovah.

#### ***162***

Published in Likkutei Sichos, Vol. 7, p. 326, and completed based on the secretariat’s copy. **Moreinu HaRav Yaakov Chaim:** Lichtenstein, Paris.

## 163

163

B"H, 1 Elul, 5711, Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

I was pleased to hear regards from you through the esteemed Chossid, who is involved in communal needs, Rabbi Yosef Weinberg, that your health is better than it was and that your planned trip did not materialize. The meaning of **"Happy are those who dwell in Your house"** is well known—that it is a virtue to **"praise You forever."**

I assume that you are participating in shiurei Torah and are also seeing to it that you support those who study in your country, in addition to the support you send outside of your country.

I am interested to know how you are feeling in terms of your health and your business, as well as regarding your spiritual (ruchnius’dike) matters. You may write to me in Yiddish or English (whichever is more comfortable for you to express your thoughts and wishes).

I would like to draw your attention—though I assume you are certainly doing this—to saying the daily Tehillim every morning after davening (as the Tehillim is divided for the days of the month). During the month of Elul until Yom Kippur, one should also add the chapters of Tehillim that my father-in-law, the Rebbe, relayed in the name of his grandfather, the Tzemach Tzedek, and the Alter Rebbe (author of the Shulchan Aruch and Tanya), which one should say during the days of Elul until Yom Kippur, as they are listed in the "Hayom Yom."

In the parsha of Re'eh, which was read yesterday, the Torah says, "See, I have set before you life... therefore choose life." My father-in-law, the Rebbe, explained that by Hashem, blessed be He, telling the Yidden, "choose"—that you should choose Torah and mitzvos, which is the path of life—with this command of "choose," Hashem gives every Yid the strength to be able to withstand the trials he faces from the outside, as well as the arguments of his yetzer hara from within, and to walk in the path of Torah and mitzvos, which gives him long life, good life, and a life of parnassah and success.

It is our custom that from the beginning of Elul, we mention *kesivah v’chasimah tovah*. I wish you, your wife, and your children, *yichyu*, a *kesivah v’chasimah tovah* for a good and sweet year.

I received the donation you sent through the esteemed Rabbi Yosef Weinberg, and I have passed it on to the "Lishkas Chashaim," whose purpose is to help people or institutions in a way that must be done without publicity, so as not to shame them or cause them harm. Such cases of tzedakah are among the highest in the virtue of tzedakah.

**P.S.**

I have just received your regards once again through the esteemed Rabbi Yosef Weinberg, as well as the long letter you wrote to him. Regarding this, I would like to draw your attention to the following:

...You write that you are worried, not being sure if you have fulfilled the wishes of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, and the instructions he gave you at the time regarding how to conduct yourself in business. You feel that perhaps you did not follow them precisely, and because of this, you are concerned that this is causing distress, *chas v’shalom*, in your health and business.

It is certainly unnecessary to emphasize that my father-in-law, the Rebbe, always wanted, and still wants today, only to make Yidden good and satisfied. Consequently, to overthink and have distress, *chas v’shalom*—even if it were as you think, that you did not follow everything as he wrote to you—that because of this one is being punished, *chas v’shalom*—is the exact opposite of how my father-in-law, the Rebbe, always conducted himself and conducts himself today: to help and to benefit others, but under no circumstances to punish, *chas v’shalom*.

My opinion is, therefore, that *bli neder*, several times a week you should study and read the memoirs and the sichos of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, and be strong in *bitachon* that all the blessings that my father-in-law, the Rebbe, gave you will certainly be fulfilled. You will want to, and will be able to, lead your home in the path of Torah and mitzvos even more than before, and to give tzedakah with a generous hand and a happy heart.

With the blessing of *kesivah v’chasimah tovah* for a good and sweet year for him and all his household, *shichyu*.

## 164

B"H, 1 Elul, 5711, Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, and distinguished, etc., our teacher Rabbi Nachman Dov, may he live and be well.

Peace and blessing!

In response to your letter of 26 Menachem Av, in which you inform me that your son, Chaim Dovid Neta, may he live, has celebrated his Bar Mitzvah, I hereby bless you that you should derive from him *Yiddishe nachas* and *Chassidishe nachas* in every detail, and that he may grow toward Torah, *chuppah*, and *maasim tovim* with peace of mind and peace of body...

I was pleased to read in your letter about your teaching a *shiur* to youths and in the *beis medrash*. There is no reason to fear that the study of *Chassidus* is beyond their understanding and grasp, for in these days, the Torah of *Chassidus* has been given in such terms that are understandable to any type of *Bnei Yisrael*. One must simply find the appropriate *maamar* or *sicha*. It is the task of the *mashpia* to find what is suitable according to the level of the listeners, similar to what our Sages said in *Shemos Rabbah* (2:2) regarding Moshe Rabbeinu—how he would seek out the appropriate herbs for each and every type of animal in his flock.

Enclosed is an excerpt from the *sicha* of the *farbrengen* of *Shabbos Mevarchim* Elul. I am certain you will publicize it in an appropriate manner.

Also enclosed is a letter to your son, may he live. If further explanation is needed, I rely on your understanding to explain to him what I have written briefly.

With blessings for success in your *avodah* and blessings for a *Kesivah Vachasimah Tovah*.

**Rabbi Nachman Dov:** Vichnin.

## 165

165

B"H, 1 Elul, 5711, Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

Last week, the Rabbanit... (may she live) was with me and also delivered the letter from your honor (may he live). A few days later, I also spoke with her husband, the Rav (may he live), and it is my hope that my words had an effect on him to be lenient in this matter.

It is worth noting that regarding the method of using *moch* (a barrier), although many of the great rabbis of Hungary are stringent on the matter, the Tzemach Tzedek permitted the placement of *moch* before *tashmish* in a case of danger, as mentioned above, and as explained in his responsa, *Even HaEzer*, siman 89. This is also the case in the responsa of his son, the Admur Rabbi Yisrael Noach (of blessed memory), which is in manuscript.

On this occasion, I wish to express my thanks to your honor, as it appears from the words of the Rabbanit (may she live) that you encouraged her spirit. May it be His will that from here on as well, you will heal not only the bodies of the patients who come to you, but also encourage their spirits and strengthen their trust in Hashem.

It is known that regarding the statement of our Sages that Chizkiyahu hid the Book of Remedies, the Rambam already cautioned that this statement should not be interpreted as being against the science of medicine. He explained that it was a book of *segulos* (Rambam’s Commentary on the Mishnah, *Pesachim*, end of chapter 4; *Moreh Nevuchim*, part 3, chapter 37), and the Torah gave permission (and according to Chassidus, it also means the power) for a doctor to heal.

And although the opinion of the Ibn Ezra (*Shemos* 21:19) is that this applies only to external ailments and not internal ones (see also Ramban in his introduction to his commentary on the Torah and at the beginning of *Parshas Bechukosai*, cited in the *Taz* to *Yoreh Deah*, end of siman 336)—the established *halacha* in Israel is like the Rambam, to utilize medicines and to trust in Hashem that He will send His word—through a certain person and a certain remedy—and heal them.

With blessings for success and a *Kesivah V’Chasimah Tovah*.

#### ***165***

**Use of *moch*:** See above, letter 122, and the references in the notes there. **Ramban... like the Rambam:** See the journal *Yagdil Torah* (N.Y.), issue 36, p. 279, in the name of the Alter Rebbe.

## 166

B"H, 3 Elul, 5711, Brooklyn.

To the great Rabbi, the great Chossid, the G-d-fearing man, who occupies himself with the needs of the community, etc., our teacher Rabbi Avraham Eliyahu, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

I received your letter from 27 Menachem Av, together with the check from the great Chossid, the G-d-fearing man, etc., our teacher Rabbi Chaim Yaakov Gass, may he live. As per your instruction in your previous letter, the receipt has been sent to our teacher Rabbi Naftali Kahana, may he live...

It is my opinion, as I wrote in my previous letter, that you must strengthen yourself in teaching Chassidus in public. It is well known that "many" (*rabim*), meaning when it is found in the plural form, is satisfied even by two, as the minimum of "many" is two (Responsa of Rabbeinu Avraham ben HaRambam, siman 86, siman 110 in the name of his father; and regarding the expression "from the Sages," see the version of the Sdeh Yehoshua in the Yerushalmi, end of Berachos). Even when the expression explicitly means a large group, three are sufficient (Gittin 46a; Yerushalmi Gittin, chapter 8, halacha 6; introduction to Tikkunei Zohar at the beginning). Especially since, with the proper effort, there will surely be many more than three.

With the blessing of *Kesivah V'chasimah Tovah* for a good and sweet year, and good health included in this — and see Rambam, Hilchos Deos, chapter 4, halacha 4.

## 168

B"H, 3 Elul, 5711, Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, learned, and distinguished, etc., Moreinu HaRav Yeshaya, may he live, HaKohen.

Greetings and blessings!

I received your *pidyon nefesh* for the *Chag HaGeulah* in due time, and I read it at the *tziyun* of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, to awaken Divine mercy for you and your household, may they live, for each of them according to their needs. In these days of favor and mercy of the month of Elul, I look forward to hearing good news from you regarding the beginning of the fulfillment of your heart’s desires for the good, concerning the matters you wrote about in your letter and *pidyon nefesh*.

It is well known that one of the acronyms for the month of Elul is "a man to his fellow and gifts to the poor" (*ish l're'ehu u'matanos la'evyonim*). Each one of us is in the category of a "poor person" (*evyon*) in relation to the Holy One, Blessed be He. It is known from our Sages that "He tells His words to Yaakov"—that whatever He commands the Jewish people to do, the Holy One, Blessed be He, does Himself. Surely, He will grant "gifts to the poor" to us all, speedily and in our days.

With blessings for being inscribed and sealed for a good and sweet year.

## 160

B”H, 3 Elul, 5711, Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

I received your letter, in which you ask regarding your wish to enroll your three-year-old daughter in a kindergarten. There is a proposal to enroll her in a kindergarten where the language of instruction is Yiddish, and you are asking for my opinion.

In my view, this is the correct course of action. The primary concern regarding the chinuch of boys and girls in general, and the beginning of their chinuch in particular, is the matter of yiras shamayim. Since everyone agrees that the chinuch there is superior to others in this regard, other considerations should not be taken into account, for everything is batel before the primary objective.

With blessings for a suitable arrangement and good parnassah, both materially and spiritually, and for Yiddishe, Chassidishe nachas from all your children, may they be well, and may you be inscribed and sealed for a good and sweet year.

## 172

B"H, 3 Elul, 5711, Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

I received your letter from 17 Menachem Av, in which you inform me that you are working as a secretary and treasurer in a Charedi settlement named Netivah, but that both you and your wife are dissatisfied with the working and living conditions there, and you ask for my opinion on whether you should arrange things differently.

In my opinion, for the time being, you should remain at your post—and I use the word "post" in both its senses: as a position and source of income, and as in the sense of "guarding" (*shomer* and *shemirah*). This means you should utilize your presence in the aforementioned settlement and your influence upon them to guard the purity of holiness in the daily life of the settlement, to uphold Yiddishkeit, and to disseminate Torah and mitzvos in an appropriate manner. This is the channel through which you will receive your blessings.

Regarding what you wrote—that due to the heavy workload you are unable to set times for Torah study—I am deeply saddened by this. I am even more saddened by the fact that you seem to believe you are justified in your claim that you are unable to do so, for as long as you believe that, you are far from rectifying the situation.

It is clear that the ability has been granted to you; it depends solely on your will, and there is nothing that can stand before the will. This is especially true regarding the matter of setting times for Torah study, both in the revealed Torah and in Chassidus, for which your *neshamah elokis* thirsts and yearns. It is only the "leaven in the dough" that is holding you back. It is obvious that if you only truly desire it, you will find a way and the time to study both the revealed Torah and Chassidus. Before long, you will be amazed at yourself, wondering how you had not done so until now. It is well known that the promise of our Sages is that the success of a Jewish person in general, and a *ben Torah* in particular, depends on his *hiskashrus* and *dveikus* to the Torah of Hashem.

You also inform me that your wife, *tichyeh*, is pregnant. May it be the will of the *Ribono shel Olam* that He fulfill her days of pregnancy and that she give birth properly, in its due time, and may you bring good tidings regarding this.

Enclosed is an excerpt from the *sicha* of the *farbrengen* of *Shabbos Mevarchim* Elul. Please publish it in appropriate language and in a suitable format in your surroundings.

With blessings for a *kesivah v’chasimah tovah* for a good and sweet year.

## 1073

1073

B"H, 3 Elul, 5711, Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

I received your letter from 17 Menachem Av... etc.

Surely you are aware that immediately after Chag HaGeulah, I was written to at great length regarding this matter, using stinging expressions, etc. Consequently, I do not understand what you intended to add in this letter of yours. It is known from our Sages that lashon hara involves three parties: the speaker, the one spoken about, and even the listener. It is also known in the poskim—Hilchos Deos, Chapter 7, Halacha 2, and in many other places—that motzi shem ra applies specifically when the matter is entirely false, whereas lashon hara is different. Therefore, even if we assume that all the things in your letter are accurate and do not contain even a grain of exaggeration, nor even a slight touch of personal bias regarding the writer’s honor, I am still puzzled: what is the purpose of writing this? It is understandable in my case, as I have no choice; I am obligated to read the letters I receive. Similarly, the esteemed Chossid... also had no choice regarding the writing of that letter. But you, your honor, being a person of free choice—as is known from Likutei Torah, Parshas Emor (33b), and as is also explained in the Kuntres of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, printed for the upcoming 18 Elul—a Jewish person, by virtue of being connected to the Atzmus and Mahus of the Ein Sof B"H, is a person of free choice. Therefore, I am surprised at you, for you were given the choice of whether to write or to refrain from doing so, yet you chose specifically to write, and at length, without my seeing any benefit in this, other than the aforementioned damage of lashon hara—and surely your intention in writing is [questionable], after others had already written to me with all the details before you.

In the course of time, perhaps you will also gladden my heart with news of the students' progress in yiras shamayim, in the study of Nigleh and the study of Chassidus. May it be the will of Hashem that, as the end of our galus—which came about, as our Sages say (Yoma 9b), due to the sin of sinas chinam—draws near, Hashem will in return place into the heart of each one of us the matter of ahavas chinam. That is, according to the perspective of one's nefesh habehamis, it is "gratuitous love," since he feels no obligation toward his fellow at all. Furthermore, even regarding the commandment of "Love your fellow as yourself"—which is a great principle of the Torah, etc.—he does not find a basis for obligation in the case at hand, because he does not wish to acknowledge his fellow; on the contrary, he sees in him all [sorts of faults], etc. Yet, despite this, he loves him—and to at least the same measure that the hatred existed which caused the Churban. In these days of mercy and favor, may Hashem grant us the merit to serve Him all together, shoulder to shoulder, as it is written: "Bless us, our Father, all of us as one, with the light of Your countenance." See Tanya, Chapter 32, and in Sefer Derech Mitzvosecha, the Mitzvah of Ahavas Yisrael. And most importantly, in Kuntres Hechalotzu.

With blessings for a kesivah v'chasimah tovah for a good and sweet year, and a year of peace and tranquility.

#### ***1073***

Printed in Likkutei Sichos, Vol. 12, p. 183, and completed based on a copy.

## 174

[3 Elul, 5711]

At the time, he conveyed to me... his regards, as well as his participation in the charity fund. I deposited his contribution into the *Lishkas Chashaim*—a fund used to assist people in need of sustenance without publicity, which is one of the highest levels of the mitzvah of *tzedakah*, as is accepted.

The aforementioned *chossid* also informed me at the time that he had reached the age of 81, may he be blessed with long, good years. May it be Hashem’s will that He bless him with long, good years, and that he may continue to assist in matters of *tzedakah*, the recitation of *Tehillim*, setting fixed times for Torah study, and participating in public *shiurim*. Through all of this, his *dveikus* and *hiskashrus* to Hashem our G-d, the living G-d, will be strengthened, as it is written: "And you who cleave to Hashem your G-d are alive, all of you, today."

Surely you are aware of the custom dating back to the Baal Shem Tov to recite the chapter of *Tehillim* corresponding to one’s age. From now on, you should certainly recite chapter 82 each morning after *davening*, which is also the *Shir Shel Yom* for Tuesday.

It is known from our Sages that "this world" and "the world to come" are referred to in the verse, "He will revive us after two days." The conclusion of the verse—"on the third day He will raise us up, and we will live before Him"—refers to the world that will exist after the coming of *Mashiach Tzidkeinu*, the world of the resurrection, which is even higher than the "world to come," i.e., *Gan Eden*.

In terms of *avodah*, "this world" represents the realm of businesspeople, whose primary occupation is in the affairs of this world, yet their conduct is according to Torah—this is the *avodah* of the tribe of Zevulun. "The world to come" represents the realm of Torah scholars and those who dwell in the tents of Torah, whose primary occupation is the study of Torah—this is the *avodah* of the tribe of Yissachar. "The third day" represents the *avodah* of both together; that is, the soul and the body participate with equal *hispaalus* in the service of Hashem. This is similar to *Adam HaRishon* before the sin, for whom there was no distinction between body and soul, as it is written, "and they were not ashamed." In this manner, "I will remove the spirit of impurity from the earth," and the body will be even more elevated than the soul, which is the ultimate intent.

In each and every one of us, a semblance of this can be achieved even now. This means that we should serve Hashem in the affairs of the body without feeling any bodily gratification from it. This is even higher than the *avodah* of "in all your ways know Him." In old age, when the desires of the body have weakened and one is closer to the truth, it is easier to attain this level of *avodah*.

May it be Hashem’s will that he continues to flourish in old age, full of sap and richness, and that he may experience much *nachas* and *taanug* in his service of Hashem, with peace of mind and peace of body.

## 175

B"H, 3 Elul, 5711, Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

I received your letter in due time, along with the *pidyon nefesh* enclosed within. When I was at the *tziyun* of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, I read the *pidyon nefesh*, and he will surely arouse Divine mercy for each of them according to their needs.

Regarding the letter you sent: I have already spoken on this matter. If our Sages, of blessed memory, said in general that leadership is not about authority, but rather about servitude—and this applies to all appointments among the Jewish people—then how much more so is this true in this case, which is a matter connected to the *nefesh, ruach, neshamah, chayah,* and *yechidah*, and even to the essence of the soul (as it is known that even the *chayah* and *yechidah* are names given to it, and not the essence itself). Consequently, one is putting everything on the line—both the writer and the recipient of the letter.

May it be the will of Hashem that all of us together, each according to his standing and situation, merit to fulfill our *shlichus* in this world with peace of mind and peace of body, and with true expansion. As is explained in the *maamar* of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, for Chai Elul—which is currently in print—true expansion is the expansion of *taanug*, and the revelations that come through understanding and comprehension will be connected to that essential expansion.

The time has already come for it to be evident in your surroundings that one of the students of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, is present there, and that the *maayanos* are being spread *chutzah*. I am interested to hear of your efforts in this regard; the saying of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, is well known: a covenant is made with *ta'amulah* (outreach) that it does not return empty-handed.

Enclosed is an excerpt from a *farbrengen* *sicha* from the Shabbos of Elul. You will surely endeavor to publicize this in an appropriate manner.

With blessings for being inscribed and sealed for a good and sweet year.

It is understood that you must strive to implement what I wrote to you regarding conduct in general, and *shalom bayis* in particular, especially regarding *shalom bayis*, with vigor and extra depth. Furthermore, without a vow, you should recite the chapter *Lamnatzeach Yaancha* every night before *Krias Shema*. After you finish the entire chapter, repeat the verse *Yaancha* once more, and while doing so, contemplate that it should be Hashem’s will as if you had intended all the *kavanos* associated with it.

With blessings that you should report good news and be inscribed and sealed for a good year, for you and your household, may they live.

B"H, 5 Elul, 5711, Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the students of the Torah institutions in general, and the yeshiva students in particular, may Hashem grant them life.

Peace and blessing!

As we approach the beginning of the study term, which comes upon us and all of Israel for good and for blessing, I send you my warm and heartfelt blessing: May He who grants man wisdom, understanding, and knowledge shine His countenance upon you, and may the beginning—and the entire year of study—be successful in every detail.

Every single action of the sons and daughters of Israel must have a desired intent and purpose. Even the vacation days that have just passed have an intent and purpose: to renew your strength and increase your courage so that you may continue—or, for those beginning, to start—the study of Torah and proper education in yiras shamayim with greater diligence and greater vitality.

It is my hope, and my prayer, that you will bring from potential into actuality the diligence, perseverance, and vitality required to acquire the Torah, which is a Torah of life, from the mouth of the Living G-d, an inheritance for the people of Israel, of whom it is said, "And you who cleave to Hashem your G-d are all alive today."

And especially in these days of the month of Elul—the month that my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, was accustomed to calling "the month of accounting," an accounting of the year that is passing and departing, and good resolutions for the future—my confidence is strong that you will make a true accounting of what is appropriate to change for the better and to rectify regarding your conduct and order in the past, so that from here on, your study and your conduct will be of the highest quality, for your benefit both materially and spiritually.

I sign with the blessing of *kesivah v’chasimah tovah* for a good and sweet year for each and every one of you, for your parents, may they live, for your educators, may they live, and for the directors of your institutions, may they live,

**M. Schneerson**

## 178

178

B.H., 5 Elul, 5711, Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and blessings!

I have received your letter, in which you write that, thank G-d, you have been spared from emotional distress until now. I hope, in accordance with my letter of 13 Nissan, that you will continue to be spared from any harm or emotional distress, G-d forbid, and that you will be able to report good news regarding this.

I was also very pleased to read in your letter that you have exerted yourself to ensure that a designated sum from the money remaining from the Jewish organization be allocated to our yeshivos in Morocco. It is difficult to describe in words the great merit one acquires by participating in the *avodas* of *chinuch* in Morocco, especially since, given the local living conditions, one can accomplish great things with relatively small sums. On the other hand, the responsibility for our brothers in Morocco is far greater, considering that the spiritual soil there is prepared; one does not need to come and fight for the idea of *chinuch hakasher*, but on the contrary, **they** come and demand, with a spiritual claim, that a *chinuch hakasher* be organized for them to save their children. And they demand, with justification, why they are not being given the full opportunity for this.

Just as in the case of material *tzedakah*, where the responsibility of the *mitzvah* of *tzedakah* is great even when one goes to the poor person, the responsibility is all the greater when the poor person comes forward, tells of his situation, and demands—even if only through his silence—why he is not being helped.

In the same way, and with even greater intensity, this applies to spiritual *tzedakah*. When one gives life to a Jewish child through Torah and *mitzvos*, one is not only bringing him to life in the World to Come, but is also making his life a happy one in this world.

I was also interested to read in your letter about the possibility and necessity of working for *chinuch hakasher* in Holland. Regarding this, please turn directly to our office in Paris and to our representative, the esteemed Rabbi, the *chossid*, who is involved in communal needs, etc., Rabbi Binyamin Gorodetzky, *sheyichyeh*. However, one does not divert funds from one *tzedakah* to another, nor does one mix one joy with another; therefore, the money designated for the work in Morocco must go there. I hope that you will be able to find enough interested people on the spot to conduct the local *chinuch* work without being hindered by a lack of financial resources. A portion of the income can also be built upon tuition, and the main thing is that, as you write, after the first year there will be a possibility to include this work in the Dutch United Jewish Appeal.

Since I will, G-d willing, be at the *tziyun* of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, on Chai Elul and Erev Rosh Hashanah, if you send me the names (along with the mothers' names) of yourself and all your family members, *sheyichyu*, I will mention them when I am at the *tziyun* for whatever they may need.

I conclude with the wish that everything should be well with your wife, and that her pregnancy and birth should be at the proper time and with ease, and that together with her you may raise all your children to Torah, to the *chuppah*, and to good deeds.

With the blessing of *Kesivah v'Chasimah Tovah* for a good and sweet year.

Enclosed is an excerpt from the *sicha* of Shabbos Mevarchim Rosh Chodesh Elul, which you will surely utilize in the appropriate manner.
