## 181

B"H, 8 Elul, 5711, Brooklyn.

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, and learned R' Yitzchak Meir, may he live:

Peace and blessing!

I have received your letter from Erev Shabbos Kodesh Parshas Re'eh, in which you write that you are a kashrus supervisor at a Joint Distribution Committee home for the elderly, and that you find it difficult to implement what you wish, as not everyone is willing to follow your instructions. You ask whether you should move on to occupy yourself with [...].

My opinion is that since Hashem has granted you such a position, where you can help ensure that the home for the elderly is conducted with kashrus, and I am certain that your presence there will allow you to exert influence—not only that what is put into the stomach should be kosher, but also that what is put into the mind should be kosher—I believe you should not leave this position. I am certain that if you seek counsel, you will find appropriate ways to influence those upon whom the implementation of your instructions depends. The reward for ensuring that the home for the elderly is conducted in purity is difficult to estimate, and therefore I am certain that this will bring you blessing and success in your personal matters, as well as nachas from your children, may they live.

With blessings for a *ksivah v'chasimah tovah* for a good and sweet year.

P.S. Enclosed is an excerpt from the sicha of Shabbos Kodesh Mevarchim Elul, and surely you will be able to utilize this in an appropriate manner among the residents of the home for the elderly, may they live.

## 182

B”H, 8 Elul, 5711, Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and blessings!

You surely received my previous letter in due time. I am writing now regarding the matter of drawing hearts closer together, as you are surely preparing during these days to return to the city... I do not know if you have sensed this, but I am endeavoring to bring your heart and the heart of the one about whom you wrote to me—albeit by allusion—closer together. It seems to me that now, at the beginning of the study season and during these days of favor and mercy, it is an opportune time to draw hearts closer, more and more.

I do not know who should take the first step in this: whether it should be the seed of Aharon, whose trait was to love the creations and draw them near, as explained at length in Avos D’Rabbi Nosson, or the Jewish person who must honor the Kohen and swiftly bring peace into the world, as per the statement of Rabbi Yehuda ben Teima, "swift as a deer." But let it be as it may, provided that there is peace upon Yisrael. I thank you in advance if you will bring me good tidings in this regard.

Enclosed is a collection regarding Chabad public communal work, which will surely interest you. The ruling of our Sages is well known—and is also brought in Shulchan Aruch, Orach Chaim—regarding the greatness of one who occupies himself with the needs of the public. I would add, as a witty remark, based on what I saw in Midrash Rabbah (Shemos Rabbah 6:2), that Rabbi Yehoshua ben Levi forgot many, many halachos. But our Sages immediately wrote the remedy alongside it: that these were halachos related to death and burial. This can be connected to the two opinions in Kesuvos 103b regarding what is greater: the deed of Chanina, who was able to restore the Torah through his pilpul, or the deed of Chiya, who ensured from the outset that the Torah would not be forgotten. The Gemara concludes how much greater the deed of Chiya is.

With blessings for a *kesivah v’chasimah tovah* for a good and sweet year.

## 183

B"H, 9 Elul, 5711, Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the Executive Committee of Agudas Chasidei Chabad in Eretz Yisrael, may it be rebuilt and established, may they live.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of 19 Menachem Av and those preceding it:

I was pleased to read in your letter that you have begun to prepare a practical work plan. You propose various details regarding your future work and ask for my opinion on these suggestions.

In my view, given the situation of Chassidei Chabad in Eretz Yisrael as I envision it, the Chassidim there generally divide into several categories: a) Various institutions, such as the yeshivos, the Kollel, etc., where each must necessarily possess a certain degree of autonomy; b) Individuals and private persons of various types, such as Rabbonim, shochtim, young people, etc.; c) All of Anash as one unified body.

Therefore, in my opinion, the role of Agudas Chasidei Chabad (Aguch) should be: (a) To represent Anash in various matters pertaining to category (c) above—namely, matters that do not belong to a private institution or a specific segment of Anash. (b) To coordinate the work of the institutions so as to prevent conflicts and confusion in each other’s work. (c) General oversight of the institutions, without interfering in their internal affairs. (d) General oversight of the various segments of Anash, such as the young people who have organized into the Tzeirei Agudas Chasidei Chabad independently, as well as the Neshei Chabad organization, which will surely also organize into a separate division, as I suggested in one of my previous letters. ([e]) To be alert to everything happening in Eretz Yisrael, to offer suggestions, and to take the initiative for new activities required by the times, such as the rescue of immigrant children, etc. To ensure there are no objections to the decisions and actions of Aguch, it is appropriate that the Executive Committee include at least one representative from each institution (even in its current composition, this condition is met, as it includes representatives of the Tomchei Temimim yeshivos, Toras Emes, the Kollel, the Kfar, the young people, etc.).

Among the urgent matters currently on the agenda are: a) To utilize the auspicious day of Chai Elul appropriately, in a way that will bring great benefit in general, and to Anash in Eretz Yisrael in particular.

b) To utilize the coming month of Tishrei for the dissemination of the wellsprings as widely as possible. c) Guidance for everyone in connection with the seventh year, the Shmittah year, both regarding arranging the acquisition of items that have no concern of Shevi'is, and in disseminating knowledge of the laws of Shevi'is, and the like. d) A most important matter, which I have already noted in my previous letter: although the time for it has in any case passed (as, according to my information, they were supposed to be in Paris on September 13), I am raising it again for the record—namely, to represent Anash before the head of the Joint [Distribution Committee] from here, who visited Eretz Yisrael recently, and who surely fulfilled my request and suggestion in this regard. I look forward to good news. e) In connection with the above, there must surely be publicity in the press and periodicals; naturally, this is also included in the work of Aguch in general.

Regarding your suggestion to divide the work among the committee members and your question as to whom I find most suitable for the various fields: it is difficult for me to express an opinion on this from a distance. In general, I do not know if it is worthwhile to restrict the methods of work in advance and then fit the committee members into that restriction. It seems more appropriate to do the opposite: take into account the talents of the committee members and arrange the work in such a way that the members' talents are utilized one hundred percent. Surely there are among them those who are more capable of representing Aguch externally, and it would be appropriate to entrust this entire field to them. Those more capable of organizing internal work should be entrusted with that work across all departments. Those more capable of publicity, whether oral or written, should naturally be entrusted with publicity in all areas, and so on.

The conclusion from all the above:

(a) In order to avoid opposition from existing institutions, Aguch should not interfere in their internal affairs. In this way, the institutions will remain in direct connection with here, and only in matters shared between them and other institutions will they turn to Aguch to connect and resolve matters.

(b) Among the most urgent matters is the work plan to utilize Chai Elul and the coming month of Tishrei.

Enclosed is a copy of my letter to the Tzeirei Agudas Chasidei Chabad committee; you will surely assist them in the matters incumbent upon them that are their special responsibility.

Sent separately is an excerpt from my sicha of Shabbos Mevarchim Chodesh Elul, which is worth publishing in an appropriate manner in the widest possible circles.

I look forward to your prompt response to this letter.

I sign with the blessing of *Kesivah V'chasimah Tovah* for a good and sweet year for each one of them, with everything they need.

**M. Schneerson**

## 184

B”H, 9 Elul, 5711, Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the Committee of Tzeirei Agudas Chabad, may they live:

Greetings and blessings!

It was with pleasure and joy that I read the minutes of your meeting, in which you are already drafting a plan for practical work. And while joy takes hold of my heart on one hand, weeping takes hold of my heart on the other, as there are many who are missing from the list of participants. However, it is my hope that in time, these, too, will join you. And the Holy One, Blessed be He, found no vessel that holds blessing for Israel other than peace. Naturally, they should join you without having to compromise on fundamental matters.

Regarding the present, I have come to urge you regarding the bright and clear day, the upcoming 18th of Elul. I am certain you will utilize it with the energy and vitality characteristic of the youth to disseminate the concept of the Baal Shem Tov and the Alter Rebbe—whose birthday, in both a spiritual and physical sense, is this 18th day—and to spread this idea in the widest circles, even those who for the time being are still far from our own environment. The saying of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, is well known regarding the distinction between the *olam’she* (the "world-people") and Chabad: the order of the great ones of the *olam’she* was that they would sit in their homes and in their places, and anyone who yearned for Torah would come to them to enjoy the radiance of their Torah. This is not so from the Baal Shem Tov and onwards; they established the order where the Baal Shem Tov would travel around to the towns, not waiting for people to come to him and say, "We are thirsty for the word of Hashem." Rather, he, in his own honor and person, would wear out his shoes from place to place, from city to city, and from village to village, and would disseminate the Torah of the words of the living G-d (Sefer HaSichos, Summer 5700, Acharon Shel Pesach, at the day’s meal).

2) To organize a work plan on how to utilize the upcoming month of Tishrei, as mentioned above, by traveling to various places in Eretz Yisrael—may it be rebuilt and established—whether during the Days of Awe or during the days of our festival (Sukkos). The main thing is that it should be done in an organized manner, and in a way that encompasses the largest possible areas and the greatest number of men, women, and children.

3) Special attention in all of the above is required for our brethren from Yemen, Persia, etc., who on one hand have, for the time being, no knowledge of the Chassidic movement, its Torah, and its ways, yet on the other hand are highly capable—by virtue of their fear of Heaven and their connection to the study of Kabbalah and faith in *tzaddikim*—of accepting every truth they are taught in the Torah of *Chassidus* that has been bequeathed to us by our Rebbes, the holy leaders, of blessed memory.

I am interested in knowing the details of the plan you have presented to yourselves regarding this. It would be most appropriate that you consult on the above with the directors of Agudas Chassidei Chabad. Although a large portion of the aforementioned work, which involves the rigors of travel and requires great energy and vitality, rests upon the shoulders of the youth, on the other hand, since our Sages have said that the destruction of the elders is a building, then all the more so is the building of the elders a true building.

For the time being, I do not have sufficient means at my disposal to cover the expenses associated with this work. However, as my desire to participate from here as well in the expenses of such a lofty matter is strong, and since it is not possible for several reasons to send money from here, I am enclosing a certificate for parcels, and our Sages have said that something of value is like money.

In a separate envelope, I am sending you a segment from the *sicha* of Shabbos Mevarchim Chodesh Elul, as well as a booklet regarding Chabad public activity that was just published. All of this is being sent via airmail; please be kind enough to acknowledge receipt of the above.

With the blessing of *Kesivah V’chasimah Tovah* to all the members, may they live, to them, their households, and all that is theirs; may they all stand ready for blessing for a good and sweet year.

Awaiting good tidings.

## 195

B”H, 9 Elul, 5711, Brooklyn.

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, and learned man, who occupies himself with communal needs, etc., R’ Nachum Dov, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

I was pleased by the visit of your sons and daughters, may they live, to me, and especially by the regards they conveyed from you (as well as the *pidyon nefesh*).

When I visit the *tziyun* of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, I will read your *pidyon nefesh*. I am certain that he will arouse great mercies so that the request you write in the *pidyon nefesh* will be fulfilled soon, and that you will be able to write and share good news regarding this yourself.

Surely you know that during this month of Elul, my father-in-law, the Rebbe, used to call it the "month of accounting." Hashem has given it to us all to make an accounting of the previous year and also to accept good resolutions for the coming year, which approaches us and all of Israel for good and for blessing.

It is stated in the *Midrash* that whatever Hashem commands the Jewish people to do, He does Himself as well. Consequently, it is understood that in this month of mercy—Elul—Hashem also makes an accounting of all the good things that Jews have done over the course of the past months of the year. (One does not make an accounting of bad deeds, for surely Jews will do *teshuvah*, and as a result, those bad deeds are erased and no trace of them remains.) However, the good deeds, which remain forever—from the beginning of the month of Elul, an accounting is made of them. And Hashem, who is the ultimate good, makes this accounting with a "generous eye," preparing to give all Jews from His full, holy, open, and wide hand everything they need. And needless to say, for those Jews who accept upon themselves good resolutions for the coming year, Hashem includes this in the accounting as well, which increases the merit and the reward for the merits that the Jew possesses.

Last year, with Hashem’s help, you increased the *gemilas chasadim* fund and also brought in *Sifrei Torah*, and you also supported religious educational institutions. This is a merit that is connected to the many. Beyond your private matters in Torah and *mitzvos* that you perform individually, I am therefore confident that Hashem has included all of this in the accounting and will increase for you from His measure of kindness and mercy. He will grant you a *kesivah v’chasimah tovah* for a good and sweet year, which includes good health, and may you be able to ascend in the study of Torah, in *tzedakah*, and in *tefillah* with the *tzibur*.

Your children, may they live, will convey personal regards from me to you. I wish to mention here what I conveyed orally and requested: that you should organize a Chassidishe *farbrengen*, once or several times. Surely, at a Chassidishe gathering, one will be aroused with *ahavas Yisrael*, *ahavas haTorah*, and *ahavas Hashem*, and they will also bless you with long, good days and years.

With the blessing of proper health for a good and sweet year.

Enclosed is the receipt for the *pidyon nefesh* funds.

***

**R’ Nachum Dov:** Denburg.

## 186

B"H, 9 Elul, 5711, Brooklyn, N.Y.

Blessings and peace!

I have received your letter of September 8, and I was pleased to read in it that you, too, are noticing, as you write in your letter, that your son is improving and is calmer, which Dr. Wilder has also stated.

As I have told you before, since the Rebbe, my father-in-law, gave his blessing that your son will be healthy, he will certainly keep his word. It is only a question of time.

It is undoubtedly difficult to wait, especially for the parents of an only son.

However, when one is strong in bitachon that the blessing will be fulfilled, it helps in two ways: it is, in the meantime, much easier to wait until one sees it in actuality, and the stronger the bitachon, the sooner the fulfillment of the tzaddik’s promise arrives.

I hope that you will be strong in bitachon, even stronger than until now, and this also strengthens my certainty that you will soon see that your son is doing much better and better in all respects.

Since you write that your son, may he live and be well, is already going to school, I hope to hear that you are receiving good reports about him.

I conclude with the wish of *kesivah v’chasimah tovah* for you, your husband, and your son, may he live and be well, for a good and sweet year.

B"H, 12 Elul, 5711, Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

I have received your letter from Sunday, stating that you are all, thank G-d, in good health, and requesting a blessing for your son who is in military service.

When I am at the Tziyun of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, I will mention him for what he needs.

If it is not possible for him to put on tefillin in the morning, he should do so at any time during the day until sunset. May Hashem protect him so that he remains whole.

In connection with the fact that you are the shaliach tzibbur for Rosh Hashanah and Yom Kippur, in particular, I would like to emphasize that my father-in-law, the Rebbe, desired that those who daven as shaliach tzibbur at the amud—especially during the Yomim Noraim—should review the meaning of the words, as well as the meaning of the piyutim.

Furthermore, at the very least, one should immerse in the mikveh on Erev Rosh Hashanah and Erev Yom Kippur.

Needless to say, all of this is in addition to the halachos and matters found in the Shulchan Aruch, regarding which it is unnecessary to urge you.

Your donation has been turned over to the Lishkas Chashaim, which assists individuals and institutions quietly and without publicity, so as not to cause them embarrassment. May the merit of this tzedakah stand for you and your family, that you may all have a kesivah v’chasimah tovah for a good and sweet year.

With blessings.

## 188

188

B.H., 12 Elul, 5711, Brooklyn.

To the esteemed and distinguished individuals, who toil faithfully in the holy work, the administrators of Yeshivas Achei Temimim Lubavitch in Dorchester-Boston, may they live:

Shalom u’vracha!

It was with great satisfaction that I received your letter informing me that next week you will be celebrating the Chanukas HaBayis, which coincides with the beginning of the new semester of study at the Yeshiva.

I would like to express my blessing to all the members of the administration, as well as to the Roshei Yeshiva and teachers, and to all those who have helped and continue to help, both materially and spiritually, that Hashem Yisbarach should bless them all in all their personal and communal matters.

It is a well-known teaching of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, which he would often repeat, based on the principle of our Sages that the Holy One, Blessed be He, rewards measure for measure. Consequently, for all those who work to bring Jews closer to our Father in Heaven—for all Jews are called His children—the Almighty, blessed be He, rewards them many times over, so that they may have much nachas, true Jewish nachas, from their own children, from their household, and from themselves.

The concept of a Chanukas HaBayis is that a person finds themselves in their home with all their belongings and all their characteristics, which the home encompasses—both the external and the internal. The home must protect them from various things that could, Heaven forbid, cause them harm. This is true to an even greater extent regarding a Yeshiva. It is certain that a Yeshiva, and especially a Lubavitcher Yeshiva, is not merely for teaching the students a specific subject; rather, it is primarily to raise them to be complete Jews in all their affairs, and also to protect them from the various winds that blow from all sides in the world—today with even greater intensity and malice—which seek, Heaven protect us, to tear Jewish children away from their source, which is Torah and mitzvos, that connect us to the Holy One, Blessed be He.

I am certain, based on the blessings that my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, bestowed upon Yeshivas Achei Temimim Lubavitch in Dorchester-Boston, that it will proceed along this aforementioned path: to raise students to be complete Jews, whether they are at home or walking in the street, whether they are in the Yeshiva or leaving the Yeshiva. I would also like to add my blessing that Hashem Yisbarach should help you so that the number of students increases more and more, such that very soon you will be able to say that the current space is insufficient and that an even larger building than the present one is required.

I conclude with the blessing of a Kesivah V’Chasimah Tovah for a good and sweet year to all those who work with this holy institution and its friends, materially and spiritually alike.

#### 188

**Chanukas HaBayis:** See above, letter 125.

## 189

189

B"H, 12 Elul, 5711, Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Rabbi, the Chassid, the G-d-fearing man, who engages in communal needs, etc., Moreinu HaRav Asher, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

In response to your notification that on the 8th of Elul, three years were completed for the child Mordechai Ze'ev ben Rizel, son of our dear friend, Moreinu HaRav Chaim Schneur Zalman, may he live, I hereby express my blessing that his parents raise him to Torah, to the chuppah, and to good deeds, in prosperity.

And this is the language of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, regarding the matter of the haircut at three years:

"...And regarding the cutting of the hair — *upsherinish* — it is a great thing in the custom of Israel, and its essence is in the chinuch of leaving the *pe'os* of the head. And from the day of the cutting and the leaving of the *pe'os* of the head, it is customary to be meticulous in accustoming the child to the wearing of *tzitzis katan*, the morning blessings, *birchas hamazon*, and *krias shema* before retiring. May Hashem be their help that they raise him to Torah, to the chuppah, and to good deeds, with ample livelihood and peace of mind, both materially and spiritually."

Signed with the blessing of *Kesivah V'chasimah Tovah* for a good and sweet year,

**M. Schneerson**

P.S. Regarding what you noted in your letter, that you are in doubt as to whether one fulfills the mitzvah of the *Arba Minim* in your country, since the government has decreed that any fruit arriving in Australia without a health certificate is confiscated, and only because the official acts on his own initiative to permit handing it over to the owners for the days of the holiday on the condition that they return it to him after the holiday for burning—a practice that has been permitted there for a long time—you are concerned that since, due to the government decree, the fruit is forbidden for consumption and must be destroyed, and the official is only acting beyond the letter of the law, there is therefore neither a status of ownership nor a permit for consumption.

Time does not permit an extensive discussion on this, but in my opinion, there is no room for concern. I will mention only two of the reasons:

1) The prohibition is not on the *esrog* itself, but rather the prohibition is on the location. A parallel to this: is it permitted to make a blessing on an *esrog* in the Beis Hamikdash, given that eating *chullin* is forbidden there? From the plain language of the Mishnah, it is clear that they would make a blessing on the *esrog* and *lulav* even in the Beis Hamikdash. The reason is that it is not that the *esrog* is forbidden for consumption, but rather that in the Beis Hamikdash it is forbidden to eat *chullin*. Similarly, in the case at hand, the *esrog* is not inherently subject to burning; rather, in the country of Australia, it is forbidden to keep fruits from abroad without a certificate.

2) It is clear that there is a status of ownership here for many matters. For instance, if the owner of the *esrog* wishes to leave the country of Australia, they certainly would not prevent him from taking the *esrog* with him. The same applies to the matter of the permit for consumption: if, immediately upon bringing the *esrog* into the country, a person wished to "destroy" it by eating it, it is seemingly clear that they would permit him to do so, provided he assumes responsibility for its health safety.

#### ***189***

From a photocopy of the letter. **Moreinu HaRav Asher:** Abramson. Further letters to him — above 881, and in the references noted there. **Mordechai Ze'ev, may he live:** Gutnick.

## 191

B"H,

The significance of the days of Chai Elul and the three days of Selichos was explained in the introduction to the Kuntres Chai Elul 5705, based on what I found in the writings of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe. I also transcribed there these letters regarding the nature of the avodah of these days, from Chai Elul onwards.

Regarding the effect of the day of Chai Elul itself upon our avodah—my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, stated in the name of the elder Chassidim that Chai Elul is the day that infused, and continues to infuse, vitality into Elul.

* * *

Elul is the month of accounting for the year that has passed, and the month of preparation for the year to come.

It can be said that for this reason, the essential categories of man’s avodah—in which there must be repentance and rectification for the past, and firm resolutions for the future—are hinted at in the name of this month.

As our Sages say: Elul is an acronym for *“Anah L’yado V’samti L’cha”* (Exodus 21:13), referring to the cities of refuge. In the avodah of man, this is the **line of Torah**, for the words of Torah provide refuge.

Elul is an acronym for *“Ani L’dodi V’dodi Li”* (Song of Songs 6:3)—the **line of avodah**, which is tefillah. Especially in these days of ours, when we have nothing but the “avodah of the heart,” which is tefillah, which binds and connects Yisrael to their Father in Heaven.

Elul is an acronym for *“Ish L’re’ehu U’matanos La’evyonim”* (Esther 9:22)—the **line of gemilus chasadim**.

And as a preface and foundation for all these lines:

Elul is an acronym for *“(U’mal Hashem Elokecha) Es Levavcha V’es Levav (Zarecha)”* (Deuteronomy 30:6)—the **concept of teshuvah**.

* * *

There have been many paths to infuse vitality into a person’s avodah to their Creator. But in these final generations, the *ikvesa d’meshicha*, where the concealments and darkness have multiplied and the world is shrouded in a double and redoubled darkness, this is the path for the many and for the individual—a path paved by our Rebbes, the Nesi’im—to attain true life in the avodah of Hashem: through engagement in the inner dimensions of Torah, the *nishmata d’oraysa*, in general, and the teachings of Chassidus in particular.

Chai Elul is the birthday of the founder of the general teachings of Chassidus—the Baal Shem Tov—and the birthday of the founder of Chabad Chassidus—our Rebbe the Alter Rebbe.

These revelations are renewed and reawakened every single year on this day.

By studying their teachings and walking in the ways of Chassidus that they have instructed for all Bnei Yisrael, one infuses a soul and vitality into all categories of avodah; one infuses *Chai* (life) into *Elul*: in teshuvah, in Torah, in avodah, and in gemilus chasadim.

Through all of this, one also brings about the Geulah, as is also hinted at in the acronym of Elul, and as our Sages say:

Elul is an acronym for *“L’Hashem Vayomru L’emor Ashira”* (Exodus 15:1)—for then all the sparks will emerge from exile, through Mashiach Tzidkeinu, speedily in our days, Amen.

**Menachem Schneerson**
13 Elul, 5711, Brooklyn, N.Y.

## 192

B"H, 13 Elul, 5711, Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, etc., R' Y., may he live:

Greetings and blessings!

Enclosed is the *kuntres* for the upcoming Chai Elul. May you merit to share it with all those under your influence, bringing them the light of Torah and the "light within the Torah" contained in this *kuntres*.

I have briefly noted in my introduction to the *kuntres*, based on a saying of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, that the effect of Chai Elul is to infuse vitality into all areas of a person’s *avodah*, including the path of Torah study.

This requires further explanation, based on the Sages' teaching: "If one merits, it becomes for him a potion of life; if one does not merit, it becomes for him a potion of death." Although the words of Torah are compared to fire—and therefore cannot contract *tumah*—this means that the Torah itself cannot contract *tumah*. However, regarding its effect upon the person, if he does not merit, it becomes for him as stated, as the Sages precisely phrased it: it becomes for **him**.

Now, learning in a way that one "does not merit"—Torah without *yiras shamayim*, studying Torah while forgetting the Giver of the Torah, which naturally allows for studying without the intent to fulfill—is possible only when the study does not engage with the love of Hashem, His fear, His oneness, etc. This is especially true when the study is clothed in the matters of this world and its materiality. This is not the case, however, with the study of the *pnimiyus* of Torah, which is called the "Tree of Life." This study does not come in the form of "clothing" [the Torah] to clarify sparks; rather, it engages in the ways of loving Hashem, fearing Him, and His oneness, or in knowing the *Seder Hishtalshelus*, through which one comes to love and fear Him. This is what brings one to a "whole heart," and one lives through them in his Torah study. Since it serves as the *neshamah* for the external aspects of Torah, it brings vitality even to the study of the revealed Torah. This is especially true of the teachings of the Baal Shem Tov, which our holy Rebbes, may they rest in peace, have bequeathed to us, "revealing and explaining the greatness and exaltation of Hashem, etc." As our Alter Rebbe wrote in *Iggeres HaKodesh*, "that knowledge of the reality of the *Hishtalshelus*, etc., brings one to a 'whole heart,' etc., which is the main thing, etc."

Especially in these days, when we all pray, "My heart says to You, 'Seek My face,'" to search for the inwardness of the heart—which is achieved through "Your face, Hashem, I will seek"—there must be engagement in the love of Hashem and His fear, and in the study and *hisbonenus* that lead to this.

This is the best preparation for the continuation and revelation of "Hashem is my light"—on Rosh Hashanah—"and my salvation"—on Yom Kippur—to be inscribed and sealed for a good year, with good that is visible and revealed, both physically and spiritually.

With blessings for a *kesivah v'chasimah tovah*,

**M. Schneerson**

For the end of our exile and the coming of Moshiach Tzidkeinu is near.

## 195

B”H, 15 Elul, 5711, Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the Administration of Yeshivas Tomchei Temimim
Lubavitch, Montreal, Canada, may Hashem protect them
May they live

Peace and blessing!

It was with pleasure that I read the minutes of the committee meeting held on 18 Menachem Av, and I was happy to see that you have already begun the actual work, and that you are gradually bringing to life the matters we discussed when you were here.

Regarding the details: concerning what you discussed at your meeting regarding the Yeshiva’s deficit, I already told you during our conversation here that until now you have attempted the method of Tzimtzum—that is, adjusting expenses to match income. It would be appropriate now to try the opposite approach: to exert effort in increasing the income to match the expenses that ought to be. This is especially true in light of the adage of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, which he quoted in the name of his father, the Rebbe Maharash: "The world says that if you cannot go under, you must go over; but I say that one should go over from the outset," with the appropriate strength.

Regarding what you wrote in the minutes about recruiting new students, and that you have spoken with the directors of HIAS about them sending the children of refugees to your Yeshiva: surely you will not rely on this alone, but will also personally oversee this matter without waiting for an *is'arusa d'leila* [awakening from above] from the directors of HIAS...

With blessings for outstanding success in your holy work in the field of proper chinuch, and may the blessing of Hashem—which my father-in-law, the Rebbe, has bestowed and continues to bestow upon you—rest upon each and every one of you, granting you blessing and success in your personal affairs as well.

I sign with blessings for a *kesivah v'chasimah tovah* for a good and sweet year.

## 196

196

B"H, 16 Elul, 5711, Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, and learned, etc., Moreinu HaRav Yosef Yehuda, may he live.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of 9 Elul, in which you describe your daily schedule and conclude with a question: because you are accustomed to davening slowly, you find yourself lacking in the matter of davening with a minyan, and sometimes even in the timing of davening:

**Response**: The conduct of Chassidim in this regard is well-known, and it was frequently based on the instruction of our Nesi'im, our holy Rebbes. Regarding davening with a minyan, they were accustomed to hearing Barechu, Kedushah (and the reading of the Torah) with the minyan, and afterwards they would daven with *m'tinus* (deliberation) and sometimes even at length. It is also well-known the explanation brought in *Kovetz HaTmimim* in the name of the Ovrucher, son of the Admur the Tzemach Tzedek, that the concept of davening with a minyan is that one gathers and unites all the powers—the ten powers of his soul—in the matter of davening...

You will surely gather on the upcoming Chai Elul, and you should also publicize the content of the excerpt from the *sicha* of Shabbos Mevarchim Elul in an appropriate manner.

And regarding your collecting on behalf of Beis Rivkah, you are surely aware of the saying of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, who said to the *meshulachim* and *shadarim*: "One should collect *gashmius* (materiality) and sow *ruchnius* (spirituality)." May Hashem grant you great success in this twofold work.

With blessings for a *kesivah v'chasimah tovah* for you and your entire household, may they live, for a good and sweet year.

#### ***196***

**Moreinu HaRav Yosef Yehuda:** Hen.

## 197

B"H, 16 Elul, 5711, Brooklyn.

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, and distinguished R' Shmuel Gedalya, may he live:

Peace and blessing!

It was with pleasure that I read your letter of 5 Elul, in which you describe your service in the army, as well as your activities there regarding the strengthening of Yiddishkeit and influencing your peers and surroundings toward yiras shamayim.

I derived great pleasure from reading the details of this, for the magnitude of such a matter cannot be described in writing. You are fulfilling a most significant shlichus, the extent of which is beyond our comprehension. Yet, considering the great value of your actions in this regard, it is fair to say that even if you had come to the army solely for this purpose, it would be enough. Once you fulfill your role in this, you will surely be able to set times for Torah study for yourself and with others, with both peace of mind and physical rest.

Enclosed here is an excerpt from a sicha of a farbrengen on Shabbos Mevarchim Elul. It would be appropriate to publicize it in a suitable manner, both among your peers in your unit and among those like-minded individuals in other units with whom you can be in contact. If further explanation is needed, I rely on your understanding to find the appropriate words for this, and I look forward to hearing of your good work in this area.

I will conclude with a personal request: please convey my blessing to all your comrades in the service (not only to those you describe in your letter as "the religious soldiers." For as the saying of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, is known: "A Yid, neither does he want to be, nor can he be, severed from Elokus." Consequently, all your comrades are religious; it is just that some of them lack the knowledge of this fact. But ultimately, "no one shall be cast away from Him," and they, too, will come to know that they are faithful to Hashem and His Torah. Therefore, please convey this to all of them): a blessing for a *kesivah v'chasimah tovah* for a good and sweet year. Especially since the coming year is a Shmittah year, may it be fulfilled through the efforts of all who dwell in it: "A Shabbos of solemn rest shall there be for the land, a Shabbos to Hashem."

With blessings for success in your influence upon your peers, and a *kesivah v'chasimah tovah* for a good and sweet year for you and all your surroundings.

## 198

198

B"H, 16 Elul, 5711, Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the avreich, the G-d-fearing, learned, and distinguished, etc., Shalom Dov, may he live.

Greetings and blessings!

I received your letter from the evening after Shabbos, 1 Elul. You describe your participation in the work of "Chaver Pe'ilei Machaneh HaTorah," noting that you see good fruit from your labor. However, because the chareidi public in Eretz Yisrael (may it be rebuilt and established) has not responded to your call as they ought, the entire burden of the work falls upon you. This causes you to miss time from your Torah study, and you ask whether this is worthwhile for you—or, in your own words, whether you are obligated to "abandon your own soul" for the sake of the souls of others.

I was startled by this question. At a time when the Ribono shel Olam has granted you success and the opportunity to save the souls of Jewish sons and daughters from heresy—Heaven forbid—and to help them remain Jews faithful to Hashem and His Torah, a fact that is visible even to the physical eye and tangible, your yetzer hara comes and incites you, saying: "Who knows if this is the right thing to do? It would be better for you to engage in other pursuits, where you might perhaps flourish in your Torah study," and so on.

The halachic ruling in the Gemara is well known: a mitzvah that cannot be performed by others takes precedence over Torah study (Moed Katan 9b). Also well known is the statement of the Gemara in Temurah regarding the verse, "The rich and the poor meet together; Hashem gives light to the eyes of them both" (Mishlei 29:13). When one who is "rich" in Torah helps one who is "poor" in Torah, Hashem illuminates the eyes of them both; the one who gives also gains an increase in his own Torah study. This is far greater than the statement of our Sages (Taanis 7a), "I have learned much from my teachers, and from my friends more than from my teachers, but from my students more than from all of them." The statement in Taanis describes what a person learns according to his own capacity—note the precision of the word "learned." In contrast, the promise of our Sages in Temurah that "Hashem illuminates the eyes of them both" refers to a *shema'ata* (a teaching) that requires *siyata d'shmaya* (Heavenly assistance); one is requesting light according to the capacity of the Infinite, which is, of course, incomparable.

My intention here is that not only are you fulfilling the command of the Torah and the words of our Sages in Moed Katan by interrupting your studies for a time, but this very interruption of Torah is itself a form of fulfillment. Through this, your heart and mind become a thousand times more refined, such that in a small amount of time you will succeed in your studies to an incomparable degree.

In this, we see how profound the words of our Sages are in Shabbos (105b): "Such is the craft of the yetzer hara: today he says to him, 'Do this,' until he says to him, 'Go and worship idols.'" My revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, emphasized the word "such"—meaning that the yetzer hara is extremely cunning, approaching each person with a claim suited to his own spirit, but in the end, he incites him and brings him to the point where he can tell him, "Go and worship idols." See the *kuntres* printed for 18 Elul, which has surely reached you by now, regarding this statement of our Sages.

I will conclude my letter with wishes for success in your holy work. Through this, you will naturally also draw down success in your Torah study and fear of Heaven, and you will go from strength to strength in both Torah and yirah.

I am interested to know what your study routine was like before you entered the work of the aforementioned Chaver Pe'ilei Machaneh HaTorah, and whether you now have fixed times for the study of *nigleh* and *Chassidus*.

With blessings for a *kesivah v'chasimah tovah* for a good and sweet year.

Enclosed is an excerpt from the *sicha* of Shabbos Mevarchim Rosh Chodesh Elul, which will interest you.

***198***

**Shalom Dov, may he live:** Lifshitz.

With the blessing of *Ksivah V'Chasimah Tovah* for a good and sweet year, and regards to all of *Anash*, may they live.

## 101

B"H, 16 Elul, 5711, Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the Administration of Yeshivas Olei Russia in Lod,

Peace and Blessing!

1. In response to your notification that you are planning to hold a celebration on the upcoming Chai Elul in connection with the opening of the buildings, and your request for a letter from me: Since it is not something "for the sake of doing" to write a letter, I will, G-d willing, send a telegram for your celebration. It is a pity that you did not provide details regarding this—whether this will be a national gathering and whether representatives from other circles will also participate.

2. You have surely received my letter regarding the beginning of the school term, as well as the excerpt from the sicha of Shabbos Mevarchim Rosh Chodesh Elul. I am enclosing a copy of this excerpt in Lashon HaKodesh as well, and it is worthwhile to publicize them in an appropriate manner within wider circles.

3. Regarding your question concerning the travels of meshulachim on behalf of your yeshiva to various places, where you write that you are restricted in certain countries: It was not my intention to rule out travel to any specific country. Rather, in my opinion, for the benefit of the matter, it is appropriate that the institutions of Anash who send out meshulachim should consult with one another. One of two things should be done: either they should conduct a joint fundraising campaign, or they should arrange the travel schedules in such a way that there is no conflict between one institution and another.

4. I would like to draw your attention to educating those among the students of your yeshiva from the Yemenite immigrants who are suitable for this, so that they may, in a short time, become educators and guides among their brethren, the Yemenite immigrants. It is understood that any elaboration regarding the great necessity of this and the great benefit that can be expected from them is entirely superfluous.

With the blessing of *Kesivah V'chasimah Tovah* for a good and sweet year,

**M. Schneerson**

## 1001

By the Grace of Hashem, 16 Elul, 5711
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d fearing, learned, and diligent in his holy work, etc.,
Rabbi Chaim Zusia, may he live.

Peace and Blessing!

I have received your letters from the 20th of Menachem Av and the 1st of Elul in due time. I am writing to clarify a few points regarding matters I have already written to you about previously, so that there will be no confusion, and—most importantly—no friction between you and the other individuals working in the various departments of Agudas Chassidei Chabad.

1. It is self-understood that when I wrote to you encouraging you to utilize your strengths within our own "four cubits," my intention was to expand the work in all possible areas, without infringing upon the honor of another, and also to ensure there is no duplication of work in places where one person suffices.

2. It follows from the above that the "Ohalei Yosef Yitzchok Lubavitch" network belongs in those cities where there are no Tomchei Temimim or Achei Temimim institutions, or even in places where they do exist, but among circles that are not yet prepared to conduct themselves in the spirit of Tomchei Temimim—namely, with the daily study of Chassidus, etc. Since the institution is not named "Tomchei Temimim," it is not strictly necessary [...] to establish an institution that would join the Ohalei Yosef Yitzchok network.

Note: One who observes the activities of the Rebbe and his father, the Rebbe Rashab, may their merits protect us, will see upon reflection that while the Rebbe Rashab’s primary work in the field of education was among Chassidim, the Rebbe, my father-in-law, paved new paths for himself in the field of education among the broader circles of our people.

3. In accordance with the above, it is appropriate that you speak in a suitable manner with the administration of Agudas Chassidei Chabad and explain to them that you are not encroaching upon the territory of the Tomchei Temimim or Achei Temimim yeshivos, as your work is only in those places where those yeshivos are not present, or among those circles that the aforementioned yeshivos or the Toras Emes yeshivos cannot reach.

4. My hope is that, based on the above, you will be able to perform your public work while remaining in direct contact with me, and on the other hand, it will also be in harmony with the work of Agudas Chassidei Chabad as a whole, and with the Tomchei Temimim and Toras Emes yeshivos in particular, without anyone encroaching upon the other’s territory; on the contrary, you will assist one another.

5. Since, for the time being, there are not yet sufficient means for major development, it is advisable to proceed from the easy to the difficult and from the small to the large. Consequently, it is not worthwhile to acquire an institution now that would force Tomchei Temimim to conduct a fundraising campaign to pay off debts, etc., especially since one can hope that in time, the acquisition will be possible under more favorable conditions than at present.

6. In accordance with the above, since the Ohalei Yosef Yitzchok network of institutions is not bound by a rigid program like the Tomchei Temimim, Achei Temimim, and Toras Emes institutions, and they encompass all matters in the field of education provided that it is on the foundation of holiness, it is obvious that this network’s program also includes instruction for students who attend other schools. However, it is to be hoped that through the few hours they study in our network, they will change completely regarding their fear of Heaven and knowledge of Chassidus, etc.

7. My general opinion is that even if it is within your ability to conduct fundraising campaigns and collect significant sums, you must arrange the campaign in such a way that it does not harm the fundraising efforts of the other Anash institutions in the Holy Land, may it be rebuilt and established.

8. Regarding your question concerning the "streams" (political/educational affiliations): since the Anash institutions have until now received support from the stream called "Between the Streams"—that is, non-partisan—this approach is most suitable for the present time...

In your letter, you mention the organization of Charedi women for the rescue of youth immigrating to the Holy Land, which they organized half a year ago. You are surely aware that some time ago I wrote to Agudas Chassidei Chabad regarding a plan to organize a branch of Agudas N'shei Chabad, and it would be worthwhile for you to speak with them; perhaps it is possible to unite the two matters.

You will surely see the letter I wrote to Tzeirei Agudas Chassidei Chabad, and aside from the official response they will surely write to me, I request that you inform me unofficially about everything written there in detail. Thank you in advance.

It is undoubtedly unnecessary to urge you to participate with **all** your ability in all the work of Tzeirei Agudas Chassidei Chabad.

... With the blessing of *Kesivah V'chasimah Tovah*. For a good and sweet year.

103

103

B”H, 16 Elul, 5711, Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed Rabbi, the Chassid, G-d-fearing, and learned scholar, who engages in communal needs, etc., etc., Moreinu Harav Sh.Y. shlita,

Shalom u’vracha!

I received your letter from Erev Shabbos Parshas Eikev, and by now, my letter containing the *kuntres* of *Reshimot* on Megillas Eichah has surely reached you as well. I also received your letter from 26 Menachem Av in due time, and enclosed is a copy of my letter to Agudas Chassidei Chabad. I am somewhat concerned that lately I have not heard of your participation in the work of Agudas Chassidei Chabad in Eretz Yisrael, may it be rebuilt and established, though I reassure myself that this is surely only due to the distance.

Some time ago, we sent the *Piskei Dinim* that we reprinted to the Chief Rabbi, Herzog shlita, and also to you, and we have not yet received confirmation of their arrival. I do not know if the books were lost in transit or if they were delayed along the way.

It is surely known to you that for a long time now, I have been working, according to the instruction of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, on the publication of the *Sdei Chemed*. Thank G-d, despite the enormous expenses involved and the very great effort, we have already published nine volumes. My hope is that after the Yomim Tovim, the final volume—the tenth—will also be published. It includes the author’s will, the *kuntres Be’er BaSadeh*, *Nitzchiyos Yosef*, etc., and most importantly, the newly compiled indices: indices of entries, indices of authors, etc. When it is published, bli neder, it will be sent to you.

I am very distressed by the discord between the Charedi parties in Eretz Yisrael, may it be rebuilt and established, and primarily by the fact that some of them prioritize the gains of their party at the expense of the loss and damage to Charedi Judaism as a whole, etc. For you, who are on the scene, elaboration on this is superfluous.

I was happy to hear in your letter that the third volume of the encyclopedia is already at the bindery, and that you are now working on the fourth volume. I would be very pleased if all the volumes were in my library, as they are of the greatest benefit to anyone interested in our holy Torah. Elaboration on this is also superfluous, and as of yet, I do not have even one volume in my library.

You expressed wonder in your letter as to why Anash in Paris are not traveling to Eretz Yisrael, may it be rebuilt and established. It seems the reason is the letters and reports they receive from their acquaintances and relatives in the country, for throughout this entire time, only a few individuals have asked me whether to move to Eretz Yisrael, and it seems those few are preparing to make aliyah.

In the coming days, I will return one of the two booklets to you.

103

## 104

104

B"H, 16 Elul, 5711, Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter, in which you commented on what was said in the section of the sicha of Shabbos Mevarchim Elul, that cities of refuge existed wherever Jews were—both in the desert and "beyond the Jordan, which is outside the Land"—and you ask whether "beyond the Jordan" and "outside the Land" are two separate matters, or if "beyond the Jordan" is considered "outside the Land."

**Response:**

If you look at the version that was edited by me, it is written there: "whether in the desert, whether in Eretz Yisrael, whether beyond the Jordan, which is outside the Land." If "outside the Land" were a fourth category, the word "whether" would have been used for it as well.

My intention is that beyond the Jordan (relative to Eretz Yisrael) is "outside the Land." See Sifrei, Parshas Masei, and Rambam, Hilchos Rotzeach, chapter 8, halacha 8, and the Kesef Mishneh there, where one explanation of the language of the Sifrei—which uses the term "outside the Land"—is that it refers to beyond the Jordan as "outside the Land" relative to Eretz Yisrael.

Regarding your question in your letter about the Sifrei—why it needs to derive the cities beyond the Jordan from the word "shall be" (*tihyena*), given that they are explicitly mentioned in the verse—it can be explained based on what is clarified in the Tosefta (chapter 2; and I believe it is also in the Yerushalmi, though I do not have it before me) of Makkos: that if these cities were destroyed, others are built, and if it is impossible to build them in their original location, they are built in **another** location, and we derive from the word "shall be" that they must, at the very least, be beyond the Jordan...

#### ***104***

Printed in Likutei Sichos, Vol. 2, p. 695. **The Sicha:** Printed in Likutei Sichos, Vol. 2, p. 623. **It is written there:** When the sicha was printed in the second edition and was edited once more by the Rebbe, in order for the meaning to be clearer, he wrote: "whether beyond the Jordan, which was outside the Land of Israel."

## 1055

1055

By the Grace of Hashem, 19 Elul, 5711, Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed Rabbi and Chassid, G-d-fearing and learned, engaged in communal needs, etc., Moreinu HaRav Asher, may he live.

Greetings and Blessings!

I received your letter in due time. I ask for your forgiveness that, due to the many pressures and the heavy workload, I have not been able to reply properly to your two letters until now. Surely, in these days of mercy and favor, you will forgive this as well.

I was pleased to read in your letter the account of how you have striven, and are still striving, to purchase a building for the Yeshiva in Melbourne, and that Hashem has granted success to your efforts in finding a suitable building. Without a doubt, in the course of time, all the necessary means for the payment of the building will also be found. The main thing is that Hashem should increase their borders with good students, and when the main thing is achieved, the secondary matters will follow suit as a matter of course.

Regarding your question about the name: if you have already chosen the name, it should not be changed. However, if you are still before the final decision, and considering that in the initial period it will be impossible to organize the institution to meet all the desired requirements according to the spirit of Anash, I suggest naming it "Oholei Yosef Yitzchak Lubavitch." Regarding the educational institutions I am currently establishing, I strive—if it is appropriate—to name them after my father-in-law, the Rebbe, from whose waters we drink and by whose words we live.

The magnitude of the matter of establishing and developing a Yeshiva based on the purity of **Kodesh**—for *chomer* (matter) in *Kodesh* is greater even than in *Terumah*, and the allusion to this is well known: *Terumah* is in the world of Beriah, while *Kodesh*, regarding which it is said in the Zohar (Vol. III, 94b) that it is "a matter in itself," is the world of Atzilus, which is why the fourth [level] is only in *Kodesh*. The corresponding part of Torah is the *Sod* (secret) of Torah, and as is known, the *Pardes* of Torah—its *Sod* and Kabbalah—is in the world of Atzilus—

This means Torah study founded upon and illuminated by the "Light of Torah," which is the *Pnimiyus* (inner dimension) of Torah—the teachings of Chassidus. It is impossible to estimate or detail [its importance], even in normal times, and certainly in this time of emergency, when the Jewish people have been scattered to places far from one another, and the powers of the soul have also been scattered by the abundance of worries and anxieties to an alarming degree compared to years past. All the more so, one must seek and strive with tremendous exertion for everything that unites, especially in Torah. Although there is only one Torah for us all, its unity is emphasized and highlighted most clearly in the *Pnimiyus* of Torah. Just as, on the simple level, there is not as much of the matter of disputes and arguments as there is in the *Nigleh* (revealed) part of Torah—and at the root of things, since this is from the "Tree of Life" and not from the "Tree of Knowledge of Good and Evil," as explained in *Iggeres HaKodesh*, section 26—it is understood as a matter of course that "there is no difficulty and no dispute there, etc." (see there in the Zohar and *Iggeres HaKodesh*). And especially in these days, the "footsteps of Mashiach," when the end of our exile and the coming of our righteous Mashiach are near, it is all the more certain that the importance of bringing light to a new place is magnified, especially when one brings the light from the Source of Light.

My prayer is that the desire of Hashem will succeed in your hands, speedily in our days—and as explained in the *Maamar* printed for 12 Tammuz this year, that it should be in a manner of "nature that is above nature," and the light should go on increasing, until "the night shines like the day." We have already been promised by our Sages that all who involve themselves in this and similar matters, the merit of the many depends upon them, to bestow upon them a blessing of good in all that they and theirs require.

Give my regards to the entire group, may they live, and please, I ask of your kindness to convey this to each one individually. Since they have chosen you as their emissary to inform me of the good news mentioned above, I will return a blessing through you to each one of them with a blessing for a *Kesivah V'Chasimah Tovah* for a good and sweet year.

**M. Schneerson**

Enclosed is a segment from the *Sicha* of *Shabbos Mevarchim* Rosh Chodesh Elul, which I am sure you will publish in an appropriate manner.

And a booklet regarding communal activity, in which I am sure you will find much of interest.

## 1113

B"H,

You should certainly make an effort to study the maamarim in a group of friends (*d'vuk chaverim*). For if Chazal praised the virtue of studying not in isolation at all times, then how much more so in the days preceding Rosh Hashanah, on Rosh Hashanah, and during the Aseres Yemei Teshuvah—when there is a special virtue in *d'vuk chaverim*.

This is as explained in the teachings of Chassidus on the verse "You are standing [nitzavim] today, all of you" —a parsha that is always read before Rosh Hashanah. It is hinted at in the word "today" (*hayom*), which refers to Rosh Hashanah, signifying that all the sparks of the souls stand and ascend to their source until they are **before** Hashem. And it must be "all of you," meaning that everyone gathers together to be united as one: "your heads, your tribes," etc., "down to the drawer of your water."

My revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, concludes with this—which he heard from his father, the holy Rebbe, which he had as a tradition from Rebbe to Rebbe: When the Alter Rebbe was in Mezritch, his teacher—the Maggid of Mezritch—revealed to him who he was. He revealed that his *avodah* was to reveal and explain the teachings of the Baal Shem Tov regarding *ahavas Hashem* and *ahavas Yisrael*, and to reveal the *derech* of Chassidus Chabad. And, first and foremost—his teacher, the Maggid of Mezritch, conveyed to him in the name of his teacher, the Baal Shem Tov—the *derech* of *avodah* is that one must also bring simple people close, because one must love a Yid simply because he is a Yid.

He adds an explanation to this: The Baal Shem Tov revealed the concept of the connection of *ahavas Hashem*, *ahavas haTorah*, and *ahavas Yisrael*. The Mezritcher Maggid revealed the *haskalah* and *hasagah* in the integration of these three loves, with the inner explanation of the three modes of love: "with all your heart, with all your soul, and with all your might." And Rabbeinu HaZaken revealed the *derech* of how every single person **can, should,** and **must** bring these three loves into *b'fo'al* (actual practice), stating that *ahavas Yisrael* is the "supernal gate," upon which is inscribed in luminous letters: "This is the gate to the Most High."

And through this—that we are all standing together as one—"Hashem our G-d establishes us today," this day of Rosh Hashanah, "as a people to Him, and He will be to us as a G-d." He is destined to illuminate us with an eternal light and redeem us with the true and complete Geulah, speedily in our days, literally.

**Menachem Mendel son of Channah**

**Schneerson**

Tuesday of Selichos, 5711, Brooklyn, N.Y.

## 1114

B”H, Tuesday of Selichos, 5711, Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, etc., Moreinu Harav Y. shlita,

Peace and blessing!

Enclosed is the Kuntres for the upcoming Rosh Hashanah. As mentioned in the introduction, you will surely endeavor to study it in a group and with the bond of friends. May it be the will [of Hashem] that, since this is one of the things through which Torah is **acquired**—

—and the precision in the change of language is well known: [it says] **things** (*devarim*), and not **virtues** (*ma’alos*) as it does at the beginning of that passage—for these are matters of preparation and humility, and the student should not say, "What will my friend add to my learning? My own strength is sufficient, and on the contrary, the other person will distract me," etc., etc.—

—may this study become an acquisition in the souls of the students, such that it is called by their name, "their Torah." As is the saying of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory: It is not only that he studied Torah, but that the Torah studied him.

My father-in-law, the Rebbe, related: My father, the Rebbe, would continue the delivery of the Chassidus maamar of the second day of Rosh Hashanah and conclude it on the night following the Yom Tov. The reason—to draw down the influences of the forty-eight hours of Rosh Hashanah into the world, so that in all matters, the light of Chassidus will be heard (*zich herin*) and will shine.

My suggestion is that everyone should likewise act to connect the hours of Rosh Hashanah with the beginning of the night following Rosh Hashanah through the study of Chassidus. And because our Nesi’im have paved this path for us, the light of Chassidus will be drawn down for us as well, in all our affairs, down to the lowest levels.

Blessing you and being blessed with a *Kesivah Vachasimah Tovah*,

**Menachem Mendel ben Chana**

**Schneerson**

## 1115

1115

B”H, 3rd day of Selichos, 5711, Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the sons and daughters of Israel, in every place and location, may Hashem grant them life.

Peace and blessing!

At the end of the year, as we prepare for the beginning of the year that is approaching for us and for all the sons and daughters of Israel for good and for blessing,

Each and every one of us draws up a plan—at least in general terms—for their conduct and activities for the days to come, with a good resolution and a decision to ascend higher and higher.

The year 5712, which is approaching, is the year of Shemitah, a year of which it is written: “The land shall have a Sabbath of solemn rest, a Sabbath to Hashem... And the Sabbath of the land shall be for you to eat... and for your cattle, etc.”

A verse does not depart from its literal meaning.

However, beyond this, our holy Torah has hinted at a great message and has prepared for us a detailed plan for the coming year:

*Shabbos Shabbaton yihyeh la’aretz* (The land shall have a Sabbath of solemn rest) — a cessation from all worldliness and materiality in our daily lives and activities.

*Shabbos la’Hashem* (A Sabbath to Hashem) — and not for the sake of false ideologies and foreign outlooks that mislead and divert the Jewish person from their original and essential path, which is the path of Hashem. This is the path for which our first forefather, Avraham, sacrificed his life, and he commanded his children and his household after him to keep this path. They did so, and it is in this path that our people, the Jewish people, have lived for more than three thousand years.

*Vehayta Shabbos ha’aretz lachem le’ochlah... u’livhemtcha* (And the Sabbath of the land shall be for you to eat... and for your cattle) — the cessation of materiality and the attainment of spirituality are not intended only for the time of tefillah and the study of Torah, after which one might say in their heart: "In my business, in my eating, and the like, the House of Israel is just like all the nations."

This is not our way.

There is **one** G-d, **one** Torah for the people of Israel, **one** nation on earth. Unity and wholeness must exist in our lives—**unified** lives, founded upon and permeated by one idea, which is: Israel, the Torah, and the Kudsha Brich Hu are all **one**.

The Sabbath of the land, the Sabbath to Hashem, must be present in **all** our affairs, even in our eating and for our cattle.

Only through such a way of life has our existence been sustained until now, and through the decision to bring this conduct into practice in our daily lives for the future as well, we will merit to be inscribed and sealed for a good and sweet year, with good that is visible and revealed.

Blessing and being blessed with a good inscription and sealing,

**Menachem Mendel son of Channah**

**Schneerson**

## 1116

1116

B"H, 3rd day of Selichos, 5711, Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the sons and daughters of Yisrael, everywhere, may Hashem grant them life,

Peace and abundant blessing!

In these days when we stand at the crossroads between the old year and the new year—which is approaching us and all the sons and daughters of Yisrael for good and for blessing—in these days of spiritual awakening and introspection,

The resolution forms within each person that the coming year should be better and more elevated—in daily life and in tangible accomplishments for oneself and for others.

If this is true of every year, it is of special significance this year, for the coming year, 5712, is the year of **Shmittah**.

The year of Shmittah is, in certain respects, unique. Just as Shabbos is the holy day within the seven days of the week, so too is the year of Shmittah the holy year within the seven-year cycle. The Torah provides a special program for the Shmittah year: "And the land shall rest" (*Veshavtah Haaretz*)—the earth must rest; "a Shabbos to Hashem" (*Shabbos LaHashem*)—a rest sanctified to Hashem.

All of this is in the material, physical sense.

In a deeper, spiritual sense, this means that the year must serve as a reminder: **"And the land shall rest"**—to detach oneself from "earthliness" and coarseness; to become more spiritual.

**"A Shabbos to Hashem"**—to shake off false ideals and pseudo-spirituality, which ultimately lead to even lower deeds and coarseness, and to rise to true refinement and spirituality through the Torah and mitzvos given by Hashem. And this refinement and spirituality must permeate life in all its details, including eating, drinking, business, and so on. Even things that are connected with physical and material daily life must also be filled with the light of Elokus.

Permeated by this thought of a Shabbos and a Shmittah in our daily lives, and determined to hold fast to the path of Torah and mitzvos with mesiras nefesh—the path our people have chosen and trodden for over three thousand years—we will surely merit a *kesivah v'chasimah tovah*, for a good and sweet year, with good that is revealed and manifest.

Blessing and being blessed with a *kesivah v'chasimah tovah*,

**Menachem Mendel ben Chana**

**Schneerson**

#### 1116

Published in *Likkutei Sichos*, Vol. 9, p. 406.

## 117

B"H, 3rd day of Selichos, 5711, Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed presidents, gabbaim, mispalelim, and members of the "Nusach Ari," "Tzemach Tzedek," and "Lubavitch" shuls, wherever they may be, may Hashem protect them and grant them life.

Shalom u’vracha!

As we approach the New Year, may it be for us and for all the sons and daughters of Yisrael for good and for blessing, I send you my blessing for a good and sweet year, both materially and spiritually.

Our Sages, of blessed memory, teach that a name carries significant inner meaning. The name "Nusach Ari," "Tzemach Tzedek," or "Lubavitch," and the like, which a shul bears, carries a profound inner significance and mission.

Your grandfathers and great-grandfathers practiced mesiras nefesh to uphold the Chassidic name, which they bore with great responsibility and pride.

You, their children and grandchildren, will surely also know how to appreciate the great responsibility that rests upon you: to guard and perpetuate the great mesorah of our fathers and the inheritance they left in your hands.

Therefore, I turn to you in these days of spiritual awakening and arousal: Strengthen the foundations of your shul, both in quantity—by increasing the number of members and mispalelim, especially among the youth—and in quality, through shiurim in the study of Torah and Chassidus: Chumash, Mishnayos, Gemara, Ein Yaakov, Shulchan Aruch, Tanya, maamarim, etc., along with a Chassidic farbrengen from time to time, so that your shul may be alive, warm, and bright.

Surely you will not let the good and appropriate time of the coming holy days pass without creating a revival in your shul regarding the aforementioned matters. I hope that you will convene, if necessary, a special meeting to carry this out in actual practice, and Hashem will surely grant you success. It will gladden me to hear good news regarding this. And according to the words of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory:

**It is a chazakah that serious work does not go to waste.**

With the blessing of kesivah v’chasimah tovah to each and every one of the mispalelim and members, he and his household, his children, and his children’s children, may they live, among all our brethren the children of Yisrael, for a good and sweet year.

**M. Schneerson**

## 118

118

B"H, 29 Elul, 5711, Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

It was with pleasure that I received your letter of 4 Elul. I was happy to read that you are continuing your work in communal activities, helping observant Jews in general, and Anash and the affairs of the yeshiva in particular. It is certain that this will not hinder your success in your business; on the contrary, it will be a cause and a vessel to expand the channels of parnassah through which Hashem will provide for you, from today onwards, from His full, open, holy, and expansive hand.

Surely you have heard the expression that my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, used to say constantly: that for all those who assist in the proper chinuch of Jewish children—who are called "children to Hashem your G-d"—Hashem gives them measure for measure, that they should have true nachas, Jewish nachas, from their own children. In this case, too, it is certain that it will be so, and that you, together with your wife, may she live, will have nachas, Jewish nachas, from your daughter, may she live.

When I was at the resting place of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, on Chai Elul—which is the birthday of our teacher the Baal Shem Tov and of the Alter Rebbe, author of the Shulchan Aruch and the Tanya—I mentioned you and your family, may they live, for whatever each of you requires. Surely he will arouse compassion on high so that you will have blessing and success.

I was pleased to make the acquaintance of your daughter, may she live—when she was with me on her way to London—and she made a good impression on me. This strengthens my confidence, as I wrote to you, that you will have Jewish nachas from her.

Regarding the distress caused by your non-Jewish partner, my opinion is that you should reflect: perhaps you have caused, whether inadvertently or under duress, distress to Jews through or within this business. When you rectify that, the distress from non-Jews will certainly be removed from you.

As we approach the New Year, which comes upon us and all of Israel for good and for blessing, I hereby express my blessing: a blessing of *kesivah v'chasimah tovah* for you and your family, may they live, for a good and sweet year, in both material and spiritual matters alike.

With blessing.

P.S. Enclosed is a message in English, as well as a *michtav klali* for Rosh Hashanah, which will surely interest you.

## 117

B"H, 29 Elul, 5711, Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and blessings!

I was pleased to read your letter of 4 Tavo, in which you write that your husband, may he live and be well, is feeling better in his health, and that your son... may he live and be well, has been helping out in the business. I hope that you will be able to report good news to me regarding yourself and all your family.

May we all soon merit the resurrection of the dead, when "He will swallow up death forever," and may the verse, "And you who cleave to Hashem your G-d are all alive today," be fulfilled literally, in a physical sense.

As we approach the New Year, which is coming upon us and all of Israel for good and for blessing, I hereby extend my blessing to your husband, to you, and to your household, may they live: a blessing of *kesivah v’chasimah tovah* for a good and sweet year, in both material and spiritual matters alike.

With blessings.

## 1220

1220

B"H, 29 Elul, 5711, Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and blessings!

I received your letter of 13 Elul with the *pidyon nefesh* with pleasure, and I read it on the auspicious day of 18 Elul at the *tziyun* of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory.

Regarding what you write in your letter about being distressed concerning your health: you have no reason to be distressed at all. You have surely read in the memoirs at length about the *avodah* of the father of the Alter Rebbe in the garden and in the field. We do not know the secret of the *birurim*, nor do we know how or in what manner we must complete the supernal intent. We rely on our Father in Heaven, who will guide us on the good path for our benefit, in a way that is good, visible, and revealed, both physically and spiritually.

I was pleased to read in your letter of your efforts in strengthening the Yiddishkeit of... I also mentioned their names at the *tziyun* of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, and I hope that your efforts with them will now be easier for you. As our Sages of blessed memory promised (*Temurah* 15a), "The rich and the poor meet; Hashem illuminates the eyes of both," etc. Since you are influencing them and the like in Yiddishkeit, Torah, and *mitzvos*, Hashem will surely illuminate your eyes as well, granting you success in your study of *nigleh* and *Chassidus*, and in all your other affairs.

As we approach the New Year, which is coming upon us and all of Israel for good and for blessing, I hereby express my blessing to you: a blessing of *kesivah v'chasimah tovah* for a good and sweet year, physically and spiritually alike.

With blessings for success in your studies and in all your affairs.

## 1221

And as we approach the new year that is coming upon us and upon all of Israel for good and for blessing, I hereby wish to express my blessing to you and to your family, *sheyichyu*, a blessing of *kesivah v'chasimah tovah* for a good and sweet year, both materially and spiritually.

With blessings.

## 1223

B"H, end of Elul, 5711

Greetings and blessings!

Your *pidyon nefesh* has been received. As we approach the New Year, which is coming for us and for all of Yisrael for good and for blessing, I hereby express my blessing for a *kesivah v’chasimah tovah* for a good and sweet year, in both material and spiritual matters alike.

With blessings for success in your studies and in *yiras shamayim*,

**M. Schneerson**

***

Regarding your question about traveling here: In my opinion, since Divine Providence has brought you to illuminate the light of *Chassidus* in Australia, you should work in this area, at least to some extent. Afterwards, you can look for "tastier" [more enjoyable] work.

As for your doubt regarding whether the other person is truly affected by you, and therefore you might stop this work—*chas v’shalom*. It is well known that *tzedakah*, even when not done for its own sake (*shelo lishmah*), sustains the poor person, even when one does not have the proper intention, etc.

***

Regarding your observation that in *Tanya*, Chapter 46, it brings a proof that the *Ribono shel Olam* Himself descended to Mitzrayim from the verse "And I have come down to deliver him," and not as the author of the *Haggadah* writes, based on the verse "And I will pass through the land of Mitzrayim," etc.:

The *Tanya* is based on the words of our Sages in *Shemos Rabbah* 32:8 and in *Pesikta Chadta* (printed in *Beis HaMidrash*, Vol. 6): "Because of His great love for them, He Himself descended to save them from Mitzrayim," etc. This is in contrast to the teaching of the author of the *Haggadah*, where it could be said that this was because of the impurity of Mitzrayim, making it impossible for an angel to descend (and not necessarily because of the love for Yisrael), as is explained in *Likutei Torah*, *Tzav* (12c). In *Tanya*, the primary intent is to emphasize the love for Yisrael, while in the *Haggadah*, the intent is to negate an angel, etc. (see there in *Likutei Torah*). Therefore, each source cited the verse that specifically clarifies its own point.
